The Master of Ballantrae 巴伦特雷少爷
by Robert Louis Stevenson 作者：罗伯特·路易斯·斯蒂文森

Chapter 1 第一章
Summary of Events During this Master’s Wanderings 大少爷流浪期间的大事摘要
The full truth of this odd matter is what the world has long been looking for, and public curiosity is sure to welcome. 这件奇事的全部真相就是世人一直所寻求的，公众的好奇心当然对这样的真相很是欢迎。
It so befell that I was intimately mingled with the last years and history of the house; and there does not live one man so able as myself to make these matters plain, or so desirous to narrate them faithfully. 我曾亲历这个家族的过去以及它的终结，这委实是种缘分；这世界上最有发言权也最乐于把它娓娓道来的，也就是我了。
I knew the Master; on many secret steps of his career I have an authentic memoir in my hand; I sailed with him on his last voyage almost alone; I made one upon that winter’s journey of which so many tales have gone abroad; and I was there at the man’s death. 我熟悉大少爷；他一生中的很多秘密我都了如指掌；在他最后一次远航中，我几乎是他唯一的伙伴，还有他那次声名远播国外的冬季旅行，我也一起去了，甚至他撒手人寰的时候，我都在场。
As for my late Lord Durrisdeer, I served him and loved him near twenty years; and thought more of him the more I knew of him. 至于已故的达里斯迪尔勋爵，我做他的仆从将近二十年，衷心地爱戴他，并且知他愈甚，思他愈切。
Altogether, I think it not fit that so much evidence should perish; the truth is a debt I owe my lord’s memory; and I think my old years will flow more smoothly, and my white hair lie quieter on the pillow, when the debt is paid. 总之，我自觉这些旧事不该泯灭于尘埃之中，我对爵爷的记忆使我觉得这是一笔账，我得把它讲出来；我已然银丝满头，等我清了这笔账，才能日日安度晚年，夜夜安然入梦。
The Duries of Durrisdeer and Ballantrae were a strong family in the south-west from the days of David First. 迪里和巴伦特雷的达里斯迪尔家族从大卫一世时期就是西南地区的名门望族。
A rhyme still current in the countryside— 有首乡间民谣至今依然传唱不衰——
Kittle folk are the Durrisdeers, 达里斯迪尔威风八面，
They ride wi’ over mony spears— 铁马银枪纵横四方。
bears the mark of its antiquity; and the name appears in another, which common report attributes to Thomas of Ercildoune himself—I cannot say how truly, and which some have applied—I dare not say with how much justice—to the events of this narration: 家族历史之长由此可见一斑；还有一首诗，作者是谁我也说不准，一般认为是爱西多恩的托马斯，说的东西跟我们要讲的事情有多大关系，我也不确定，在此姑且一提：
Twa Duries in Durrisdeer, 达里斯迪尔的迪里小两口，
Ane to tie and ane to ride, 穿衣打马各自忙，　
An ill day for the groom 儿郎无意空惆怅，
And a waur day for the bride. 娇娘有情理红妆。
Authentic history besides is filled with their exploits which (to our modern eyes) seem not very commendable: and the family suffered its full share of those ups and downs to which the great houses of Scotland have been ever liable. 除此之外的那些家族“光荣史”，以我们现在的眼光来看，没什么值得赞美；它真正的过往正如很多苏格兰的大宅一样，几经沉浮，飘摇于无常的世事之间。
But all these I pass over, to come to that memorable year 1745, when the foundations of this tragedy were laid. 前事我就不再赘言了，直接从1745年讲起，那一年，悲剧已然奏响了它的序曲。
At that time there dwelt a family of four persons in the house of Durrisdeer, near St. Bride’s, on the Solway shore; a chief hold of their race since the Reformation. 那时候达里斯迪尔一家四口住在圣伯莱德教堂附近索尔威海岸边的大宅子里；宗教改革后，他们是家族主要的一脉。
My old lord, eighth of the name, was not old in years, but he suffered prematurely from the disabilities of age; his place was at the chimney side; there he sat reading, in a lined gown, with few words for any man, and wry words for none: the model of an old retired housekeeper; and yet his mind very well nourished with study, and reputed in the country to be more cunning than he seemed. 我的老主人在兄弟中排行第八，虽非高龄，却有些未老先衰，行动不怎么灵活；他经常穿着衬里长衫坐在壁炉边读书，本来就少言寡语，得罪人的话更是从不出口，看起来就像是一位退休老管家；不过他博学广读，自然不会头脑简单，乡里盛传他远远没有看似那般好说话。
The master of Ballantrae, James in baptism, took from his father the love of serious reading; some of his tact perhaps as well, but that which was only policy in the father became black dissimulation in the son. 然后是巴伦特雷大少爷，教名詹姆斯，倒是继承了他父亲善读的习惯；只是他父亲的一些策略，到了他这里就成了阴谋。
The face of his behaviour was merely popular and wild: he sat late at wine, later at the cards; had the name in the country of “an unco man for the lasses;” and was ever in the front of broils. 他浪荡不羁，名声在外，日日饮酒至深夜，夜夜打牌到黎明，得了“花花公子”的称号不说，一有打架斗殴的事情，他就迫不及待地冲锋陷阵。
But for all he was the first to go in, yet it was observed he was invariably the best to come off; and his partners in mischief were usually alone to pay the piper. 有趣的是，第一个去的是他，第一个脱身的也是他，他是什么麻烦也不沾身，他身边的同伴往往就得给他当炮灰了。
This luck or dexterity got him several ill-wishers, but with the rest of the country, enhanced his reputation; so that great things were looked for in his future, when he should have gained more gravity. 他在这方面可谓小运连连，技巧纯熟，可同时也给自己招来了不少怨怼，乡下地方，流言就跟得了水的野草一样疯长；本一个前途无量的大好青年，就这么在本该更稳重的年月葬送掉了自己的好名声。
One very black mark he had to his name; but the matter was hushed up at the time, and so defaced by legends before I came into those parts, that I scruple to set it down. 他确是名声不佳，但他惹的那些麻烦总能烟消云散，再加上那些都是我来之前的传说了，我犹豫了一段时间还是在他家安定下来。
If it was true, it was a horrid fact in one so young; and if false, it was a horrid calumny. 不过我得说，若传言为真，这年轻人惹麻烦的本领可是非比寻常；若为假，这诽谤未免太过恶毒了些。
I think it notable that he had always vaunted himself quite implacable, and was taken at his word; so that he had the addition among his neighbours of “an ill man to cross.” 我还发现他总是标榜自己爱憎分明，觉得自己说什么人家都信；邻里只得又给他加了个“实难相处”的评价。
Here was altogether a young nobleman (not yet twenty-four in the year ’45) who had made a figure in the country beyond his time of life. 1745年那时他还不到24岁，不管是以哪种方式，这个年轻的贵族闻名乡里的程度早就已经不是同年龄的人可以企及的了。
The less marvel if there were little heard of the second son, Mr. Henry (my late Lord Durrisdeer), who was neither very bad nor yet very able, but an honest, solid sort of lad like many of his neighbours. 无怪乎别人对这家的二儿子少有耳闻了，亨利先生（即后任达里斯迪尔勋爵）既不惊才绝绝也不声名狼藉，但跟很多年轻人一样诚实可靠。
Little heard, I say; but indeed it was a case of little spoken. 我说别人对他少有耳闻，其实他根本是无人提及。
He was known among the salmon fishers in the firth, for that was a sport that he assiduously followed; he was an excellent good horse-doctor besides; and took a chief hand, almost from a boy, in the management of the estates. 打鲑鱼的渔民们倒是与他相熟，这也算是他常年不辍的一项运动；他是位不错的马医；此外，几乎是从小时候起，他就主管家中的地产事宜。
How hard a part that was, in the situation of that family, none knows better than myself; nor yet with how little colour of justice a man may there acquire the reputation of a tyrant and a miser. 再也没有人比我更了解料理这事的难处了，何况还是在那种豪门深府，别人能想都不想就把专横和吝悭的名号安到你身上，根本不考虑这对你公平不公平。
The fourth person in the house was Miss Alison Graeme, a near kinswoman, an orphan, and the heir to a considerable fortune which her father had acquired in trade. 第四位就是艾莉森·格雷姆小姐了，是个孤儿，作为这家的亲戚住在这里，她父亲生前做买卖给她留了一笔可观的遗产。
This money was loudly called for by my lord’s necessities; indeed the land was deeply mortgaged; and Miss Alison was designed accordingly to be the Master’s wife, gladly enough on her side; with how much good-will on his, is another matter. 老主人对这笔钱趋之若鹜——实际上家里很多地产都已经被抵押出去了，所以他想让艾莉森小姐成为这家未来的主母，以婚事解决财事。女方对这事，那是满心欢喜；至于男方打的什么主意，又是另一回事了。
She was a comely girl, and in those days very spirited and self-willed; for the old lord having no daughter of his own, and my lady being long dead, she had grown up as best she might. 小姐长得很标致，性格刚烈而任性；老主人膝下无女，妻子又去世多年，对小姐可算是娇宠万分。
To these four came the news of Prince Charlie’s landing, and set them presently by the ears. 这四位听说查理王子登陆的消息后，没多久就吵了起来。
My lord, like the chimney-keeper that he was, was all for temporising. 我的老主人还是那副稳坐壁炉前雷打不动的架势，力主求和。
Miss Alison held the other side, because it appeared romantical; and the Master (though I have heard they did not agree often) was for this once of her opinion. 艾丽森小姐则主张开打，因为那明显更刺激点儿；而大少爷则跟她一个想法，要知道，他俩达成共识的时候可真是不多。
The adventure tempted him, as I conceive; he was tempted by the opportunity to raise the fortunes of the house, and not less by the hope of paying off his private liabilities, which were heavy beyond all opinion. 我琢磨着，对大少爷来说，打仗一来可以满足他那期待冒险、躁动不安的心；二来可以为家族带来更多的财富；但最投他所好的，就是他可以发发战争财，把他的那些私债填平。
As for Mr. Henry, it appears he said little enough at first; his part came later on. 至于亨利先生，一开始就没怎么表达意见，过后才加入争论。
It took the three a whole day’s disputation, before they agreed to steer a middle course, one son going forth to strike a blow for King James, my lord and the other staying at home to keep in favour with King George. 三个人花了一天时间才争论出个折中之法：一个儿子跟着詹姆斯国王起义，另一个儿子跟老主人一起留在家中，继续作乔治国王的良民。
Doubtless this was my lord’s decision; and, as is well known, it was the part played by many considerable families. 这自然是老主人的决定，也是其他很多世家大族的做法。
But the one dispute settled, another opened. 然而前浪初定，后波又起。
For my lord, Miss Alison, and Mr. Henry all held the one view: that it was the cadet’s part to go out; and the Master, what with restlessness and vanity, would at no rate consent to stay at home. 老主人、艾莉森小姐和亨利先生一致认为：出门打仗是幺儿干的事；可本来就被打仗引得心神不定、个性又狂妄自负的大少爷则根本就不同意留在家里。
My lord pleaded, Miss Alison wept, Mr. Henry was very plain spoken: all was of no avail. 老主人哀声恳求，小姐声泪俱下，弟弟苦口婆心，大少爷都视若草芥。
“It is the direct heir of Durrisdeer that should ride by his King’s bridle,” says the Master. 大少爷言之凿凿：“唯有达里斯迪尔之嫡子能与王者为伍。”
“If we were playing a manly part,” says Mr. Henry, “there might be sense in such talk. “若我们在行勇者之事，”亨利先生说，“你还算是言之有理。
But what are we doing? 可我们现在是干什么？
Cheating at cards!” 不过偷梁换柱，赌命一场！”
“We are saving the house of Durrisdeer, Henry,” his father said. “咱们可是在救这个家于水火啊，亨利。”老主人附和道。
“And see, James,” said Mr. Henry, “if I go, and the Prince has the upper hand, it will be easy to make your peace with King James. “你看，詹姆斯，”亨利先生说道，“要是我去跟着王子起义，王子要是占了上风，你之后再投诚那是很简单的事。
But if you go, and the expedition fails, we divide the right and the title. 要是你去，起义一旦失败，咱们家从此可就失势了。
And what shall I be then?” 到时候我该如何自处呢？”
“You will be Lord Durrisdeer,” said the Master. “那你就继任达里斯迪尔勋爵呗，”大少爷接口，
“I put all I have upon the table.” “我要背水一战。”
“I play at no such game,” cries Mr. Henry. “这事我恕不奉陪！”亨利先生几乎是在咆哮了，
“I shall be left in such a situation as no man of sense and honour could endure. “哪个有身份有脑子的男人会把自己弄到那个境地里去？
I shall be neither fish nor flesh!” he cried. 我到时是里外不是人啊！”他高声喊道。
And a little after he had another expression, plainer perhaps than he intended. 过了一会儿，他脸上渐渐现出另一种表情，那表情甚至比他自己想的更加坦白。
“It is your duty to be here with my father,” said he. “陪着父亲是你的责任，”他说道，
“You know well enough you are the favourite.” “你比谁都清楚你才是父亲的宠儿。”
“Ay?” said the Master. “啊？”大少爷说道，
“And there spoke Envy! “你终于把那点儿嫉妒露出来了？
Would you trip up my heels—Jacob?” said he, and dwelled upon the name maliciously. 迫不及待地来给我穿小鞋了是吧——雅各？”大少爷喊亨利先生的教名时还恶意地停顿了一下。
Mr. Henry went and walked at the low end of the hall without reply; for he had an excellent gift of silence. 这下，亨利先生发挥了他沉默是金的本性，一声不吭地踱步到大厅的另一边去了。
Presently he came back. 不过一会儿他又走回来说道：
“I am the cadet and I SHOULD go,” said he. “我是次子，所以我才应该去。”他说，
“And my lord here in the master, and he says I SHALL go. “再说咱们的父亲，现任勋爵也这么认为。
What say ye to that, my brother?” 这你又怎么说呢，大哥？”
“I say this, Harry,” returned the Master, “that when very obstinate folk are met, there are only two ways out: Blows—and I think none of us could care to go so far; or the arbitrament of chance—and here is a guinea piece. “我认为，”大少爷答道，“要是咱俩都固执己见，那就只有两条路可走了：要么谈崩了打起来——咱俩可都不想；要么就让命运做主——这儿刚好有个一先令的硬币。
Will you stand by the toss of the coin?” 你敢用硬币赌一场么？”　　　
“I will stand and fall by it,” said Mr. Henry. “我还就站这儿看着了，”亨利先生说道，
“Heads, I go; shield, I stay.” “人头，我去；背面，你去。”
The coin was spun, and it fell shield. 硬币转了两下，背面朝上。
“So there is a lesson for Jacob,” says the Master. “雅各布这回可是上了一课了。”大少爷冷嘲热讽。
“We shall live to repent of this,” says Mr. Henry, and flung out of the hall. “我们俩以后就等着为今天的决定付出代价吧。”亨利先生说着疯了一般地冲出了大厅。
As for Miss Alison, she caught up that piece of gold which had just sent her lover to the wars, and flung it clean through the family shield in the great painted window. 而艾莉森小姐，抓起那枚把情人送上战场的硬币，顺着窗户把它扔到了院子里。
“If you loved me as well as I love you, you would have stayed,” cried she. “你要是跟我爱你一样那么爱我，你就会留下来了！”她哭得梨花带雨。
“‘I could not love you, dear, so well, loved I not honour more,’” sang the Master. “我已不能再多爱你一点儿，好男儿远大前程任我追。”大少爷随口哼了首小调。
“Oh!” she cried, “you have no heart—I hope you may be killed!” and she ran from the room, and in tears, to her own chamber. “噢！”她哭着叫道，“你这个没心的，最好死在外面！”她抹着眼泪跑回自己房里去了。
It seems the Master turned to my lord with his most comical manner, and says he, “This looks like a devil of a wife.” 大少爷尽量做出嬉皮笑脸的样子，对老爷说：“这老婆可是个祸害啊。”
“I think you are a devil of a son to me,” cried his father, “you that have always been the favourite, to my shame be it spoken. “我看你这个儿子才是个祸害！”老爷终于忍不住喊起来，“一直都宠着你惯着你，我现在对这些事都羞于启齿。
Never a good hour have I gotten of you, since you were born; no, never one good hour,” and repeated it again the third time. 从你一下生来，我就没过过一个小时的好日子；没有！一个小时都没有！”老爷声嘶力竭地喊了三遍。
Whether it was the Master’s levity, or his insubordination, or Mr. Henry’s word about the favourite son, that had so much disturbed my lord, I do not know; but I incline to think it was the last, for I have it by all accounts that Mr. Henry was more made up to from that hour. 不知道是因为大少爷的反复无常，离经叛道，还是亨利少爷那些谁是宠儿的言论，反正老爷被弄得心烦意乱，但我更倾向于认为是后者，因为打那以后，亨利少爷说话就更谨慎了些。
Altogether it was in pretty ill blood with his family that the Master rode to the North; which was the more sorrowful for others to remember when it seemed too late. 大少爷去北方打仗的事情本来就让全家担心不已；而当一切为时已晚后，大家想起他去北方的事就不禁更加伤心。
By fear and favour he had scraped together near upon a dozen men, principally tenants’ sons; they were all pretty full when they set forth, and rode up the hill by the old abbey, roaring and singing, the white cockade in every hat. 大少爷走的时候连哄带骗地带走了十几个喽啰，大部分都是佃户的孩子；他们走的时候意气风发，策马翻过老修道院的那座山的时候，马声长嘶军歌高唱，每顶帽子上都绣着白色的花结。　
It was a desperate venture for so small a company to cross the most of Scotland unsupported; and (what made folk think so the more) even as that poor dozen was clattering up the hill, a great ship of the king’s navy, that could have brought them under with a single boat, lay with her broad ensign streaming in the bay. 这么一小撮人在没有外援的情况下翻越几乎整个苏格兰，简直就是亡命之举；就在这可怜的小军团翻山越岭的时候，国王来镇压叛军的战船入了港，军旗飘飘，胜意凛然，其实要收拾大少爷那点儿人，真用不着那么大一艘船。
The next afternoon, having given the Master a fair start, it was Mr. Henry’s turn; and he rode off, all by himself, to offer his sword and carry letters from his father to King George’s Government. 大少爷走后，转天下午就轮到亨利先生启程了，他带着父亲的信，独自佩剑骑马去投奔乔治国王。
Miss Alison was shut in her room, and did little but weep, till both were gone; only she stitched the cockade upon the Master’s hat, and (as John Paul told me) it was wetted with tears when he carried it down to him. 他俩成行前，艾莉森小姐除了给大少爷缝制军帽上的花结外，终日都呆在房间里以泪洗面；约翰·保罗后来告诉我，他把军帽交给大少爷时，上面布满了小姐的泪痕。
In all that followed, Mr. Henry and my old lord were true to their bargain. 自那以后，亨利先生和老爷都忠实地扮演着拍国王马屁的角色。
That ever they accomplished anything is more than I could learn; and that they were anyway strong on the king’s side, more than believe. 至于效果如何我便不得而知了，反正他们是站定国王这边了。
But they kept the letter of loyalty, corresponded with my Lord President, sat still at home, and had little or no commerce with the Master while that business lasted. 他们与王室和总统保持通信，闭门不出，战事未休的时候几乎切断了与大少爷的联系。
Nor was he, on his side, more communicative. 而大少爷也差不多音信全无。
Miss Alison, indeed, was always sending him expresses, but I do not know if she had many answers. 艾莉森小姐倒是总给大少爷寄包裹信件，至于回音几何我就不知道了。
Macconochie rode for her once, and found the highlanders before Carlisle, and the Master riding by the Prince’s side in high favour; he took the letter (so Macconochie tells), opened it, glanced it through with a mouth like a man whistling, and stuck it in his belt, whence, on his horse passageing, it fell unregarded to the ground. 麦克诺奇曾经为小姐跑过一次腿，他在卡莱尔城前的高地上找到了大少爷，看到他很得势地与王子并驾齐驱；麦克诺奇回来说大少爷拿到信后随手撕开，打着口哨轻佻地扫了一眼就塞到了腰间的皮带里，他的马打着斜横步，信飘落到了地上，他还浑然不觉。
It was Macconochie who picked it up; and he still kept it, and indeed I have seen it in his hands. 他扬长而去后，麦克诺奇捡起了那封信。到现在他依然保存着，有一次在他那里我还亲眼看到了。
News came to Durrisdeer of course, by the common report, as it goes travelling through a country, a thing always wonderful to me. 这些传闻当然也传到了达里斯迪尔府，让我搞不懂的是，居然是通过乡里的传闻，显然这些已经是全国上下周知了。
By that means the family learned more of the Master’s favour with the Prince, and the ground it was said to stand on: for by a strange condescension in a man so proud—only that he was a man still more ambitious—he was said to have crept into notability by truckling to the Irish. 家里也知道了大少爷得到了王子的赏识，而传闻说这种赏识是建立在大少爷对爱尔兰人献媚的基础之上的；能让大少爷那么不可一世的人纡尊降贵就只有一种可能，那就是为了实现他那蛰伏的野心。
Sir Thomas Sullivan, Colonel Burke and the rest, were his daily comrades, by which course he withdrew himself from his own country-folk. 他平日总与托马斯·苏利文爵士及伯克上校等爱尔兰人混在一起，自然而然地也把自己放逐在同乡的圈子之外了。
All the small intrigues he had a hand in fomenting; thwarted my Lord George upon a thousand points; was always for the advice that seemed palatable to the Prince, no matter if it was good or bad; and seems upon the whole (like the gambler he was all through life) to have had less regard to the chances of the campaign than to the greatness of favour he might aspire to, if, by any luck, it should succeed. 所有的小阴谋他都得插一脚；那些小绊子弄得乔治国王那方不胜其烦；凡是合乎王子口味的主意，他无论良莠，照单全收；而在大事上，他更是发挥了他的赌侠风范，永远把如何赢得王子的青睐放在第一位，绝少顾及战局的发展。这仗他们要是能赢，那就有鬼了。
For the rest, he did very well in the field; no one questioned that; for he was no coward. 至于其他的，阵前他确实是英勇无匹，这一点没人质疑，因为他绝对不是个懦夫。
The next was the news of Culloden, which was brought to Durrisdeer by one of the tenants’ sons—the only survivor, he declared, of all those that had gone singing up the hill. 然后传来的就是克洛登战役的惨讯了，消息是由去参战的一个佃户的儿子带回达里斯迪尔的——他自称是那次战役唯一的幸存者，当时他们还高唱战歌，怎么也没料到自己是赶着赴死。
By an unfortunate chance John Paul and Macconochie had that very morning found the guinea piece—which was the root of all the evil—sticking in a holly bush; they had been “up the gait,” as the servants say at Durrisdeer, to the change-house; and if they had little left of the guinea, they had less of their wits. 那天早上,约翰·保罗和麦克诺奇刚好命运不济地在冬青丛里找到了那枚一先令硬币——整个悲剧的源头；宅子里的仆人们后来形容他们是立刻就踮着脚跑到小酒店去挥霍掉了，他们当时花得越多，知道这个消息之后越得吓得魂飞魄散。
What must John Paul do but burst into the hall where the family sat at dinner, and cry the news to them that “Tam Macmorland was but new lichtit at the door, and—wirra, wirra—there were nane to come behind him”? 这也就是为什么一家人吃晚饭的时候，约翰·保罗上气不接下气地冲进大厅里，连喊带叫：“汤姆·麦克莫兰刚回来啦，天……天哪……就他一个人回来啦！”
They took the word in silence like folk condemned; only Mr. Henry carrying his palm to his face, and Miss Alison laying her head outright upon her hands. 惊雷平地起，一瞬间所有人都沉默了；唯有亨利先生用手捂住了脸，艾莉森小姐则把头深深地埋在了双手间。
As for my lord, he was like ashes. 而老爷子则面如死灰。
“I have still one son,” says he. “我还有一个儿子，”他说道，
“And, Henry, I will do you this justice—it is the kinder that is left.” “亨利，我这次还你个公道——还是活着的这个更良善些。”
It was a strange thing to say in such a moment; but my lord had never forgotten Mr. Henry’s speech, and he had years of injustice on his conscience. 在这个时候说这些是不太合适的；但老爷子一直对亨利先生之前的话念念不忘，而这么多年，对于自己明显的偏爱，老爷子也委实良心不安。
Still it was a strange thing, and more than Miss Alison could let pass. 但这时谁还想得到那些呢？死者为大，艾莉森小姐当即就抓着这句不放了。
She broke out and blamed my lord for his unnatural words, and Mr. Henry because he was sitting there in safety when his brother lay dead, and herself because she had given her sweetheart ill words at his departure, calling him the flower of the flock, wringing her hands, protesting her love, and crying on him by his name—so that the servants stood astonished. 她放声大哭，怨老爷那句不近人情的话，怨亨利先生的无动于衷，也怨心上人临走时自己一气之下说的那些不吉利的言词。她的双手痛苦地绞在一起，一边为自己的爱情正名，一边哭诉爱人的离去，她哭着叫大少爷的名字——仆人们惊得当场呆立。
Mr. Henry got to his feet, and stood holding his chair. 亨利先生扶着椅子缓缓地站起来。
It was he that was like ashes now. 这次轮到他面如死灰了。
“Oh!” he burst out suddenly, “I know you loved him.” “够了！”他突然爆发了出来，“我知道你爱过他！”
“The world knows that, glory be to God!” cries she; and then to Mr. Henry: “There is none but me to know one thing—that you were a traitor to him in your heart.” “全世界都知道，荣耀归于上帝！”她哭喊道。接着她又对亨利先生说道：“只有我知道——你心底里是恨着他的。”
“God knows,” groans he, “it was lost love on both sides.” “上帝自有公断，”亨利先生的声音已经因为痛苦而含混不清了，“他是你的爱人，也是我的哥哥，我们是同悲于此啊。”
Time went by in the house after that without much change; only they were now three instead of four, which was a perpetual reminder of their loss. 那场变故发生后，宅子里并未发生几多变化；除了四口变成三口，而这却无时无刻不在提醒着所有人大少爷已然战死沙场的事实。　
Miss Alison’s money, you are to bear in mind, wag highly needful for the estates; and the one brother being dead, my old lord soon set his heart upon her marrying the other. 艾莉森小姐继承的那些遗产，对这个家来说是不可或缺的；既然她原来的未婚夫大少爷已死，老爷很快就把主意打到了二儿子身上。
Day in, day out, he would work upon her, sitting by the chimney-side with his finger in his Latin book, and his eyes set upon her face with a kind of pleasant intentness that became the old gentleman very well. 日复一日，老爷始终在探小姐的口风，他一如往常般坐在壁炉旁，手里拿着那些拉丁文写就的书籍，看的却是小姐的态度，带着一位老绅士对一位年轻淑女所能表现出来的最体面慈祥的关切。
If she wept, he would condole with her like an ancient man that has seen worse times and begins to think lightly even of sorrow; if she raged, he would fall to reading again in his Latin book, but always with some civil excuse; if she offered, as she often did, to let them have her money in a gift, he would show her how little it consisted with his honour, and remind her, even if he should consent, that Mr. Henry would certainly refuse. 她若哭泣，老爷便安慰她，像一位饱经风霜、常屹苍凉世事不倒的老者；她若是发怒，老爷便找个说得过去的理由侧过脸去继续读他的书；如果她一如既往地用自己继承的遗产施舍这个家，老爷便要显示出他是多么地于心不忍，并且会提醒她，即使自己同意收下，亨利先生也一定会拒绝的。
NON VI SED SAEPE CADENDO was a favourite word of his; and no doubt this quiet persecution wore away much of her resolve; no doubt, besides, he had a great influence on the girl, having stood in the place of both her parents; and, for that matter, she was herself filled with the spirit of the Duries, and would have gone a great way for the glory of Durrisdeer; but not so far, I think, as to marry my poor patron, had it not been—strangely enough—for the circumstance of his extreme unpopularity. “他人之财不可染指”是老爷的口头禅。毫无疑问，这种冷暴力让小姐犹豫不决，除此之外，老爷亦父亦母的身份对小姐有着无可置否的影响。也正因为此，她骨子里有着迪里家族的灵魂，也愿意为对达里斯迪尔家的荣耀而贡献自己的力量——但显然，我认为这种贡献还没到可以献身嫁给可怜的亨利先生那地步，奇怪的是，这并不是因为亨利先生当时那大失人心的处境。
This was the work of Tam Macmorland. 这种尴尬的处境完全要“归功于”汤姆·麦克莫兰。
There was not much harm in Tam; but he had that grievous weakness, a long tongue; and as the only man in that country who had been out—or, rather, who had come in again—he was sure of listeners. 汤姆确不是什么大奸大恶之人，可他有一个严重的缺点——长舌头；而他是唯一一个出门打了仗又能活着回来的，自然是不乏听信之人的。
Those that have the underhand in any fighting, I have observed, are ever anxious to persuade themselves they were betrayed. 据我观察，那些在任何争斗中落了下乘的人，总是急于用被别人出卖的理由来给自己的失败作借口。
By Tam’s account of it, the rebels had been betrayed at every turn and by every officer they had; they had been betrayed at Derby, and betrayed at Falkirk; the night march was a step of treachery of my Lord George’s; and Culloden was lost by the treachery of the Macdonalds. 据汤姆所言，他们起义的每一个关键点都存在着背叛，每一个指挥者都是叛徒；德比战役、福尔柯克战役中他们被出卖了；夜行军是乔治国王那方背信弃义的一步棋；克卢顿战役的失败则是由于麦克唐纳兹的出卖。
This habit of imputing treason grew upon the fool, till at last he must have in Mr. Henry also. 这蠢货把他肆意捏造背叛者的习惯发扬光大，最后终于把亨利先生也给卷进去了。
Mr. Henry (by his account) had betrayed the lads of Durrisdeer; he had promised to follow with more men, and instead of that he had ridden to King George. 汤姆说亨利先生背叛了达里斯迪尔的小伙子们，说他明明许诺带更多的人去帮他们起义的，结果背地里却投奔了乔治国王。
“Ay, and the next day!” “啊，就在第二天！”
Tam would cry. 汤姆哭喊着，
“The puir bonnie Master, and the puir, kind lads that rade wi’ him, were hardly ower the scaur, or he was aff—the Judis! “大少爷和他后面跟着的一群小伙子，无所畏惧，天哪！
Ay, weel—he has his way o’t: he’s to be my lord, nae less, and there’s mony a cold corp amang the Hieland heather!” 啊——大少爷杀伐决断：他是我的主子，即使高原的树林里到处都是尸体！”
And at this, if Tam had been drinking, he would begin to weep. 每次说到这里，要是正赶上汤姆在喝酒，他一定就会伤心地哭起来。
Let anyone speak long enough, he will get believers. 任谁把什么话说了很多遍，总会有人开始相信他的。
This view of Mr. Henry’s behaviour crept about the country by little and little; it was talked upon by folk that knew the contrary, but were short of topics; and it was heard and believed and given out for gospel by the ignorant and the ill-willing. 关于亨利先生的不良传言在当地慢慢流传开来；真正知道内情的人们虽然都为他说好话，但是显然恶毒的流言对于那些无知的或者居心叵测的人更有说服力。
Mr. Henry began to be shunned; yet awhile, and the commons began to murmur as he went by, and the women (who are always the most bold because they are the most safe) to cry out their reproaches to his face. 开始的时候，亨利先生只是被人远远避开；后来渐渐地有人开始在看到他的时候当着他的面说闲话；直到有些女人敢当面辱骂他——因为她们都知道他不敢拿女人怎么样。
The Master was cried up for a saint. 与此同时，死去的大少爷在人们心中倒是神圣化了。
It was remembered how he had never any hand in pressing the tenants; as, indeed, no more he had, except to spend the money. 人们说大少爷生前从不压榨佃户——这倒是事实，只是得在他还有钱花的情况下。
He was a little wild perhaps, the folk said; but how much better was a natural, wild lad that would soon have settled down, than a skinflint and a sneckdraw, sitting, with his nose in an account book, to persecute poor tenants! 大少爷是有一点儿浪荡，但人们觉得他浪荡得自然——而且随着婚事的到来，他说不定马上就要稳定下来了——因此他比那个整天埋首账簿、锱铢必较地琢磨着怎么迫害佃户的亨利先生强多了。
One trollop, who had had a child to the Master, and by all accounts been very badly used, yet made herself a kind of champion of his memory. 有个曾经怀了大少爷孩子的女人，大少爷生前本来对她十分不好，可此时，这个女人却成了追忆大少爷的领头人。
She flung a stone one day at Mr. Henry. 有一天她朝着亨利先生扔石头。
“Whaur’s the bonnie lad that trustit ye?” she cried. “枉大少爷那么信你，现在他去哪里了？”她哭喊道。
Mr. Henry reined in his horse and looked upon her, the blood flowing from his lip. 亨利先生勒马望向她，血从嘴角流了下来。
“Ay, Jess?” says he. “啊，杰丝？”他说道。
“You too? “连你也这样？
And yet ye should ken me better.” 你该知道我的为人啊！”
For it was he who had helped her with money. 因为亨利先生才是那个接济过她的人。
The woman had another stone ready, which she made as if she would cast; and he, to ward himself, threw up the hand that held his riding-rod. 这女人早就拣好了另一块石头，做出又要扔的架势；亨利先生出于自卫举起了他的马鞭子。
“What, would ye beat a lassie, ye ugly—?” cries she, and ran away screaming as though he had struck her. “看看，你居然要打女人！你这个怪物！”她哭叫着跑开了，跟当真挨了亨利先生的打似的。
Next day word went about the country like wildfire that Mr. Henry had beaten Jessie Broun within an inch of her life. 第二天，亨利先生打了杰丝·布龙的传言像野火一般传遍整个乡里。
I give it as one instance of how this snowball grew, and one calumny brought another; until my poor patron was so perished in reputation that he began to keep the house like my lord. 这些流言就是这样，像雪球似的一点一点滚起来，直到我那可怜的亨利先生彻底声名狼藉，跟老爷一样把自己关在宅子里，闭门不出。
All this while, you may be very sure, he uttered no complaints at home; the very ground of the scandal was too sore a matter to be handled; and Mr. Henry was very proud and strangely obstinate in silence. 在这期间，你可以相信，亨利先生在家中没有半句抱怨之词；要调查这流言的起因，对于当事人来说也是一件非常痛苦的事；作为一个非常重视个人声誉的人，亨利先生在这件事上却非常奇怪地保持了沉默。
My old lord must have heard of it, by John Paul, if by no one else; and he must at least have remarked the altered habits of his son. 老爷肯定从约翰·保尔那里对这件事有所耳闻，对儿子反常的举止也颇有非议。
Yet even he, it is probable, knew not how high the feeling ran; and as for Miss Alison, she was ever the last person to hear news, and the least interested when she heard them. 而且就算是老爷，也不可能知道这些流言在外已经传到了何种程度；至于艾莉森小姐，那更是两耳不闻窗外事，就算听到了也不怎么感兴趣。
In the height of the ill-feeling (for it died away as it came, no man could say why) there was an election forward in the town of St. Bride’s, which is the next to Durrisdeer, standing on the Water of Swift; some grievance was fermenting, I forget what, if ever I heard; and it was currently said there would be broken heads ere night, and that the sheriff had sent as far as Dumfries for soldiers. 在流言的汹涌程度达到最高潮的时候（这流言来得快去的也快，谁也不知道是怎么回事），圣伯莱德教堂举行了一次表决。这座教堂坐落在斯威夫特湖畔，达里斯迪尔府邸的旁边；这次表决也不知道是为了什么事，就算我听说了现在也早就忘了；据说是前夜有人为此打得头破血流，治安官不得不派人来达里斯迪尔家借调人手来平息这件事。
My lord moved that Mr. Henry should be present, assuring him it was necessary to appear, for the credit of the house. 老爷认为，考虑到家族的声誉，亨利先生得去露个面才行。
“It will soon be reported,” said he, “that we do not take the lead in our own country.” “要是咱们在当地不带个头儿，”老爷说道，“很快就会有人向上面汇报咱们的不是。”
“It is a strange lead that I can take,” said Mr. Henry; and when they had pushed him further, “I tell you the plain truth,” he said, “I dare not show my face.” “这种奇怪的头儿，不带也罢。”亨利先生说；等别人再催促他时，他干脆直说了：“我告诉你实话吧，我没脸出去见人。”
“You are the first of the house that ever said so,” cries Miss Alison. “咱这宅子，能说出这种窝囊话的，你可是头一个。”艾莉森小姐嚷道。
“We will go all three,” said my lord; and sure enough he got into his boots (the first time in four years—a sore business John Paul had to get them on), and Miss Alison into her riding-coat, and all three rode together to St. Bride’s. “那咱们三个一起去吧。”老爷说着穿起了他的靴子（这可是四年来老爷头一次为了出门穿靴子——约翰·保尔费了好大的劲才帮他穿上），艾莉森小姐也穿上了她的骑手装，三个人骑着马去了圣伯莱德教堂。
The streets were full of the rift-raff of all the countryside, who had no sooner clapped eyes on Mr. Henry than the hissing began, and the hooting, and the cries of “Judas!” and “Where was the Master?” and “Where were the poor lads that rode with him?” 街上挤满了好事之徒，不久就把注意力从事件本身转移到了亨利先生身上。他们轻蔑地打着口哨朝亨利先生喊着：“叛徒！大少爷哪儿去了？那些跟着他的可怜的兄弟们哪儿去了？”
Even a stone was cast; but the more part cried shame at that, for my old lord’s sake, and Miss Alison’s. 更有甚者，还朝亨利先生扔石头；不过还是有人瞧着老爷和艾莉森小姐的面子出来制止了。
It took not ten minutes to persuade my lord that Mr. Henry had been right. 不消十分钟的时间，老爷就明白了亨利先生闭门不出的决定是正确的。
He said never a word, but turned his horse about, and home again, with his chin upon his bosom. 亨利先生一言不发，让马兜着圈子，一路低着头直到回家。
Never a word said Miss Alison; no doubt she thought the more; no doubt her pride was stung, for she was a bone-bred Durie; and no doubt her heart was touched to see her cousin so unjustly used. 艾莉森小姐对此不置一言，但显然对此思虑良多；作为达里斯迪尔家的一分子，她的自尊心无疑受到了伤害，对于自己表兄受到如此不公正的对待也无法坐壁而观。
That night she was never in bed; I have often blamed my lady - when I call to mind that night, I readily forgive her all; and the first thing in the morning she came to the old lord in his usual seat. 那夜她辗转反侧；即便我后来对这位女主人多有微词，想起那一夜的事情，我也心中释然；第二天一早，她就来到自己与老爷经常谈天的地方。
“If Henry still wants me,” said she, “he can have me now.” “要是亨利还愿意娶我的话，”她说道，“我们现在就结婚吧。”
To himself she had a different speech: “I bring you no love, Henry; but God knows, all the pity in the world.” 不过对亨利先生她又换了一套说辞：“尽管我不爱你，亨利；但主用同情灌溉世间的土地。”
June the 1st, 1748, was the day of their marriage. 1784年6月1日，他们举行了婚礼。
It was December of the same year that first saw me alighting at the doors of the great house; and from there I take up the history of events as they befell under my own observation, like a witness in a court. 同年12月份我才来到了这座府邸；而自那以后的所有事情，都是我亲眼所见，我可以像证人一样出庭作证。
Chapter 2 第二章
Summary of Events (continued) 大事摘要（续）
I made the last of my journey in the cold end of December, in a mighty dry day of frost, and who should be my guide but Patey Macmorland, brother of Tam! 在十二月末寒冷的空气中，我走完了旅程的最后一段。那是寒冷而干燥的一天，来给我带路的自然是汤姆的表兄，佩提·麦克莫兰！
For a tow-headed, bare-legged brat of ten, he had more ill tales upon his tongue than ever I heard the match of; having drunken betimes in his brother’s cup. 可能是因为总喝他哥哥杯子里的酒，这个蓬头垢面、光着脚丫的十岁小孩肚子里装的乱七八糟的故事比我知道的任何一个孩子装的都多。
I was still not so old myself; pride had not yet the upper hand of curiosity; and indeed it would have taken any man, that cold morning, to hear all the old clashes of the country, and be shown all the places by the way where strange things had fallen out. 那时候，我年纪尚轻，好奇心远胜过自尊心；实际上，在那么一个寒冷的清晨，任何人都不会拒绝听听当地的旧事，看看沿途发生过奇事的地方。
I had tales of Claverhouse as we came through the bogs, and tales of the devil, as we came over the top of the scaur. 过沼泽的时候，他给我讲了克拉夫府邸的故事；翻过司高尔山的时候，他又给我讲了一些鬼怪故事。
As we came in by the abbey I heard somewhat of the old monks, and more of the freetraders, who use its ruins for a magazine, landing for that cause within a cannon-shot of Durrisdeer; and along all the road the Duries and poor Mr. Henry were in the first rank of slander. 路过修道院的时候，我听到了一些关于老修士的传言，还有关于私枭的一些传说：他们把这些遗迹用作自己的弹药库，这些弹药库都在达里斯迪尔爵府的射程之内等等。不过沿途他主要讲的还是达里斯迪尔家族和可怜的亨利先生。
My mind was thus highly prejudiced against the family I was about to serve, so that I was half surprised when I beheld Durrisdeer itself, lying in a pretty, sheltered bay, under the Abbey Hill; the house most commodiously built in the French fashion, or perhaps Italianate, for I have no skill in these arts; and the place the most beautified with gardens, lawns, shrubberies, and trees I had ever seen. 这让我心中对即将服务的家族产生了严重的偏见。这也就是为什么当我真正看到达里斯迪尔府邸的时候，心中还有那么一点儿反差带来的惊讶。府邸坐落在教堂山下美丽而隐蔽的海边，建筑风格可能是法式的，也可能是意式的，反正我对建筑没什么研究。主宅在花园、草坪、灌木和绿林的掩映下，风格独具，别致非凡，是我见过的最漂亮的。
The money sunk here unproductively would have quite restored the family; but as it was, it cost a revenue to keep it up. 这些用在装饰上的大笔花费，本来可以用来缓解家族在经济上的窘境；可惜每年家族还是撒了大笔的金钱用于维持这个美好的外观。
Mr. Henry came himself to the door to welcome me: a tall dark young gentleman (the Duries are all black men) of a plain and not cheerful face, very strong in body, but not so strong in health: taking me by the hand without any pride, and putting me at home with plain kind speeches. 亨利先生亲自到门口来迎接我。他是个身材高大、皮肤黝黑的年轻人（达里斯迪尔家族的人皮肤都黑），长相普通，表情严肃。他身体健壮，实际上却并不怎么健康。他非常亲切地和我握手，质朴的言辞让我顿生宾至如归之感。
He led me into the hall, booted as I was, to present me to my lord. 还没等我脱下靴子，他就引我到大厅面见老爷。
It was still daylight; and the first thing I observed was a lozenge of clear glass in the midst of the shield in the painted window, which I remember thinking a blemish on a room otherwise so handsome, with its family portraits, and the pargeted ceiling with pendants, and the carved chimney, in one corner of which my old lord sat reading in his Livy. 那时候还是白天，我留意到的第一件事就是一块菱形的透明玻璃镶嵌在彩色玻璃的中间，就像这间完美屋子里的一个污点，墙上挂着全家福，白色的天花板上悬吊着很多装饰物，在精雕细琢的壁炉旁的角落里，老爷正读着李维的名著。
He was like Mr. Henry, with much the same plain countenance, only more subtle and pleasant, and his talk a thousand times more entertaining. 他和亨利先生都有些其貌不扬，只是比亨利先生更圆滑世故，言谈上也更令人愉快。
He had many questions to ask me, I remember, of Edinburgh College, where I had just received my mastership of arts, and of the various professors, with whom and their proficiency he seemed well acquainted; and thus, talking of things that I knew, I soon got liberty of speech in my new home. 我记得他问了我很多问题，比如关于我刚刚取得文学硕士学位的爱丁堡大学，我们学校的一些教授甚至他们擅长的领域他都知之甚多；由于交谈的都是我熟悉的话题，我在新家里立刻找到了说话的自由感。
In the midst of this came Mrs. Henry into the room; she was very far gone, Miss Katharine being due in about six weeks, which made me think less of her beauty at the first sight; and she used me with more of condescension than the rest; so that, upon all accounts, I kept her in the third place of my esteem. 在这中间，我见到了亨利太太。她和我的预料相去甚远，可能是由于再过六个星期就要生下孩子的缘故，第一眼看去不怎么漂亮；和其他人相比，她和我说话时明显有纡尊降贵之感；因此，我在尊重程度上把她排到了第三位。
It did not take long before all Patey Macmorland’s tales were blotted out of my belief, and I was become, what I have ever since remained, a loving servant of the house of Durrisdeer. 没过多久，佩提·麦克莫兰讲的那些种种不好就在我脑子中烟消云散。此后所有的时间里，我都是达里斯迪尔家族忠诚的仆人。
Mr. Henry had the chief part of my affection. 让我如此忠心的主要原因就是亨利先生。
It was with him I worked; and I found him an exacting master, keeping all his kindness for those hours in which we were unemployed, and in the steward’s office not only loading me with work, but viewing me with a shrewd supervision. 大部分时间我都与他在一起工作；他是一位非常严格的主人，只在工作之余才展现他的仁慈。在办公室里亨利先生不仅给我布置了很多的工作，同时在监督上也明察秋毫。
At length one day he looked up from his paper with a kind of timidness, and says he, “Mr. Mackellar, I think I ought to tell you that you do very well.” 有一天，他从正在看的文件里抬起头来，略带腼腆地对我说：“麦凯勒先生，我觉得我有必要告诉你，你干得相当不错。”
That was my first word of commendation; and from that day his jealousy of my performance was relaxed; soon it was “Mr. Mackellar” here, and “Mr. Mackellar” there, with the whole family; and for much of my service at Durrisdeer, I have transacted everything at my own time, and to my own fancy, and never a farthing challenged. 这是对我工作的第一个评价；从那天起，它平息了宅子里对我的各种猜忌。很快，“麦凯勒先生”这个称谓就在整个家族里叫开了。在达里斯迪尔，我恪尽职守，我自己的时间里换取了这一切。让我满意的是，再也没人对我有过一丝非议。
Even while he was driving me, I had begun to find my heart go out to Mr. Henry; no doubt, partly in pity, he was a man so palpably unhappy. 虽然亨利先生经常驱使我干这干那，但我依然发现自己对他越来越有好感；当然，有一部分是出于对他的同情，他是那么一个缺乏快乐的人。
He would fall into a deep muse over our accounts, staring at the page or out of the window; and at those times the look of his face, and the sigh that would break from him, awoke in me strong feelings of curiosity and commiseration. 在我们做账时，他经常盯着账目或望着窗外陷入沉思；他那时的表情和不时发出的叹息让我产生了强烈的好奇心和恻隐之心。
One day, I remember, we were late upon some business in the steward’s room. 有一天，我们俩在账务室工作到很晚。
This room is in the top of the house, and has a view upon the bay, and over a little wooded cape, on the long sands; and there, right over against the sun, which was then dipping, we saw the freetraders, with a great force of men and horses, scouring on the beach. 账务室在顶层，从那里可以俯瞰海岸，越过长着稀疏树林的海角，还可以看到长长的沙滩；那里正对着即将落山的太阳，我们看到那些私枭和他们的骑兵正在海滩逡巡。
Mr. Henry had been staring straight west, so that I marvelled he was not blinded by the sun; suddenly he frowns, rubs his hand upon his brow, and turns to me with a smile. 亨利先生一直盯着西坠的太阳，我很惊奇，他居然没有被日光刺伤了眼睛；突然间，他眉头微蹙，用手揉揉眉，转过头来笑着看我。
“You would not guess what I was thinking,” says he. “你一定猜不到我在想什么，”他说道，
“I was thinking I would be a happier man if I could ride and run the danger of my life, with these lawless companions.” “我在想，如果跟着这些目无法纪的浪荡子们纵马人生，我可能会是个更加快乐的人。”
I told him I had observed he did not enjoy good spirits; and that it was a common fancy to envy others and think we should be the better of some change; quoting Horace to the point, like a young man fresh from college. 我告诉他我也发现他心情不佳，还告诉他羡慕别人的生活，认为自己换个活法会更好是所有人经常陷入的幻想。像所有刚从学校里走出的年轻人一样，我还援引了赫拉斯的话来宽慰他。
“Why, just so,” said he. “是啊，这就是生活，”他说道，
“And with that we may get back to our accounts.” “现在咱们得接着算账了。”
It was not long before I began to get wind of the causes that so much depressed him. 没过多久，我就知道了他沮丧的原因。
Indeed a blind man must have soon discovered there was a shadow on that house, the shadow of the Master of Ballantrae. 瞎子都能看出来这个宅子笼罩在一片阴影之下，这片阴影，就是巴伦特雷大少爷。
Dead or alive (and he was then supposed to be dead) that man was his brother’s rival: his rival abroad, where there was never a good word for Mr. Henry, and nothing but regret and praise for the Master; and his rival at home, not only with his father and his wife, but with the very servants. 不管他是死了还是活着（当时大家都认为他死了），大少爷都是亨利先生的竞争对手：一个远在外地的竞争对手。亨利先生当时处在千夫所指的境况中，他的兄弟则是让人充满遗憾和赞誉的大少爷；就算在家里，他的父亲和妻子，甚至是每个仆人也都和他过不去。
They were two old serving-men that were the leaders. 在这件事情上，仆人们分为两派，每派都有一个老仆人领头。
John Paul, a little, bald, solemn, stomachy man, a great professor of piety and (take him for all in all) a pretty faithful servant, was the chief of the Master’s faction. 忠于大少爷的那一派人，以约翰·保尔为首，他矮小、秃顶、严肃，一副神学教授的架势，还算是一个尽忠职守的仆人。
None durst go so far as John. 宅子里没人像他一样敢把事情做得如此过头。
He took a pleasure in disregarding Mr. Henry publicly, often with a slighting comparison. 他经常把大少爷和亨利先生相提并论，当众表现对亨利先生的轻慢，并从中深得其乐。
My lord and Mrs. Henry took him up, to be sure, but never so resolutely as they should; and he had only to pull his weeping face and begin his lamentations for the Master—“his laddie,” as he called him—to have the whole condoned. 老爷和亨利夫人当然会就这件事情教训他，但教训的程度从来没有符合过一个父亲和妻子应该做到的水平；他总是做出一副要哭的表情来开始他对大少爷的追悼——“我的主子啊”他一直都这么叫大少爷——然后他一切轻慢亨利先生的行为就都被原谅了。
As for Henry, he let these things pass in silence, sometimes with a sad and sometimes with a black look. 至于亨利先生，他通常只是沉默，有时候显出失落或者沉一下脸就让这些事情过去。
There was no rivalling the dead, he knew that; and how to censure an old serving-man for a fault of loyalty, was more than he could see. 他知道，活人永远没法和死人竞争；他也不知道怎样去责怪一个跟错了主子的老仆人，忠心是他唯一的错误。
His was not the tongue to do it. 所以亨利先生根本没有立场去责怪他。
Macconochie was chief upon the other side; an old, ill-spoken, swearing, ranting, drunken dog; and I have often thought it an odd circumstance in human nature that these two serving-men should each have been the champion of his contrary, and blackened their own faults and made light of their own virtues when they beheld them in a master. 麦克诺奇是另一派的领头，年纪一大把了还声名狼藉，每天都醉醺醺的，动不动就赌咒发誓。我经常想，这是人性中一种非常奇特的情况：这两个老仆人深陷在这场争斗中，他们把自己的缺点夸大，优点淡化，然后再把这些优点和缺点投射在对方支持的主人身上。
Macconochie had soon smelled out my secret inclination, took me much into his confidence, and would rant against the Master by the hour, so that even my work suffered. 麦克诺奇不久就嗅出了我的好恶，把我列入了他的阵营，就算我工作紧张到生不如死的程度，他也要抓紧所有时间跟我说大少爷的不是。
“They’re a’ daft here,” he would cry, “and be damned to them! “他们都是些白痴，”他会大声嚷嚷，“都是该遭天谴的白痴！
The Master—the deil’s in their thrapples that should call him sae! it’s Mr. Henry should be master now! 管大少爷叫主人？那是大少爷到地狱里小鬼儿们给他的称呼，现在亨利先生才是主人！
They were nane sae fond o’ the Master when they had him, I’ll can tell ye that. 大少爷在世的时候从来没见他们那么待见他，我告诉你。
Sorrow on his name! 现在他们倒是一提到大少爷的名字就假惺惺地掉眼泪！
Never a guid word did I hear on his lips, nor naebody else, but just fleering and flyting and profane cursing—deil hae him! 大少爷在世的时候我从来就没听他说过一句体面的话，谁也没听过，要么就是贫嘴要么就是挑事，要么就是恶毒的诅咒。
There’s nane kent his wickedness: him a gentleman! 他是绅士？见他娘的鬼去吧！
Did ever ye hear tell, Mr. Mackellar, o’ Wully White the wabster? 麦凯勒先生，您听说过沃利·怀特么？
No? 没听过？
Aweel, Wully was an unco praying kind o’ man; a dreigh body, nane o’ my kind, I never could abide the sight o’ him; onyway he was a great hand by his way of it, and he up and rebukit the Master for some of his on- goings. 那好，我告诉你，沃利这个人有点儿怪，但他对上帝很虔诚，面黄肌瘦的样子特可怜，跟我没法比。他是织布的，活还不错。那次也不知道是因为什么事他来找大少爷说道说道。
It was a grand thing for the Master o’ Ball’ntrae to tak up a feud wi’ a’ wabster, wasnae’t?” 堂堂大少爷跟一个织布的莽夫较劲不是太可笑了么？”
Macconochie would sneer; indeed, he never took the full name upon his lips but with a sort of a whine of hatred. 麦克诺奇在这时候会露出讥笑的表情；实际上，他也从来没有叫过大少爷的全名，只用一种憎恨的方式称呼大少爷。
“But he did! “结果他还真就这么干了！
A fine employ it was: chopping at the man’s door, and crying ‘boo’ in his lum, and puttin’ poother in his fire, and pee-oys[1] in his window; till the man thocht it was auld Hornie was come seekin’ him. 简单地说就是：他砍了人家屋门，嘴里骂骂咧咧，把湿柴弄进人家火炉里去，还在人家窗户边放炮；直到那可怜的织布工以为自己被哪位魔鬼大人找上门了。
Weel, to mak a lang story short, Wully gaed gyte. 咱长话短说，沃利后来被抓起来了。
At the hinder end, they couldnae get him frae his knees, but he just roared and prayed and grat straucht on, till he got his release. 他在地上长跪不起，跟疯了一样自言自语，祈祷道歉，直到他被放出来。
It was fair murder, a’body said that. 有人说这可真是一场神不知鬼不觉的完美谋杀。
Ask John Paul—he was brawly ashamed o’ that game, him that’s sic a Christian man! 不信你问问约翰·保尔——他可是一提到这事就恨得牙痒痒，他也是虔诚的基督徒！
Grand doin’s for the Master o’ Ball’ntrae!” 你看我们伟大的巴伦特雷少爷都干了些什么好事！”
I asked him what the Master had thought of it himself. 我问他大少爷自己对这件事情是怎么想的。
“How would I ken?” says he. “我哪儿知道？”他说道，
“He never said naething.” “他连提都没提过。”
And on again in his usual manner of banning and swearing, with every now and again a “Master of Ballantrae” sneered through his nose. 然后他又开始骂骂咧咧，用他一贯的轻蔑的鼻音叫起“巴伦特雷大少爷”。
It was in one of these confidences that he showed me the Carlisle letter, the print of the horse-shoe still stamped in the paper. 在这些交谈中，他把卡里索捡到的信给我看了，上面还清晰地留有被马践踏过的蹄印。
Indeed, that was our last confidence; for he then expressed himself so ill-naturedly of Mrs. Henry that I had to reprimand him sharply, and must thenceforth hold him at a distance. 实际上，这是我们之间的最后一次谈话；因为后来他说亨利夫人的坏话，我严词反驳了他，然后就一直和他保持距离。
My old lord was uniformly kind to Mr. Henry; he had even pretty ways of gratitude, and would sometimes clap him on the shoulder and say, as if to the world at large: “This is a very good son to me.” 老爷一如既往地表达着对亨利先生的关心；他有很多表达赏识之情的方式，比如拍着他儿子的肩膀，好像跟所有人显示什么一样：“我这儿子可真是好啊。”
And grateful he was, no doubt, being a man of sense and justice. 毫无疑问，他的这种自豪也只是人应有的明智和公正。
But I think that was all, and I am sure Mr. Henry thought so. 这也就是一个父亲对亨利先生的全部给予了，而且我确定亨利先生也明白这些。
The love was all for the dead son. 所有的父爱都跟着死去的儿子一并入了土。
Not that this was often given breath to; indeed, with me but once. 他自己也是这个意思，他确实跟我就曾经提到过一回。
My lord had asked me one day how I got on with Mr. Henry, and I had told him the truth. 有一天，老爷问我和亨利先生相处得怎么样，我就照实说了。
“Ay,” said he, looking sideways on the burning fire, “Henry is a good lad, a very good lad,” said he. “好，”他说道，把视线移到了炉火上，“亨利是个好孩子，特别好的一个孩子。”
“You have heard, Mr. Mackellar, that I had another son? “不过你一定听说过，麦凯勒先生，我还有一个儿子？
I am afraid he was not so virtuous a lad as Mr. Henry; but dear me, he’s dead, Mr. Mackellar! and while he lived we were all very proud of him, all very proud. 恐怕那个孩子没有亨利那么多优点；但他是我的心头爱，麦凯勒先生！他活着的时候是所有人的骄傲，所有人。
If he was not all he should have been in some ways, well, perhaps we loved him better!” 说他是我的全部也许不大可能，但一定是最重要的那个，也许，我们所有人都更爱他！”
This last he said looking musingly in the fire; and then to me, with a great deal of briskness, “But I am rejoiced you do so well with Mr. Henry. 说到这里，他盯着炉火陷入了沉思，露出了由追忆带来的喜悦，“不过我很高兴你和亨利相处融洽。
You will find him a good master.” 你会发现他是一个好主人的。”
And with that he opened his book, which was the customary signal of dismission. 然后他打开自己的书，这是表示我可以退下了的惯用信号。
But it would be little that he read, and less that he understood; Culloden field and the Master, these would be the burthen of his thought; and the burthen of mine was an unnatural jealousy of the dead man for Mr. Henry’s sake, that had even then begun to grow on me. 不过在这时候，他看书只是做做样子，即使看了也不怎么过脑子，克卢敦战役中死去的大少爷，一直在他的思绪中挥之不去；而我也开始为亨利先生吃起醋来。
I am keeping Mrs. Henry for the last, so that this expression of my sentiment may seem unwarrantably strong: the reader shall judge for himself when I have done. 我把亨利太太放到最后来说，可能会显得个人感情色彩太过强烈，不过等我说完，读者可以自己去评判。
But I must first tell of another matter, which was the means of bringing me more intimate. 不过我得先说另一件事，因为这件事让我知道了更多内情。
I had not yet been six months at Durrisdeer when it chanced that John Paul fell sick and must keep his bed; drink was the root of his malady, in my poor thought; but he was tended, and indeed carried himself, like an afflicted saint; and the very minister, who came to visit him, professed himself edified when he went away. 我来到达里斯迪尔府邸不到六个月时，正好赶上约翰·保尔生病卧床；我认为主要的病因还是他酗酒的恶习，不过他得到了良好的照顾。他在床上装得像个受难的圣人，连来看望他的牧师都在临走时表示自己的灵魂得到了净化。
The third morning of his sickness, Mr. Henry comes to me with something of a hang-dog look. 在他病后的第三个早晨，亨利先生带着一副可怜兮兮的神情过来找我。
“Mackellar,” says he, “I wish I could trouble you upon a little service. “麦凯勒，”他说道，“我想麻烦你一件事。
There is a pension we pay; it is John’s part to carry it, and now that he is sick I know not to whom I should look unless it was yourself. 我们得给一个人去送生活费，这本是约翰的工作，现在他病了，除了你，我再也找不到别人可以去了。
The matter is very delicate; I could not carry it with my own hand for a sufficient reason; I dare not send Macconochie, who is a talker, and I am—I have—I am desirous this should not come to Mrs. Henry’s ears,” says he, and flushed to his neck as he said it. 这是一件很敏感的事情，我自己没有理由亲自去。我不敢把它交给麦克诺奇，他管不住自己的嘴，我希望——或者说我必须保证这件事不要传到亨利夫人的耳朵里。”他说着，脸红到了脖子。
To say truth, when I found I was to carry money to one Jessie Broun, who was no better than she should be, I supposed it was some trip of his own that Mr. Henry was dissembling. 说实话，当我知道钱是要送给杰丝·布龙那个泼妇的时候，我以为亨利先生是在掩盖他曾经犯下的错误。
I was the more impressed when the truth came out. 因而，当真相浮出水面的时候，我对这件事情的印象更加深刻。
It was up a wynd off a side street in St. Bride’s that Jessie had her lodging. 拐入圣伯莱德的一条狭窄的巷子后，我就找到了杰丝的住处。
The place was very ill inhabited, mostly by the freetrading sort. 整个街区杂乱无章，周围住着各种小贩。
There was a man with a broken head at the entry; half-way up, in a tavern, fellows were roaring and singing, though it was not yet nine in the day. 在巷子的入口，我就看到个脑袋被打破了的男人；走到一半，我看到一家小酒馆，那时候才早上9点，里面传出的喧哗声和唱歌声就已经不绝于耳了。
Altogether, I had never seen a worse neighbourhood, even in the great city of Edinburgh, and I was in two minds to go back. 走到半路，两次我都想折返回去，即使在爱丁堡这样的大城市，我也从没见过如此混乱糟糕的街区。
Jessie’s room was of a piece with her surroundings, and herself no better. 杰丝的住处与周围的环境和她自己的人品在概念上达到了高度统一。
She would not give me the receipt (which Mr. Henry had told me to demand, for he was very methodical) until she had sent out for spirits, and I had pledged her in a glass; and all the time she carried on in a light-headed, reckless way—now aping the manners of a lady, now breaking into unseemly mirth, now making coquettish advances that oppressed me to the ground. 起初她死活不肯给我写收条，后来她叫人买来酒，我向她敬了一杯，她才勉强应允（亨利先生为人严谨，临行前嘱咐过我一定要拿到收条）；她始终是一副轻浮的样子：一会儿装成体面的贵妇，一会儿又发出矫揉造作的笑声，一会儿又跟我卖弄风情，她在这几个模式中毫无预警地进行切换，让我不胜惶恐。
Of the money she spoke more tragically. 一提到钱，她的语调相当悲切。
“It’s blood money!” said she; “I take it for that: blood money for the betrayed! “这是沾满血腥的钱啊！”她说道，“这是血淋淋的背叛换来的抚恤金啊！
See what I’m brought down to! 看看我现在这幅惨象！
Ah, if the bonnie lad were back again, it would be changed days. 啊，要是我的大少爷还在，现在绝对是另一番光景啊。
But he’s deid—he’s lyin’ deid amang the Hieland hills—the bonnie lad, the bonnie lad!” 可是他死了——死在了苏格兰高地的崇山峻岭中——我的大少爷，我的大少爷！”
She had a rapt manner of crying on the bonnie lad, clasping her hands and casting up her eyes, that I think she must have learned of strolling players; and I thought her sorrow very much of an affectation, and that she dwelled upon the business because her shame was now all she had to be proud of. 她专注地哭喊着她的大少爷，双手紧紧地捂住自己的双眼，我觉得她肯定和街头艺人学过两下子；我感慨地欣赏着她的激情演出，因为她把过去的耻辱全部变成了现在炫耀忠贞的资本。
I will not say I did not pity her, but it was a loathing pity at the best; and her last change of manner wiped it out. 不得不说我还是有一点儿可怜她的，不过至多就是轻蔑的可怜；可惜的是，就算是这点儿轻蔑的可怜也在她最后的情绪切换后烟消云散。
This was when she had had enough of me for an audience, and had set her name at last to the receipt. 这时候，对于拿我当观众这件事，她已经腻烦了，最后在收条上签了字。
“There!” says she, and taking the most unwomanly oaths upon her tongue, bade me begone and carry it to the Judas who had sent me. 她说道：“拿走吧！”用的是一个女人口中可能出现的最没有女人味的语气，催我快滚，赶紧回去和差使自己的“叛徒”交差。
It was the first time I had heard the name applied to Mr. Henry; I was staggered besides at her sudden vehemence of word and manner, and got forth from the room, under this shower of curses, like a beaten dog. 这是我第一次直接听人叫亨利先生叛徒；这突如其来的潮水似的愤怒把我弄得步履蹒跚，像一条打败了的狗一般，在狂风暴雨般的诅咒声中离开了她的住所。
But even then I was not quit, for the vixen threw up her window, and, leaning forth, continued to revile me as I went up the wynd; the freetraders, coming to the tavern door, joined in the mockery, and one had even the inhumanity to set upon me a very savage small dog, which bit me in the ankle. 可就算我从屋子里逃出来，她还是没有放过我。我走在巷子里的时候，她还从窗子里探出脑袋来继续叫骂；那些酒馆的小贩们捡到个便宜热闹可以凑，也纷纷加入了叫骂的大军，还有个没人性的，放了条小野狗出来，把我的脚踝给咬伤了。
This was a strong lesson, had I required one, to avoid ill company; and I rode home in much pain from the bite and considerable indignation of mind. 这件事情给我上了人生沉重的一课，要避免和恶人为伍；我带着被咬伤的脚踝和心中极度的愤怒回到了家中。
Mr. Henry was in the steward’s room, affecting employment, but I could see he was only impatient to hear of my errand. 亨利先生正在账房忙着做账，但我能看出来他急不可耐地想要知道我此行的结果。
“Well?” says he, as soon as I came in; and when I had told him something of what passed, and that Jessie seemed an undeserving woman and far from grateful: “She is no friend to me,” said he; “but, indeed, Mackellar, I have few friends to boast of, and Jessie has some cause to be unjust. “怎样？”我一进来，他便问道。我告诉他我经历的一切，还和他说杰丝不配和亨利先生有任何交往，她的行为远远称不上体面。亨利先生说道：“我跟她没什么关系，但是杰丝现在这样疯疯癫癫是有原因的。
I need not dissemble what all the country knows: she was not very well used by one of our family.” 我没有必要去掩盖所有人都知道的事实，我们家有个人对不起她。”
This was the first time I had heard him refer to the Master even distantly; and I think he found his tongue rebellious even for that much, but presently he resumed—“This is why I would have nothing said. 虽然没有直接指名道姓，但亨利先生在我面前提起大少爷这还是头一遭。我觉得就算只是提起也让亨利先生舌头打结，但是他还是调整过来接着说道：“这就是为什么我对这件事保持沉默。
It would give pain to Mrs. Henry ...and to my father,” he added, with another flush. 如果说出来，会给亨利夫人和我的父亲……带来痛苦。”说着，他的脸又红了。
“Mr. Henry,” said I, “if you will take a freedom at my hands, I would tell you to let that woman be. “亨利先生，”我说道，“要是你让我来处理这件事情，我会告诉你，让这个女人自生自灭吧。
What service is your money to the like of her? 你给她钱又能怎么样？
She has no sobriety and no economy—as for gratitude, you will as soon get milk from a whinstone; and if you will pretermit your bounty, it will make no change at all but just to save the ankles of your messengers.” 她根本就不知道什么叫节俭和节制——要说从她那里得到感激，那更是缘木求鱼；您要是能省省您的慷慨，事情也根本就没什么区别，还能顺便把您仆人的脚踝从野狗的牙齿下拯救出来。”　　
Mr. Henry smiled. 亨利先生笑了。
“But I am grieved about your ankle,” said he, the next moment, with a proper gravity. “对你脚踝的事情，我深表遗憾。”然后，他露出了沉重的表情。
“And observe,” I continued, “I give you this advice upon consideration; and yet my heart was touched for the woman in the beginning.” “您看，”我继续说道，“我的建议可是经过了深思熟虑的；尽管一开始我也挺同情那个女人的。”
“Why, there it is, you see!” said Mr. Henry. “就是这样了，你看！”亨利先生说道，
“And you are to remember that I knew her once a very decent lass. “我以前就认识她，她曾经是个非常像样的小姑娘。
Besides which, although I speak little of my family, I think much of its repute.” 除此之外，尽管我平常不怎么提及我的家庭，但是我必须维护它的名声。”
And with that he broke up the talk, which was the first we had together in such confidence. 谈话就这样结束了，这是我们第一次交心的谈话。
But the same afternoon I had the proof that his father was perfectly acquainted with the business, and that it was only from his wife that Mr. Henry kept it secret. 不过当天下午，我就证实了老爷对这件事早就了然，唯一被蒙在鼓里的，也就只有亨利夫人了。
“I fear you had a painful errand to-day,” says my lord to me, “for which, as it enters in no way among your duties, I wish to thank you, and to remind you at the same time (in case Mr. Henry should have neglected) how very desirable it is that no word of it should reach my daughter. “今天的事情让你受惊了，”老爷对我说道，“这本不是你的职责所在，所以我想谢谢你，同时还要提醒你一下（要是亨利先生没说的话），千万别让我那闺女知道这件事情。
Reflections on the dead, Mr. Mackellar, are doubly painful.” 勾起别人对逝者的回忆是很痛苦的，麦凯勒先生。”
Anger glowed in my heart; and I could have told my lord to his face how little he had to do, bolstering up the image of the dead in Mrs. Henry’s heart, and how much better he were employed to shatter that false idol; for by this time I saw very well how the land lay between my patron and his wife. 我怒火中烧。当时真应该当面指责老爷的这种做法，他就不能多为活人考虑一些么？老爷本来不费吹灰之力就能粉碎夫人心中那个虚假的形象，可他即便使用隐瞒的方式，也要维持夫人心中那已死之人的完美；而在那个时候，连我都已经很清楚地知道活着的女主人和男主人之间存在巨大的隔阂了。
My pen is clear enough to tell a plain tale; but to render the effect of an infinity of small things, not one great enough in itself to be narrated; and to translate the story of looks, and the message of voices when they are saying no great matter; and to put in half a page the essence of near eighteen months—this is what I despair to accomplish. 我只能陈述这个普通的故事，但是让我把这期间所有不值一提却又浩如星海的琐事及至这18个月中我所见的每一个表情、声音全部重现在这半页纸的篇幅内，恐非我笔力所及。
The fault, to be very blunt, lay all in Mrs. Henry. 实话实说，这错误全在亨利夫人身上。
She felt it a merit to have consented to the marriage, and she took it like a martyrdom; in which my old lord, whether he knew it or not, fomented her. 她认为答应这门婚事是自己美德的体现，是一种崇高的自我牺牲；而老爷，不管他清楚与否，居然一直在为她这种想法添砖加瓦。
She made a merit, besides, of her constancy to the dead, though its name, to a nicer conscience, should have seemed rather disloyalty to the living; and here also my lord gave her his countenance. 她与亨利先生结婚，展现了自己的美德，同时，她还要保持对已逝之人爱情的忠贞，咱们换个更好的逻辑，这完全是对生者的不忠，可笑的是，老爷却对她的做法用沉默的方式表示赞同。
I suppose he was glad to talk of his loss, and ashamed to dwell on it with Mr. Henry. 我觉得在别人面前，老爷肯定常常提及自己的丧子之痛，只不过在亨利先生面前不方便表现罢了。
Certainly, at least, he made a little coterie apart in that family of three, and it was the husband who was shut out. 而且，在这个只有三个人的家庭里，老爷还要划定自己的小圈子，而被这个小圈子排除在外的，只有亨利先生自己。
It seems it was an old custom when the family were alone in Durrisdeer, that my lord should take his wine to the chimney-side, and Miss Alison, instead of withdrawing, should bring a stool to his knee, and chatter to him privately; and after she had become my patron’s wife the same manner of doing was continued. 达里斯迪尔家一直持续着一个老传统，老爷端着自己的酒坐在壁炉边，艾莉森小姐不回避，反倒带着凳子坐在老爷膝边，进行着专属于两人之间的谈话；等到艾莉森小姐成为亨利夫人以后，这个习惯居然延续了下来。
It should have been pleasant to behold this ancient gentleman so loving with his daughter, but I was too much a partisan of Mr. Henry’s to be anything but wroth at his exclusion. 老绅士和他备受宠爱的养女之间的这种促膝长谈本是一幅让观者为之愉悦的幸福画面，但我实在是觉得，无论如何，亨利先生也不应该是那个被排除在外的人。
Many’s the time I have seen him make an obvious resolve, quit the table, and go and join himself to his wife and my Lord Durrisdeer; and on their part, they were never backward to make him welcome, turned to him smilingly as to an intruding child, and took him into their talk with an effort so ill-concealed that he was soon back again beside me at the table, whence (so great is the hall of Durrisdeer) we could but hear the murmur of voices at the chimney. 很多次，我都注意到亨利先生鼓起勇气，离开桌子，想加入到自己妻子和父亲之间的谈话中来；可是他们对亨利先生的到来没有一点儿欢迎的表示，勉强地把他纳入到谈话中来，并且对这种“勉强”不加掩饰，这让亨利先生非常不自在，不一会儿就被迫回到桌边跟我坐到一起，（达里斯迪尔府的大厅颇具规模）我们只能隔很远，听壁炉那边传来的不甚清晰的私语。
There he would sit and watch, and I along with him; and sometimes by my lord’s head sorrowfully shaken, or his hand laid on Mrs. Henry’s head, or hers upon his knee as if in consolation, or sometimes by an exchange of tearful looks, we would draw our conclusion that the talk had gone to the old subject and the shadow of the dead was in the hall. 这时，他只能自己坐在一旁看着，而我则陪着他。有时候老爷悲伤地摇摇头，或者轻轻抚摸亨利太太的头发；有时亨利太太会把手放在老爷的膝盖上以示宽慰之意，或者俩人干脆就泪眼相对。一看就知道他们的话题又转到老路子上了，于是整个大厅就又笼罩在死亡的阴影之下了。
I have hours when I blame Mr. Henry for taking all too patiently; yet we are to remember he was married in pity, and accepted his wife upon that term. 我曾经一连几个小时责怪亨利先生脾气太好，然后我们又都想起他的整个婚姻都是建立在别人同情的基础之上。
And, indeed, he had small encouragement to make a stand. 实际上，他基本上没有勇气来提高自己在家中的地位。
Once, I remember, he announced he had found a man to replace the pane of the stained window, which, as it was he that managed all the business, was a thing clearly within his attributions. 我记得有一次，他说他想招人把彩色窗户上那块不太和谐的玻璃换掉，他把一切事情都安排好了，而且这件事他来做主也是完全合乎情理的。
But to the Master’s fancies, that pane was like a relic; and on the first word of any change, the blood flew to Mrs. Henry’s face. 但大少爷之前把这块玻璃当文物一样宝贝，所以当亨利先生一提起换玻璃的事情，亨利太太立刻涨红了脸。
“I wonder at you!” she cried. “你想怎么样？”她喊道。
“I wonder at myself,” says Mr. Henry, with more of bitterness than I had ever heard him to express. “我也想知道我要怎样。”亨利先生说到，用一种我之前很少听到的辛酸的口吻说道。　
Thereupon my old lord stepped in with his smooth talk, so that before the meal was at an end all seemed forgotten; only that, after dinner, when the pair had withdrawn as usual to the chimney- side, we could see her weeping with her head upon his knee. 这时，老爷带着他的和声细语走了过来，晚饭前，这件事情姑且算过去了；只不过晚饭后，那对老少二人组又齐聚壁炉前，我们都能看到夫人趴在老爷膝上哭泣。
Mr. Henry kept up the talk with me upon some topic of the estates—he could speak of little else but business, and was never the best of company; but he kept it up that day with more continuity, his eye straying ever and again to the chimney, and his voice changing to another key, but without check of delivery. 亨利先生一刻不停地跟我说着地产的事情——除了这些事务上的事情，他跟别人也基本不说起其他话题；但他那天一直说个不停，好像在分散自己的注意力一般，时不时还会瞟一下壁炉那边，说话时的声音和往日不同，但还是同样的话题。
The pane, however, was not replaced; and I believe he counted it a great defeat. 那块玻璃到最后也没换成；我觉得亨利先生肯定把这看作自己的一次惨败。
Whether he was stout enough or no, God knows he was kind enough. 不论他是否有足够的决断力，所有人都知道他是个绝对善良的人。
Mrs. Henry had a manner of condescension with him, such as (in a wife) would have pricked my vanity into an ulcer; he took it like a favour. 亨利夫人老是用一种纡尊降贵的姿态来对待他，一般人绝对受不了，可他依然甘之如饴。
She held him at the staff’s end; forgot and then remembered and unbent to him, as we do to children; burthened him with cold kindness; reproved him with a change of colour and a bitten lip, like one shamed by his disgrace: ordered him with a look of the eye, when she was off her guard; when she was on the watch, pleaded with him for the most natural attentions, as though they were unheard-of favours. 她总是把他放到最后一位去考虑，忘了可以全然抛诸脑后，想起来又对他千依百顺，跟哄孩子似的；一会儿咬着嘴唇变脸，好像自己丈夫有多么丢人似的：当她不爽快的时候，一个眼神就能命令他；等她心情好的时候，又用“真情”祈求他的爱恋，好像他们正在初恋之中。
And to all this he replied with the most unwearied service, loving, as folk say, the very ground she trod on, and carrying that love in his eyes as bright as a lamp. 而他却报以不知疲倦的爱，就像人们常说的：连她踏过的土地，都能让他用灿若明灯的眼神打量一番。
When Miss Katharine was to be born, nothing would serve but he must stay in the room behind the head of the bed. 凯瑟琳小姐出生的时候，他说什么都要守在她的床头。
There he sat, as white (they tell me) as a sheet, and the sweat dropping from his brow; and the handkerchief he had in his hand was crushed into a little ball no bigger than a musket-bullet. 他站在那里，脸色苍白如纸（别人告诉我的），焦急的汗水沿着眉头流了下来；手里的帕子被捏得比个子弹大不了多少。
Nor could he bear the sight of Miss Katharine for many a day; indeed, I doubt if he was ever what he should have been to my young lady; for the which want of natural feeling he was loudly blamed. 他许多天都不看凯瑟琳小姐一眼；事实上，我怀疑他是个不怎么称职的父亲；夫人经常为这件事情怪罪他。
Such was the state of this family down to the 7th April, 1749, when there befell the first of that series of events which were to break so many hearts and lose so many lives. 以上就是1749年4月7日以前这个家的情况。那之后，发生了很多让人心碎，甚至还牵扯到人命的事件。
On that day I was sitting in my room a little before supper, when John Paul burst open the door with no civility of knocking, and told me there was one below that wished to speak with the steward; sneering at the name of my office. 那天，离晚餐时间还有一段时间，约翰·保尔连门都不敲地就冲进我的办公室，一边说楼下有人找管家，一边还用奚落的语气嘲笑我办公室的名字。
I asked what manner of man, and what his name was; and this disclosed the cause of John’s ill-humour; for it appeared the visitor refused to name himself except to me, a sore affront to the major-domo’s consequence. 我问他那人姓甚名谁；但那人明显只有见到我才会吐露自己的真实姓名，这就解释了约翰·保尔那酸溜溜的语气是为什么了——这明显挫了他这个总管的面子。
“Well,” said I, smiling a little, “I will see what he wants.” “好吧，”我说道，笑了一下，“我去看看他有何贵干。”
I found in the entrance hall a big man, very plainly habited, and wrapped in a sea-cloak, like one new landed, as indeed he was. 我看到大厅门口站着一个身材高大的人，衣着简单，裹着一件航海斗篷，跟个刚上岸的人似的，事实上他也确实刚从船上下来。
Not, far off Macconochie was standing, with his tongue out of his mouth and his hand upon his chin, like a dull fellow thinking hard; and the stranger, who had brought his cloak about his face, appeared uneasy. 麦克诺奇在不远的地方站着，吐着舌头托着腮，像是个努力思考中的蠢蛋；而那个陌生人，斗篷一直遮到脸上，一副心神不宁的样子。
He had no sooner seen me coming than he went to meet me with an effusive manner. 他一看到我走过来就态度热情地迎上了我。
“My dear man,” said he, “a thousand apologies for disturbing you, but I’m in the most awkward position. “我亲爱的先生，”他说道，“打搅你让我觉得非常抱歉，但我现在的处境很尴尬。
And there’s a son of a ramrod there that I should know the looks of, and more betoken I believe that he knows mine. 我刚碰见一个我应该是认识的人，我有理由相信他也能认出我。
Being in this family, sir, and in a place of some responsibility (which was the cause I took the liberty to send for you), you are doubtless of the honest party?” 在这个家里，先生，我之所以让人去叫您出来，您肯定是这个家里值得信赖的人吧？”
“You may be sure at least,” says I, “that all of that party are quite safe in Durrisdeer.” “您得知道，”我说道，“达里斯迪尔府上的所有人都是值得信赖的人。”
“My dear man, it is my very thought,” says he. “我亲爱的先生，我也是这么想的，”他说道，
“You see, I have just been set on shore here by a very honest man, whose name I cannot remember, and who is to stand off and on for me till morning, at some danger to himself; and, to be clear with you, I am a little concerned lest it should be at some to me. “您瞧，是一位诚实可靠的人派我来的，我没有记住他的名字，不过他现在正冒着风险在海滩上等我的消息，他将一直等到清晨。说实话，我还真觉得自己有点儿冒险呢。
I have saved my life so often, Mr.—, I forget your name, which is a very good one—that, faith, I would be very loath to lose it after all. 我也是九死一生，什么先生来着？——对不起，我忘记您的名字，那是个好名字——说实话，我还很是舍不得自己这条命呢。
And the son of a ramrod, whom I believe I saw before Carlisle ...” 还有我刚才碰见的那个可能认识我的人，我觉得我在卡莱索附近见过他……”
“Oh, sir,” said I, “you can trust Macconochie until to-morrow.” “噢，先生，”我说道，“明天之前您完全可以信赖麦克诺奇。”
“Well, and it’s a delight to hear you say so,” says the stranger. “好吧，听您这样说真是太好了，”陌生人说道，
“The truth is that my name is not a very suitable one in this country of Scotland. “其实我的名字在苏格兰这个国家真的不便透露。
With a gentleman like you, my dear man, I would have no concealments of course; and by your leave I’ll just breathe it in your ear. 向您这样体面的人，我亲爱的先生，我当然要实言相告；不过我得悄悄跟您说才行。
They call me Francis Burke—Colonel Francis Burke; and I am here, at a most damnable risk to myself, to see your masters—if you’ll excuse me, my good man, for giving them the name, for I’m sure it’s a circumstance I would never have guessed from your appearance. 他们叫我弗朗西斯·伯克——弗朗西斯·伯克上校；而我冒着巨大的危险来这里见您的主人——请您，我亲爱的先生，把我的姓名通报给您的主人，因我从您的外表真的猜不出这里情况如何。
And if you would just be so very obliging as to take my name to them, you might say that I come bearing letters which I am sure they will be very rejoiced to have the reading of.” 您通报我姓名的的时候，您可以说我是来送信的，这信里绝对有他们想知道的消息。”
Colonel Francis Burke was one of the Prince’s Irishmen, that did his cause such an infinity of hurt, and were so much distasted of the Scots at the time of the rebellion; and it came at once into my mind, how the Master of Ballantrae had astonished all men by going with that party. 弗朗西斯·伯克上校是王子手下的那一群爱尔兰人中的一个，他们给王子拖了后腿，在叛乱时期，所有的爱尔兰人都对他们深恶痛绝；这时候，我脑袋里的头一个想法就是——大少爷和这种人为伍是一件多么让人震惊的事。
In the same moment a strong foreboding of the truth possessed my soul. 同时，我心里还有一种真相即将到来的预感。
“If you will step in here,” said I, opening a chamber door, “I will let my lord know.” “请跟我来吧，”我说道，打开另一扇门，“我去通报我的主人。”
“And I am sure it’s very good of you, Mr. What-is-your-name,” says the Colonel. “您真好，那什么先生，请问您怎么称呼啊。”上校说道。
Up to the hall I went, slow-footed. 我慢慢地走入大厅。
There they were, all three—my old lord in his place, Mrs. Henry at work by the window, Mr. Henry (as was much his custom) pacing the low end. 他们三个都在，老爷还在壁炉边，亨利先生在窗边办公，亨利太太则一如既往地做着针线。
In the midst was the table laid for supper. 中间是已经置备好晚饭的餐桌。
I told them briefly what I had to say. 我简要地说明了一番。
My old lord lay back in his seat. 听后，老爷仰靠在椅背上。
Mrs. Henry sprang up standing with a mechanical motion, and she and her husband stared at each other’s eyes across the room; it was the strangest, challenging look these two exchanged, and as they looked, the colour faded in their faces. 亨利太太用一种非常不自然的动作跳了起来，隔着房间，和自己的丈夫对看着；这是他们第一次交换这么奇特的、互相挑衅的目光，看着看着，两人都变得面色苍白。
Then Mr. Henry turned to me; not to speak, only to sign with his finger; but that was enough, and I went down again for the Colonel. 然后亨利先生转向了我；做了个手势让我下去把人带进来。
When we returned, these three were in much the same position I same left them in; I believe no word had passed. 等我带着上校回来的时候，他们三个还站在原来的位置上一动不动，我估计三人之间一句话也没说。
“My Lord Durrisdeer, no doubt?” says the Colonel, bowing, and my lord bowed in answer. “是达里斯迪尔勋爵，没错吧？”上校说着弯腰行礼，老爷也跟着回了礼。
“And this,” continues the Colonel, “should be the Master of Ballantrae?” “那这位，”上校接着说道，“应该就是巴伦特雷少爷了？”
“I have never taken that name,” said Mr. Henry; “but I am Henry Durie, at your service.” “我还没用那个称谓，”亨利先生说道；“您可以叫我亨利·迪里，愿意为您效劳。”
Then the Colonel turns to Mrs. Henry, bowing with his hat upon his heart and the most killing airs of gallantry. 然后上校转向亨利夫人，非常殷勤地脱帽行礼。
“There can be no mistake about so fine a figure of a lady,” says he. “没错的话，这一定就是那位美丽的小姐了，”他说道，
“I address the seductive Miss Alison, of whom I have so often heard?” “就是我经常听到的那位极具魅力的艾莉森小姐，对吧？”
Once more husband and wife exchanged a look. 丈夫和妻子再一次交换了下眼神。
“I am Mrs. Henry Durie,” said she; “but before my marriage my name was Alison Graeme.” “我是亨利·迪里的妻子，”她说道，“但婚前的名字是艾莉森·格里姆。”
Then my lord spoke up. 这时老爷开腔了。
“I am an old man, Colonel Burke,” said he, “and a frail one. “我上了年纪了，伯克上校，”他说道，“身体不好。
It will be mercy on your part to be expeditious. 直入主题是对我最大的仁慈。
Do you bring me news of—” he hesitated, and then the words broke from him with a singular change of voice—“my son?” 您是不是给我带来了——”他顿了一下，然后声音就突然变了一下，“——我儿子的什么消息？”
“My dear lord, I will be round with you like a soldier,” said the Colonel. “尊敬的阁下，让我用军人的简洁方式来回答您，”上校说道，
“I do.” “是的。”
My lord held out a wavering hand; he seemed to wave a signal, but whether it was to give him time or to speak on, was more than we could guess. 老爷颤抖着挥了挥手；看上去是在打着手势，但我们又说不准他的意思是想让上校继续说下去还是让我们给他一点儿接受的时间，或者别的什么。
At length he got out the one word, “Good?” 最后，他只说出两个字，“活着？”
“Why, the very best in the creation!” cries the Colonel. “当然活着，还活得好好的呢！”上校大声说道，
“For my good friend and admired comrade is at this hour in the fine city of Paris, and as like as not, if I know anything of his habits, he will be drawing in his chair to a piece of dinner. “我这位亲爱的朋友兼可敬的盟友正在巴黎，以我对他的了解，现在应该正在搬椅子准备用晚餐呢。
—Bedad, I believe the lady’s fainting.” ——啊，我觉得夫人好像昏倒了。”
Mrs. Henry was indeed the colour of death, and drooped against the window-frame. 亨利夫人面如死灰地摔倒在窗框边。
But when Mr. Henry made a movement as if to run to her, she straightened with a sort of shiver. 在亨利先生正准备冲到她身边的时候，她又颤抖着站了起来。
“I am well,” she said, with her white lips. “我还好。”她说道，嘴唇发白。
Mr. Henry stopped, and his face had a strong twitch of anger. 亨利先生停住了脚步，面露狂怒的表情。
The next moment he had turned to the Colonel. 下一刻他转向上校。
“You must not blame yourself,” says he, “for this effect on Mrs. Durie. “您不必为迪里太太的反应自责。”他说道，
It is only natural; we were all brought up like brother and sister.” “这是很自然的事情，我们三个从小像兄妹，一起长大的。”
Mrs. Henry looked at her husband with something like relief or even gratitude. 亨利夫人看向自己丈夫的眼神带着如释重负甚至是感激的味道。
In my way of thinking, that speech was the first step he made in her good graces. 我觉得，这是亨利先生第一次为她挽回了面子。
“You must try to forgive me, Mrs. Durie, for indeed and I am just an Irish savage,” said the Colonel; “and I deserve to be shot for not breaking the matter more artistically to a lady. “您得原谅我，迪里夫人，实际上我就是个爱尔兰大老粗，”上校说道，“用这么莽撞的方式把这件事情说出来，我真该挨枪子儿。
But here are the Master’s own letters; one for each of the three of you; and to be sure (if I know anything of my friend’s genius) he will tell his own story with a better grace.” 但这里有大少爷的亲笔信；他给你们一人写了一封；以我对他的了解，我确定他一定会把事情用更婉转的方式告诉你们的。”
He brought the three letters forth as he spoke, arranged them by their superscriptions, presented the first to my lord, who took it greedily, and advanced towards Mrs. Henry holding out the second. 他一边说着一边把信拿了出来，按照字母顺序排列，第一封是给老爷的，老爷急不可耐地接了过去，第二封信是给亨利夫人的。
But the lady waved it back. 可是夫人挥了挥手没有接。
“To my husband,” says she, with a choked voice. “给我丈夫吧。”她用哽咽的声音说道。
The Colonel was a quick man, but at this he was somewhat nonplussed. 上校是个机灵人，可这种情况也让他不知所措起来。
“To be sure!” says he; “how very dull of me! “这是自然的！”上校说道；“我怎么这么傻呢！
To be sure!” 这是自然的！”
But he still held the letter. 但他依然拿着信没松手。
At last Mr. Henry reached forth his hand, and there was nothing to be done but give it up. 直到亨利先生来取他手里的信，他也只得松手了。
Mr. Henry took the letters (both hers and his own), and looked upon their outside, with his brows knit hard, as if he were thinking. 亨利先生拿着两封信（给自己的和给亨利夫人的），看了看信封，眉头紧锁，好像在思考着什么。
He had surprised me all through by his excellent behaviour; but he was to excel himself now. 他遇事的镇静一直都让我叹服；而这次的镇定更是大大超越了他一贯的表现。
“Let me give you a hand to your room,” said he to his wife. “我先带你回房吧，”他对妻子说道，
“This has come something of the suddenest; and, at any rate, you will wish to read your letter by yourself.” “这件事发生得太突然；而且，不管怎么说，你都应该自己读这封信。”
Again she looked upon him with the same thought of wonder; but he gave her no time, coming straight to where she stood. 她再次用探究的眼神看着她；但他没给她时间，直接走到她身边。
“It will be better so, believe me,” said he; “and Colonel Burke is too considerate not to excuse you.” “相信我，回去吧，”他说道，“伯克上校那么通情达理，一定不会怪你的。”
And with that he took her hand by the fingers, and led her from the hall. 他牵着她的手，把她带离了大厅。
Mrs. Henry returned no more that night; and when Mr. Henry went to visit her next morning, as I heard long afterwards, she gave him the letter again, still unopened. 那天晚上，亨利夫人没再出现在大厅里。第二天早上，亨利先生去看她的时候，我在一旁刚好听到她把没拆的信又交给了亨利先生。
“Oh, read it and be done!” he had cried. “噢，你看了就行了。”他喊道。
“Spare me that,” said she. “放过我吧。”她说道。
And by these two speeches, to my way of thinking, each undid a great part of what they had previously done well. 在我看来，就这两句话，使他们一度不错的关系又开始走下坡路。
But the letter, sure enough, came into my hands, and by me was burned, unopened. 最后那信到了我手里，信没有拆开，就直接被烧掉了。
To be very exact as to the adventures of the Master after Culloden, I wrote not long ago to Colonel Burke, now a Chevalier of the Order of St. Louis, begging him for some notes in writing, since I could scarce depend upon my memory at so great an interval. 为了把大少爷在克卢敦战役之后的情形说清楚，我前一段时间致信给伯克上校，他现在已经被授予了圣路易斯骑士爵位。我请求他写一些记录给我，以免事隔多年，我的记忆靠不住。
To confess the truth, I have been somewhat embarrassed by his response; for he sent me the complete memoirs of his life, touching only in places on the Master; running to a much greater length than my whole story, and not everywhere (as it seems to me) designed for edification. 他的回复让我深感惭愧，他几乎以他的终生回忆为馈，仅是关于大少爷的那一部分，就比我的整个故事还要长，而且也并不是所有的部分都适合作为有教化意义的故事写出来。
He begged in his letter, dated from Ettenheim, that I would find a publisher for the whole, after I had made what use of it I required; and I think I shall best answer my own purpose and fulfil his wishes by printing certain parts of it in full. 他在信中请求我，信的内容从埃滕海姆开始，等我用完了我需要的部分，就找一家出版商把他的整个故事付梓。我打算先取我所需，截取他的一部分故事印刷出来。
In this way my readers will have a detailed, and, I believe, a very genuine account of some essential matters; and if any publisher should take a fancy to the Chevalier’s manner of narration, he knows where to apply for the rest, of which there is plenty at his service. 这样，我的读者们就能详尽而真实地了解这些关键事情；而且要是哪家出版社对出版骑士回忆录感兴趣的话，也能直接找到他，这也是我能付出的最大努力了。
I put in my first extract here, so that it may stand in the place of what the Chevalier told us over our wine in the hall of Durrisdeer; but you are to suppose it was not the brutal fact, but a very varnished version that he offered to my lord. 我先概括一下情形，这就是那天晚餐桌上，骑士酒后在达里斯迪尔府的大厅里的叙述。但你可以猜测，这不是残酷的事实，其中肯定有很多渲染夸张之处，都是为了讨好我们家老爷。
[1] A kind of firework made with damp powder. [1]一种用紧压粉末的方式制作的爆竹。
Chapter 3 第三章
The Master’s Wanderings. 大少爷的流浪旅程
From the Memoirs of the Chevalier De Burke. 摘自伯克骑士的回忆录
...I left Ruthven (it’s hardly necessary to remark) with much greater satisfaction than I had come to it; but whether I missed my way in the deserts, or whether my companions failed me, I soon found myself alone. ……相比来的时候，我离开拉斯文时（无需赘述）是带着巨大的满足感的；但不知道是我在沙漠里迷了路，还是和同伴走散了，我很快就孤身一人了。
This was a predicament very disagreeable; for I never understood this horrid country or savage people, and the last stroke of the Prince’s withdrawal had made us of the Irish more unpopular than ever. 这绝对不是什么好兆头，因为这个地方的恐怖程度和这里的居民未开化的程度远远超乎了我的想象，王子最后的撤军更是让我们这些爱尔兰人变得跟过街老鼠一样，人人喊打。
I was reflecting on my poor chances, when I saw another horseman on the hill, whom I supposed at first to have been a phantom, the news of his death in the very front at Culloden being current in the army generally. 正为自己的不幸境遇发愁时，我在山坡上看见了另一个骑马的人。乍一看到他，我还以为自己见鬼了，那人在卡洛登战役中阵亡的消息早就是部队里人所共知的了。
This was the Master of Ballantrae, my Lord Durrisdeer’s son, a young nobleman of the rarest gallantry and parts, and equally designed by nature to adorn a Court and to reap laurels in the field. 这就是巴伦特雷大少爷，达里斯迪尔爵爷的儿子，一位具备世间少有的胆识和勇气的青年贵族，为皇族增光，在战场上拔得头筹的英雄。
Our meeting was the more welcome to both, as he was one of the few Scots who had used the Irish with consideration, and as he might now be of very high utility in aiding my escape. 我们俩能碰上，对我们两个人都有好处。他是少数几个不轻视爱尔兰籍兵士的苏格兰人之一，我的逃亡之旅很大程度上可得指望他了。
Yet what founded our particular friendship was a circumstance, by itself as romantic as any fable of King Arthur. 不过我们真正结下情谊还是因为一件特别的事，其传奇性绝对不亚于任何一段亚瑟王的故事。
This was on the second day of our flight, after we had slept one night in the rain upon the inclination of a mountain. 那是逃亡路上的第二天，前一个晚上我们在山坡上冒雨休息了一晚。
There was an Appin man, Alan Black Stewart (or some such name, [1] but I have seen him since in France) who chanced to be passing the same way, and had a jealousy of my companion. 这时候来了一个阿平的伙计，名叫艾伦·布雷克·斯图尔特（或者是跟这个差不多的名字，［1］反正我之前在法国见过他），他跟我们一个方向，刚好也路过这里，对我们两个能结伴而行心生嫉妒。
Very uncivil expressions were exchanged; and Stewart calls upon the Master to alight and have it out. 双方都说了几句粗野的话，然后斯图尔特就要大少爷下马比个高低。
“Why, Mr. Stewart,” says the Master, “I think at the present time I would prefer to run a race with you.” “为什么要下马？斯图尔特先生，”大少爷说，“我觉得咱们现在可以比比赛跑。”
And with the word claps spurs to his horse. 说着他就驱马向前。
Stewart ran after us, a childish thing to do, for more than a mile; and I could not help laughing, as I looked back at last and saw him on a hill, holding his hand to his side, and nearly burst with running. 斯图尔特跟在我们后面跑了得有一英里，过程跟耍小孩儿似的；最后，回头看见他插着腰站在一个小山头上累得要死，我更是禁不住大声笑了起来。
“But, all the same,” I could not help saying to my companion, “I would let no man run after me for any such proper purpose, and not give him his desire. 但我还是忍不住对我的旅伴说：“但是，无论为了什么事情，我都不会让别人跟在我屁股后面跑，却什么也不答应他。
It was a good jest, but it smells a trifle cowardly.” 这确实是个不错的玩笑，但未免显得有些胆怯了。”
He bent his brows at me. 他朝我皱了皱眉。
“I do pretty well,” says he, “when I saddle myself with the most unpopular man in Scotland, and let that suffice for courage.” “我觉得我干得还不错啊，”他说道，“跟苏格兰最不受欢迎的人比试，这本来就是件很有勇气的事。”
“O, bedad,” says I, “I could show you a more unpopular with the naked eye. “噢，别扯了，”我说道，“现在我就能给你找个更不受待见的人出来。
And if you like not my company, you can ‘saddle’ yourself on some one else.” 你要是不想让我跟着你，你完全可以去找别人。”
“Colonel Burke,” says he, “do not let us quarrel; and, to that effect, let me assure you I am the least patient man in the world.” “伯克上校，”他说道，“咱俩就别吵了，而且我得让你知道，我是这个世界上最没耐心的人。”
“I am as little patient as yourself,” said I. “我比你还没耐心，”我说道，
“I care not who knows that.” “而且我根本就不介意别人知不知道。”
“At this rate,” says he, reining in, “we shall not go very far. “看样子，”他勒马说道，“咱俩好像不能再往前走了。
And I propose we do one of two things upon the instant: either quarrel and be done; or make a sure bargain to bear everything at each other’s hands.” 我建议现在就找个方式决定一下：咱俩是要接着吵下去，然后分道扬镳呢？还是约定一下携手共进？”
“Like a pair of brothers?” said I. “像兄弟那样么？”我问道。
“I said no such foolishness,” he replied. “我才不用那么愚蠢的形容词，”他回答，
“I have a brother of my own, and I think no more of him than of a colewort. “我有个亲生弟弟，可是我根本就看不上他。
But if we are to have our noses rubbed together in this course of flight, let us each dare to be ourselves like savages, and each swear that he will neither resent nor deprecate the other. 但是，如果咱俩打算在之后的路上一起走，我们就得用最原始的方式结为同盟，约定彼此绝不厌弃或者拆对方的台。
I am a pretty bad fellow at bottom, and I find the pretence of virtues very irksome.” 实际上，我是个十分坏的伙伴，而且我也最讨厌满口假仁假义的家伙。”
“O, I am as bad as yourself,” said I. “噢，这一点咱俩倒是坏到一块去了，”我说道，
“There is no skim milk in Francis Burke. “我，弗朗西斯·伯克绝对不是娘娘腔。
But which is it to be? 那怎么着？
Fight or make friends?” 为敌还是为友？”
“Why,” says be, “I think it will be the best manner to spin a coin for it.” “好吧，”他说道，“我觉得最好的方式还是抛硬币决定吧。”
This proposition was too highly chivalrous not to take my fancy; and, strange as it may seem of two well-born gentlemen of to-day, we span a half-crown (like a pair of ancient paladins) whether we were to cut each other’s throats or be sworn friends. 这种颇具骑士风格的决定方式甚合我意；虽然现在看来，两个出身名门的贵族做这种抛硬币的事情还真是奇怪，但我们还真的拿出了一枚半克朗的硬币（像以前的骑士那样）来决定是打个你死我活还是义结金兰。
A more romantic circumstance can rarely have occurred; and it is one of those points in my memoirs, by which we may see the old tales of Homer and the poets are equally true to-day—at least, of the noble and genteel. 几乎再没有比这件事更具英侠豪情的了；在我的记忆里，整件事有很多地方仿佛是荷马史诗再世，又仿佛是上流社会那些流芳百世的诗篇中所描绘的东西成了真。
The coin fell for peace, and we shook hands upon our bargain. 硬币指向和解，我们握手以示缔结约定。
And then it was that my companion explained to me his thought in running away from Mr. Stewart, which was certainly worthy of his political intellect. 然后，我的旅伴就给我解释了他想要甩掉斯图尔特先生的原因，这确实符合他在政治上的一贯风格和立场。
The report of his death, he said, was a great guard to him; Mr. Stewart having recognised him, had become a danger; and he had taken the briefest road to that gentleman’s silence. 他说自己阵亡的消息是故意放出来掩人耳目的，斯图尔特先生认出了他已经让他身陷危险之中，而甩掉他则是让他闭嘴的捷径。
“For,” says he, “Alan Black is too vain a man to narrate any such story of himself.” “因为，”他说道，“斯图尔特是个虚荣的人，他一定会为了博人注意而把这件事情说出去的。”
Towards afternoon we came down to the shores of that loch for which we were heading; and there was the ship, but newly come to anchor. 下午时，我们到达了目的地——那条狭长海湾的海滨，那里刚停了一艘船。
She was the SAINTE-MARIE-DES-ANGES, out of the port of Havre-de-Grace. 这条名为“圣玛丽天使号”的船是从美国的格雷斯港开过来的。
The Master, after we had signalled for a boat, asked me if I knew the captain. 等我们打手势把船招过来后，大少爷问我认不认识那位船长。
I told him he was a countryman of mine, of the most unblemished integrity, but, I was afraid, a rather timorous man. 我告诉他船长是我老乡，为人倒是正直，就是有点儿胆小怕事。
“No matter,” says he. “没关系，”他说道，
“For all that, he should certainly hear the truth.” “咱们应该把实话都告诉他。”
I asked him if he meant about the battle? for if the captain once knew the standard was down, he would certainly put to sea again at once. 我问他“实话”是不是就是指战况？因为船长一旦知道王子的颓势，他马上就会起锚逃跑。
“And even then!” said he; “the arms are now of no sort of utility.” “那又怎么样！”他说道，“现在有武器也没用了。”
“My dear man,” said I, “who thinks of the arms? “我亲爱的朋友，”我说道，“谁跟你说武器的事了？
But, to be sure, we must remember our friends. 但是咱们得记着自己的战友。
They will be close upon our heels, perhaps the Prince himself, and if the ship be gone, a great number of valuable lives may be imperilled.” 他们还指着咱们救命呢，这其中也许还包括王子自己，船要是走了，那么多条宝贵的性命不就危险了么？”
“The captain and the crew have lives also, if you come to that,” says Ballantrae. “你要是这么说，船长和船员的命也是命啊。”巴伦特雷说道。
This I declared was but a quibble, and that I would not hear of the captain being told; and then it was that Ballantrae made me a witty answer, for the sake of which (and also because I have been blamed myself in this business of the SAINTE-MARIE-DES-ANGES) I have related the whole conversation as it passed. 我认为这完全就是诡辩，我绝对不同意让船长知道实情，结果巴伦特雷给了我一个诙谐机智的回答，为此（当然也因为之后由于圣玛丽天使号上的事情，我招人怪罪），就算这段话已经过去很久了，我还是记得他当时的原话。
“Frank,” says he, “remember our bargain. “弗朗克，”他说道，“你还记得我们的协定吗？
I must not object to your holding your tongue, which I hereby even encourage you to do; but, by the same terms, you are not to resent my telling.” 你保持沉默我绝不会反对，甚至此时我还鼓励你沉默，但是根据我们的协定，你不能对我要说的话有任何异议。”
I could not help laughing at this; though I still forewarned him what would come of it. 我忍不住大笑起来，但我还是忍不住警告他这样做可能发生的后果。
“The devil may come of it for what I care,” says the reckless fellow. “就我看来，这样肯定会搞砸的，”这个鲁莽的同伴这样说道，
“I have always done exactly as I felt inclined.” “而我从来都是跟着感觉走。”
As is well known, my prediction came true. 众所周知，我的预言应验了。
