The captain had no sooner heard the news than he cut his cable and to sea again; and before morning broke, we were in the Great Minch. 船长一听到消息立马就再次起锚，天还没亮我们就到了大明奇。
The ship was very old; and the skipper, although the most honest of men (and Irish too), was one of the least capable. 船已经很旧了。船长（也是爱尔兰人）为人诚实，不过明显能力不足。
The wind blew very boisterous, and the sea raged extremely. 海上狂风怒号，巨浪翻滚。
All that day we had little heart whether to eat or drink; went early to rest in some concern of mind; and (as if to give us a lesson) in the night the wind chopped suddenly into the north-east, and blew a hurricane. 那一整天我们都无心吃喝，满怀心事地早早入睡。（仿佛是要给我们一个教训）夜里风向突然转成东北风，刮起了飓风。
We were awaked by the dreadful thunder of the tempest and the stamping of the mariners on deck; so that I supposed our last hour was certainly come; and the terror of my mind was increased out of all measure by Ballantrae, who mocked at my devotions. 我们在令人毛骨悚然的狂风暴雨、电闪雷鸣和甲板上水手们凌乱的脚步声中醒来，我觉得我们命不久矣。我开始祈祷，在被巴伦特雷狠狠嘲笑了一番之后，恐惧感不降反升。
It is in hours like these that a man of any piety appears in his true light, and we find (what we are taught as babes) the small trust that can be set in worldly friends. 在这样的生死关头，任何像我这样笃信宗教的人都会发出心中最诚恳的祷告，结果我发现，（就像我们从小被教导的一样）那些表面上和你称兄道弟的人永远不能相信。
I would be unworthy of my religion if I let this pass without particular remark. 如果我不把这件事拿出来说说，真是对不起我信仰多年的教义。
For three days we lay in the dark in the cabin, and had but a biscuit to nibble. 我们连续三天都窝在黑漆漆的船舱里，只能靠咬两口饼干度日。
On the fourth the wind fell, leaving the ship dismasted and heaving on vast billows. 第四天风势渐缓，但船桅已经被吹折了，船在巨浪中随波逐流。
The captain had not a guess of whither we were blown; he was stark ignorant of his trade, and could do naught but bless the Holy Virgin; a very good thing, too, but scarce the whole of seamanship. 船长根本不知道我们正被吹向何方，除了向圣母玛利亚祈祷之外他什么也做不了，虽然祈祷是一件好事，但他对自己的职业一无所知，连一点儿航海技术也不懂。
It seemed, our one hope was to be picked up by another vessel; and if that should prove to be an English ship, it might be no great blessing to the Master and myself. 我们当时唯一的希望就是有另一艘船经过，把我们营救出来；当然，如果来得是一艘英国船，我和大少爷可就没有好日子过了。
The fifth and sixth days we tossed there helpless. 第五天和第六天我们都在无助中度过。
The seventh some sail was got on her, but she was an unwieldy vessel at the best, and we made little but leeway. 第七天船上扬起了一些帆，不过由于船体笨重，几乎没什么效果。
All the time, indeed, we had been drifting to the south and west, and during the tempest must have driven in that direction with unheard-of violence. 事实上，我们一直在朝西南方向漂流，由此可见，当时在暴风雨中，我们朝着这个方向的漂流速度有多快。
The ninth dawn was cold and black, with a great sea running, and every mark of foul weather. 第九天清晨寒冷而阴沉，浪涛依旧汹涌，天气不佳。
In this situation we were overjoyed to sight a small ship on the horizon, and to perceive her go about and head for the SAINTE-MARIE. 在这个时候，我们狂喜地看到地平线上出现一艘小船，正朝我们驶来。
But our gratification did not very long endure; for when she had laid to and lowered a boat, it was immediately filled with disorderly fellows, who sang and shouted as they pulled across to us, and swarmed in on our deck with bare cutlasses, cursing loudly. 但是我们的兴奋没能持续多久，因为那船停了下来，放下一条小船，立马一群衣冠不整的人挤满了小船。他们边唱歌叫喊边向我们划来，一窝蜂地迈上我们的甲板，手中挥着短弯刀，嘴里说着不干净的话。
Their leader was a horrible villain, with his face blacked and his whiskers curled in ringlets; Teach, his name; a most notorious pirate. 他们的头儿是个令人恐惧的恶棍，一张黑脸，络腮胡子打着卷；他名叫蒂奇，是个声名狼藉的大海盗。
He stamped about the deck, raving and crying out that his name was Satan, and his ship was called Hell. 他在甲板上一边跺着脚一边大嚷他名唤魔君撒旦，所到之船，皆为地狱。
There was something about him like a wicked child or a half-witted person, that daunted me beyond expression. 他讲话时给人的感觉就像个坏孩子或智力有缺陷的人，我所受到的惊吓已经不能用言语形容。
I whispered in the ear of Ballantrae that I would not be the last to volunteer, and only prayed God they might be short of hands; he approved my purpose with a nod. 我对巴伦特雷耳语说要不然跟他们申请入伙好了，但愿他们最好缺人手，他对我点了点头以示同意。
“Bedad,” said I to Master Teach, “if you are Satan, here is a devil for ye.” “天哪，”我对蒂奇说，“您要是魔君，我就是您的小鬼儿啊。”
The word pleased him; and (not to dwell upon these shocking incidents) Ballantrae and I and two others were taken for recruits, while the skipper and all the rest were cast into the sea by the method of walking the plank. 这话取悦了他；（还有些惊心动魄的小事我就不赘言了）巴伦特雷、我，还有其他两个人加入了海盗船，船长和其他船员全都被迫跳海自杀了。
It was the first time I had seen this done; my heart died within me at the spectacle; and Master Teach or one of his acolytes (for my head was too much lost to be precise) remarked upon my pale face in a very alarming manner. 这是我第一次见识到这样的场景，情景之惨烈吓得我的心跳都几乎停止了。忘了是蒂奇还是他的哪个手下（我的脑袋总是没法把细节记得太准确）用一种让我觉得很危险的口吻谈论我苍白的脸色。
I had the strength to cut a step or two of a jig, and cry out some ribaldry, which saved me for that time; but my legs were like water when I must get down into the skiff among these miscreants; and what with my horror of my company and fear of the monstrous billows, it was all I could do to keep an Irish tongue and break a jest or two as we were pulled aboard. 我只能勉强收拾情绪，用那种吉格舞的姿态走了几步，随口喷了几句下流的话，反正是混过去了；可是只要一想到接下来要和这些穷凶极恶之徒共赴海盗船，我就吓得两腿发软；我对自己伙伴和海上巨浪感到恐惧，在被船带往外国的路上，我只能用爱尔兰腔说几句笑话。
By the blessing of God, there was a fiddle in the pirate ship, which I had no sooner seen than I fell upon; and in my quality of crowder I had the heavenly good luck to get favour in their eyes. 真是老天保佑，我都没想到，这海盗船上居然还有把小提琴，我看到后就立刻演奏起来，加上我原本在起哄上就有两下子，马上就博得了很多人的好感。
CROWDING PAT was the name they dubbed me with; and it was little I cared for a name so long as my skin was whole. 我立刻就得了个“起哄小鬼”的名号，不过只要我还能留得发肤之全，叫我什么我都介意不得了。
What kind of a pandemonium that vessel was, I cannot describe, but she was commanded by a lunatic, and might be called a floating Bedlam. 海盗船上的混乱喧嚣我简直难以形容，船上的头儿就是个疯子，所以叫这艘船为海上疯人院也不为过。
Drinking, roaring, singing, quarrelling, dancing, they were never all sober at one time; and there were days together when, if a squall had supervened, it must have sent us to the bottom; or if a king’s ship had come along, it would have found us quite helpless for defence. 喝酒的、吼叫的、唱歌的、吵架的、跳舞的，他们从来没有在同一个时间集体清醒过。要是一连几天遇上风暴，我们就得全体葬身鱼腹，要是被官船发现，船上连最基本的抵御能力都没有。
Once or twice we sighted a sail, and, if we were sober enough, overhauled it, God forgive us! and if we were all too drunk, she got away, and I would bless the saints under my breath. 有那么一两次，我们发现附近有船，要是大家还都没醉倒的话就可以好好干上一票，上帝原谅我们！要是大家都喝晕了，就让那船遛了，我在心里呼喊圣人保佑。
Teach ruled, if you can call that rule which brought no order, by the terror he created; and I observed the man was very vain of his position. 蒂奇统领全船，如果那也能叫统领的话，他除了制造恐惧之外基本没定任何规矩，我觉得这海盗头子完全浪费了他的统领地位。
I have known marshals of France—ay, and even Highland chieftains—that were less openly puffed up; which throws a singular light on the pursuit of honour and glory. 我认识好几个法国将军——啊，甚至还有几个高地的首领——虽然都是在追求名誉和荣耀，但没有一个跟他一样如此明目张胆、趾高气扬。
Indeed, the longer we live, the more we perceive the sagacity of Aristotle and the other old philosophers; and though I have all my life been eager for legitimate distinctions, I can lay my hand upon my heart, at the end of my career, and declare there is not one—no, nor yet life itself—which is worth acquiring or preserving at the slightest cost of dignity. 实际上，人活得越久，越能感知亚里士多德及其他希腊先贤的智慧。我虽然穷极一生追求仕途和功名，我也可以在生命结束前拍着自己的胸口声明，这世界上没有什么——没有，连性命在内——是值得用哪怕一点点的尊严去交换或保全的。
It was long before I got private speech of Ballantrae; but at length one night we crept out upon the boltsprit, when the rest were better employed, and commiserated our position. 过了很久，我才有机会和巴伦特雷单独说话。有一天夜里，趁其他所有人都在喝酒的时候，我们俩凑到了船首斜桅那里，感叹我们自身的处境。
“None can deliver us but the saints,” said I. “现在只有神才能救我们了。”我说道。
“My mind is very different,” said Ballantrae; “for I am going to deliver myself. “我不这么想，”巴伦特雷说道，“因为我打算要自救。
This Teach is the poorest creature possible; we make no profit of him, and lie continually open to capture; and,” says he, “I am not going to be a tarry pirate for nothing, nor yet to hang in chains if I can help it.” 蒂奇是造物主失败作品的极致，我们跟着他好不了，只能干等着被抓，还有，”他说，“我可不想白白当个半路出家的海盗，也不想被抓起来，我必须干点儿什么。”
And he told me what was in his mind to better the state of the ship in the way of discipline, which would give us safety for the present, and a sooner hope of deliverance when they should have gained enough and should break up their company. 然后他告诉我，他打算怎么整顿船上的规矩，这样才能在目前给我们创造一个安全的环境，然后等到他们弄到了足够的钱，该散伙回家的时候，我们就能早点儿摆脱现在的困境。
I confessed to him ingenuously that my nerve was quite shook amid these horrible surroundings, and I durst scarce tell him to count upon me. 我诚实地告诉他，我的神经在这种可怕的环境下已然不堪重负，让他就别指着我了。
“I am not very easy frightened,” said he, “nor very easy beat.” “我可不是这么容易被吓倒的，”他说道，“也没那么容易被打倒。”
A few days after, there befell an accident which had nearly hanged us all; and offers the most extraordinary picture of the folly that ruled in our concerns. 几天以后发生的一件事差点儿让我们所有人都送了命，这件事也直接反映了海盗船上管理失序的现状。
We were all pretty drunk: and some bedlamite spying a sail, Teach put the ship about in chase without a glance, and we began to bustle up the arms and boast of the horrors that should follow. 我们都喝醉了，有个疯子发现了一艘船，蒂奇连看都不看就喊追，我们就开始拿着武器，自吹自擂一场恐怖即将到来。
I observed Ballantrae stood quiet in the bows, looking under the shade of his hand; but for my part, true to my policy among these savages, I was at work with the busiest and passing Irish jests for their diversion. 我发现巴伦特雷此时一言不发地站在船首，手搭在额头上，仔细观瞧；我则继续遵循自己在这群野蛮人中的生存法则，忙着讲那些爱尔兰笑话哄他们开心。
“Run up the colours,” cries Teach. “把旗子给我打起来，”蒂奇喊道，
“Show the—s the Jolly Roger!” “把咱的旗子亮起来！”
It was the merest drunken braggadocio at such a stage, and might have lost us a valuable prize; but I thought it no part of mine to reason, and I ran up the black flag with my own hand. 在这种情况下，只有喝醉酒的人才会做这种打草惊蛇式的虚张声势，还有可能让到手的肥羊跑了，但我觉得我没法计较这些，于是亲手升起了海盗旗。
Ballantrae steps presently aft with a smile upon his face. 巴伦特雷带着微笑走上前来。
“You may perhaps like to know, you drunken dog,” says he, “that you are chasing a king’s ship.” “你可能会想知道，你这条醉狗，”他说道，“你在追的，是条官船。”
Teach roared him the lie; but he ran at the same time to the bulwarks, and so did they all. 蒂奇大声责怪他说谎，但他同时也跑到船舷边上张望，船上所有人都跟过去看。
I have never seen so many drunken men struck suddenly sober. 我从来没见过这么多醉汉齐齐清醒。
The cruiser had gone about, upon our impudent display of colours; she was just then filling on the new tack; her ensign blew out quite plain to see; and even as we stared, there came a puff of smoke, and then a report, and a shot plunged in the waves a good way short of us. 那官船本来都要走了，看到我们公然升起海盗旗，立刻改变了航向；人家船上的国旗一眼就能看清，就在我们盯着人家看的时候，那边船上冒起了一阵浓烟，接着一声炮响，炮弹就落在了离我们不远的海面上。
Some ran to the ropes, and got the SARAH round with an incredible swiftness. 有些人赶紧去拉缆绳，把萨拉号以不可思议的速度转了个方向。
One fellow fell on the rum barrel, which stood broached upon the deck, and rolled it promptly overboard. 有个人摔倒在甲板上的朗姆酒桶上，碰倒了酒桶，酒桶很快就滚到海里去了。
On my part, I made for the Jolly Roger, struck it, tossed it in the sea; and could have flung myself after, so vexed was I with our mismanagement. 旗子是我升起来的，自然也是我去扯下来，我把旗子往海里丢的时候自己差点儿就跟着掉海里去了，看到船上的混乱管理，我不由得怒火中烧。
As for Teach, he grew as pale as death, and incontinently went down to his cabin. 至于蒂奇，他面如死灰，跌跌撞撞地钻进了自己的船舱。
Only twice he came on deck that afternoon; went to the taffrail; took a long look at the king’s ship, which was still on the horizon heading after us; and then, without speech, back to his cabin. 他只在那天下午的时候到甲板上看过两回。他跑到船尾去看后面的官船，看到那船还在后面远远跟着，然后一言不发，又回了他的船舱。
You may say he deserted us; and if it had not been for one very capable sailor we had on board, and for the lightness of the airs that blew all day, we must certainly have gone to the yard-arm. 也可以说他在这么重要的时候抛弃了我们，要不是有个非常称职的水手，还有那天飘散了一整天的薄雾，我们现在肯定都已经镣铐加身了。
It is to be supposed Teach was humiliated, and perhaps alarmed for his position with the crew; and the way in which he set about regaining what he had lost, was highly characteristic of the man. 蒂奇肯定也知道自己丢了脸，而且这件事还有可能威胁到自己在船上的地位，不过他挽回地位的方式，跟他的性格一样无稽。
Early next day we smelled him burning sulphur in his cabin and crying out of “Hell, hell!” which was well understood among the crew, and filled their minds with apprehension. 转天上午，我们闻到他船舱里有烧焦的味道，还听见他喊着“见鬼去吧”。船员们都知道以蒂奇的性格，这就是什么事情即将发生的信号。
Presently he comes on deck, a perfect figure of fun, his face blacked, his hair and whiskers curled, his belt stuck full of pistols; chewing bits of glass so that the blood ran down his chin, and brandishing a dirk. 不一会儿，他就来到甲板上，跟个小丑一样，满脸乌黑，头发和胡须都烧卷了，腰上别满了手枪，嘴里嚼着玻璃碴子，结果鲜血顺着下巴往下滴，手上还挥着短刀。
I do not know if he had taken these manners from the Indians of America, where he was a native; but such was his way, and he would always thus announce that he was wound up to horrid deeds. 我不知道他这些习惯是不是源于他的印第安人出身，但他总叫嚣着要做出什么让人恐惧的事情来。
The first that came near him was the fellow who had sent the rum overboard the day before; him he stabbed to the heart, damning him for a mutineer; and then capered about the body, raving and swearing and daring us to come on. 第一个走近他的人是昨天把朗姆桶滚到海里去的那位，蒂奇直接把刀子捅进了他的心脏，说他是个背叛者，还玩弄他的尸体，喊着让我们都过去试试。
It was the silliest exhibition; and yet dangerous too, for the cowardly fellow was plainly working himself up to another murder. 这简直就是一场愚蠢的闹剧，同时也很危险，因为这个虚张声势的胆小鬼正在找他的下一个目标。
All of a sudden Ballantrae stepped forth. 突然间巴伦特雷走到了他面前。
“Have done with this play-acting,” says he. “你这戏也演得差不多了吧，”他说道，
“Do you think to frighten us with making faces? “你觉得就你那愚蠢样能吓着我们么？
We saw nothing of you yesterday, when you were wanted; and we did well without you, let me tell you that.” 昨天需要你的时候你不在，我告诉你，没你我们也弄得挺好。”
There was a murmur and a movement in the crew, of pleasure and alarm, I thought, in nearly equal parts. 船员们开始交头接耳，四下里开始有了动作，有高兴的，也有吓着的，我觉得，大部分人都兼有这两种情绪。
As for Teach, he gave a barbarous howl, and swung his dirk to fling it, an art in which (like many seamen) he was very expert. 至于蒂奇，他野蛮地怒吼着，挥刀就要来捅，（像很多水手一样）动刀子这种事他是把好手。
“Knock that out of his hand!” says Ballantrae, so sudden and sharp that my arm obeyed him before my mind had understood. “把他的刀子打掉！”巴伦特雷说道，我还没来得及思考，我的胳膊就直接服从了他的命令。
Teach stood like one stupid, never thinking on his pistols. 蒂奇跟个傻子似的站在那里，连自己还有枪这件事都不记得了。
“Go down to your cabin,” cries Ballantrae, “and come on deck again when you are sober. “滚回你的船舱吧，”巴伦特雷喊道，“等你酒醒了再上来吧。
Do you think we are going to hang for you, you black-faced, half-witted, drunken brute and butcher? 你觉得我们都得跟你一块上绞刑架吗？你这个黑脸的傻子，喝醉的畜生、屠夫！
Go down!” 滚下去吧！”
And he stamped his foot at him with such a sudden smartness that Teach fairly ran for it to the companion. 紧接着他又不失时机地对着那个家伙猛跺一脚，惊得蒂奇赶紧跑开了。
“And now, mates,” says Ballantrae, “a word with you. “那现在，伙计们，”巴伦特雷说道，“我有话要说。
I don’t know if you are gentlemen of fortune for the fun of the thing, but I am not. 我不知道你们是不是都腰缠万贯为了找乐子才来当海盗的，反正我不是。
I want to make money, and get ashore again, and spend it like a man. 我是想抢够了钱，回到陆地上，过人过的日子。
And on one thing my mind is made up: I will not hang if I can help it. 我下定决心，不想被抓起来，我必须干点儿什么。
Come: give me a hint; I’m only a beginner! 来啊！都给我表个态，我不过就是个发起者。
Is there no way to get a little discipline and common sense about this business?” 咱们就真不能定点儿咱们这行的规矩和常识么？”
One of the men spoke up: he said by rights they should have a quartermaster; and no sooner was the word out of his mouth than they were all of that opinion. 其中一个人发了言，说这船上得有一个大副。他的话音刚落，所有人就都响应了起来。
The thing went by acclamation, Ballantrae was made quartermaster, the rum was put in his charge, laws were passed in imitation of those of a pirate by the name of Roberts, and the last proposal was to make an end of Teach. 口头表决的结果是，由巴伦特雷来担任这个职务，船上的朗姆酒都归他管，效仿名海盗罗伯茨的法规也被表决通过，最后讨论的问题就是如何处死蒂奇。
But Ballantrae was afraid of a more efficient captain, who might be a counterweight to himself, and he opposed this stoutly. 不过巴伦特雷怕砍掉蒂奇之后会有更强的对手来跟他争抢，所以就坚决地反对。
Teach, he said, was good enough to board ships and frighten fools with his blacked face and swearing; we could scarce get a better man than Teach for that; and besides, as the man was now disconsidered and as good as deposed, we might reduce his proportion of the plunder. 他说蒂奇的黑脸与嘶吼在登船和吓唬人这两点上有着得天独厚的优势，再找这么个人也挺难的；另外，这个人如此不得人心就跟撤了职一样，可以减少他分赃的份额。
This carried it; Teach’s share was cut down to a mere derision, being actually less than mine; and there remained only two points: whether he would consent, and who was to announce to him this resolution. 这也通过了，蒂奇的份额被减到很少，比我的还少。然后就剩下两件事了：第一是他愿不愿意，第二是谁去和他讲这件事。
“Do not let that stick you,” says Ballantrae, “I will do that.” “你们就不用犯愁了，”巴伦特雷说道，“这件事就由我来办吧。”
And he stepped to the companion and down alone into the cabin to face that drunken savage. 他走过人群，独自一人下去船舱去见那个喝醉的野蛮人。
“This is the man for us,” cries one of the hands. “这才是我们的头儿，”人群中有人大喊，
“Three cheers for the quartermaster!” which were given with a will, my own voice among the loudest, and I dare say these plaudits had their effect on Master Teach in the cabin, as we have seen of late days how shouting in the streets may trouble even the minds of legislators. “让我们来三呼大副！”大家由衷地叫起来，我的呼声最高，我敢说，这欢呼声肯定给舱内的蒂奇带来了巨大的影响，就跟街头游行也能造成麻烦，甚至影响立法者的想法一样。
What passed precisely was never known, though some of the heads of it came to the surface later on; and we were all amazed, as well as gratified, when Ballantrae came on deck with Teach upon his arm, and announced that all had been consented. 虽然后面发生的一些事情能透露出一些端倪，但两人在舱内谈话的细节，别人就不得而知了。巴伦特雷和蒂奇手挽手回到甲板上宣布所有决议都通过的时候，大家都又惊又喜。
I pass swiftly over those twelve or fifteen months in which we continued to keep the sea in the North Atlantic, getting our food and water from the ships we over-hauled, and doing on the whole a pretty fortunate business. 我们在北大西洋徘徊了十二个或十五个月，吃的喝的全是抢来的，运气也一直不错。
Sure, no one could wish to read anything so ungenteel as the memoirs of a pirate, even an unwilling one like me! 当然，没有人愿意读海盗回忆录之类缺乏教养的东西，就算是我这个被迫当海盗的人也不会。
Things went extremely better with our designs, and Ballantrae kept his lead, to my admiration, from that day forth. 事情比我们设想的还要好，让我心生崇敬的是，自那以后，巴伦特雷一直保持了他头领的位置。
I would be tempted to suppose that a gentleman must everywhere be first, even aboard a rover: but my birth is every whit as good as any Scottish lord’s, and I am not ashamed to confess that I stayed Crowding Pat until the end, and was not much better than the crew’s buffoon. 我不禁想：一位人中龙凤，到哪里都能不同凡响。我的出身与任何苏格兰勋爵的身份不相上下，但我也就不为自己粉饰了，我直到最后都只是船上的起哄小鬼，在船员中一直扮演哄大家开心的跳梁小丑的角色。
Indeed, it was no scene to bring out my merits. 实际上，船上也并非我的用武之地。
My health suffered from a variety of reasons; I was more at home to the last on a horse’s back than a ship’s deck; and, to be ingenuous, the fear of the sea was constantly in my mind, battling with the fear of my companions. 我身体一直不好，因为甲板上不太适合我，战马上才是我纵横驰骋的地方；而且，实话实说，与其说我恐海，还不如说我怕我那些疯狂的海盗同伴们多一点儿。
I need not cry myself up for courage; I have done well on many fields under the eyes of famous generals, and earned my late advancement by an act of the most distinguished valour before many witnesses. 不是我给自己歌功颂德，以前我在很多有名的将军手下打过很多场仗，而且还因为勇猛而在众人面前得到提升。
But when we must proceed on one of our abordages, the heart of Francis Burke was in his boots; the little eggshell skiff in which we must set forth, the horrible heaving of the vast billows, the height of the ship that we must scale, the thought of how many might be there in garrison upon their legitimate defence, the scowling heavens which (in that climate) so often looked darkly down upon our exploits, and the mere crying of the wind in my ears, were all considerations most unpalatable to my valour. 可如今一到上船打劫的时候，我弗朗西斯·伯克立刻就变得胆小如鼠。我们的小船跟鸡蛋壳一般脆弱，一路上骇浪滔天，我们得爬上那些庞大的船只，那上面可能还有严阵以待的卫兵，再加上我们做那些伤天害理的事情时老天爷那讽刺的表情（我指的是天气），还有在耳边呼啸的狂风，这些都和我骁勇善战的英雄气概完全挨不着边。
Besides which, as I was always a creature of the nicest sensibility, the scenes that must follow on our success tempted me as little as the chances of defeat. 除此之外，我还是个非常敏感善良的人，因此无论打劫是成功还是失败，都无法让我高兴起来。
Twice we found women on board; and though I have seen towns sacked, and of late days in France some very horrid public tumults, there was something in the smallness of the numbers engaged, and the bleak dangerous sea-surroundings, that made these acts of piracy far the most revolting. 有两次我们打劫的船上发现了女人，尽管我曾目睹过城镇被洗劫一空，不久前还见到法国发生的骚乱，但毕竟参与的人数相对较少，而在求救无望的海上，海盗的行为就更加令人作呕。
I confess ingenuously I could never proceed unless I was three parts drunk; it was the same even with the crew; Teach himself was fit for no enterprise till he was full of rum; and it was one of the most difficult parts of Ballantrae’s performance, to serve us with liquor in the proper quantities. 我承认要是没醉到一定程度，我是不会参与他们的这些勾当的，别的人也多是如此。蒂奇不喝够他的朗姆酒就是个窝囊废，这让巴伦特雷的工作更加难以进行，那就是一方面给我们酒，一方面还得保证我们不喝醉。
Even this he did to admiration; being upon the whole the most capable man I ever met with, and the one of the most natural genius. 他真是让我崇拜，是我平生见过的最有能力的天才。
He did not even scrape favour with the crew, as I did, by continual buffoonery made upon a very anxious heart; but preserved on most occasions a great deal of gravity and distance; so that he was like a parent among a family of young children, or a schoolmaster with his boys. 他从不像我一样绞尽脑汁跟小丑似的博取船员的好感，而是始终稳健持重，和人保持着适当的距离，所以他在船员们中的位置就像一群孩子的父亲，或者一所学校的校长。
What made his part the harder to perform, the men were most inveterate grumblers; Ballantrae’s discipline, little as it was, was yet irksome to their love of licence; and what was worse, being kept sober they had time to think. 不过他也有难处，这伙人怨天尤人的习惯早就根深蒂固；巴伦特雷的那些法规自然也让他们很讨厌；而最大的难处就在于，由于他们有了更多清醒的时间，所以他们居然开始思考了。　
Some of them accordingly would fall to repenting their abominable crimes; one in particular, who was a good Catholic, and with whom I would sometimes steal apart for prayer; above all in bad weather, fogs, lashing rain and the like, when we would be the less observed; and I am sure no two criminals in the cart have ever performed their devotions with more anxious sincerity. 有些人就开始忏悔自己犯下的罪，其中有一个虔诚的天主教徒，经常和我躲到一起祈祷，大多在一些有雾或者下雨等天气不好的时候，这样别人就不怎么注意到我们了。我敢肯定再也没有哪两个罪犯能像我们一样迫不及待，虔诚地祈祷了。
But the rest, having no such grounds of hope, fell to another pastime, that of computation. 那些没有信仰的人就纷纷用算账的方式打发时间。
All day long they would he telling up their shares or grooming over the result. 一天到晚他们都在絮絮叨叨自己最后能分到多少不义之财。
I have said we were pretty fortunate. 我得说，这还真是一笔不小的数目。
But an observation fails to be made: that in this world, in no business that I have tried, do the profits rise to a man’s expectations. 但是我发现，这世界上，我做过的任何事从来没有一件能如愿以偿。
We found many ships and took many; yet few of them contained much money, their goods were usually nothing to our purpose—what did we want with a cargo of ploughs, or even of tobacco?—and it is quite a painful reflection how many whole crews we have made to walk the plank for no more than a stock of biscuit or an anker or two of spirit. 我们碰到很多目标，也抢了很多；大部分船上都没什么钱，船上的东西也大多是我们不想抢的——你说一船爬犁或者烟丝我们要来能干什么？——但最让人心痛的是，我们还是得为了一桶饼干或者几盏烈酒逼着一船船的海员跳海。
In the meanwhile our ship was growing very foul, and it was high time we should make for our PORT DE CARRENAGE, which was in the estuary of a river among swamps. 在这期间，我们的船已经变得破烂不堪，也该是时候靠岸了，在河流入海处的沼泽刚好有一个可以停泊的地方。
It was openly understood that we should then break up and go and squander our proportions of the spoil; and this made every man greedy of a little more, so that our decision was delayed from day to day. 大家都明白靠岸以后我们就可以分赃、散伙，各自回家了，这让所有人变得更加贪婪，结果使我们的靠岸时间一推再推。
What finally decided matters, was a trifling accident, such as an ignorant person might suppose incidental to our way of life. 最后让我们拿定主意的还是一件小事，在外人看来这件小事对海盗来说简直就是微不足道。
But here I must explain: on only one of all the ships we boarded, the first on which we found women, did we meet with any genuine resistance. 不过我得说明一下：我们抢的船里，只有在第一艘有女人的船上我们受到了像样的抵抗。
On that occasion we had two men killed and several injured, and if it had not been for the gallantry of Ballantrae we had surely been beat back at last. 那次我们死了两个人，还有几个受了伤，要不是巴伦特雷的勇猛，估计我们早就退败了。
Everywhere else the defence (where there was any at all) was what the worst troops in Europe would have laughed at; so that the most dangerous part of our employment was to clamber up the side of the ship; and I have even known the poor souls on board to cast us a line, so eager were they to volunteer instead of walking the plank. 其余的那些船上基本就没有防御可言，连欧洲最差强人意的兵士都可以对之进行嘲笑。其实对海盗来说，最危险的时刻就是爬船舷的瞬间，可是有些船居然主动放绳子下来让我们爬，他们以为这样我们就不会逼他们跳海了。
This constant immunity had made our fellows very soft, so that I understood how Teach had made so deep a mark upon their minds; for indeed the company of that lunatic was the chief danger in our way of life. 这些事开始让我旁边的伙计们多愁善感起来。也正是如此，我才能感受到当初蒂奇的疯狂留给他们精神上的烙印到底有多深。事实上，那个疯子的存在才是我们路上最大的危险。
The accident to which I have referred was this:- We had sighted a little full-rigged ship very close under our board in a haze; she sailed near as well as we did - I should be nearer truth if I said, near as ill; and we cleared the bow-chaser to see if we could bring a spar or two about their ears. 我提到的那件小事是这样的：我们看见一艘装备完整的小船离我们挺近；它离我们越来越近——后来我们才知道离这么近对我们双方都不是什么好事——我们架起炮，准备给他们耳边轰上两炮。
The swell was exceeding great; the motion of the ship beyond description; it was little wonder if our gunners should fire thrice and be still quite broad of what they aimed at. 浪头很大，船只晃动得厉害，简直难以形容。我们的炮手开了三炮，居然一炮也没有打中，这也不算奇怪。
But in the meanwhile the chase had cleared a stern gun, the thickness of the air concealing them; and being better marksmen, their first shot struck us in the bows, knocked our two gunners into mince-meat, so that we were all sprinkled with the blood, and plunged through the deck into the forecastle, where we slept. 不过在同时，对方也架起了炮，浓雾让我们视线不清；但对方的炮手明显更专业一点儿，第一炮就打中我们的船首，并把我们的两个炮手炸成了肉片，我们全身上下都沾满鲜血，赶紧钻进平常睡觉的舱内。
Ballantrae would have held on; indeed, there was nothing in this CONTRETEMPS to affect the mind of any soldier; but he had a quick perception of the men’s wishes, and it was plain this lucky shot had given them a sickener of their trade. 巴伦特雷本来是要顶住的，而实际上，这种意外对任何士兵来说都不算什么。不过他看了一下船上所有人的情况，立刻就明白众人心中的共同想法，最幸运的是，那一炮把海盗的饭碗砸了。
In a moment they were all of one mind: the chase was drawing away from us, it was needless to hold on, the SARAH was too foul to overhaul a bottle, it was mere foolery to keep the sea with her; and on these pretended grounds her head was incontinently put about and the course laid for the river. 那一刻我们同心同德：目标船已经开远了，再追根本就没有意义，而且萨拉号现在破得连个瓶子都追不着，不适合再与海为伴了；这些个理由终于让我们的船改道朝河口的停泊点驶去。
It was strange to see what merriment fell on that ship’s company, and how they stamped about the deck jesting, and each computing what increase had come to his share by the death of the two gunners. 欢乐诡异地降临在了这艘海盗船上，海盗们在甲板上又唱又跳，心里都在盘算，死去了两个炮手后，自己的分成会增加多少。
We were nine days making our port, so light were the airs we had to sail on, so foul the ship’s bottom; but early on the tenth, before dawn, and in a light lifting haze, we passed the head. 由于风力太弱，船底又太破，我们花了九天时间才到达停泊的地点。第十天凌晨，我们在晨曦和薄雾之中到达了目的地。
A little after, the haze lifted, and fell again, showing us a cruiser very close. 过了一会儿，雾起了又落，在那期间，我们注意到有一艘巡洋舰离我们很近。
This was a sore blow, happening so near our refuge. 在我们就快获得解脱的时候遇到这种事情，真是一个不小的打击。
There was a great debate of whether she had seen us, and if so whether it was likely they had recognised the SARAH. 大家开始争辩它是否留意到了我们这件事，是否认出我们萨拉号了。
We were very careful, by destroying every member of those crews we overhauled, to leave no evidence as to our own persons; but the appearance of the SARAH herself we could not keep so private; and above all of late, since she had been foul, and we had pursued many ships without success, it was plain that her description had been often published. 我们已经很小心了，每抢一艘船，一个活口都不留，一点儿指向我们的证据都没留。但是萨拉号的外观我们没法保密，船本身就破，而且我们还有好多想抢的船没追上，所以估计萨拉号的外观早就被那些水手们传得沸沸扬扬了。
I supposed this alert would have made us separate upon the instant. 我还以为这么一吓，大家会马上散伙分家，各谋出路。
But here again that original genius of Ballantrae’s had a surprise in store for me. 结果巴伦特雷那个天才又给我露了一手。
He and Teach (and it was the most remarkable step of his success) had gone hand in hand since the first day of his appointment. 他和蒂奇在他就任海盗头子的那天曾经手牵手出现在甲板上（这也是他成功的最重要的一步）。
I often questioned him upon the fact, and never got an answer but once, when he told me he and Teach had an understanding “which would very much surprise the crew if they should hear of it, and would surprise himself a good deal if it was carried out.” 我经常问他关于这件事的真相，从来没有得到过直接的答案，除了有一次，他说：“要是别的海盗知道我和蒂奇之间的事一定会大吃一惊，要是他们的计划能成功连他自己都觉得惊讶。”
Well, here again he and Teach were of a mind; and by their joint procurement the anchor was no sooner down than the whole crew went off upon a scene of drunkenness indescribable. 这会儿，他和蒂奇又演起了好兄弟，他们俩一起平息了船上不安的情绪，以至于船一抛锚，所有人又都不可思议地开始饮酒作乐。
By afternoon we were a mere shipful of lunatical persons, throwing of things overboard, howling of different songs at the same time, quarrelling and falling together, and then forgetting our quarrels to embrace. 到下午的时候，满船都是醉鬼，有向船外乱扔东西的，有大声唱歌的，还有争执吵架的，反正都把之前的争论抛诸脑后，转而拥抱在一起了。
Ballantrae had bidden me drink nothing, and feign drunkenness, as I valued my life; and I have never passed a day so wearisomely, lying the best part of the time upon the forecastle and watching the swamps and thickets by which our little basin was entirely surrounded for the eye. 巴伦特雷提前嘱咐过我想要命的话，什么也不要喝，装醉即可。对我来说，那是有生以来最无聊的一天，把一天最好的时间都用来躺在舱内看周围的沼泽和蓊郁葳蕤的灌木丛。
A little after dusk Ballantrae stumbled up to my side, feigned to fall, with a drunken laugh, and before he got his feet again, whispered me to “reel down into the cabin and seem to fall asleep upon a locker, for there would be need of me soon.” 天擦黑的时候，巴伦特雷装作醉醺醺的样子晃晃悠悠地走到我身边，假装摔倒，然后在站起来的一刻凑到我耳边轻声说：“钻船舱里去找个隔间装睡，一会儿我还有其他事要做。”
I did as I was told, and coming into the cabin, where it was quite dark, let myself fall on the first locker. 我照他说的做了，钻进一个小隔间，那里太黑了，结果我摔在了别人身上。
There was a man there already; by the way he stirred and threw me off, I could not think he was much in liquor; and yet when I had found another place, he seemed to continue to sleep on. 那里已经有个人了，他烦躁地把我推开，从他推我的方式来看，我觉得他并没有喝得很醉，但等我换到旁边躺下的时候，他看上去像是继续睡了。
My heart now beat very hard, for I saw some desperate matter was in act. 我心跳得厉害，觉得有什么大事一触即发。
Presently down came Ballantrae, lit the lamp, looked about the cabin, nodded as if pleased, and on deck again without a word. 过了一会儿，巴伦特雷提着灯走了下来，看了看船舱，满意地点了点头，一句话没说又回到了甲板上。
I peered out from between my fingers, and saw there were three of us slumbering, or feigning to slumber, on the lockers: myself, one Dutton and one Grady, both resolute men. 我从手指尖的缝隙瞥见了这些，还看见这橱柜上一共有三个人在睡觉，或者在装睡，这三个人分别是我自己、达顿和格雷迪，都是意志坚定的汉子。
On deck the rest were got to a pitch of revelry quite beyond the bounds of what is human; so that no reasonable name can describe the sounds they were now making. 甲板上的喧闹已经超过了人类所能创造的极限，那种声音已经不能用语言去形容。
I have heard many a drunken bout in my time, many on board that very SARAH, but never anything the least like this, which made me early suppose the liquor had been tampered with. 萨拉号上的喝酒作乐我见过很多次，没有哪一次像这回一样，让我不得不怀疑酒里是不是下了什么药。
It was a long while before these yells and howls died out into a sort of miserable moaning, and then to silence; and it seemed a long while after that before Ballantrae came down again, this time with Teach upon his heels. 过了很久，这些叫喊声渐渐淡了下来，变成了悲切的呜咽，然后就完全安静下来。又过了很久，巴伦特雷从甲板上下来，后面还跟着蒂奇。
The latter cursed at the sight of us three upon the lockers. 蒂奇看到我们三个在小隔间里躺着，不由得叫骂了几声。
“Tut,” says Ballantrae, “you might fire a pistol at their ears. “闭嘴，”巴伦特雷说，“你朝他们放一枪都弄不醒他们。
You know what stuff they have been swallowing.” 你又不是不知道他们都喝了什么。”
There was a hatch in the cabin floor, and under that the richest part of the booty was stored against the day of division. 船舱地板下面有一个暗格，存着赃物里最有价值的财宝，准备分赃那天再打开。
It fastened with a ring and three padlocks, the keys (for greater security) being divided; one to Teach, one to Ballantrae, and one to the mate, a man called Hammond. 门上有个环，还有三把锁，为了保险起见，钥匙分别在蒂奇、巴伦特雷和哈蒙德手里。
Yet I was amazed to see they were now all in the one hand; and yet more amazed (still looking through my fingers) to observe Ballantrae and Teach bring up several packets, four of them in all, very carefully made up and with a loop for carriage. 我惊讶地发现这三把钥匙现在都到了巴伦特雷的手里，更惊讶的是（从我的指缝看到的）巴伦特雷和蒂奇提着四个袋子，好像是精心准备好的，上面还有环状的提手。
“And now,” says Teach, “let us be going.” “那现在，”蒂奇说，“让我们开始吧。”
“One word,” says Ballantrae. “总之一句话，”巴伦特雷说道，
“I have discovered there is another man besides yourself who knows a private path across the swamp; and it seems it is shorter than yours.” “我发现，除你之外，还有人知道穿越沼泽的秘密路径，而且他的那条路似乎还比你的那条短。”
Teach cried out, in that case, they were undone. 蒂奇大惊，因为如果这是真的，他和巴伦特雷的秘密协定就算完了。
“I do not know for that,” says Ballantrae. “具体的我不清楚，”巴伦特雷说道，
“For there are several other circumstances with which I must acquaint you. “不过我倒是还有几件事要告诉你。
First of all, there is no bullet in your pistols, which (if you remember) I was kind enough to load for both of us this morning. 一.（你还记得吧）今天早上我给咱俩手枪都上了子弹，但我其实没给你上。
Secondly, as there is someone else who knows a passage, you must think it highly improbable I should saddle myself with a lunatic like you. 二.如果还有别人知道出去的路径，那么跟你这个疯子做伴就完全没有必要了。
Thirdly, these gentlemen (who need no longer pretend to be asleep) are those of my party, and will now proceed to gag and bind you to the mast; and when your men awaken (if they ever do awake after the drugs we have mingled in their liquor), I am sure they will be so obliging as to deliver you, and you will have no difficulty, I daresay, to explain the business of the keys.” 三.装睡的先生们（你们都不用再装了）都是我的人，他们马上就会来封上你的嘴然后把你绑在桅杆上，等你的人酒醒后（酒里下了毒，如果他们还能醒过来的话），他们一定会负责把你放下来的，然后你就可以毫无困难地跟他们解释解释钥匙的事了。”
Not a word said Teach, but looked at us like a frightened baby as we gagged and bound him. 蒂奇哑口无言，任凭我们绑住他封上他的嘴，跟个吓傻的孩子似的。
“Now you see, you moon-calf,” says Ballantrae, “why we made four packets. “现在你明白了吧，你这个疯子，”巴伦特雷说道，“你明白为什么我要做四个袋子了吧。
Heretofore you have been called Captain Teach, but I think you are now rather Captain Learn.” 以前人家叫你蒂奇船长，现在人家得叫你‘没脑子’船长了。”
That was our last word on board the SARAH. 那就是我们在萨拉号上留下的最后一句话。
We four, with our four packets, lowered ourselves softly into a skiff, and left that ship behind us as silent as the grave, only for the moaning of some of the drunkards. 我们四个带着四个袋子，无声无息地登上了小船，把大船抛在了后面，除了远远传来的几声醉汉的呻吟，那大船静得像墓地一般。
There was a fog about breast-high on the waters; so that Dutton, who knew the passage, must stand on his feet to direct our rowing; and this, as it forced us to row gently, was the means of our deliverance. 水面上是齐胸高的雾气，知道路的达顿得站直了身子才能给我们指路，我们得轻轻划桨才能避人耳目。
We were yet but a little way from the ship, when it began to come grey, and the birds to fly abroad upon the water. 离开大船没多久，天色转灰，鸟儿在水面上盘旋不止。
All of a sudden Dutton clapped down upon his hams, and whispered us to be silent for our lives, and hearken. 突然，达顿拍了下大腿，小声嘱咐我们安静，让他仔细听听周围的声音。
Sure enough, we heard a little faint creak of oars upon one hand, and then again, and further off, a creak of oars upon the other. 然后，我们就听到了一边传来划桨的声音，接着，另一边传来了同样的声音。
It was clear we had been sighted yesterday in the morning; here were the cruiser’s boats to cut us out; here were we defenceless in their very midst. 昨天早上，我们肯定被人发现了，那巡洋舰发了好几条小船对我们进行围追堵截，我们只得被围在中间束手待擒。
Sure, never were poor souls more perilously placed; and as we lay there on our oars, praying God the mist might hold, the sweat poured from my brow. 真是屋漏偏逢连夜雨，我只能祈祷上帝别让浓雾散去，我的额头上已经汗如雨下。
Presently we heard one of the boats where we might have thrown a biscuit in her. 不久，我们听到有条船离我们很近，近得简直可以把饼干扔到那条船上。
“Softly, men,” we heard an officer whisper; and I marvelled they could not hear the drumming of my heart. “轻点儿，伙计们。”我听到一个长官轻声地说道，我很惊讶他们竟然没听到我剧烈的心跳声。
“Never mind the path,” says Ballantrae; “we must get shelter anyhow; let us pull straight ahead for the sides of the basin.” “别管什么路不路的了，”巴伦特雷说，“咱们必须赶紧先藏起来，先划到对岸去。”
This we did with the most anxious precaution, rowing, as best we could, upon our hands, and steering at a venture in the fog, which was (for all that) our only safety. 我们小心翼翼地划着船，大雾是我们唯一的掩护屏障。
But Heaven guided us; we touched ground at a thicket; scrambled ashore with our treasure; and having no other way of concealment, and the mist beginning already to lighten, hove down the skiff and let her sink. 上帝指引着我们，我们踉踉跄跄地背着财宝在一片灌木丛旁登了岸。此时，雾开始散了，为了掩盖行踪，我们只得把小舟沉了。
We were still but new under cover when the sun rose; and at the same time, from the midst of the basin, a great shouting of seamen sprang up, and we knew the SARAH was being boarded. 我们刚刚藏好，太阳就升起来了。这时，大船上传来了喧哗声，我们都知道警官们登上了萨拉号。
I heard afterwards the officer that took her got great honour; and it’s true the approach was creditably managed, but I think he had an easy capture when he came to board. [2] 后来我听说登上萨拉号的警官立了大功，我们觉得他找到萨拉号确实挺不容易的，但在登船上肯定没费什么劲。[2]
I was still blessing the saints for my escape, when I became aware we were in trouble of another kind. 我还在为成功脱逃而感谢上苍，但却马上发现我们正面临着另一个麻烦。
We were here landed at random in a vast and dangerous swamp; and how to come at the path was a concern of doubt, fatigue, and peril. 由于匆忙，我们随便找了一处广阔却危机丛生的沼泽地登陆，让人疲惫和绝望的是，我们都不清楚怎样才能找到秘密通道。
Dutton, indeed, was of opinion we should wait until the ship was gone, and fish up the skiff; for any delay would be more wise than to go blindly ahead in that morass. 实际上,达顿的意思是我们在这里等候，直到官船开走，再把小舟打捞上来；等着总比在情况完全不熟悉的沼泽地里瞎撞好些。
One went back accordingly to the basin-side and (peering through the thicket) saw the fog already quite drunk up, and English colours flying on the SARAH, but no movement made to get her under way. 我们中的一个人跑到岸边透过灌木丛去探查情况，看到大雾快要散完了，萨拉号上飘着英国国旗，根本没有要开走的迹象。
Our situation was now very doubtful. 我们现在的处境令人担忧。
The swamp was an unhealthful place to linger in; we had been so greedy to bring treasures that we had brought but little food; it was highly desirable, besides, that we should get clear of the neighbourhood and into the settlements before the news of the capture went abroad; and against all these considerations, there was only the peril of the passage on the other side. 沼泽地绝对不是人该呆的地方，我们出来时都只顾着拿财宝，食物带得很少，现在最好是趁着风声还没有传出去赶紧离开这里找个地方安顿下来。最主要的是，我们也不知道对岸那条秘密通道到底是不是安全。
I think it not wonderful we decided on the active part. 我认为我们最终采取的主动方法是很不明智的。
It was already blistering hot when we set forth to pass the marsh, or rather to strike the path, by compass. 我们准备穿越沼泽地的时候，天已经酷热难当了。准确地说，我们是靠着指南针在开辟一条道路。
Dutton took the compass, and one or other of us three carried his proportion of the treasure. 达顿看着指南针，剩下的三个人轮流替他背着财宝。
I promise you he kept a sharp eye to his rear, for it was like the man’s soul that he must trust us with. 我向你保证，他一直机敏地看着后面，就好像他把灵魂交给了我们一样。
The thicket was as close as a bush; the ground very treacherous, so that we often sank in the most terrifying manner, and must go round about; the heat, besides, was stifling, the air singularly heavy, and the stinging insects abounded in such myriads that each of us walked under his own cloud. 灌木密得跟堵墙似的，地面上危机四伏，我们经常陷进危险的泥潭里，只能尽量绕过去。空气燥热得令人窒息，蚊虫铺天盖地，每个人头上都笼罩着沉闷的情绪。
It has often been commented on, how much better gentlemen of birth endure fatigue than persons of the rabble; so that walking officers who must tramp in the dirt beside their men, shame them by their constancy. 经常有人说，那些出身高贵的绅士比那些出身贫贱的愚夫更能吃苦，所以很多长官跟他的士兵同甘苦共患难，用自己的坚忍来感召他们的兵士。
This was well to be observed in the present instance; for here were Ballantrae and I, two gentlemen of the highest breeding, on the one hand; and on the other, Grady, a common mariner, and a man nearly a giant in physical strength. 这正是当前场景的写照：一方面，巴伦特雷和我是出身高贵的绅士，另一方面格雷迪是个普通的水手，还有一个体力超强的男人一同跋涉在泥泞的沼泽中。
The case of Dutton is not in point, for I confess he did as well as any of us. [3] 达顿还好，他和我们一样坚忍。
But as for Grady, he began early to lament his case, tailed in the rear, refused to carry Dutton’s packet when it came his turn, clamoured continually for rum (of which we had too little), and at last even threatened us from behind with a cooked pistol, unless we should allow him rest. 不过格雷迪则早就开始自怨自艾，走着走着就落在队伍后面，轮到他背达顿的财宝时出声拒绝，一直要我们所剩不多的朗姆酒，最后还用上了膛的枪逼着我们允许他停下来休息。
Ballantrae would have fought it out, I believe; but I prevailed with him the other way; and we made a stop and ate a meal. 我相信巴伦特雷本来是要跟他大干一场的，不过我劝他不要那样，大家还是停下来吃点儿东西比较好。
It seemed to benefit Grady little; he was in the rear again at once, growling and bemoaning his lot; and at last, by some carelessness, not having followed properly in our tracks, stumbled into a deep part of the slough where it was mostly water, gave some very dreadful screams, and before we could come to his aid had sunk along with his booty. 不过休息对格雷迪来说收效甚微，他马上又落到队伍的后面，继续他的抱怨，最后由于粗心大意、没有跟紧我们的步伐，他一不小心踩进了泥潭，发出令人毛骨悚然的叫喊，由于他落下太远，我们赶到的时候，他已经和他的财宝一起葬身沼泽了。
His fate, and above all these screams of his, appalled us to the soul; yet it was on the whole a fortunate circumstance and the means of our deliverance, for it moved Dutton to mount into a tree, whence he was able to perceive and to show me, who had climbed after him, a high piece of the wood, which was a landmark for the path. 他的死加上他死前的惨叫把我们都吓坏了，不过对我们全队来说倒是减轻了负担，这未尝不是件好事。随后达顿爬上一棵大树，我跟在他后面爬了上去，他伸手把标示路径的木牌子指给我看。
He went forward the more carelessly, I must suppose; for presently we saw him sink a little down, draw up his feet and sink again, and so twice. 我肯定他在前面走得更加粗心大意，因为不一会儿，我们看到他自己也踩到了泥潭，刚抽出一只脚就又陷了下去，那么来回了两次。
Then he turned his face to us, pretty white. 他把脸转向我们，面色苍白。
“Lend a hand,” said he, “I am in a bad place.” “拉我一把，”他说道，“我陷进去了。”
“I don’t know about that,” says Ballantrae, standing still. “我还真没看出来。”巴伦特雷说着，居然站着没动。
Dutton broke out into the most violent oaths, sinking a little lower as he did, so that the mud was nearly to his waist, and plucking a pistol from his belt, “Help me,” he cries, “or die and be damned to you!” 达顿一下就急了，大声地叫骂着，又陷下去一点儿，很快泥就没了腰间，他抽出手枪喊道：“帮帮我，要不咱们就同归于尽吧！”
“Nay,” says Ballantrae, “I did but jest. “别别别，”巴伦特拉说道，“我就开个玩笑。
I am coming.” 我马上就来。”
And he set down his own packet and Dutton’s, which he was then carrying. 他放下背着的自己和达顿的财宝。
“Do not venture near till we see if you are needed,” said he to me, and went forward alone to where the man was bogged. “我不叫你，你千万别过来。”巴伦特雷对我说着，然后自己走向了达顿陷进去的那个泥潭。
He was quiet now, though he still held the pistol; and the marks of terror in his countenance were very moving to behold. 达顿一声不发，依旧举着他的枪，脸上的表情很吓人。
“For the Lord’s sake,” says he, “look sharp.” “看在上帝的份上，”他说道，“你给我快点儿。”
Ballantrae was now got close up. 巴伦特雷这会儿已经走近他的身边。
“Keep still,” says he, and seemed to consider; and then, “Reach out both your hands!” “别动，”他说道，然后想了一下，接着说，“把双手都伸过来！”
Dutton laid down his pistol, and so watery was the top surface that it went clear out of sight; with an oath he stooped to snatch it; and as he did so, Ballantrae leaned forth and stabbed him between the shoulders. 达顿放下手枪，沼泽上全是水，手枪一下就没了踪影，他骂了一声赶紧去拣，就在这时候，巴伦特雷一步上前把刀插进了他的脖子里。
Up went his hands over his head—I know not whether with the pain or to ward himself; and the next moment he doubled forward in the mud. 达顿高举双手——我也不知道是过于痛苦还是出于本能的自卫，然后他就向前扑倒在泥潭里。
Ballantrae was already over the ankles; but he plucked himself out, and came back to me, where I stood with my knees smiting one another. 巴伦特雷的脚也陷在泥淖里，不过他自己就能把脚抽出来，走回我身边，我吓得两腿发颤。
“The devil take you, Francis!” says he. “见你妈的鬼，弗朗西斯！”他说道，
“I believe you are a half-hearted fellow, after all. “我看你根本就是个半调子。
I have only done justice on a pirate. 我只不过是砍了个海盗伸张正义而已。
And here we are quite clear of the SARAH! 现在我们跟萨拉号一点儿关系也没有了。
Who shall now say that we have dipped our hands in any irregularities?” 现在谁还知道我们曾经干过那些违法的勾当？”
I assured him he did me injustice; but my sense of humanity was so much affected by the horridness of the fact that I could scarce find breath to answer with. 我确定他是冤枉了我，但是我还有人性，事发突然又过于恐怖，我根本就没有多余的力气回答他。
“Come,” said he, “you must be more resolved. “来吧，”他说道，“你必须得果断一些。
The need for this fellow ceased when he had shown you where the path ran; and you cannot deny I would have been daft to let slip so fair an opportunity.” 这个人把路指给我们以后就没什么用了，你也知道，那么好的机会，我要是放过就太愚蠢了。”
I could not deny but he was right in principle; nor yet could I refrain from shedding tears, of which I think no man of valour need have been ashamed; and it was not until I had a share of the rum that I was able to proceed. 我不能否认他在原则上是对的，但也禁不住落泪，我觉得再勇猛的人也不该为自己在这时候落泪而感到难为情，我不得不给自己灌了几口酒才能勉强上路。
I repeat, I am far from ashamed of my generous emotion; mercy is honourable in the warrior; and yet I cannot altogether censure Ballantrae, whose step was really fortunate, as we struck the path without further misadventure, and the same night, about sundown, came to the edge of the morass. 我再重复一遍，我一点儿也不为自己动了感情而感到害臊，勇士最大的美德就是仁慈，但同时我也不能完全指责巴伦特雷，他走的每一步都运气十足，我们没费多大劲就上了小路，同一天夜里，我们接近了沼泽地的边缘。
We were too weary to seek far; on some dry sands, still warm with the day’s sun, and close under a wood of pines, we lay down and were instantly plunged in sleep. 我们累得再也走不动了；在一棵松树下，我们躺在还留有太阳余温的干燥沙地上，倒头便睡。
We awaked the next morning very early, and began with a sullen spirit a conversation that came near to end in blows. 第二天，我们起得很早，交谈时两人都心情不佳，差点儿没吵起来。
We were now cast on shore in the southern provinces, thousands of miles from any French settlement; a dreadful journey and a thousand perils lay in front of us; and sure, if there was ever need for amity, it was in such an hour. 我们现在在南方诸省的海边，离法国殖民地还有千里之遥，前方道路危机四伏，如果说有什么时候最需要同伴间的和睦相处，那绝对是现在。
I must suppose that Ballantrae had suffered in his sense of what is truly polite; indeed, and there is nothing strange in the idea, after the sea-wolves we had consorted with so long; and as for myself, he fubbed me off unhandsomely, and any gentleman would have resented his behaviour. 我只能认为巴伦特雷现在对自己的教养产生了强烈的质疑。实际上，我的想法一点儿也不古怪，跟一群海盗共度了这么长时间哪可能一点儿也不受影响呢？至于他对待我的那种缺乏善意的方式，我想任何有身份的人都会为我鸣不平的。
I told him in what light I saw his conduct; he walked a little off, I following to upbraid him; and at last he stopped me with his hand. 我对他讲了我对他行为的看法，他走开了一点儿，我跟过去责备他，最后他用手制止了我。
“Frank,” says he, “you know what we swore; and yet there is no oath invented would induce me to swallow such expressions, if I did not regard you with sincere affection. “弗兰克，”他说道，“你当然知道我们曾经发下的誓言，我要是不真心待你，我随时可以食言，哪管什么誓言。
It is impossible you should doubt me there: I have given proofs. 你根本没立场怀疑我，我早就给了你证据。
Dutton I had to take, because he knew the pass, and Grady because Dutton would not move without him; but what call was there to carry you along? 达顿我必须带着，因为他知道路，没有格雷迪，达顿又不肯跟我走，我也只能带着他，但是你告诉我有什么理由让我必须带着你呢？
You are a perpetual danger to me with your cursed Irish tongue. 你那该死的爱尔兰腔一直都让我担心得要死。
By rights you should now be in irons in the cruiser. 真该让你现在披枷带锁地呆在官船里。
And you quarrel with me like a baby for some trinkets!” 省得你现在就为了一点儿珠宝跟我吵架！”
I considered this one of the most unhandsome speeches ever made; and indeed to this day I can scarce reconcile it to my notion of a gentleman that was my friend. 我觉得这可以算是有生以来最没涵养的争吵了，实际上直到今天，我都觉得这话不该出自一位绅士、一位朋友之口。
I retorted upon him with his Scotch accent, of which he had not so much as some, but enough to be very barbarous and disgusting, as I told him plainly; and the affair would have gone to a great length, but for an alarming intervention. 我讥讽他的苏格兰腔，尽管他的口音不怎么重，不过我还是明白地告诉他，他的口音土里土气缺乏教养。但我们的争吵还没进一步升级，就被一个突发事件打断了。
We had got some way off upon the sand. 我们吵到了沙滩上。
The place where we had slept, with the packets lying undone and the money scattered openly, was now between us and the pines; and it was out of these the stranger must have come. 争吵的地点和昨天睡觉的地点有一段距离，装财宝的袋子大敞四开地放在我们和松树之间的地上，吸引了不速之客的眼球。
There he was at least, a great hulking fellow of the country, with a broad axe on his shoulder, looking open-mouthed, now at the treasure, which was just at his feet, and now at our disputation, in which we had gone far enough to have weapons in our hands. 那是一个身形粗壮的农家汉子，肩上扛着一柄大斧头，张大了嘴惊讶地看着自己脚边的财宝，那时候我们吵得已经亮出了各自的武器。
We had no sooner observed him than he found his legs and made off again among the pines. 我们一看到他，他就闪身进了松树林。
This was no scene to put our minds at rest: a couple of armed men in sea-clothes found quarrelling over a treasure, not many miles from where a pirate had been captured—here was enough to bring the whole country about our ears. 这下我们脑子里只剩下一个场景：两个带着武器穿着水手行头的人为了一笔财宝大肆争吵，几英里外，刚有一伙海盗被捕——这些已经足够让我们成为众矢之的了。
The quarrel was not even made up; it was blotted from our minds; and we got our packets together in the twinkling of an eye, and made off, running with the best will in the world. 争吵甚至还没出结果，我们马上就把它抛诸脑后了，眨眼间收拾好东西，赶紧跑路，心中只能期待所有好事都发生在自己头上。
But the trouble was, we did not know in what direction, and must continually return upon our steps. 但问题是，我们根本不知道朝哪个方向走，老是走回头路。
Ballantrae had indeed collected what he could from Dutton; but it’s hard to travel upon hearsay; and the estuary, which spreads into a vast irregular harbour, turned us off upon every side with a new stretch of water. 巴伦特雷从达顿那里已经把能知道的都知道了，但是走路光靠听说是不行的，整个河口是一个不规则的海湾，我们往哪个方向走都会遇到水。
We were near beside ourselves, and already quite spent with running, when, coming to the top of a dune, we saw we were again cut off by another ramification of the bay. 我们俩人已经接近极限，一直在狂奔，等我们到了一个沙丘顶部的时候，我们发现自己又被另一个海湾的支流拦住了去路。
This was a creek, however, very different from those that had arrested us before; being set in rocks, and so precipitously deep that a small vessel was able to lie alongside, made fast with a hawser; and her crew had laid a plank to the shore. 这个海湾比较狭窄，跟之前困住我们的那个完全不同，岩石环绕，十分陡峭深邃，一条小船被拴在岸边，小船和岸中间放了一块木板方便行走。
Here they had lighted a fire, and were sitting at their meal. 船员们升起一堆火，正在吃饭。
As for the vessel herself, she was one of those they build in the Bermudas. 那小船是那种百慕大地区的样式。
The love of gold and the great hatred that everybody has to pirates were motives of the most influential, and would certainly raise the country in our pursuit. 世人对于金钱的爱和对海盗的恨足以成为一种巨大的力量，这绝对可以让整个地区的人都想抓住我们。
Besides, it was now plain we were on some sort of straggling peninsula, like the fingers of a hand; and the wrist, or passage to the mainland, which we should have taken at the first, was by this time not improbably secured. 此外，现在我们在一个偏远的半岛上，半岛就像手指，而手腕，即通往内陆的路径已经被我们错过去了，而且现在那条路上应该也是追兵密布。
These considerations put us on a bolder counsel. 对此，我们只能采取更铤而走险的办法。
For as long as we dared, looking every moment to hear sounds of the chase, we lay among some bushes on the top of the dune; and having by this means secured a little breath and recomposed our appearance, we strolled down at last, with a great affectation of carelessness, to the party by the fire. 我们呆了一会儿，时刻注意听周围有没有追兵的声音，躺在沙丘顶的灌木丛里喘了口气，整理了一下衣服，装作一副若无其事的样子走了下去，凑到了那些船员的火堆旁。
It was a trader and his negroes, belonging to Albany, in the province of New York, and now on the way home from the Indies with a cargo; his name I cannot recall. 船上是一个商人和他的黑奴，他来自美国纽约州的奥尔巴尼，从东印度群岛运货回国，现在正在回程路上，商人的名字我记不清了。
We were amazed to learn he had put in here from terror of the SARAH; for we had no thought our exploits had been so notorious. 我们很惊讶地听说他停在这里是因为害怕萨拉号上的海盗，我们还从来不知道自己这么有名。
As soon as the Albanian heard she had been taken the day before, he jumped to his feet, gave us a cup of spirits for our good news, and sent big negroes to get sail on the Bermudan. 奥尔巴尼人一听我们说前天萨拉号被荡平的消息，高兴得差点儿没跳起来，还特意分给我们一杯酒来感谢我们带来这个好消息，然后告诉他的黑奴，准备起航。
On our side, we profited by the dram to become more confidential, and at last offered ourselves as passengers. 对我们而言，这个消息使我们更加可信，然后就告诉他我们想搭他的船。
He looked askance at our tarry clothes and pistols, and replied civilly enough that he had scarce accommodation for himself; nor could either our prayers or our offers of money, in which we advanced pretty far, avail to shake him. 他怀疑地看了看我们乱七八糟的衣着和腰间别着的手枪，非常礼貌地拒绝了我们，说船上空间有限。我们请求他，还用大笔的钱吸引他，均不奏效。
“I see, you think ill of us,” says Ballantrae, “but I will show you how well we think of you by telling you the truth. “我知道了，你觉得我们不是善茬儿，”巴伦特雷说道，“但我想告诉您实话来证明我们的诚实。
We are Jacobite fugitives, and there is a price upon our heads.” 我们是拥护詹姆士二世的起义军，正在被悬赏捉拿。”
At this, the Albanian was plainly moved a little. 听到这，奥尔巴尼人在态度上明显有些松动。
He asked us many questions as to the Scotch war, which Ballantrae very patiently answered. 他问了很多关于爱尔兰战争的事情，巴伦特雷都为他一一解答了。
And then, with a wink, in a vulgar manner, “I guess you and your Prince Charlie got more than you cared about,” said he. 随后，他眨了下眼，用一种很粗鲁的语气说道：“我猜你们和你们的王子一定弄到了很多你们自己都没想要的东西。”
“Bedad, and that we did,” said I. “哎呀，那是自然，”我说道，
“And, my dear man, I wish you would set a new example and give us just that much.” “那，我亲爱的先生，我希望你们也得像样地给我点儿什么才行。”
This I said in the Irish way, about which there is allowed to be something very engaging. 我用我那种爱尔兰腔说的这句话，这时候说这种逗趣的话非常应景。
It’s a remarkable thing, and a testimony to the love with which our nation is regarded, that this address scarce ever fails in a handsome fellow. 在我的国家，这种话是在表现亲密，在体面人面前说这种话一般也是有求必应。
I cannot tell how often I have seen a private soldier escape the horse, or a beggar wheedle out a good alms by a touch of the brogue. 我无数次见过开小差的雇佣兵或者乞丐用这种方式得到自己想要的东西。
And, indeed, as soon as the Albanian had laughed at me I was pretty much at rest. 事实上，奥尔巴尼人一听就笑了，我大舒了一口气。
Even then, however, he made many conditions, and—for one thing—took away our arms, before he suffered us aboard; which was the signal to cast off; so that in a moment after, we were gliding down the bay with a good breeze, and blessing the name of God for our deliverance. 就算是那样，他还是有很多条件，比如要收了我们的武器才让上船，当然这也说明他马上就要开船了，因此没过多久我们就在和煦的微风中离开了海湾，感激上帝待我们不薄。
Almost in the mouth of the estuary, we passed the cruiser, and a little after the poor SARAH with her prize crew; and these were both sights to make us tremble. 接近海口的时候，我们路过了官船，接着是可怜的萨拉号及它被捕的船员，我们不禁生出九死一生之感。
The Bermudan seemed a very safe place to be in, and our bold stroke to have been fortunately played, when we were thus reminded of the case of our companions. 百慕大商船十分安全，我们靠着勇气和运气才没和昔日的同伴落到同一个下场。
For all that, we had only exchanged traps, jumped out of the frying-pan into the fire, ran from the yard-arm to the block, and escaped the open hostility of the man-of-war to lie at the mercy of the doubtful faith of our Albanian merchant. 不过，我们只是换个笼子待待，从油锅跳进了火里，从过街老鼠变成靠阿尔巴尼商人半怀疑半信任的慈悲过活的可怜人。
From many circumstances, it chanced we were safer than we could have dared to hope. 不过很多情况证明，我们现在的境况比自己期待的要更加安全。
The town of Albany was at that time much concerned in contraband trade across the desert with the Indians and the French. 当时的奥尔巴尼市对横跨印第安沙漠和法国之间的贸易管理甚严。
This, as it was highly illegal, relaxed their loyalty, and as it brought them in relation with the politest people on the earth, divided even their sympathies. 由于贸易非法，当地人对国家法律的忠诚感明显不足，而与世界最文明国家的交往同时让他们的民族意识有所淡化。
In short, they were like all the smugglers in the world, spies and agents ready- made for either party. 简而言之，跟世界其他地方的走私贩子一样，双方都有探子和间谍。
Our Albanian, besides, was a very honest man indeed, and very greedy; and, to crown our luck, he conceived a great delight in our society. 而我们的奥尔巴尼商人则是个非常诚实的人，他毫不掩饰自己的贪婪，最幸运的是，我们十分投机。
Before we had reached the town of New York we had come to a full agreement, that he should carry us as far as Albany upon his ship, and thence put us on a way to pass the boundaries and join the French. 到达纽约之前我们就达成协议，他会带我们到奥尔巴尼，然后把我们送过边境直达法国。
For all this we were to pay at a high rate; but beggars cannot be choosers, nor outlaws bargainers. 我们也答应会给他一大笔钱；因为有求于人就没有谈条件的余地，不法之徒也一样。
We sailed, then, up the Hudson River, which, I protest, is a very fine stream, and put up at the “King’s Arms” in Albany. 我们航行至哈德孙河，我觉得这是条非常美丽的河，之后我们登上奥尔巴尼的皇家军火库码头，在那里投宿。
The town was full of the militia of the province, breathing slaughter against the French. 这个城市全是民兵，严阵以待准备跟法国人血拼。
Governor Clinton was there himself, a very busy man, and, by what I could learn, very near distracted by the factiousness of his Assembly. 克林顿总督是个非常忙碌的人，他正身陷议会内部的政治风暴之中。
The Indians on both sides were on the war-path; we saw parties of them bringing in prisoners and (what was much worse) scalps, both male and female, for which they were paid at a fixed rate; and I assure you the sight was not encouraging. 两方之间的印第安区域是战场沟通的要道，我们看到印第安人用抓来的俘虏甚至是（更可怕的是）死人的头皮，有男有女，来换取一定数额的赏金，我可以确定地告诉你那绝对不是什么赏心悦目的场景。
Altogether, we could scarce have come at a period more unsuitable for our designs; our position in the chief inn was dreadfully conspicuous; our Albanian fubbed us off with a thousand delays, and seemed upon the point of a retreat from his engagements; nothing but peril appeared to environ the poor fugitives, and for some time we drowned our concern in a very irregular course of living. 总的来说，很难挑到这么不合时宜的时间来到这里。我们出现在高级旅馆里也显得很可疑，奥尔巴尼人把我们的事情一拖再拖，看起来是想毁约。对于逃亡者来说，没有比这更让人绝望的事了，有些时间我们都在担忧这段不太平的日子什么时候才会过去。
This, too, proved to be fortunate; and it’s one of the remarks that fall to be made upon our escape, how providentially our steps were conducted to the very end. 不过我们的运气还是很好的。好运是我们逃亡路上的关键词，每一步都好像为下一步铺路。
What a humiliation to the dignity of man! 真是羞辱人的尊严啊！
My philosophy, the extraordinary genius of Ballantrae, our valour, in which I grant that we were equal—all these might have proved insufficient without the Divine blessing on our efforts. 以我的人生哲学来看，巴伦特雷确实是个超凡的天才，我们在勇气上也算是旗鼓相当——不过要是没有上帝的保佑，我们不可能这么顺利。
And how true it is, as the Church tells us, that the Truths of Religion are, after all, quite applicable even to daily affairs! 教堂里的牧师常常讲，教义的伟大之处在于它就算在生活的琐碎中也能闪现！
At least, it was in the course of our revelry that we made the acquaintance of a spirited youth by the name of Chew. 至少，我们遇上了一位叫做楚的活力青年。
He was one of the most daring of the Indian traders, very well acquainted with the secret paths of the wilderness, needy, dissolute, and, by a last good fortune, in some disgrace with his family. 他是最大胆的印第安商人之一，对野外的小路非常熟悉。他狂浪不羁，穷得叮当响，最让我们觉得幸运的是，他还和家里闹得很不愉快。
Him we persuaded to come to our relief; he privately provided what was needful for our flight, and one day we slipped out of Albany, without a word to our former friend, and embarked, a little above, in a canoe. 我们把他说得动了心，他偷偷准备了我们路上需要的行头。一天，我们溜出奥尔巴尼，不辞而别，三个人登上了一条独木舟。
To the toils and perils of this journey, it would require a pen more elegant than mine to do full justice. 这一路上的艰辛波折非我笔力所能及。
The reader must conceive for himself the dreadful wilderness which we had now to thread; its thickets, swamps, precipitous rocks, impetuous rivers, and amazing waterfalls. 读者可以自行想象野外的种种可怕之处——丛林、沼泽、陡崖、河流，还有壮观的瀑布。
Among these barbarous scenes we must toil all day, now paddling, now carrying our canoe upon our shoulders; and at night we slept about a fire, surrounded by the howling of wolves and other savage animals. 我们必须在恶劣的环境中终日赶路，有时行船，有时还要扛着我们的独木舟，晚上我们睡在篝火旁，在狼嚎和其他丛林野兽的包围中入睡。
It was our design to mount the headwaters of the Hudson, to the neighbourhood of Crown Point, where the French had a strong place in the woods, upon Lake Champlain. 我们计划渡过哈德孙河的上游，那里毗邻克朗波因特，法国人在那里设了一个据点，就在尚普兰湖附近的丛林里。
But to have done this directly were too perilous; and it was accordingly gone upon by such a labyrinth of rivers, lakes, and portages as makes my head giddy to remember. 不过我们不可能直达，因为直达太危险了，所以我们只能在迷宫一样的河、湖、陆地之间穿梭，我现在都记得当时头晕眼花的感觉。
These paths were in ordinary times entirely desert; but the country was now up, the tribes on the war-path, the woods full of Indian scouts. 这些路径在平日毫无人烟，但是现在整个国家都在备战状态，各个部落盘踞着战略要道，树林里到处都是印第安探子。
Again and again we came upon these parties when we least expected, them; and one day, in particular, I shall never forget, how, as dawn was coming in, we were suddenly surrounded by five or six of these painted devils, uttering a very dreary sort of cry, and brandishing their hatchets. 我们在自己最意想不到的时刻一次一次地遭遇他们。有一天我永远也忘不了，刚破晓，四五个印第安人就把我们包围了，他们把自己涂得跟魔鬼一样，一边怪叫着一边挥舞着手里的斧头。
It passed off harmlessly, indeed, as did the rest of our encounters; for Chew was well known and highly valued among the different tribes. 实际上，我们每次都能全身而退，因为楚在当地很有名气，在几个部落中都很吃得开。
Indeed, he was a very gallant, respectable young man; but even with the advantage of his companionship, you must not think these meetings were without sensible peril. 他本来也是一个很勇敢、很值得尊敬的年轻人。不过就算有他为伴，也不能保证一路上就安全无虞。
To prove friendship on our part, it was needful to draw upon our stock of rum—indeed, under whatever disguise, that is the true business of the Indian trader, to keep a travelling public-house in the forest; and when once the braves had got their bottle of SCAURA (as they call this beastly liquor), it behoved us to set forth and paddle for our scalps. 为了表示友好，我们得拿出自己的朗姆酒招待他们——实际上，无论怎么遮掩，这就是一个印第安商人做生意的真谛，也是在丛林里穿行的必备佳品，只要那些印第安人搞到了他们的司高拉（这就是他们对烈酒的称呼），他们就会立即放行，也绝不追赶。
Once they were a little drunk, goodbye to any sense or decency; they had but the one thought, to get more SCAURA. 这些人一旦尝到了酒，就基本告别了理智和体面，就只剩一个想法——得到更多的司高拉。
They might easily take it in their heads to give us chase, and had we been overtaken, I had never written these memoirs. 他们要是当时动了一点儿追赶我们的念头，我今天就没命写这个回忆录了。
We were come to the most critical portion of our course, where we might equally expect to fall into the hands of French or English, when a terrible calamity befell us. 我们到了旅程最艰险的区域，法国人和英国人都可能抓到我们，这时候，更可怕的事情降临到了我们头上。
Chew was taken suddenly sick with symptoms like those of poison, and in the course of a few hours expired in the bottom of the canoe. 楚突然间跟中毒了一般病倒了，几个小时内就倒在独木舟里撒手人寰了。
We thus lost at once our guide, our interpreter, our boatman, and our passport, for he was all these in one; and found ourselves reduced, at a blow, to the most desperate and irremediable distress. 我们一下子失去了向导、翻译、舵手和活人通行证，他对我们来说是那么重要，我们一下子就陷入无可挽回的绝望境地。
Chew, who took a great pride in his knowledge, had indeed often lectured us on the geography; and Ballantrae, I believe, would listen. 楚生前对自己的丛林知识非常骄傲，常给我们讲地理，我相信巴伦特雷一直在听。
But for my part I have always found such information highly tedious; and beyond the fact that we were now in the country of the Adirondack Indians, and not so distant from our destination, could we but have found the way, I was entirely ignorant. 不过我一直都觉得这些非常无聊，除了这时候我们是在阿迪朗达克印第安人的区域内，要是能找到路的话，就离我们的目的地已然不远这个事实之外，其他的我什么都不知道。
The wisdom of my course was soon the more apparent; for with all his pains, Ballantrae was no further advanced than myself. 我认路的天赋很快就显现出来，巴伦特雷辛辛苦苦学了那么久也没比我强多少。
He knew we must continue to go up one stream; then, by way of a portage, down another; and then up a third. 他知道我们要继续在一条河上逆流行驶，到下一条，再沿着第三条河逆流行驶。
But you are to consider, in a mountain country, how many streams come rolling in from every hand. 不过你得考虑在一个山地国家，到底有多少条无名的溪流。
And how is a gentleman, who is a perfect stranger in that part of the world, to tell any one of them from any other? 你怎么能指望一个人，在一个完全陌生的国家，把这些溪流一条条地分清呢？
Nor was this our only trouble. 这还不是我们唯一的麻烦。
We were great novices, besides, in handling a canoe; the portages were almost beyond our strength, so that I have seen us sit down in despair for half an hour at a time without one word; and the appearance of a single Indian, since we had now no means of speaking to them, would have been in all probability the means of our destruction. 我们都不怎么会划独木舟，过河基本上在我们的能力范围以外，因此我们经常一言不发地在河边绝望地一坐半小时。如果再碰上个印第安人，由于我们都不懂他们的语言，无法沟通，基本上就意味着我们该到地狱去报到了。
There is altogether some excuse if Ballantrae showed something of a grooming disposition; his habit of imputing blame to others, quite as capable as himself, was less tolerable, and his language it was not always easy to accept. 这些都导致巴伦特雷经常心情忧郁。他有迁怒别人的习惯，由于他自己能力强，宽忍之心就相对较少，他的说话方式也不那么容易让人接受。
Indeed, he had contracted on board the pirate ship a manner of address which was in a high degree unusual between gentlemen; and now, when you might say he was in a fever, it increased upon him hugely. 实际上，他在海盗船上沾染的说话方式对绅士而言是非常不合适的。不过现在，你要是说他不正常，会大大激发他的怒火。
The third day of these wanderings, as we were carrying the canoe upon a rocky portage, she fell, and was entirely bilged. 我们游荡的第三天，在扛着独木舟穿越一段岩石密布的路段时，我们不小心把独木舟摔了个稀巴烂。
The portage was between two lakes, both pretty extensive; the track, such as it was, opened at both ends upon the water, and on both hands was enclosed by the unbroken woods; and the sides of the lakes were quite impassable with bog: so that we beheld ourselves not only condemned to go without our boat and the greater part of our provisions, but to plunge at once into impenetrable thickets and to desert what little guidance we still had—the course of the river. 这段路在两湖之间，湖水都很深，路径的两端都连着水，四周都被密林环绕；湖滨是沼泽，根本无法通行：结果是我们不进失去了船和大部分的补给，还得立刻进入难以穿越的丛林，并且舍弃仅有的地理标记——河道。
Each stuck his pistols in his belt, shouldered an axe, made a pack of his treasure and as much food as he could stagger under; and deserting the rest of our possessions, even to our swords, which would have much embarrassed us among the woods, we set forth on this deplorable adventure. 我们把枪别在腰上，扛着斧头，把能扛得动的财宝和食物打包，其余全部丟弃，其中包括我们的长剑，这东西在林子里也确实没什么用，然后继续这可悲的旅程。
The labours of Hercules, so finely described by Homer, were a trifle to what we now underwent. 荷马史诗中描绘过的大力神的功绩，跟我们现在相比简直就是小事一桩。
Some parts of the forest were perfectly dense down to the ground, so that we must cut our way like mites in a cheese. 森林里有些地方树木长得太茂密，我们不得不像小虫在奶酪里打洞一般，披荆斩棘，才能前进。
In some the bottom was full of deep swamp, and the whole wood entirely rotten. 有些地下全部是深不可测的沼泽，连树木都完全腐烂了。
I have leaped on a great fallen log and sunk to the knees in touchwood; I have sought to stay myself, in falling, against what looked to be a solid trunk, and the whole thing has whiffed away at my touch like a sheet of paper. 我曾经倚在一棵腐木上，结果陷在了齐腰深的木碴子里，转手扶另一棵看似坚固的树干想保持平衡，但那树干立刻就跟碎纸屑一般飘散在空气中。
Stumbling, falling, bogging to the knees, hewing our way, our eyes almost put out with twigs and branches, our clothes plucked from our bodies, we laboured all day, and it is doubtful if we made two miles. 摔跤、跌倒和陷入沼泽都是家常便饭，在及膝的泥中前行我们的眼珠子都快被荆棘和树枝弄瞎了，衣服被刮得千疮百孔，走了一整天也不知道有没有走出两英里去。
What was worse, as we could rarely get a view of the country, and were perpetually justled from our path by obstacles, it was impossible even to have a guess in what direction we were moving. 更糟糕的是，森林遮天蔽日，我们看不见目的地，一路上都是障碍，天知道我们正在朝哪个方向走。
A little before sundown, in an open place with a stream, and set about with barbarous mountains, Ballantrae threw down his pack. 夕阳西下之前，我们来到溪边的一片开阔地，周围是荒无人迹的群山，巴伦特雷把自己的行李一把甩到地上。
“I will go no further,” said he, and bade me light the fire, damning my blood in terms not proper for a chairman. “我不走了。”他说道，让我点了篝火，又说了很多与上等人身份不符的话来咒骂我的血统。
I told him to try to forget he had ever been a pirate, and to remember he had been a gentleman. 我告诉他尽量把自己当过海盗的事情忘掉，要记得自己还曾经是个绅士。
“Are you mad?” he cried. “你是疯了吧？”他喊道，
“Don’t cross me here! “在这儿别惹我！”
And then, shaking his fist at the hills, “To think,” cries he, “that I must leave my bones in this miserable wilderness! 然后又朝着群山挥拳头，喊道：“想想吧，我他妈就要死在这荒无人烟的野地里了！
Would God I had died upon the scaffold like a gentleman!” 还不如当初在绞刑架上死得光荣！”
This he said ranting like an actor; and then sat biting his fingers and staring on the ground, a most unchristian object. 他就像个演员那样咆哮着，然后坐下，咬着手指盯着地面，一点儿基督徒的样子也没有。
I took a certain horror of the man, for I thought a soldier and a gentleman should confront his end with more philosophy. 我已经有点儿怕这个人了，我觉得对待死亡，一位战士和绅士应该更加豁达。
I made him no reply, therefore, in words; and presently the evening fell so chill that I was glad, for my own sake, to kindle a fire. 我没回答他，夜幕四合，空气微凉，我自得其乐地点着篝火。
And yet God knows, in such an open spot, and the country alive with savages, the act was little short of lunacy. 上帝才知道，在这种蛮荒之国的空地上点篝火是一件多么疯狂的事。
Ballantrae seemed never to observe me; but at last, as I was about parching a little corn, he looked up. 巴伦特雷完全没有看我，等我准备烤玉米的时候，他才抬起头来看我。
“Have you ever a brother?” said be. “你有兄弟么？”他说道。
“By the blessing of Heaven,” said I, “not less than five.” “上帝保佑，”我说道：“不少于五个。”
“I have the one,” said he, with a strange voice; and then presently, “He shall pay me for all this,” he added. “我只有一个，”他用一种奇怪的声音说道，“他得为我遭受的一切付出代价。”
And when I asked him what was his brother’s part in our distress, “What!” he cried, “he sits in my place, he bears my name, he courts my wife; and I am here alone with a damned Irishman in this tooth-chattering desert! 当我问他弟弟跟我们这些不幸有什么关系时，他喊道：“凭什么？他占我的位置，挂我的头衔，睡我的老婆，然后我就得在这儿跟个爱尔兰糙人在这该死的荒地里等死！
Oh, I have been a common gull!” he cried. 噢，我他妈的就是个白痴！”他喊道。
The explosion was in all ways so foreign to my friend’s nature that I was daunted out of all my just susceptibility. 这种情绪爆发不太符合我朋友一贯的性格，把我吓傻了。
Sure, an offensive expression, however vivacious, appears a wonderfully small affair in circumstances so extreme! 诚然，这表达很有攻击性，不过再怎么恶毒，在这种生死关头面前是小事一桩。
But here there is a strange thing to be noted. 有件奇怪的事我得提一下。
He had only once before referred to the lady with whom he was contracted. 他的未婚妻他之前只提过一次。
That was when we came in view of the town of New York, when he had told me, if all had their rights, he was now in sight of his own property, for Miss Graeme enjoyed a large estate in the province. 我们刚到纽约的时候他告诉我，要是事情顺利的话，他自己的财产马上就要到手，因为格雷姆小姐在乡下有一大笔房产。
And this was certainly a natural occasion; but now here she was named a second time; and what is surely fit to be observed, in this very month, which was November, ’47, and I BELIEVE UPON THAT VERY DAY AS WE SAT AMONG THESE BARBAROUS MOUNTAINS, his brother and Miss Graeme were married. 而这个场景无疑是很顺其自然的。但现在巴伦特雷第二次提起了她，在1947年11月，当我们坐在荒无人烟的群山里等死的时候，他的弟弟和格雷姆小姐却已经成婚。
I am the least superstitious of men; but the hand of Providence is here displayed too openly not to be remarked. [4] 我不是一个迷信的人，可是上帝之手伸到你面前的时候，总不能装瞎子吧。[4]
The next day, and the next, were passed in similar labours; Ballantrae often deciding on our course by the spinning of a coin; and once, when I expostulated on this childishness, he had an odd remark that I have never forgotten. 第二天和第三天我们都这么艰难地前行，巴伦特雷经常抛硬币决定我们该往哪走，当我怪他太幼稚的时候，他说了一句让我此生难忘的怪语。
“I know no better way,” said he, “to express my scorn of human reason.” “我不知道还有什么更好的方式，”他说道，“可以表现我对人类理性的蔑视。”
I think it was the third day that we found the body of a Christian, scalped and most abominably mangled, and lying in a pudder of his blood; the birds of the desert screaming over him, as thick as flies. 我想那是我们发现那个基督徒的尸体后的第三天，尸体被剥了头皮，分了尸，倒在血泊里，密密麻麻的鸟就像苍蝇那样多，在尸体旁边发出阵阵尖叫声。
I cannot describe how dreadfully this sight affected us; but it robbed me of all strength and all hope for this world. 我没法形容这场景对我们来说有多么恐怖，它把我仅存的生存意志和对这个世界的希望抹杀殆尽。
The same day, and only a little after, we were scrambling over a part of the forest that had been burned, when Ballantrae, who was a little ahead, ducked suddenly behind a fallen trunk. 同一天，我们正在一片烧焦的林子里踉跄前行，走在前面的巴伦特雷突然躲到一棵倒下的树干后面。
I joined him in this shelter, whence we could look abroad without being seen ourselves; and in the bottom of the next vale, beheld a large war party of the savages going by across our line. 我紧随其后，在那里我们可以看到外面的情势而不被发现，前头的山谷里有一大群土著士兵正在我们刚才走过的路上行军。
There might be the value of a weak battalion present; all naked to the waist, blacked with grease and soot, and painted with white lead and vermilion, according to their beastly habits. 看样子差不多有一个营，全都光着上身，皮肤涂得漆黑，还描着白色和朱红色的颜料，颇具他们的野兽派风格。
They went one behind another like a string of geese, and at a quickish trot; so that they took but a little while to rattle by, and disappear again among the woods. 他们一个跟着一个走得像一群鹅，走得还很急；所以没过一会儿，他们就从我们旁边过去了，又消失在树林里。
Yet I suppose we endured a greater agony of hesitation and suspense in these few minutes than goes usually to a man’s whole life. 不过这几分钟里，我们担惊受怕，度日如年。
Whether they were French or English Indians, whether they desired scalps or prisoners, whether we should declare ourselves upon the chance, or lie quiet and continue the heart-breaking business of our journey: sure, I think these were questions to have puzzled the brains of Aristotle himself. 我们不知道这些印第安人到底是法属区的还是英属区的，他们是要抓获俘虏还是割取头皮，我们是应该主动投降还是安静潜伏以继续进行我们的心碎之旅。我想亚里士多德想这些问题肯定都得头疼。
Ballantrae turned to me with a face all wrinkled up and his teeth showing in his mouth, like what I have read of people starving; he said no word, but his whole appearance was a kind of dreadful question. 巴伦特雷把他那张遍布皱纹的脸转向我，还冲我龇牙咧嘴的，好像饿鬼一样。他一句话没说，但他的整个表情就是个令人毛骨悚然的疑问句。
“They may be of the English side,” I whispered; “and think! the best we could then hope, is to begin this over again.” “应该是英国那边的，”他轻声说道，“想想吧！那我们就只能把最大的希望寄托在原路返回上了！”
“I know—I know,” he said. “我就知道——我就知道，”他喊道，
“Yet it must come to a plunge at last.” “反正到最后还是得铤而走险。”
And he suddenly plucked out his coin, shook it in his closed hands, looked at it, and then lay down with his face in the dust. 他突然间拿出自己的硬币，双手一拢，把硬币摇了几下儿，然后看了看它，自己就趴在了地上。
ADDITION BY MR. MACKELLAR. 麦凯勒先生加注
—I drop the Chevalier’s narration at this point because the couple quarrelled and separated the same day; and the Chevalier’s account of the quarrel seems to me (I must confess) quite incompatible with the nature of either of the men. ——骑士的叙述我就截取到这里为止，他们在这一天吵崩了就此分手；而骑士对他们争执的叙述对我来说（我承认是对我来说）与他们两个人的性格都有很大出入，难以自圆其说。
Henceforth they wandered alone, undergoing extraordinary sufferings; until first one and then the other was picked up by a party from Fort St. Frederick. 之后他们各自游荡，受尽各种折磨，然后先后到达了圣·弗雷德里克要塞。
Only two things are to be noted. 只有两点我要提一下。
And first (as most important for my purpose) that the Master, in the course of his miseries buried his treasure, at a point never since discovered, but of which he took a drawing in his own blood on the lining of his hat. 第一点，（也是最重要的）大少爷路遇艰辛，被迫把宝藏埋在了一个之后再也没人找得到的地方，但是他在帽子里蘸着自己的血画了一幅藏宝图。
And second, that on his coming thus penniless to the Fort, he was welcomed like a brother by the Chevalier, who thence paid his way to France. 第二点，当大少爷身无分文地来到要塞的时候，骑士像兄弟一般迎接了他，还给了他去法国的盘缠。
The simplicity of Mr. Burke’s character leads him at this point to praise the Master exceedingly; to an eye more worldly wise, it would seem it was the Chevalier alone that was to be commended. 伯克先生心思简单，那时候还在赞赏大少爷，但用更加世俗老练的眼光看，骑士的做法才是值得称道的。
I have the more pleasure in pointing to this really very noble trait of my esteemed correspondent, as I fear I may have wounded him immediately before. 我指出这一点是为了对记录者的崇高品质表示敬意，尽管在之前我恐怕已经伤害了他的感情。
I have refrained from comments on any of his extraordinary and (in my eyes) immoral opinions, for I know him to be jealous of respect. 我知道他是一位重视自身名誉的人，因此，对他记录中一些不合常理或者（在我看来）不道德的观点我就不予评论了。
But his version of the quarrel is really more than I can reproduce; for I knew the Master myself, and a man more insusceptible of fear is not conceivable. 不过他们争吵的真相我就真的不得而知了；因为我知道大少爷那种无畏无惧的性格，因此伯克上校的叙述绝对是不可信的。
I regret this oversight of the Chevalier’s, and all the more because the tenor of his narrative (set aside a few flourishes) strikes me as highly ingenuous. 我很遗憾骑士在这一点上的疏忽，更是因为他那坦率的叙述（除了一些渲染或修辞）打动了我。
[1] “NOTE BY MR. MACKELLAR. [1]麦凯勒先生注
Should not this be Alan BRECK Stewart, afterwards notorious as the Appin murderer? 是不是他的名字应该是艾伦·布雷克·斯图尔特？也就是后来臭名昭著的阿平杀手？
The Chevalier is sometimes very weak on names. 骑士有时记不清人名。
[2] NOTE BY MR. MACKELLAR. [2]麦凯勒先生注
This Teach of the SARAH must not be confused with the celebrated Blackbeard. 一定不能把这个萨拉号上的蒂奇和著名的黑胡子船长搞混。
The dates and facts by no means tally. 日期和时间完全不符合。
It is possible the second Teach may have at once borrowed the name and imitated the more excessive part of his manners from the first. 有可能这个伪蒂奇只是借了真蒂奇的名字，还模仿了真蒂奇最过分的那一部分脾性。
Even the Master of Ballantrae could make admirers. 就算是巴伦特雷少爷也能有崇拜者。
[3] NOTE BY MR. MACKELLAR. [3]麦凯勒先生注
And is not this the whole explanation? since this Dutton, exactly like the officers, enjoyed the stimulus of some responsibility. 这就是全部的解释？因为这个达顿跟警察一样，喜欢享受责任带来的刺激感。
[4] NOTE BY MR. MACKELLAR: A complete blunder: there was at this date no word of the marriage: see above in my own narration. [4]麦凯勒先生注：这完全是胡扯，这个日期他们还没结婚呢，请参看我在前文中的叙述。
Chapter 4 第四章
Persecutions Endured by Mr. Henry. 亨利先生忍辱负重
You can guess on what part of his adventures the Colonel principally dwelled. 读者能猜到上校主要对大少爷探险旅程的哪一部分大谈特谈。
Indeed, if we had heard it all, it is to be thought the current of this business had been wholly altered; but the pirate ship was very gently touched upon. 事实上，如果听了故事的来龙去脉，就知道这趟探险根本就不是上校讲的那样，而且他对海盗船也只是略微提了提。
Nor did I hear the Colonel to an end even of that which he was willing to disclose; for Mr. Henry, having for some while been plunged in a brown study, rose at last from his seat and (reminding the Colonel there were matters that he must attend to) bade me follow him immediately to the office. 他想说的那些，我也没有听完，而亨利先生，沉思了一会儿后，终于从座位上起来了（告诉上校他还有些事情要处理），让我立即跟他去办公室。
Once there, he sought no longer to dissemble his concern, walking to and fro in the room with a contorted face, and passing his hand repeatedly upon his brow. 到了那里，他再也不掩饰自己的担忧，在房间里走来走去，愁容满面，手一而再地抚着额头。
“We have some business,” he began at last; and there broke off, declared we must have wine, and sent for a magnum of the best. 他终于开口说话了：“我们有些事情要做。”然后就打住了，示意我们得喝点儿酒，吩咐我拿一大瓶最好的。
This was extremely foreign to his habitudes; and what was still more so, when the wine had come, he gulped down one glass upon another like a man careless of appearances. 这一点儿也不符合他的习惯，酒上来后，他一杯接一杯地喝，完全不顾形象，这更不像他了。
But the drink steadied him. 但是，酒却让他平静了下来。
“You will scarce be surprised, Mackellar,” says he, “when I tell you that my brother—whose safety we are all rejoiced to learn—stands in some need of money.” 他说：“麦凯勒，我告诉你，我哥哥（知道他安然无恙，我们都很开心）现在需要钱，你不会感到奇怪吧。”
I told him I had misdoubted as much; but the time was not very fortunate, as the stock was low. 我告诉他我对大少爷去世的消息本来就不怎么相信，但现在时机非常不利，因为家里的积蓄已然很少了。
“Not mine,” said he. “不是用我的钱，”他说道，
“There is the money for the mortgage.” “家里还有抵押来的钱。”
I reminded him it was Mrs. Henry’s. 我提醒他那是他太太的。
“I will be answerable to my wife,” he cried violently. 他狠狠地说：“我会给我太太说清楚的。”
“And then,” said I, “there is the mortgage.” 我说：“那么还是用抵押的钱吧。”
“I know,” said he; “it is on that I would consult you.” 他说：“我就是要问你这个呢。”
I showed him how unfortunate a time it was to divert this money from its destination; and how, by so doing, we must lose the profit of our past economies, and plunge back the estate into the mire. 我向他说明了，现在挪用那笔钱多么不是时候，倘若这么做，我们一定会损失以前的利润，使得财产再次陷入困境。
I even took the liberty to plead with him; and when he still opposed me with a shake of the head and a bitter dogged smile, my zeal quite carried me beyond my place. 我甚至壮着胆子求他，可他还是摇了摇头，面带苦笑地表示反对我热心得过了头，这不是我该管的事。
“This is midsummer madness,” cried I; “and I for one will be no party to it.” 我喊道：“您真是傻到家了，我再也不插手这件事了。”
“You speak as though I did it for my pleasure,” says he. 他说道：“你好像是说我这样做只是为了玩玩。
“But I have a child now; and, besides, I love order; and to say the honest truth, Mackellar, I had begun to take a pride in the estates.” 可是，我已经当爸爸了，我是个循规蹈矩的人。说实话，麦凯勒，我早就为这些财产感到骄傲。”
He gloomed for a moment. 他沮丧了一会儿。
“But what would you have?” he went on. “可是你又能得到什么呢？”他继续说道，
“Nothing is mine, nothing. “什么也得不到，什么也得不到。
This day’s news has knocked the bottom out of my life. 今天这个消息让我变得一无所有。
I have only the name and the shadow of things—only the shadow; there is no substance in my rights.” 只有虚名和一些虚无缥缈的东西，虚无缥缈的东西，没有任何实在的权利。”
“They will prove substantial enough before a court,” said I. 我说：“到了法庭上，这些就都实实在在是您的了。”
He looked at me with a burning eye, and seemed to repress the word upon his lips; and I repented what I had said, for I saw that while he spoke of the estate he had still a side-thought to his marriage. 他怒火中烧地望着我，好似要憋住想说的话。我为刚说的话感到后悔，因为我意识到，他说财产这个词时，考虑到了他的婚姻。
And then, of a sudden, he twitched the letter from his pocket, where it lay all crumpled, smoothed it violently on the table, and read these words to me with a trembling tongue: “‘My dear Jacob’—This is how he begins!” cries he—“‘My dear Jacob, I once called you so, you may remember; and you have now done the business, and flung my heels as high as Criffel.’ 突然，他猛地从口袋里拽出了那封皱皱巴巴的信，接着又在桌子上用力展平，用颤抖的声音向我读出了以下的话：“‘亲爱的雅各布’——这就是他的开头！”他喊道，“‘亲爱的雅各布，你可能还记得我曾这样称呼你，可是你现在做起生意来，就把我扔到九霄云外了。’
What do you think of that, Mackellar,” says he, “from an only brother? 麦凯勒，对这样一封来自唯一的哥哥的信，你怎么看？
I declare to God I liked him very well; I was always staunch to him; and this is how he writes! 我发誓我非常喜欢他，也很忠于他，而他在信里却这样写！
But I will not sit down under the imputation”—walking to and fro—“I am as good as he; I am a better man than he, I call on God to prove it! 面对这样的诬告，我可不能坐以待毙”他依然走来走去，“我丝毫不逊于他，而且比他更优秀，我将请求上帝来予以证明！
I cannot give him all the monstrous sum he asks; he knows the estate to be incompetent; but I will give him what I have, and it in more than he expects. 他要的巨款，我不能如数给他，他知道房产不值那么多，但是我还是会给他我的所有，并且比他预想的还多。
I have borne all this too long. 这一切，我已忍了很久很久。
See what he writes further on; read it for yourself: ‘I know you are a niggardly dog.’ 他接下来写的是什么，你自己看看：‘我知道你是个吝啬鬼。’
A niggardly dog! 吝啬鬼！
I niggardly? 我吝啬吗？
Is that true, Mackellar? 麦凯勒，我真的吝啬吗？
You think it is?” 你这样认为吗？”
I really thought he would have struck me at that. 他那样真的吓到我了。
“Oh, you all think so! “天啊！你们都这样认为！
Well, you shall see, and he shall see, and God shall see. 哼，总有一天，你会知道，他会知道，上帝会知道。
If I ruin the estate and go barefoot, I shall stuff this bloodsucker. 就算我毁了这座房子，变得一无所有，我也会满足这个吸血鬼。
Let him ask all—all, and he shall have it! 让他要这一切吧，这一切，他会得到的！
It is all his by rights. 这本来就是他的。
Ah!” he cried, “and I foresaw all this, and worse, when he would not let me go.” 天啊！”　他叫道，“当年他不让我去的时候，我就做好了更糟的打算。”
He poured out another glass of wine, and was about to carry it to his lips, when I made so bold as to lay a finger on his arm. 他又倒了一杯酒，酒杯就要碰到嘴唇的时候，我壮起胆子，拉住了他的胳膊。
He stopped a moment. 他停顿了片刻。
“You are right,” said he, and flung glass and all in the fireplace. “你是对的，”他说道，然后把酒杯、酒瓶都扔到了壁炉里，接着说，
“Come, let us count the money.” “来，我们数数钱吧。”
