I durst no longer oppose him; indeed, I was very much affected by the sight of so much disorder in a man usually so controlled; and we sat down together, counted the money, and made it up in packets for the greater ease of Colonel Burke, who was to be the bearer. 我再也不敢反对他了。事实上，看到一个平常非常克己的人表现得如此反常时，我已经被深深地影响到了。我们坐在一起数好钱，又装成一袋袋的，好方便拿钱的人——伯克上校。
This done, Mr. Henry returned to the hall, where he and my old lord sat all night through with their guest. 做完这些后，亨利先生回到了大厅，他和老爷在那了陪了客人一整个晚上。
A little before dawn I was called and set out with the Colonel. 黎明前夕，我受命与上校一同出发。
He would scarce have liked a less responsible convoy, for he was a man who valued himself; nor could we afford him one more dignified, for Mr. Henry must not appear with the freetraders. 若不是我在家里负有责任，上校不会让我做他的陪同，因为他一向对自己非常看重。再说，我们也没法给他提供一位地位比我更高的人选，因为亨利先生是断然不会和走私贩出现在一起的。
It was a very bitter morning of wind, and as we went down through the long shrubbery the Colonel held himself muffled in his cloak. 那天早上寒风凛冽，我们沿着灌木林而下，上校用斗篷把自个包裹得严严实实。
“Sir,” said I, “this is a great sum of money that your friend requires. 我说：“先生，您朋友要的真是一大笔钱啊！
I must suppose his necessities to be very great.” 我认为他一定有很多开销吧。”
“We must suppose so,” says he, I thought drily; but perhaps it was the cloak about his mouth. “我们是该这么想。”他的语气似乎很冷淡，可能是他嘴上蒙着斗篷的缘故。
“I am only a servant of the family,” said I. “我只是这个家里的仆人，”我说道，
“You may deal openly with me. “您不必对我有所顾忌。
I think we are likely to get little good by him?” 从大少爷那儿，我们有可能得不到好处吧？”
“My dear man,” said the Colonel, “Ballantrae is a gentleman of the most eminent natural abilities, and a man that I admire, and that I revere, to the very ground he treads on.” 上校道：“亲爱的麦凯勒，巴伦特雷是个极具天赋的绅士，对他，我十分钦佩，佩服得五体投地。”
And then he seemed to me to pause like one in a difficulty. 接着他不做声了，好似有什么难言之隐。
“But for all that,” said I, “we are likely to get little good by him?” 我说：“尽管如此，我们有可能从他那儿得不到一点儿好处吧？”
“Sure, and you can have it your own way, my dear man,” says the Colonel. 上校说：“当然了，亲爱的麦凯勒，你可以这么理解。”
By this time we had come to the side of the creek, where the boat awaited him. 此时，我们到了海湾旁，船在那里等他。
“Well,” said be, “I am sure I am very much your debtor for all your civility, Mr. Whatever-your-name-is; and just as a last word, and since you show so much intelligent interest, I will mention a small circumstance that may be of use to the family. 他说：“嗯，不管你姓甚名谁，对于你的以礼相待，我非常感谢。由于你如此有见地，临别之际，我向你透露点儿可能对这个家庭有用的信息。
For I believe my friend omitted to mention that he has the largest pension on the Scots Fund of any refugee in Paris; and it’s the more disgraceful, sir,” cries the Colonel, warming, “because there’s not one dirty penny for myself.” 我认为我的朋友没有提到一件事，就是他在巴黎得到了苏格兰基金发放给所有逃亡者抚恤金中最大的一份，更可耻的是，”上校激动地喊道，“他没有给我一分钱，真是丢人。”
He cocked his hat at me, as if I had been to blame for this partiality; then changed again into his usual swaggering civility, shook me by the hand, and set off down to the boat, with the money under his arms, and whistling as he went the pathetic air of SHULE AROON. 他朝我竖起了他的帽子，好像怪我造成了他的不公待遇似的，接着他又一次变回通常那种自鸣得意的样子，与我握了握手，挟着钱，吹着口哨朝船走去，吹的是一首名为《亲爱的疏勒》的伤感歌曲。
It was the first time I had heard that tune; I was to hear it again, words and all, as you shall learn, but I remember how that little stave of it ran in my head after the freetraders had bade him “Wheesht, in the deil’s name,” and the grating of the oars had taken its place, and I stood and watched the dawn creeping on the sea, and the boat drawing away, and the lugger lying with her foresail backed awaiting it. 这是我第一次听到这个调子；各位读者在下文中会发现我又一次听到了这首歌，不只是调子，还有歌词，我记得走私贩命令他“该死的，住嘴”后，那首曲子依然萦绕脑海，接着划桨的刺耳声淹没了他的口哨声，我伫立着，看着海平面上渐渐破晓，小船渐渐驶远，帆船落着帆樯在远处等着它。
The gap made in our money was a sore embarrassment, and, among other consequences, it had this: that I must ride to Edinburgh, and there raise a new loan on very questionable terms to keep the old afloat; and was thus, for close upon three weeks, absent from the house of Durrisdeer. 我们没有给伯克上校大少爷要的钱数，令我们极度难堪，加上其他的原因，造成了下面这种后果：我必须去爱丁堡，贷一笔期限不明的款来还上以前的贷款。因此，我要离开达里斯迪尔庄园整整三个星期。
What passed in the interval I had none to tell me, but I found Mrs. Henry, upon my return, much changed in her demeanour. 在这三个星期里发生了什么，我一点儿也不知道，但我回来后发现亨利太太行为举止大大不同于以前。
The old talks with my lord for the most part pretermitted; a certain deprecation visible towards her husband, to whom I thought she addressed herself more often; and, for one thing, she was now greatly wrapped up in Miss Katharine. 和老爷谈话的习惯没有了，对自己丈夫的依稀可见蔑视，但与自己丈夫的谈话变多了。并且一方面，现在她的心思都在凯瑟琳小姐身上。
You would think the change was agreeable to Mr. Henry; no such matter! 读者可能觉得这种改变合亨利先生的意，那可大错特错了。
To the contrary, every circumstance of alteration was a stab to him; he read in each the avowal of her truant fancies. 恰恰相反，每一种改变都会给他带来一种刺痛，令他觉得她难以捉摸。
That constancy to the Master of which she was proud while she supposed him dead, she had to blush for now she knew he was alive, and these blushes were the hated spring of her new conduct. 她以前认为他死了，关于自己对大少爷忠贞不渝的爱，她是很自豪的；然而现在知道他还活着，她感到羞愧了，这种羞愧感正是她最近反常表现的原因。
I am to conceal no truth; and I will here say plainly, I think this was the period in which Mr. Henry showed the worst. 我不想掩盖真相，说实话，这段时间是亨利先生脾气最不好的时候。
He contained himself, indeed, in public; but there was a deep-seated irritation visible underneath. 事实上，他那段时间在公共场合一直克制自己，而内心深处却存在显而易见的愤怒。
With me, from whom he had less concealment, he was often grossly unjust, and even for his wife he would sometimes have a sharp retort: perhaps when she had ruffled him with some unwonted kindness; perhaps upon no tangible occasion, the mere habitual tenor of the man’s annoyance bursting spontaneously forth. 在我面前，他很少隐藏，经常极度不公允，甚至对他妻子，有时也针锋相对：有时她出人意料的温柔也会激怒他；有时他会无缘无故地把心中的烦恼全都发泄出来。
When he would thus forget himself (a thing so strangely out of keeping with the terms of their relation), there went a shook through the whole company, and the pair would look upon each other in a kind of pained amazement. 当他忘了自己已为人夫时（他们明明是夫妻关系，弄到这个地步很奇怪），在场的人都感到震惊，夫妻俩面面相觑，表情既痛苦，又惊讶。
All the time, too, while he was injuring himself by this defect of temper, he was hurting his position by a silence, of which I scarce know whether to say it was the child of generosity or pride. 一直以来，气大伤身，他又一言不发，形势就更加糟糕了，我真不知他这种态度究竟是大度还是傲慢的产物。
The freetraders came again and again, bringing messengers from the Master, and none departed empty-handed. 走私贩来了一拨儿又一拨儿，带来大少爷的信使，没有人是空手离去。
I never durst reason with Mr. Henry; he gave what was asked of him in a kind of noble rage. 我从不敢问亨利先生为什么会这样，不管大少爷要什么，他都很慷慨地奉上，心里却暗暗窝火。
Perhaps because he knew he was by nature inclining to the parsimonious, he took a backforemost pleasure in the recklessness with which he supplied his brother’s exigence. 也许是因为他知道自己打骨子里就小气，他为落难的兄长慷慨解囊，从中获得了极大的满足。
Perhaps the falsity of the position would have spurred a humbler man into the same excess. 处在这种虚假地位之人，即使再龌龊，也会像他一样豪爽的。
But the estate (if I may say so) groaned under it; our daily expenses were shorn lower and lower; the stables were emptied, all but four roadsters; servants were discharged, which raised a dreadful murmuring in the country, and heated up the old disfavour upon Mr. Henry; and at last the yearly visit to Edinburgh must be discontinued. 但全家的资财（如果还称得上的话）却因此而受累；我们日常开支越来越少；马厩都空了，只剩四匹马；仆人都解雇了，这在村子里引发了一场可怕的骚动，以前那种对亨利先生的不友好再次甚嚣尘上；最终一年一度的爱丁堡之旅也中断了。
This was in 1756. 此时为1756年。
You are to suppose that for seven years this bloodsucker had been drawing the life’s blood from Durrisdeer, and that all this time my patron had held his peace. 读者们应该知道大少爷这个吸血鬼这七年来一直吞噬着达里斯迪尔家的生命，我主子一直以来自己默默地承受。
It was an effect of devilish malice in the Master that he addressed Mr. Henry alone upon the matter of his demands, and there was never a word to my lord. 这是因为邪恶的大少爷只给亨利先生写信，让他满足自己的需求，从没给老爷写过一个字。
The family had looked on, wondering at our economies. 全家人都蒙在鼓里，对家里的经济状况感到疑虑。
They had lamented, I have no doubt, that my patron had become so great a miser—a fault always despicable, but in the young abhorrent, and Mr. Henry was not yet thirty years of age. 我坚信他们抱怨主子成了守财奴——大家都讨厌小气鬼，尤其讨厌年轻人这样，而亨利先生还不到而立之年。
Still, he had managed the business of Durrisdeer almost from a boy; and they bore with these changes in a silence as proud and bitter as his own, until the coping-stone of the Edinburgh visit. 更糟糕的是，他从儿时起就打理达里斯迪尔家的生意，他们同他一起承受着这些改变，荣辱与共，直到爱丁堡之旅泡汤。
At this time I believe my patron and his wife were rarely together, save at meals. 这段时间，我相信主人和他妻子除了吃饭以外几乎不碰面。
Immediately on the back of Colonel Burke’s announcement Mrs. Henry made palpable advances; you might say she had laid a sort of timid court to her husband, different, indeed, from her former manner of unconcern and distance. 伯克上校宣告大少爷没死后，亨利太太当即做出了明显的改变；各位读者会发现亨利太太对她丈夫不再是以前的冷漠与疏远，而是怯生生地献起殷勤来。
I never had the heart to blame Mr. Henry because he recoiled from these advances; nor yet to censure the wife, when she was cut to the quick by their rejection. 我从来没有因为亨利先生厌恶这些主动示好而责备他，也从没有在她的示好遭到拒绝深受伤害时谴责她。
But the result was an entire estrangement, so that (as I say) they rarely spoke, except at meals. 最终的结果是彻底的分居，因此（如同我前面说过的那样）他们除了在饭桌上说话外，几乎没有交谈。
Even the matter of the Edinburgh visit was first broached at table, and it chanced that Mrs. Henry was that day ailing and querulous. 甚至是关于爱丁堡之旅也是在饭桌上第一次谈到，碰巧也是那天，亨利太太身体抱恙，动不动就发牢骚。
She had no sooner understood her husband’s meaning than the red flew in her face. 一听丈夫说完不去爱丁堡的理由，她就气得满脸通红。
“At last,” she cried, “this is too much! 她喊道：“这也太过分了！
Heaven knows what pleasure I have in my life, that I should be denied my only consolation. 天知道我活着还有什么乐趣，连唯一的慰藉都给剥夺了。
These shameful proclivities must be trod down; we are already a mark and an eyesore in the neighbourhood. 这些可耻的癖好必须打住，在街坊邻居看来，我们已经劣迹斑斑、格格不入了。
I will not endure this fresh insanity.” 对这个荒唐的行为，我再也无法忍受了。”
“I cannot afford it,” says Mr. Henry. 亨利先生说：“我负担不起”。
“Afford?” she cried. 她嚷道：“负担不起？
“For shame! 太不要脸了！
But I have money of my own.” 可是我自己还有钱呢！”
“That is all mine, madam, by marriage,” he snarled, and instantly left the room. 他气急败坏地说：“夫人，结婚后，那可都成我的了。”接着他马上离开了房间。
My old lord threw up his hands to Heaven, and he and his daughter, withdrawing to the chimney, gave me a broad hint to be gone. 老爷双手举起，同她儿媳去了壁炉那里，意思明显是让我离开。
I found Mr. Henry in his usual retreat, the steward’s room, perched on the end of the table, and plunging his penknife in it with a very ugly countenance. 亨利先生又逃到老地方——管家的房间，他坐在桌子角上，把小折刀用力插进桌子里，脸色很难看。
“Mr. Henry,” said I, “you do yourself too much injustice, and it is time this should cease.” 我说：“亨利先生，您对自己太不公平了，该停止了。”
“Oh!” cries he, “nobody minds here. 他喊道：“天啊！没人会理会的。
They think it only natural. 他们认为这很自然。
I have shameful proclivities. 说我这人有可耻的癖好。
I am a niggardly dog,” and he drove his knife up to the hilt. 说我是个小气鬼，”他把刀子扔得老远，
“But I will show that fellow,” he cried with an oath, “I will show him which is the more generous.” 发誓道，“我会向那个家伙证明，向他证明谁才更慷慨大方。”
“This is no generosity,” said I; “this is only pride.” 我说：“这不是什么大方不大方，这是尊严。”
“Do you think I want morality?” he asked. 他问我：“我还需要别人的教训吗？”
I thought he wanted help, and I should give it him, willy-nilly; and no sooner was Mrs. Henry gone to her room than I presented myself at her door and sought admittance. 我认为他需要帮助，不管怎样，我都得帮他。亨利太太一回到自己的房间，我就站在门口等着她叫我进去了。
She openly showed her wonder. 她毫不掩饰她的惊讶。
“What do you want with me, Mr. Mackellar?” said she. 她问道：“麦凯勒先生，你想怎么着？”
“The Lord knows, madam,” says I, “I have never troubled you before with any freedoms; but this thing lies too hard upon my conscience, and it will out. 我答道：“夫人，上帝知道我以前从未叨扰过您，可是这件事却让我良心不安，我必须得跟您说。
Is it possible that two people can be so blind as you and my lord? and have lived all these years with a noble gentleman like Mr. Henry, and understand so little of his nature?” 像亨利先生这样的好人，您和老爷同他一起生活了这么些年，怎能如此熟视无睹，如此不了解他的本性呢？”
“What does this mean?” she cried. 她嚷道：“你这是什么意思？”
“Do you not know where his money goes to? his—and yours—and the money for the very wine he does not drink at table?” “您不知道他的钱都去哪儿了吗？他的钱，您的钱，还有买饭桌上那瓶他没有喝的酒的钱？”
I went on. 我继续说，
“To Paris—to that man! “钱都去巴黎了——给那个男人了！
Eight thousand pounds has he had of us in seven years, and my patron fool enough to keep it secret!” 七年来，给了他八千镑，主子竟然不说，他真傻啊！”
“Eight thousand pounds!” she repeated. 她重复道：“八千镑！
“It in impossible; the estate is not sufficient.” 不可能，我们没有那么多财产呀！”
“God knows how we have sweated farthings to produce it,” said I. 我说：“老天知道我们是怎样一分一分挤出来的。
“But eight thousand and sixty is the sum, beside odd shillings. 不算零钱，一共是八千零六十镑。
And if you can think my patron miserly after that, this shall be my last interference.” 如果您现在还认为主子小气，那我就再也不叨扰您了。”
“You need say no more, Mr. Mackellar,” said she. 她说：“麦凯勒先生，你无需多言了，
“You have done most properly in what you too modestly call your interference. 虽然你谦称之为叨扰，其实你做得一点儿也不过分。
I am much to blame; you must think me indeed a very unobservant wife” (looking upon me with a strange smile), “but I shall put this right at once. 是我的错，你一定认为我是个没眼力见儿的妻子”（抬头看了看我，笑得很奇怪），“但我会立即改正。
The Master was always of a very thoughtless nature; but his heart is excellent; he is the soul of generosity. 大少爷虽然很轻率，但他心地善良，很慷慨。
I shall write to him myself. 我会亲自写信给他。
You cannot think how you have pained me by this communication.” 你不知道，这次谈话令我多么痛苦。”
“Indeed, madam, I had hoped to have pleased you,” said I, for I raged to see her still thinking of the Master. 看到她现在还对大少爷念念不忘，我很生气，说道：“夫人，其实我还以为这会让您高兴。”
“And pleased,” said she, “and pleased me of course.” 她说：“高兴，我当然高兴了。”
That same day (I will not say but what I watched) I had the satisfaction to see Mr. Henry come from his wife’s room in a state most unlike himself; for his face was all bloated with weeping, and yet he seemed to me to walk upon the air. 那天，（我只说我看到的）我看到亨利先生从他太太房间里出来，像是换了一个人似的，虽然他的脸上挂满了泪水，但在我看来，他很得意，我也就感到很满意。
By this, I was sure his wife had made him full amends for once. 有鉴于此，我肯定他太太向他赔了不是。
“Ah,” thought I to myself, “I have done a brave stroke this day.” 我自忖道：“噢，我今天可做了一件大事。”
On the morrow, as I was seated at my books, Mr. Henry came in softly behind me, took me by the shoulders, and shook me in a manner of playfulness. 第二天，我正坐在书架旁，亨利先生从我后面轻轻地进来了，抓着我的双肩摇了几下，看似很开心。
“I find you are a faithless fellow after all,” says he, which was his only reference to my part; but the tone he spoke in was more to me than any eloquence of protestation. 他说道：“我发现你这家伙太不忠心了。”这是他唯一一次提到我插手一事，可是他的语调听起来一点儿也不像是反对我这样做，而更像是和我话家常。
Nor was this all I had effected; for when the next messenger came (as he did not long afterwards) from the Master, he got nothing away with him but a letter. 这又不全是我自己的功劳，因为大少爷下一个信使来了之后（其实与上次间隔时间不长）除了一封信外，别的什么也没带走。
For some while back it had been I myself who had conducted these affairs; Mr. Henry not setting pen to paper, and I only in the dryest and most formal terms. 那之前有段时间，只有我自己处理这些事情，亨利先生从不写回信，而我回信的用语都很正式，干巴巴的，不带任何感情。
But this letter I did not even see; it would scarce be pleasant reading, for Mr. Henry felt he had his wife behind him for once, and I observed, on the day it was despatched, he had a very gratified expression. 然而这封信，我连见都没见到，我敢肯定这封信读起来肯定不会让人高兴，因为这是第一次亨利先生得到他妻子的支持，我还看到，信寄出去的那天，他流露出了一种欣慰的神情。
Things went better now in the family, though it could scarce be pretended they went well. 尽管称不上宽裕，但是家里的境况变得好点儿了。
There was now at least no misconception; there was kindness upon all sides; and I believe my patron and his wife might again have drawn together if he could but have pocketed his pride, and she forgot (what was the ground of all) her brooding on another man. 至少现在家里人之间没了误解，到处弥漫着善意。我相信，只要主子收起他那种骄傲、他太太忘记对另一个男人的思念（这是问题的根本原因），他们夫妻俩就能够和好如初。
It is wonderful how a private thought leaks out; it is wonderful to me now how we should all have followed the current of her sentiments; and though she bore herself quietly, and had a very even disposition, yet we should have known whenever her fancy ran to Paris. 一个人的心思是怎样泄露出来的，真叫人百思不得其解；而我们怎样顺着她现在的心思，也让我想不通；尽管她克制得很好，情绪平稳，可是不管她的心思什么时候飞到巴黎，我们都能察觉到。
And would not any one have thought that my disclosure must have rooted up that idol?
I think there is the devil in women: all these years passed, never a sight of the man, little enough kindness to remember (by all accounts) even while she had him, the notion of his death intervening, his heartless rapacity laid bare to her; that all should not do, and she must still keep the best place in her heart for this accursed fellow, is a thing to make a plain man rage. 我认为女人有邪恶的一面：这么多年过去了，她见都没见过他，也没有任何是值得留恋的（据大家所说），他们谈恋爱的时候，他死的噩耗传了来，他无情的贪婪暴露在她的面前；尽管那个男人做了那么多不该做的事，可是她的心里依然装着那个可憎的家伙，即使搁在一个大老粗身上，他也会勃然大怒的。
I had never much natural sympathy for the passion of love; but this unreason in my patron’s wife disgusted me outright with the whole matter. 我对爱情，一直没什么感同身受，可是少奶奶的无理取闹却令我作呕。
I remember checking a maid because she sang some bairnly kickshaw while my mind was thus engaged; and my asperity brought about my ears the enmity of all the petticoats about the house; of which I reeked very little, but it amused Mr. Henry, who rallied me much upon our joint unpopularity. 我记得有一次，我正在出神，一位女仆因为唱起了幼稚的儿歌，我便狠狠地申斥了她；我的苛刻引发了家里女佣的集体仇视，对那些我根本不在乎，这却逗乐了亨利先生，他与我一道都讨人嫌。
It is strange enough (for my own mother was certainly one of the salt of the earth, and my Aunt Dickson, who paid my fees at the University, a very notable woman), but I have never had much toleration for the female sex, possibly not much understanding; and being far from a bold man, I have ever shunned their company. 我母亲是个社会精英，迪克森姑姑又为我交了大学学费，她还是个名人。但是奇怪的是，我对女人一直没什么耐心，或是不了解她们，一见到他们就胆怯地逃得老远。
Not only do I see no cause to regret this diffidence in myself, but have invariably remarked the most unhappy consequences follow those who were less wise. 我不仅不为自己的胆怯后悔，还经常谈起那些不明智的家伙的可悲下场。
So much I thought proper to set down, lest I show myself unjust to Mrs. Henry. 我插手此事就此为止，以免对亨利太太有失公允。
And, besides, the remark arose naturally, on a re-perusal of the letter which was the next step in these affairs, and reached me, to my sincere astonishment, by a private hand, some week or so after the departure of the last messenger. 可是，那些糟糕下场又自然而然地跑了出来，接下来就是那封信了，令我震惊的是，这封信是让人捎来的，离上封信有好几个星期了。
Letter from Colonel BURKE (afterwards Chevalier) to MR. MACKELLAR. 寄信人：伯克上校（即后来的伯克骑士） 收信人：麦凯勒先生
TROYES IN CHAMPAGNE, July 12, 1756 法国香槟省特鲁瓦市，1756 年 7 月 12 日
My Dear Sir,—You will doubtless be surprised to receive a communication from one so little known to you; but on the occasion I had the good fortune to rencounter you at Durrisdeer, I remarked you for a young man of a solid gravity of character: a qualification which I profess I admire and revere next to natural genius or the bold chivalrous spirit of the soldier. 亲爱的麦凯勒先生，收到一个陌生人的来信，您无疑会感到吃惊，有幸在达里斯迪尔家见到您，我觉得您是个很庄重的人，这种性格就像是天才或战士的骑士精神一样让我欣赏和崇拜。
I was, besides, interested in the noble family which you have the honour to serve, or (to speak more by the book) to be the humble and respected friend of; and a conversation I had the pleasure to have with you very early in the morning has remained much upon my mind. 还有，我对您有幸侍奉，或者（确切地说）您这么谦逊可敬的人所结交的那个家族很感兴趣。那天早上我与您那段愉悦的谈话，依然铭记于我的脑海中。
Being the other day in Paris, on a visit from this famous city, where I am in garrison, I took occasion to inquire your name (which I profess I had forgot) at my friend, the Master of B.; and a fair opportunity occurring, I write to inform you of what’s new. 有一天，我随军队驻守在巴黎，参观这个著名城市的时候，我向我的朋友巴伦特雷少爷，询问了您的名字（我的确忘了），绝佳机会出现了，我可以写信告诉您一些新消息。
The Master of B. (when we had last some talk of him together) was in receipt, as I think I then told you, of a highly advantageous pension on the Scots Fund. 巴伦特雷少爷（上次我们谈到了他）收到了苏格兰基金会的高额抚恤金，这一点我想我上次已经告诉您了。
He next received a company, and was soon after advanced to a regiment of his own. 接着他掌管了一个连，很快又发展成了一个团。
My dear sir, I do not offer to explain this circumstance; any more than why I myself, who have rid at the right hand of Princes, should be fubbed off with a pair of colours and sent to rot in a hole at the bottom of the province. 亲爱的麦凯勒先生，我不会解释这件事情，也不想解释为什么以前我是王公贵族的左右手，竟会被一对勋章给打发到了穷乡僻壤。
Accustomed as I am to Courts, I cannot but feel it is no atmosphere for a plain soldier; and I could never hope to advance by similar means, even could I stoop to the endeavour. 虽然我已经习惯了宫廷生活，可是我现在所处的环境就是普通的士兵也适应不了。即使我可以同样卑鄙，也从没希望用相同的手段去达到那一目的。
But our friend has a particular aptitude to succeed by the means of ladies; and if all be true that I have heard, he enjoyed a remarkable protection. 可是我们的朋友却习惯于利用女人来达到目的，如果我听说的都是真的，那么他倒乐于石榴裙的保护。
It is like this turned against him; for when I had the honour to shake him by the hand, he was but newly released from the Bastille, where he had been cast on a sealed letter; and, though now released, has both lost his regiment and his pension. 可是现在这种依赖却不利于他了，当我这次有幸同他握手的时候，他刚从巴士底狱释放出来，有封密信告发了他。虽然被释放，但他却不光失去了军团，也没了抚恤金。
My dear sir, the loyalty of a plain Irishman will ultimately succeed in the place of craft; as I am sure a gentleman of your probity will agree. 亲爱的麦凯勒先生，我相信在权谋的道路上，一个平凡的爱尔兰人能靠他的忠诚最终取得成功，我同样相信您这样一位正直的绅士也这样认为。
Now, sir, the Master is a man whose genius I admire beyond expression, and, besides, he is my friend; but I thought a little word of this revolution in his fortunes would not come amiss, for, in my opinion, the man’s desperate. 先生，大少爷的才智令我崇拜得无以言表，加上他还是我的朋友，所以说两句他现在时运不济，也没有不妥之处，因为在我看来，他已穷途末路了。
He spoke, when I saw him, of a trip to India (whither I am myself in some hope of accompanying my illustrious countryman, Mr. Lally); but for this he would require (as I understood) more money than was readily at his command. 我见到他的时候，他说要去印度（我自己也有可能跟一个叫拉利的杰出老乡去），可是要去印度他需要（据我所知）更多的钱，他手里的不够。
You may have heard a military proverb: that it is a good thing to make a bridge of gold to a flying enemy? 你可能听过军旅里的一条谚语：穷寇莫追。
I trust you will take my meaning and I subscribe myself, with proper respects to my Lord Durrisdeer, to his son, and to the beauteous Mrs. Durie, 我相信你会明白我的意思，替我问候达里斯迪尔老爷、少爷以及漂亮的少奶奶。
My dear Sir, 此致
Your obedient humble servant, 敬礼
FRANCIS BURKE. 弗朗西斯·伯克
This missive I carried at once to Mr. Henry; and I think there was but the one thought between the two of us: that it had come a week too late. 我立即把这封信呈给了亨利先生，我认为我们只有一个想法：就是这封信晚到了一周。
I made haste to send an answer to Colonel Burke, in which I begged him, if he should see the Master, to assure him his next messenger would be attended to. 我马上给伯克上校写了回信，在信中我求他如果他能见到大少爷，告诉他，他的下个信差一定不会空手而归。
But with all my haste I was not in time to avert what was impending; the arrow had been drawn, it must now fly. 尽管我一刻不敢耽搁，但我还是不能阻止将要发生的事情，箭在弦上，不得不发。
I could almost doubt the power of Providence (and certainly His will) to stay the issue of events; and it is a strange thought, how many of us had been storing up the elements of this catastrophe, for how long a time, and with how blind an ignorance of what we did. 我几乎怀疑上帝（还有他的意愿）阻止事情发生的能力；我还有个奇怪的念头，是我们让灾难一步步到了这个地步，很长时间以来，我们对自己的所作所为是多么熟视无睹。
From the coming of the Colonel’s letter, I had a spyglass in my room, began to drop questions to the tenant folk, and as there was no great secrecy observed, and the freetrade (in our part) went by force as much as stealth, I had soon got together a knowledge of the signals in use, and knew pretty well to an hour when any messenger might be expected. 自从上校来信后，我在房间里装了一个小型望远镜，开始询问佃户，也没发现什么大秘密。此时我们这一带的走私活动，既有暗地里的，也有使用武力的，我很快就侦查到了通用信号及信使出现的时间，可以精确到小时。
I say, I questioned the tenants; for with the traders themselves, desperate blades that went habitually armed, I could never bring myself to meddle willingly. 我是说，我询问了些佃户，因为那些走私犯都是些全副武装的亡命之徒，我可不愿意和他们有什么瓜葛。
Indeed, by what proved in the sequel an unhappy chance, I was an object of scorn to some of these braggadocios; who had not only gratified me with a nickname, but catching me one night upon a by-path, and being all (as they would have said) somewhat merry, had caused me to dance for their diversion. 事后我不幸地成了这些吹牛大王的讽刺对象，他们不仅给我起了外号，而且一天晚上从小路上抓到了我，他们竟十分开心，让我跳舞供他们消遣。
The method employed was that of cruelly chipping at my toes with naked cutlasses, shouting at the same time “Square-Toes”; and though they did me no bodily mischief, I was none the less deplorably affected, and was indeed for several days confined to my bed: a scandal on the state of Scotland on which no comment is required. 他们折磨我的法子是一边用水手刀戳我的脚趾，还一边喊着“方脚趾”；尽管他们没对我造成身体上的伤害，却使我沮丧不已，不得不在床上躺了好几天，这在苏格兰称得上是丑闻了，只是没人议论罢了。
It happened on the afternoon of November 7th, in this same unfortunate year, that I espied, during my walk, the smoke of a beacon fire upon the Muckleross. 那年真是流年不利， 11 月 7 日下午，我散步时，突然看见马克尔罗思烽火台冒起了烟。
It was drawing near time for my return; but the uneasiness upon my spirits was that day so great that I must burst through the thickets to the edge of what they call the Craig Head. 离回家的时刻越来越近，可是那天我心情非常烦躁，非得穿过灌木林到大家称之为头型角的边缘。
The sun was already down, but there was still a broad light in the west, which showed me some of the smugglers treading out their signal fire upon the Ross, and in the bay the lugger lying with her sails brailed up. 太阳虽已下山，可是西方仍有一大片亮光，我看见那些走私犯正在烽火台里走出来，海湾上一艘帆船正卷起帆篷。
She was plainly but new come to anchor, and yet the skiff was already lowered and pulling for the landing-place at the end of the long shrubbery. 这艘船也就是刚靠岸，不过小木筏已放了下来，正朝长灌木林尾端的海岸驶去。
And this I knew could signify but one thing, the coming of a messenger for Durrisdeer. 我知道这肯定意味着，达里斯迪尔来了一位信使。
I laid aside the remainder of my terrors, clambered down the brae—a place I had never ventured through before, and was hid among the shore-side thickets in time to see the boat touch. 我把那恐惧抛在了脑后，走下了陡坡——这个地方我以前从不敢走，藏到岸边的灌木林里，从这里可以看到船靠岸。
Captain Crail himself was steering, a thing not usual; by his side there sat a passenger; and the men gave way with difficulty, being hampered with near upon half a dozen portmanteaus, great and small. 克雷尔船长亲自驾驶，这不寻常，他旁边坐着一名乘客，船上的人行走很不方便，因为旁边五六个大大小小的旅行衣箱造成了不少麻烦。
But the business of landing was briskly carried through; and presently the baggage was all tumbled on shore, the boat on its return voyage to the lugger, and the passenger standing alone upon the point of rock, a tall slender figure of a gentleman, habited in black, with a sword by his side and a walking-cane upon his wrist. 不过船靠岸却很顺利，现在行李都已搬到了岸上，小船也往回划了，那个乘客独自站在岩石上，他很高很瘦，看似是个绅士，穿着一身黑色衣服，佩着剑，拄着手杖。
As he so stood, he waved the cane to Captain Crail by way of salutation, with something both of grace and mockery that wrote the gesture deeply on my mind. 他站在那里朝船长挥着拐杖致敬，既庄重又滑稽的形象深深地印在我的脑海里。
No sooner was the boat away with my sworn enemies than I took a sort of half courage, came forth to the margin of the thicket, and there halted again, my mind being greatly pulled about between natural diffidence and a dark foreboding of the truth. 载着与我不共戴天的仇人的船一离开，我就鼓起勇气走向灌木林的边缘地带，停在那里，我脑子里满是胆怯和对事实的不祥预兆。
Indeed, I might have stood there swithering all night, had not the stranger turned, spied me through the mists, which were beginning to fall, and waved and cried on me to draw near. 事实上，要不是那个陌生人转过身来，透过薄雾（那时已开始下雾了）看见我，并朝我招手叫我走近他，我可能一整晚都站在那里犹豫不决。
I did so with a heart like lead. 我怀着沉重的心情走近他。
“Here, my good man,” said he, in the English accent, “there are some things for Durrisdeer.” 他操着英格兰口音说道：“你好，善良的人，这儿有一些给达里斯迪尔家的东西。”
I was now near enough to see him, a very handsome figure and countenance, swarthy, lean, long, with a quick, alert, black look, as of one who was a fighter, and accustomed to command; upon one cheek he had a mole, not unbecoming; a large diamond sparkled on his hand; his clothes, although of the one hue, were of a French and foppish design; his ruffles, which he wore longer than common, of exquisite lace; and I wondered the more to see him in such a guise when he was but newly landed from a dirty smuggling lugger. 我现在已离他很近，能看清他，他皮肤黝黑，很帅，身材也很好，看着很精明，好似一个战士，习惯于发号施令；脸颊上有颗痣，并不显得突兀；手上戴着一颗闪闪发光的大钻石；他穿的衣服虽只有一个颜色，却是法国的浮华式样；衣服上的花边比常人的要长，且带有精致的蕾丝；他刚从一艘肮脏的走私船上登岸，怎么是这种漂亮的形象呢，我真是想不通。
At the same time he had a better look at me, toised me a second time sharply, and then smiled. 这时，他用稍微柔和的目光看了看我，又打量了我一番，笑了。
“I wager, my friend,” says he, “that I know both your name and your nickname. 他说：“朋友，我敢打赌我不但知道你的名字，甚至连你的外号都知道。
I divined these very clothes upon your hand of writing, Mr. Mackellar.” 麦凯勒先生，根据你的笔迹，我就能猜到你的衣着打扮。”
At these words I fell to shaking. 听到他的话，我开始颤抖起来。
“Oh,”’ says he, “you need not be afraid of me. 他又说：“哈，你用不着怕我。
I bear no malice for your tedious letters; and it is my purpose to employ you a good deal. 对你那乏味的信我没任何不满，请你吃顿大餐就是我此行的目的。
You may call me Mr. Bally: it is the name I have assumed; or rather (since I am addressing so great a precision) it is so I have curtailed my own. 你也可以叫我巴利，这是我的化名，或更正确的说是我把名字简化成了这样。
Come now, pick up that and that”—indicating two of the portmanteaus. 快点儿，拿起这个箱子，还有那个，”他指着两个行李箱说，
“That will be as much as you are fit to bear, and the rest can very well wait. “你提两个正好，剩下的先搁在这儿。
Come, lose no more time, if you please.” 来，请吧，别耽误时间了。”
His tone was so cutting that I managed to do as he bid by a sort of instinct, my mind being all the time quite lost. 他的语调如此强硬，我不知不觉地就照他说的做了，我脑子里当时一片空白。
No sooner had I picked up the portmanteaus than he turned his back and marched off through the long shrubbery, where it began already to be dusk, for the wood is thick and evergreen. 我一提起那些箱子，他就转过身，朝着长长的灌木林里走去了，因为灌木很粗，又是四季常青，所以当时林子里已经很暗了。
I followed behind, loaded almost to the dust, though I profess I was not conscious of the burthen; being swallowed up in the monstrosity of this return, and my mind flying like a weaver’s shuttle. 我跟在他后面，虽然我说行李不重，可我已累得快趴下了，回来的路上带着这么重的行李，我的思绪就像织工的梭子来回思索着。
On a sudden I set the portmanteaus to the ground and halted. 突然，我把箱子放地上，不走了。
He turned and looked back at me. 他转过身，回头看着我。
“Well?” said he. 问道：“你怎么了？”
“You are the Master of Ballantrae?” “您是巴伦特雷少爷吗？”
“You will do me the justice to observe,” says he, “I have made no secret with the astute Mackellar.” 他说：“你应该看出来了，我在精明的麦凯勒先生面前可没什么秘密可言。”
“And in the name of God,” cries I, “what brings you here? 我喊道：“以上帝的名义回答我，您为什么到这儿来？
Go back, while it is yet time.” 趁着还不晚，赶紧回去！”
“I thank you,” said he. 他说：“谢谢了。
“Your master has chosen this way, and not I; but since he has made the choice, he (and you also) must abide by the result. 是你家少爷自己选择让我来的，又不是我自己愿意来，既然他这样决定了，那么他（还有你）就得承担后果。
And now pick up these things of mine, which you have set down in a very boggy place, and attend to that which I have made your business.” 你把我的东西放在了一个很脏的地方，现在立刻拾起来，照我刚才的吩咐做。”
But I had no thought now of obedience; I came straight up to him. 我现在可不想任人宰割，我径直朝他走去。
“If nothing will move you to go back,” said I; “though, sure, under all the circumstances, any Christian or even any gentleman would scruple to go forward ...” 说道：“如果没什么事能让您回去，那么，不管是什么原因，任何一个基督教人或任何一个绅士都不会无所顾忌地朝前走……”
“These are gratifying expressions,” he threw in. 他插嘴说：“这话听着倒是顺耳。”
“If nothing will move you to go back,” I continued, “there are still some decencies to be observed. 我继续说道：“如果没什么可以让您打道回府，那您也该懂点儿礼貌吧。
Wait here with your baggage, and I will go forward and prepare your family. 和您的行李在这儿等着，我先去告诉您的家人。
Your father is an old man; and ...” 您的父亲已年迈，还有……”
I stumbled ...“there are decencies to be observed.” 我结结巴巴地说，“规矩还是要遵守的。”
“Truly,” said he, “this Mackellar improves upon acquaintance. 他说：“现在这个麦凯勒先生的确比刚才那个更让我刮目相看啊！
But look you here, my man, and understand it once for all—you waste your breath upon me, and I go my own way with inevitable motion.” 但是，看看你是什么样子，我让你彻底明白，你白费口舌了，我不会有任何改变，还是照自己的计划进行。”
“Ah!” says I. 我喊道：“啊！
“Is that so? 是吗？
We shall see then!” 那我们走着瞧！”
And I turned and took to my heels for Durrisdeer. 我转身朝着达里斯迪尔府邸走去。
He clutched at me and cried out angrily, and then I believe I heard him laugh, and then I am certain he pursued me for a step or two, and (I suppose) desisted. 他一把抓住我，生气地叫喊，然后我又听到他笑，接着，我肯定他又紧追了我一两步，最后（我猜想）他停住了脚步。
One thing at least is sure, that I came but a few minutes later to the door of the great house, nearly strangled for the lack of breath, but quite alone. 我清楚地记得，几分钟后我来到了那栋大房子门前，我累得差点儿没喘过气，门口没人。
Straight up the stair I ran, and burst into the hall, and stopped before the family without the power of speech; but I must have carried my story in my looks, for they rose out of their places and stared on me like changelings. 我径直跑上台阶，冲到大厅里，在全家人面前停了下来，已累得说不出话；但是他们肯定从我脸上看出来发生了什么事情，他们都从座位上站了起来，像呆子一样盯着我看。
“He has come,” I panted out at last. 终于，我气喘吁吁地说：“他来了。”
“He?” said Mr. Henry. 亨利先生问：“他？”
“Himself,” said I. 我答道：“就他一个人。”
“My son?” cried my lord. 老爷喊道：“我的儿子吗？
“Imprudent, imprudent boy! 傻孩子！傻孩子！
Oh, could he not stay where he was safe!” 他就不能呆在那个安全的地方吗？”
Never a word says Mrs. Henry; nor did I look at her, I scarce knew why. 亨利太太一句话也没说，我也没看她，也不知道这是为什么。
“Well,” said Mr. Henry, with a very deep breath, “and where is he?” 亨利先生深吸一口气说：“好吧，他在哪里？”
“I left him in the long shrubbery,” said I. 我说：“我让他呆在长灌木林里。”
“Take me to him,” said he. 他说：“带我去见他。”
So we went out together, he and I, without another word from any one; and in the midst of the gravelled plot encountered the Master strolling up, whistling as he came, and beating the air with his cane. 于是，他和我一块出去了，两人一言不发，在砾石铺的土地上碰到了正在闲逛的大少爷，他吹着口哨走来，随手甩着手杖。
There was still light enough overhead to recognise, though not to read, a countenance. 在落日的余晖中依然能看见他，只是看不清他的脸而已。
“Ah! “哈！
Jacob,” says the Master. 雅各布，”大少爷说道，
“So here is Esau back.” “呵，以扫回来了！”
“James,” says Mr. Henry, “for God’s sake, call me by my name. 亨利先生说：“詹姆斯，看在上帝的份上，请叫我的名字吧。
I will not pretend that I am glad to see you; but I would fain make you as welcome as I can in the house of our fathers.” 我不会假装很高兴见到你，但我还是会在先辈的房子里尽量地欢迎你。
“Or in MY house? or YOURS?” says the Master. 大少爷说：“是我的房子，或是你的？
“Which were you about to say? 你说是谁的？
But this is an old sore, and we need not rub it. 这是一块旧伤疤，我们不必去揭它。
If you would not share with me in Paris, I hope you will yet scarce deny your elder brother a corner of the fire at Durrisdeer?” 如果你不愿与我在巴黎有难同当，我希望你能在达里斯迪尔给我一席之地。”
“That is very idle speech,” replied Mr. Henry. “这都是些废话，”亨利先生说，
“And you understand the power of your position excellently well.” “你很清楚地知道你在这个家的地位。”
“Why, I believe I do,” said the other with a little laugh. 大少爷浅笑着说：“我有什么理由不知道呢，我相信我确实明白。
And this, though they had never touched hands, was (as we may say) the end of the brothers’ meeting; for at this the Master turned to me and bade me fetch his baggage. 尽管他们连手都没握，但这的确就是（我们可以这么说）两兄弟见面的结束，因为此时大少爷转身命令我拿着他的行李。
I, on my side, turned to Mr. Henry for a confirmation; perhaps with some defiance. 而我，却转身询问亨利先生的答允，也许我这么做带有一些挑衅。
“As long as the Master is here, Mr. Mackellar, you will very much oblige me by regarding his wishes as you would my own,” says Mr. Henry. 亨利先生说道：“麦凯勒先生，既然大少爷回来了，你就像服从我的命令一样，服从大少爷。
“We are constantly troubling you: will you be so good as send one of the servants?”—with an accent on the word. 我们一直都在麻烦你，你能找个佣人来吗？”——佣人这个词他说得很重。
If this speech were anything at all, it was surely a well-deserved reproof upon the stranger; and yet, so devilish was his impudence, he twisted it the other way. 如果这段对话有所指，那就是对这个陌生人当之无愧的谴责，可是大少爷却如此厚颜无耻，竟把它歪曲成另外一回事儿。
“And shall we be common enough to say ‘Sneck up’?” inquires he softly, looking upon me sideways. 大少爷斜眼看着我，柔声地问：“说‘滚开’是不是更像老百姓的说法啊？”
Had a kingdom depended on the act, I could not have trusted myself in words; even to call a servant was beyond me; I had rather serve the man myself than speak; and I turned away in silence and went into the long shrubbery, with a heart full of anger and despair. 如果管理一个地方需要装腔作势，那么我可不认为我有什么能耐能把佣人叫来，何况命令佣人超出了我的权限。我宁愿自己伺候这个人，也不愿去叫别人。我默默地走开了，心里充满着愤怒和绝望走向了长长的灌木林。
It was dark under the trees, and I walked before me and forgot what business I was come upon, till I near broke my shin on the portmanteaus. 树林里很黑，我一直走，要不是我差点儿在箱子上磕坏我的小腿，我早忘了我是来干嘛的了。
Then it was that I remarked a strange particular; for whereas I had before carried both and scarce observed it, it was now as much as I could do to manage one. 接着我发现了一件特别奇怪的事，尽管我以前碰到过两次，并且都没发现，但这次我已经有能力解决这件事情了。
And this, as it forced me to make two journeys, kept me the longer from the hall. 这件差事让我跑了两趟，让我离达里斯迪尔家更远了。
When I got there, the business of welcome was over long ago; the company was already at supper; and by an oversight that cut me to the quick, my place had been forgotten. 当我到家的时候，“欢迎仪式”早完了，全家人都已经在吃晚饭，我一眼就看见桌子旁没了我的座位。
I had seen one side of the Master’s return; now I was to see the other. 这是大少爷回来的第一个影响，很快我就看到了第二个影响。
It was he who first remarked my coming in and standing back (as I did) in some annoyance. 他第一个注意到我进入屋内且带点儿怒气地站在后面（我的确如此）。
He jumped from his seat. 他从座位上跳起来。
“And if I have not got the good Mackellar’s place!” cries he. “可不是我抢了麦凯勒先生的座位吧！”他喊道，
“John, lay another for Mr. Bally; I protest he will disturb no one, and your table is big enough for all.” “约翰，为巴利少爷另搬个座位，我坚信他不会碍到任何人，家里的桌子够大，能容下我们所有的人。”
I could scarce credit my ears, nor yet my senses, when he took me by the shoulders and thrust me, laughing, into my own place—such an affectionate playfulness was in his voice. 我真不敢相信自己的眼睛，也不敢相信自己的感觉，大少爷竟抓着我的双肩把我推到我自己的座位上——他的腔调里充满着亲昵的嬉闹。
And while John laid the fresh place for him (a thing on which he still insisted), he went and leaned on his father’s chair and looked down upon him, and the old man turned about and looked upwards on his son, with such a pleasant mutual tenderness that I could have carried my hand to my head in mere amazement. 约翰为他新加了一个座位（他一直这样要求），他倚着父亲的座位，朝下望着老人，而老爷转过身来仰望着自己的儿子，流露出一种让人欣喜的互亲互爱的神情，我惊讶地直挠头。
Yet all was of a piece. 而这些只是九牛一毛。
Never a harsh word fell from him, never a sneer showed upon his lip. 大少爷一句严厉的话也没说，也没表现出任何不恭。
He had laid aside even his cutting English accent, and spoke with the kindly Scots’ tongue, that set a value on affectionate words; and though his manners had a graceful elegance mighty foreign to our ways in Durrisdeer, it was still a homely courtliness, that did not shame but flattered us. 他讲话甚至不带一点儿英格兰口音，而是一口亲切的苏格兰腔，使得那些亲昵的词汇让人听起来更舒服。尽管他那优雅庄重的言行与达里斯迪尔府的方式迥异，但依然是种家常礼貌，不但没有让我们感到羞耻，反而让我们受宠若惊。
All that, he did throughout the meal, indeed, drinking wine with me with a notable respect, turning about for a pleasant word with John, fondling his father’s hand, breaking into little merry tales of his adventures, calling up the past with happy reference—all he did was so becoming, and himself so handsome, that I could scarce wonder if my lord and Mrs. Henry sat about the board with radiant faces, or if John waited behind with dropping tears. 这顿饭，他时而与我对饮，流露出一种显而易见的尊重，时而转过身与约翰说两句令人开心的话，时而摸着父亲的手，时而讲一些他旅行中的趣事，回想起过去，他一脸的开心——他的言谈举止是如此温文尔雅，以至于我不难想象坐在桌子边的老爷和少奶奶一定是春风得意的样子，而在后面服侍的约翰早已泪流满面了。
As soon as supper was over, Mrs. Henry rose to withdraw. 饭一吃完，亨利太太就起身离开。
“This was never your way, Alison,” said he. 大少爷道：“艾莉森，你以前可不是这样啊？”
“It is my way now,” she replied: which was notoriously false, “and I will give you a good-night, James, and a welcome—from the dead,” said she, and her voice dropped and trembled. “我现在就是这样，”她答道，但这可是弥天大谎啊，“詹姆斯，晚安，恭喜你死里逃生。”她的声音低了下来，并颤抖着。
Poor Mr. Henry, who had made rather a heavy figure through the meal, was more concerned than ever; pleased to see his wife withdraw, and yet half displeased, as he thought upon the cause of it; and the next moment altogether dashed by the fervour of her speech. 可怜的亨利先生，整顿饭都很尴尬，此时更加愁绪满怀了，看到太太离座，他很开心，可是想到她离开的原因就又很不快，而听到她的话后就悲喜交加了。
On my part, I thought I was now one too many; and was stealing after Mrs. Henry, when the Master saw me. 我觉得自己在这里是多余的，就跟在少奶奶后面想溜走，可此时大少爷看见了我。
“Now, Mr. Mackellar,” says he, “I take this near on an unfriendliness. 他说：“麦凯勒先生，我认为这可不礼貌啊！
I cannot have you go: this is to make a stranger of the prodigal son; and let me remind you where—in his own father’s house! 我不可能让你走，你这是把我这个回头浪子当外人啊！你可别忘了，这可是在浪子父亲的家里啊！
Come, sit ye down, and drink another glass with Mr. Bally.” 来，坐下，和巴利先生再喝一杯。”
“Ay, ay, Mr. Mackellar,” says my lord, “we must not make a stranger either of him or you. 老爷说：“对，对，麦凯勒，我们既不能把他当外人，也不能拿你当外人。
I have been telling my son,” he added, his voice brightening as usual on the word, “how much we valued all your friendly service.” 我一直对我的儿子说，对你友好的服侍我们是多么感激。”说到“儿子”这个词时，如往常一样，老爷的声音格外洪亮。
So I sat there, silent, till my usual hour; and might have been almost deceived in the man’s nature but for one passage, in which his perfidy appeared too plain. 于是我一声不吭地坐在那里，直到我休息，要不是因为一段插曲暴露出了他那背信弃义的本质，我可能就被大少爷骗了。
Here was the passage; of which, after what he knows of the brothers’ meeting, the reader shall consider for himself. 这个插曲是这样的，各位读者知道这俩兄弟怎样见面后，也不难想象接下来会发生什么了。
Mr. Henry sitting somewhat dully, in spite of his best endeavours to carry things before my lord, up jumps the Master, passes about the board, and claps his brother on the shoulder. 尽管亨利先生在老爷面前尽力讨其欢心，可是他看起来有些呆滞，大少爷跳起来，绕过桌子，拍着弟弟的肩膀，
“Come, come, HAIRRY LAD,” says he, with a broad accent such as they must have used together when they were boys, “you must not be downcast because your brother has come home. 用他们小时候的腔调说：“拜托，小亨利，别因为大哥回来了，就那么垂头丧气。
All’s yours, that’s sure enough, and little I grudge it you. 一切都是你的，千真万确，我一点儿也不怪你。
Neither must you grudge me my place beside my father’s fire.” 你也别因为我在父亲身边的位置就怨我。"
“And that is too true, Henry,” says my old lord with a little frown, a thing rare with him. “亨利，这是真的。”老爷略皱眉头（这很稀奇）道，
“You have been the elder brother of the parable in the good sense; you must be careful of the other.” “确切地说，你可是寓言里的老大，你必须爱惜自己的兄弟。”
“I am easily put in the wrong,” said Mr. Henry. 亨利先生说：“你们可冤枉我了。”
“Who puts you in the wrong?” cried my lord, I thought very tartly for so mild a man. 老爷喊道：“谁冤枉你了？”对老爷这样温和的人而言，这语调实在是太犀利了。
“You have earned my gratitude and your brother’s many thousand times: you may count on its endurance; and let that suffice.” “我一直都感激你，你哥哥对你更是万分的感激，我们会一直感激你的，你知足吧。”
“Ay, Harry, that you may,” said the Master; and I thought Mr. Henry looked at him with a kind of wildness in his eye. 大少爷说：“呃，亨利，我们会一直感激你的。”我觉得亨利先生瞪着他，眼里带着一种愤怒。
On all the miserable business that now followed, I have four questions that I asked myself often at the time and ask myself still:- Was the man moved by a particular sentiment against Mr. Henry? or by what he thought to be his interest? or by a mere delight in cruelty such as cats display and theologians tell us of the devil? or by what he would have called love? 发生了那么多悲惨的事情后，我一直不停地问自己四个问题，现在也还没有找到答案，这四个问题是：第一，大少爷是不是对亨利先生有种天生的敌意？第二，他是否太沉湎于自己的兴趣？第三，他是否乐于残忍的游戏，就像猫捉老鼠或神学家所谓的邪恶？第四，他是否被所谓的爱情所驱使？
My common opinion halts among the three first; but perhaps there lay at the spring of his behaviour an element of all. 我认为是前三个原因导致他的所作所为，不过也许是几个原因兼而有之。
As thus:—Animosity to Mr. Henry would explain his hateful usage of him when they were alone; the interests he came to serve would explain his very different attitude before my lord; that and some spice of a design of gallantry, his care to stand well with Mrs. Henry; and the pleasure of malice for itself, the pains he was continually at to mingle and oppose these lines of conduct. 具体如下：对亨利先生的敌意可能是他私下对其恶意利用的原因；他对利益的追求则是他在老爷面前迥异态度的原因；他那刻意的殷勤是为了给亨利太太留下个好印象；以残忍为乐则是他一直以来时而把它们混合，时而把它们对立的原因。
Partly because I was a very open friend to my patron, partly because in my letters to Paris I had often given myself some freedom of remonstrance, I was included in his diabolical amusement. 可能是因为我对主子忠心耿耿，有目共睹，也可能是因为在我写往巴黎的信中表达了一些不满，我也成了他恶魔般消遣的对象。
When I was alone with him, he pursued me with sneers; before the family he used me with the extreme of friendly condescension. 我与他独处时，他会嘲笑着对我刨根问底；在家人面前，他则利用我到极致来显示他的纡尊降贵。
This was not only painful in itself; not only did it put me continually in the wrong; but there was in it an element of insult indescribable. 不仅这些事本身就令人痛苦，而且他一直在利用我，还有种不可名状的侮辱。
That he should thus leave me out in his dissimulation, as though even my testimony were too despicable to be considered, galled me to the blood. 他可以假装眼里没我这号人，认为我的话可鄙，根本不予考虑，羞辱我到骨子里。
But what it was to me is not worth notice. 但这对我而言并不值一提。
I make but memorandum of it here; and chiefly for this reason, that it had one good result, and gave me the quicker sense of Mr. Henry’s martyrdom. 我在这里只是记流水账，恰恰因为这，让我更快地看到了亨利先生所受的苦难。
It was on him the burthen fell. 他承担了一切。
How was he to respond to the public advances of one who never lost a chance of gibing him in private? 他是怎样应对一个私下不放掉任何机会嘲弄他的人，在别人面前对他的那种殷勤？
How was he to smile back on the deceiver and the insulter? 他怎么能对那个欺骗自己、侮辱自己的人以德报怨？
He was condemned to seem ungracious. 亨利先生因为貌似无礼而受到谴责。
He was condemned to silence. 因保持沉默受到谴责。
Had he been less proud, had he spoken, who would have credited the truth? 如果他不那么骄傲，如果他不保持沉默，谁还会相信真相呢？
The acted calumny had done its work; my lord and Mrs. Henry were the daily witnesses of what went on; they could have sworn in court that the Master was a model of long-suffering good-nature, and Mr. Henry a pattern of jealousy and thanklessness. 恶意的诽谤起了作用，老爷和亨利太太坐视每天发生的事，他们坚信大少爷是长期受委屈的大好人，而亨利先生则是一个既妒忌他人又忘恩负义的角色。
And ugly enough as these must have appeared in any one, they seemed tenfold uglier in Mr. Henry; for who could forget that the Master lay in peril of his life, and that he had already lost his mistress, his title, and his fortune? 这在任何人看来已极尽丑恶，但亨利先生的丑恶千倍于此。对于那个曾命在旦夕、赔了夫人、丢了爵位、失去财产的大少爷，谁能不可怜呢？
“Henry, will you ride with me?” asks the Master one day. 一天大少爷问道：“亨利，你愿意和我一块儿骑马吗？”
And Mr. Henry, who had been goaded by the man all morning, raps out: “I will not.” 而被大少爷气了一早上的亨利先生厉声道：“不愿意。”
“I sometimes wish you would be kinder, Henry,” says the other, wistfully. 大少爷惆怅地说：“有时候我真希望你的脾气能好点儿。”
I give this for a specimen; but such scenes befell continually. 我只是拿这举个例子，以后这种事情还接踵而至。
Small wonder if Mr. Henry was blamed; small wonder if I fretted myself into something near upon a bilious fever; nay, and at the mere recollection feel a bitterness in my blood. 难怪亨利先生老挨训；我烦躁不已，近乎发狂，现在回想起来也痛到骨子里。
Sure, never in this world was a more diabolical contrivance: so perfidious, so simple, so impossible to combat. 大少爷的行径绝对是最邪恶的阴谋，因为他的背信弃义是赤裸裸的，但却难以揭穿。
And yet I think again, and I think always, Mrs. Henry might have road between the lines; she might have had more knowledge of her husband’s nature; after all these years of marriage she might have commanded or captured his confidence. 我认为，其实我一直这样认为，亨利太太可能早已看出端倪，可能更了解丈夫的本性，结婚这么多年了，她可能已经获得了他的信任。
And my old lord, too—that very watchful gentleman—where was all his observation? 还有老爷——如此善于观察的绅士——这时怎么看不出所以然来呢？
But, for one thing, the deceit was practised by a master hand, and might have gulled an angel. 原因可能有四：第一，大少爷是个骗子老手，甚至能骗到神仙。
For another (in the case of Mrs. Henry), I have observed there are no persons so far away as those who are both married and estranged, so that they seem out of ear-shot or to have no common tongue. 第二，对亨利太太而言，我还没见过有像这两口子的夫妻呢，他们俩不管是结婚时，还是分居后，彼此置若罔闻，没有共同语言。
For a third (in the case of both of these spectators), they were blinded by old ingrained predilection. 第三，对于这两个旁观者，老爷和少奶奶都被根深蒂固的偏爱蒙蔽了双眼。
And for a fourth, the risk the Master was supposed to stand in (supposed, I say—you will soon hear why) made it seem the more ungenerous to criticise; and, keeping them in a perpetual tender solicitude about his life, blinded them the more effectually to his faults. 第四，大少爷理应处于的危险（我说的“理应”，读者们在下文里能读到原因），让他的阴谋诡计躲过一劫，不会遭到批判；大家一直担忧他的性命，因此蒙蔽了双眼，看不见他的恶行。
It was during this time that I perceived most clearly the effect of manner, and was led to lament most deeply the plainness of my own. 就是从大少爷的所作所为中，我发现了行为举止的巨大作用，开始哀叹自己完全不懂这套。
Mr. Henry had the essence of a gentleman; when he was moved, when there was any call of circumstance, he could play his part with dignity and spirit; but in the day’s commerce (it is idle to deny it) he fell short of the ornamental. 亨利先生有着绅士的优秀品质，当他被感染，或周围环境需要时，他能够本份地做好自己的工作，且不失庄重与活力。可在日常生活的经营中（不用否认），他不善于花言巧语。
The Master (on the other hand) had never a movement but it commanded him. 而大少爷骨子里就善于这套。
So it befell that when the one appeared gracious and the other ungracious, every trick of their bodies seemed to call out confirmation. 当一个看起来高尚，一个看起来低俗时，他们的一言一行也会被大家认为有高尚低俗之分。
Not that alone: but the more deeply Mr. Henry floundered in his brother’s toils, the more clownish he grew; and the more the Master enjoyed his spiteful entertainment, the more engagingly, the more smilingly, he went! 不止如此，亨利先生越在他哥哥的阴谋里打转，他就变得越滑稽；大少爷越得意于自己那刻毒的乐趣，则陷得越来越深，不可自拔。
So that the plot, by its own scope and progress, furthered and confirmed itself. 因此随着阴谋一步步升级，就变本加厉了。
It was one of the man’s arts to use the peril in which (as I say) he was supposed to stand. 利用自身所处的危险，是大少爷的手段。
He spoke of it to those who loved him with a gentle pleasantry, which made it the more touching. 他用温和、幽默的方式把危险讲给那些真心爱他的人听，使这些危险更感人。
To Mr. Henry he used it as a cruel weapon of offence. 面对亨利先生，他就把这当作对付他的残忍武器。
I remember his laying his finger on the clean lozenge of the painted window one day when we three were alone together in the hall. 我记得有天，大厅里只有我们三个人，大少爷把手指放在彩色玻璃的菱形花纹上。
“Here went your lucky guinea, Jacob,” said he. 说道：“雅各布，这是你的幸运币。”
And when Mr. Henry only looked upon him darkly, “Oh!” he added, “you need not look such impotent malice, my good fly. 而此时亨利先生只是呆若木鸡地抬头望着他，他又说：“哈！我可怜的苍蝇啊，你不用在乎这无果的邪恶。
You can be rid of your spider when you please. 随你的意，你任何时候都能脱离这蜘蛛网。
How long, O Lord? 我的上帝啊！究竟需要多长时间呢？
When are you to be wrought to the point of a denunciation, scrupulous brother? 我那谨慎老实的弟弟呀，你何时才会谴责、揭发我呀？
It is one of my interests in this dreary hole. 这可是我在这沉闷的地方的乐趣之一。
I ever loved experiment.” 我一直都喜欢探险。”
Still Mr. Henry only stared upon him with a grooming brow, and a changed colour; and at last the Master broke out in a laugh and clapped him on the shoulder, calling him a sulky dog. 亨利先生依然一言不发，只是盯着大少爷，眉头微皱，有点儿抑郁，他的脸色变了，最后大少爷突然笑起来，拍着亨利的肩膀说他是个生气的小狗。
At this my patron leaped back with a gesture I thought very dangerous; and I must suppose the Master thought so too, for he looked the least in the world discountenance, and I do not remember him again to have laid hands on Mr. Henry. 此时我的主子向后跳去，伴着一个我认为非常危险的手势，我相信大少爷也认为如此，因为他看起来大惊失色，我记得大少爷再也没有把手放到亨利先生的身上了。
But though he had his peril always on his lips in the one way or the other, I thought his conduct strangely incautious, and began to fancy the Government—who had set a price upon his head—was gone sound asleep. 尽管他总是把自己经历的危险挂在嘴边，但我还是觉得他的行为有点儿不慎，开始怀疑政府（曾悬赏捉拿他）是不是睡着了。
I will not deny I was tempted with the wish to denounce him; but two thoughts withheld me: one, that if he were thus to end his life upon an honourable scaffold, the man would be canonised for good in the minds of his father and my patron’s wife; the other, that if I was anyway mingled in the matter, Mr. Henry himself would scarce escape some glancings of suspicion. 我不否认自己想告发他，但一想到下面这两点，我就打住了这种想法。第一，如果他光荣地死在绞刑架上，这家伙在他父亲和我主子夫人的心目中则就成了圣人；第二，如果我掺和进这件事，亨利先生也脱不了干系。
And in the meanwhile our enemy went in and out more than I could have thought possible, the fact that he was home again was buzzed about all the country-side, and yet he was never stirred. 与此同时，我和主子的对手进进出出，多得让我没想到，而且他又回来了，整个村子已经议论纷纷了，但是他却不为所动。
Of all these so-many and so-different persons who were acquainted with his presence, none had the least greed—as I used to say in my annoyance—or the least loyalty; and the man rode here and there—fully more welcome, considering the lees of old unpopularity, than Mr. Henry—and considering the freetraders, far safer than myself. 认识大少爷的形形色色的人中，没有一个贪婪的——当我心烦的时候，我经常这么说——也没有一个忠于他；大少爷骑着马到处走，考虑到他之前的毫不受欢迎，现在他可是比亨利先生还受欢迎了；考虑到走私贩，他现在可比我自己还要安全。
Not but what he had a trouble of his own; and this, as it brought about the gravest consequences, I must now relate. 但他也有个麻烦，这个麻烦带来了最严重的后果，我现在必须写写了。
The reader will scarce have forgotten Jessie Broun; her way of life was much among the smuggling party; Captain Crail himself was of her intimates; and she had early word of Mr. Bally’s presence at the house. 各位读者肯定没有忘记杰丝·布龙，她几乎整天和走私贩混在一处，克雷尔船长就和她很熟，她早就知道巴利先生回来的消息了。
In my opinion, she had long ceased to care two straws for the Master’s person; but it was become her habit to connect herself continually with the Master’s name; that was the ground of all her play-acting; and so now, when he was back, she thought she owed it to herself to grow a haunter of the neighbourhood of Durrisdeer. 我认为她早就不在乎大少爷这个人了，与大少爷纠缠不清可能已经成了她的习惯，这是她哗众取宠的资本，而现在大少爷回来了，她认为自己可以常来达里斯迪尔府周围逛游了。
The Master could scarce go abroad but she was there in wait for him; a scandalous figure of a woman, not often sober; hailing him wildly as “her bonny laddie,” quoting pedlar’s poetry, and, as I receive the story, even seeking to weep upon his neck. 几乎大少爷每次出门，她都在那里等着，这个女人水性杨花，常常醉得一塌糊涂，用小贩的语气称大少爷为“她的帅情郎”，据我所知，她还搂着大少爷的脖子哭呢！
I own I rubbed my hands over this persecution; but the Master, who laid so much upon others, was himself the least patient of men. 说真的，看到这种情况，我倒是有点儿兴奋，不过这个对别人要求太多的人现在倒是忍不住了。
There were strange scenes enacted in the policies. 据说出现了一些奇怪的情况。
Some say he took his cane to her, and Jessie fell back upon her former weapons—stones. 有些人说他用手杖打了杰丝，她就重操旧武器——石子儿。
It is certain at least that he made a motion to Captain Crail to have the woman trepanned, and that the Captain refused the proposition with uncommon vehemence. 至少可以肯定的是，大少爷曾让克雷尔船长把杰丝碎尸万段，但船长以极其强烈的口吻拒绝了这一提议。
And the end of the matter was victory for Jessie. 最后，这件事以杰丝的胜利告终。
Money was got together; an interview took place, in which my proud gentleman must consent to be kissed and wept upon; and the woman was set up in a public of her own, somewhere on Solway side (but I forget where), and, by the only news I ever had of it, extremely ill-frequented. 大少爷必须给杰死抚恤金，两人进行了一次谈判，我们那骄傲的绅士还被她吻了吻，抱着脖子哭泣。这个女人在索尔韦附近（具体地点我忘了）开了个酒馆，之后我听到的唯一消息是，那个地方没什么生意。
This is to look forward. 继续往下看。
After Jessie had been but a little while upon his heels, the Master comes to me one day in the steward’s office, and with more civility than usual, “Mackellar,” says he, “there is a damned crazy wench comes about here. 杰丝刚开始纠缠大少爷的时候，他就来到管家的房间，比以往礼貌得多，说：“麦凯勒先生，有个该死的贱人来了。
I cannot well move in the matter myself, which brings me to you. 我自己解决不了，所以我来找你帮忙了。
Be so good as to see to it: the men must have a strict injunction to drive the wench away.” 小心点儿，让下人们把这贱人赶走。”
“Sir,” said I, trembling a little, “you can do your own dirty errands for yourself.” 我说：“先生，您还是自行解决这件丑事吧！”我的声音有点儿颤抖。
He said not a word to that, and left the room. 他一句话也没说，就走了出去。
Presently came Mr. Henry. 这时，亨利先生进来了。
“Here is news!” cried he. 喊道：“这是怎么了！
“It seems all is not enough, and you must add to my wretchedness. 看起来我的麻烦还不够，你还火上浇油。
It seems you have insulted Mr. Bally.” 你好像冒犯大少爷了。”
“Under your kind favour, Mr. Henry,” said I, “it was he that insulted me, and, as I think, grossly. 我说：“亨利先生，承蒙相助，是大少爷侮辱我，而且是狠狠地侮辱了我。
But I may have been careless of your position when I spoke; and if you think so when you know all, my dear patron, you have but to say the word. 不过可能是我说话时没考虑您的立场，主子，如果您知道了事情的来龙去脉后还这么想，那您就说是我冒犯了大少爷吧。
For you I would obey in any point whatever, even to sin, God pardon me!” 您的命令，我无条件服从。即使让我做罪恶的事情，上帝也会宽恕我！”
And thereupon I told him what had passed. 接着我告诉了他发生了什么。
Mr. Henry smiled to himself; a grimmer smile I never witnessed. 亨利先生自己笑了起来，我从未听过如此阴森的笑声。
“You did exactly well,” said he. 他说：“你做得非常好，
“He shall drink his Jessie Broun to the dregs.” 他必须自己吞下杰丝·布龙这颗恶果。”
And then, spying the Master outside, he opened the window, and crying to him by the name of Mr. Bally, asked him to step up and have a word. 然后，他看见大少爷在外面，就打开窗户，喊着巴利先生，让他上楼说句话。
“James,” said he, when our persecutor had come in and closed the door behind him, looking at me with a smile, as if he thought I was to be humbled, “you brought me a complaint against Mr. Mackellar, into which I have inquired. 大少爷进来，关上了门，笑着看着我，好像认为我要服从他的命令似的，这时亨利先生说：“詹姆斯，我刚知道了你为什么埋怨麦凯勒先生。
I need not tell you I would always take his word against yours; for we are alone, and I am going to use something of your own freedom. 不用我告诉你，我一直站在他一边，因为这儿没外人，我想委屈你一回。
Mr. Mackellar is a gentleman I value; and you must contrive, so long as you are under this roof, to bring yourself into no more collisions with one whom I will support at any possible cost to me or mine. 麦凯勒先生是我敬重的正人君子，只要你还在这个屋檐下,你必须设法与他不发生任何冲突，因为我会不惜一切代价挺他。
As for the errand upon which you came to him, you must deliver yourself from the consequences of your own cruelty, and, none of my servants shall be at all employed in such a case.” 至于你刚才要他做的事，你必须自行承担你恶行的后果，我的仆人不会为你干这种事。”
“My father’s servants, I believe,” says the Master. 大少爷说：“我看应该是父亲的仆人吧！”
“Go to him with this tale,” said Mr. Henry. 亨利先生道：“那就把这件事告诉他！”
The Master grew very white. 大少爷脸色煞白。
He pointed at me with his finger. 他用手指着我。
“I want that man discharged,” he said. “我要辞掉那家伙。”他说道。
“He shall not be,” said Mr. Henry. 亨利先生说：“他不会被辞的。”
“You shall pay pretty dear for this,” says the Master. 大少爷道：“你要为此付出沉重代价。”
“I have paid so dear already for a wicked brother,” said Mr. Henry, “that I am bankrupt even of fears. 亨利先生说：“我已经因为有个邪恶的哥哥而付出了巨大代价，我现在已天不怕，地不怕了。
You have no place left where you can strike me.” 你没什么可威胁我的了。”
“I will show you about that,” says the Master, and went softly away. 大少爷说：“咱们走着瞧。”然后就轻轻地走了。
“What will he do next, Mackellar?” cries Mr. Henry. 亨利先生喊道：“麦凯乐，接下来他要做什么？”
“Let me go away,” said I. 我说：“让我走吧！
“My dear patron, let me go away; I am but the beginning of fresh sorrows.” 我的好主子啊！让我走吧，我会给您招惹新麻烦的。”
“Would you leave me quite alone?” said he. 他说：“你要撇下我自个儿一人吗？”
We were not long in suspense as to the nature of the new assault. 我们担心不久就有新的事情要发生。
Up to that hour the Master had played a very close game with Mrs. Henry; avoiding pointedly to be alone with her, which I took at the time for an effect of decency, but now think to be a most insidious art; meeting her, you may say, at meal-time only; and behaving, when he did so, like an affectionate brother. 不久，大少爷在亨利太太身上花了很多心思；他避免与她独处，当时我还以为那是君子行径，现在方知那是大少爷最阴险的手段。读者朋友们可能会说，大少爷只有在吃饭的时候，才能见到她；而他的行为举止就像是一个温柔的兄长。
Up to that hour, you may say he had scarce directly interfered between Mr. Henry and his wife; except in so far as he had manoeuvred the one quite forth from the good graces of the other. 在那之前，我们可以说他并没有直接介入亨利先生和他太太当中，只是仗着一个的善良，在另外一个面前耍点儿花招。
Now all that was to be changed; but whether really in revenge, or because he was wearying of Durrisdeer and looked about for some diversion, who but the devil shall decide? 现在，一切都有了变化，不知是为了报仇，还是因为厌倦了达里斯迪尔的生活，而做些改变？鬼才知道呢！
From that hour, at least, began the siege of Mrs. Henry; a thing so deftly carried on that I scarce know if she was aware of it herself, and that her husband must look on in silence. 他至少是从那时开始了对亨利太太的围攻，他做得很巧妙，以致我都怀疑少奶奶是否察觉到，同时她的丈夫也没有采取任何行动。
The first parallel was opened (as was made to appear) by accident. 第一回合偶然间开始了（好似计划好了一样）。
The talk fell, as it did often, on the exiles in France; so it glided to the matter of their songs. 就像往常一样，大少爷与亨利太太的谈话从他流亡法国开始，然后又谈到了流亡者唱的歌。
“There is one,” says the Master, “if you are curious in these matters, that has always seemed to me very moving. 大少爷说：“如果你对流亡的事感兴趣，有那么一首歌感人至深。
The poetry is harsh; and yet, perhaps because of my situation, it has always found the way to my heart. 歌词虽然有点儿粗俗，但也许是因为我当时的处境，它总能唱出我的心声。
It is supposed to be sung, I should tell you, by an exile’s sweetheart; and represents perhaps, not so much the truth of what she is thinking, as the truth of what he hopes of her, poor soul! in these far lands.” 我应该告诉你，这首歌其实是流亡者的心肝宝贝唱的，内容不是她在想什么，而是他对她的希望，远方可怜的人啊！”
And here the Master sighed, “I protest it is a pathetic sight when a score of rough Irish, all common sentinels, get to this song; and you may see, by their falling tears, how it strikes home to them. 此时大少爷叹了口气，接着说，“我坚信十几个粗鄙的爱尔兰哨兵一齐唱这首歌是多么悲惨的场面啊！看到他们流泪，可以想象到他们是多么思念家乡。”
It goes thus, father,” says he, very adroitly taking my lord for his listener, “and if I cannot get to the end of it, you must think it is a common case with us exiles.” 详细情形是这样的，父亲，”大少爷很巧妙地让老爷也成了他的听众，“如果我不把这件事情讲清楚，你们一定会认为这对我们流亡者而言，是司空见惯的事。”
And thereupon he struck up the same air as I had heard the Colonel whistle; but now to words, rustic indeed, yet most pathetically setting forth a poor girl’s aspirations for an exiled lover; of which one verse indeed (or something like it) still sticks by me:— 接着我听到与上校口哨声同样的曲调，而且还附上了歌词，但是低俗不堪，唱出了可怜的少女对流亡在外的情人痛苦的思念之情，其中有一段也打动了我，这段貌似如下：
O, I will dye my petticoat red, 噢！我要把裙子染红，
With my dear boy I’ll beg my bread, 为情郎讨顿饭菜，
Though all my friends should wish me dead, 因威利死于荒原，
For Willie among the rushes, O! 朋友皆劝我与他共赴黄泉。
He sang it well, even as a song; but he did better yet a performer. 虽然这首歌他唱得很好，但他表演得更好。
I have heard famous actors, when there was not a dry eye in the Edinburgh theatre; a great wonder to behold; but no more wonderful than how the Master played upon that little ballad, and on those who heard him, like an instrument, and seemed now upon the point of failing, and now to conquer his distress, so that words and music seemed to pour out of his own heart and his own past, and to be aimed directly at Mrs. Henry. 我听说过演技好的演员能把爱丁堡剧院的观众感动得无一不落泪。尽管那很神奇，但也没大少爷唱的这一曲厉害，他唱歌如同奏乐一样，随着声音渐渐逝去，他如泣如诉，有时也克制自己的感情，他的心声和他的过去都随着这些歌词和音乐流泻出来，好似是直接唱给亨利太太听的。
And his art went further yet; for all was so delicately touched, it seemed impossible to suspect him of the least design; and so far from making a parade of emotion, you would have sworn he was striving to be calm. 他的表演登峰造极，在场的每个人都深受感动，根本没有对他的虚情假意有任何怀疑，但他并没有露出任何炫耀的神情，他一定是在尽力保持平静。
When it came to an end, we all sat silent for a time; he had chosen the dusk of the afternoon, so that none could see his neighbour’s face; but it seemed as if we held our breathing; only my old lord cleared his throat. 大少爷唱完后，我们都坐那里一言不发，他故意选在黄昏时分来唱，好让大家都看不清周围的人的脸，但大家似乎都屏住了呼吸，只有老爷清了清嗓子。
The first to move was the singer, who got to his feet suddenly and softly, and went and walked softly to and fro in the low end of the hall, Mr. Henry’s customary place. 第一个有所动作的是唱歌的大少爷，他突然在大厅的一边轻轻地走来走去，在亨利先生喜欢的、惯常的位置。
We were to suppose that he there struggled down the last of his emotion; for he presently returned and launched into a disquisition on the nature of the Irish (always so much miscalled, and whom he defended) in his natural voice; so that, before the lights were brought, we were in the usual course of talk. 我们想他尽力克制住了自己的感情，因为很快他就用平静的声音，对爱尔兰人的性格（经常被误解，他此时正在为其辩解）发表了长篇大论，因此，在蜡烛点亮前，我们就在昏暗中继续谈话。
But even then, methought Mrs. Henry’s face was a shade pale; and, for another thing, she withdrew almost at once. 即使大厅里很暗，但我也能看到亨利太太脸色煞白，她很快就离开了。
The next sign was a friendship this insidious devil struck up with innocent Miss Katharine; so that they were always together, hand in hand, or she climbing on his knee, like a pair of children. 第二个回合是，这个忘恩负义的恶魔竟对无辜的凯瑟琳小姐下手了，他们总是在一块，手牵着手，她有时爬到他的膝盖上，玩得像两个孩子。
Like all his diabolical acts, this cut in several ways. 像他所有邪恶的行为一样，这一举动带来的危害是多方面的。
It was the last stroke to Mr. Henry, to see his own babe debauched against him; it made him harsh with the poor innocent, which brought him still a peg lower in his wife’s esteem; and (to conclude) it was a bond of union between the lady and the Master. 这是对亨利先生最沉重的一击，看到自己的孩子被人教唆着跟自己作对，这让亨利先生对单纯的小姐很严厉，自己的妻子也因此更加看不起他，总之，大少爷与亨利太太结成了同盟。
Under this influence, their old reserve melted by daily stages. 在这一影响下，日复一日，他们旧情复燃了。
Presently there came walks in the long shrubbery, talks in the Belvedere, and I know not what tender familiarity. 此时，他们俩常在长灌木林里散步，在阳台上聊天，我不知道还有没有别的什么逾矩之行。
I am sure Mrs. Henry was like many a good woman; she had a whole conscience but perhaps by the means of a little winking. 我肯定虽然亨利太太是个好女人，但老虎也有打盹的时候。
For even to so dull an observer as myself, it was plain her kindness was of a more moving nature than the sisterly. 连我这个无聊的旁观者都能看出，她现在的温柔可不只是作为一个弟媳该有的。
The tones of her voice appeared more numerous; she had a light and softness in her eye; she was more gentle with all of us, even with Mr. Henry, even with myself; methought she breathed of some quiet melancholy happiness. 话多了，眼里满是柔情蜜意，她不管和我们大家在一起，还是与亨利先生独处，甚至是只和我在一起的时候，她都更温柔了。我想她心中正窃喜呢！
To look on at this, what a torment it was for Mr. Henry! 然而这些事对亨利先生而言，是多么大的折磨啊！
And yet it brought our ultimate deliverance, as I am soon to tell. 可是这却最终拯救了我们，我下面就写到了。
The purport of the Master’s stay was no more noble (gild it as they might) than to wring money out. 大少爷回来的目的，不管别人怎么美化，其实他就是来要钱。
He had some design of a fortune in the French Indies, as the Chevalier wrote me; and it was the sum required for this that he came seeking. 伯克骑士写信告诉过我，大少爷想去印度挣钱，所以他回家弄点儿本钱。
For the rest of the family it spelled ruin; but my lord, in his incredible partiality, pushed ever for the granting. 虽然这对家里其他人而言是灭顶之灾，但老爷可是拼命地给他攒钱。
The family was now so narrowed down (indeed, there were no more of them than just the father and the two sons) that it was possible to break the entail and alienate a piece of land. 这个家，人越来越少（事实上只有老爷和他的两个儿子了），也就有可能打破规矩卖地了。
And to this, at first by hints, and then by open pressure, Mr. Henry was brought to consent. 刚开始时，还只是偷偷进行，后来就明目张胆了，亨利先生不得不同意。
He never would have done so, I am very well assured, but for the weight of the distress under which he laboured. 我非常确信，要不是他承受的巨大的痛苦，亨利先生是不会这么做的。
But for his passionate eagerness to see his brother gone, he would not thus have broken with his own sentiment and the traditions of his house. 要不是为了让自己的哥哥快点儿离开，他才不会为了解脱自己而打破家族的传统呢。
And even so, he sold them his consent at a dear rate, speaking for once openly, and holding the business up in its own shameful colours. 即使是这样，他们还是花了好大劲才让他默许的，他只公开地说过一次，自己还感觉很羞愧呢。
“You will observe,” he said, “this is an injustice to my son, if ever I have one.” 亨利先生说：“你们会看到，假如我有儿子的话，这对他不公平。”
“But that you are not likely to have,” said my lord. 老爷说：“可你不可能有儿子啊！”
“God knows!” says Mr. Henry. 亨利先生答道：“谁知道呢！
“And considering the cruel falseness of the position in which I stand to my brother, and that you, my lord, are my father, and have the right to command me, I set my hand to this paper. 考虑到哥哥给我带来的悲惨境遇，老爷，也就是我的父亲，您有权命令我，我这就同意签字卖地。
But one thing I will say first: I have been ungenerously pushed, and when next, my lord, you are tempted to compare your sons, I call on you to remember what I have done and what he has done. 但有件事我得提前说明，大家一直以为我是小气鬼，以后您在比较您两个儿子的时候，请记住他做了什么，我又做了什么。
Acts are the fair test.” 事实胜于雄辩！”
My lord was the most uneasy man I ever saw; even in his old face the blood came up. 老爷此时忧愁满面，我再也没见过比这还忧愁的脸了，即使他已年迈，可此时也脸红脖子粗地说：
“I think this is not a very wisely chosen moment, Henry, for complaints,” said he. “亨利，我可不认为这是你发牢骚的好时候，
“This takes away from the merit of your generosity.” 这让你看起来可小气了。”
“Do not deceive yourself, my lord,” said Mr. Henry. 亨利先生答道：“老爷，别自欺欺人了。
“This injustice is not done from generosity to him, but in obedience to yourself.” 您的不公可不是为了对他大方，而是为了您自己吧。”
“Before strangers ...” begins my lord, still more unhappily affected. 此时老爷依然不大高兴，开始说道：“当着外人……”
“There is no one but Mackellar here,” said Mr. Henry; “he is my friend. 亨利先生说：“除了麦凯勒，这儿没外人，他是我的朋友。
And, my lord, as you make him no stranger to your frequent blame, it were hard if I must keep him one to a thing so rare as my defence.” 老爷，责备他的时候您怎么不拿他当外人了，现在我要为自己辩解的时候，也就不能把他算作外人了。”
Almost I believe my lord would have rescinded his decision; but the Master was on the watch. 我几乎以为老爷要改变主意了，可大少爷也就在后面看着。
“Ah! “喂！
Henry, Henry,” says he, “you are the best of us still. 亨利，亨利，你依然是咱们哥俩中最棒的。
Rugged and true! 千真万确！
Ah! man, I wish I was as good.” 我真希望自己和你一样好。”大少爷说道。
And at that instance of his favourite’s generosity my lord desisted from his hesitation, and the deed was signed. 在他慷慨的提议之下，老爷不再犹豫，签下了卖地的契约。
As soon as it could he brought about, the land of Ochterhall was sold for much below its value, and the money paid over to our leech and sent by some private carriage into France. 交易一达成，奥彻豪的土地就卖了，价钱远低于它的市值，卖地的钱都给了大少爷这个吸血鬼，他用马车都运到了法国。
Or so he said; though I have suspected since it did not go so far. 反正他自己是这么说的，我可怀疑这些钱不等到法国就给他花光了。
And now here was all the man’s business brought to a successful head, and his pockets once more bulging with our gold; and yet the point for which we had consented to this sacrifice was still denied us, and the visitor still lingered on at Durrisdeer. 现在他的目的达成，口袋里又装满了我们的金子，我们做出了如此大的牺牲，可他还不感激我们，依然赖在达里斯迪尔府。
Whether in malice, or because the time was not yet come for his adventure to the Indies, or because he had hopes of his design on Mrs. Henry, or from the orders of the Government, who shall say? but linger he did, and that for weeks. 不管他是有不当目的，是前往印度群岛的时机不到，是他对亨利太太的阴谋诡计还未结束，或是政府禁止他出国，究竟为何，谁知道呢？但他又在家呆了几个星期。
You will observe I say: from the orders of Government; for about this time the man’s disreputable secret trickled out. 从政府的命令中，你会明白我什么意思的，因为此时大少爷臭名昭著、不为人知的秘密昭然若揭了。
The first hint I had was from a tenant, who commented on the Master’s stay, and yet more on his security; for this tenant was a Jacobitish sympathiser, and had lost a son at Culloden, which gave him the more critical eye. 关于这方面的线索，我先是从一个佃户那里得知的，他对大少爷依然呆在家里说三道四，议论他的人身安全，因为这个佃户是一个同情詹姆斯二世的人，又因在卡洛登战役中失去了一个儿子，这让他更加愤世嫉俗。
“There is one thing,” said he, “that I cannot but think strange; and that is how he got to Cockermouth.” 他说：“我觉得有件事很奇怪，大少爷是怎么去科克茅斯的。”
“To Cockermouth?” said I, with a sudden memory of my first wonder on beholding the man disembark so point-de-vice after so long a voyage. “去科克茅斯？”我问道。这勾起了我对他在海上航行了那么长时间后怎么如此狼狈上岸的第一次疑惑。
“Why, yes,” says the tenant, “it was there he was picked up by Captain Crail. 那个佃户答道：“怎么了，是科克茅斯啊！就是在那儿克雷尔船长救了他。
You thought he had come from France by sea? 你以为他是从法国乘船回来的？
And so we all did.” 我们以前也都那样以为。”
I turned this news a little in my head, and then carried it to Mr. Henry. 我把这个消息在脑子里捋了一下，然后就去告诉亨利先生了。
“Here is an odd circumstance,” said I, and told him. 我告诉他：“有个怪事儿。”
“What matters how he came, Mackellar, so long as he is here?” groans Mr. Henry. 亨利先生哼道：“麦凯勒，只要他在这儿一天，那他是怎么回来的，又有什么关系呢？”
“No, sir,” said I, “but think again! 我回答道：“不是，再猜！
Does not this smack a little of some Government connivance? 这是否意味着政府对他的纵容呢？
You know how much we have wondered already at the man’s security.” 你知道我们对他的安全已经多么担忧了。”
“Stop,” said Mr. Henry. 亨利先生说：“住嘴！
“Let me think of this.” 我再考虑考虑。”
And as he thought, there came that grim smile upon his face that was a little like the Master’s. 他思考的时候脸上现出了一种有点儿像大少爷的冷笑。
“Give me paper,” said he. 说道：“拿纸来。”
And he sat without another word and wrote to a gentleman of his acquaintance—I will name no unnecessary names, but he was one in a high place. 他再也没说话，坐下来给一个认识的绅士写信——我不用指名道姓，但是个有头有脸的人。
This letter I despatched by the only hand I could depend upon in such a case—Macconochie’s; and the old man rode hard, for he was back with the reply before even my eagerness had ventured to expect him. 我把这封信交给了在这种情况下唯一信任的邮差——麦科诺基，这个老家伙骑马飞快，我想都没想到他能这么快带着答复回来！
Again, as he read it, Mr. Henry had the same grim smile. 亨利先生读信时，脸上又现出了那种冷笑。
“This is the best you have done for me yet, Mackellar,” says he. 他说：“麦凯勒，这是你为我做得最漂亮的一件事了，
“With this in my hand I will give him a shog. 有这封信在手，我会给他点儿颜色瞧瞧。
Watch for us at dinner.” 吃饭时，等着看好戏吧！”
At dinner accordingly Mr. Henry proposed some very public appearance for the Master; and my lord, as he had hoped, objected to the danger of the course. 吃饭时，亨利先生提议让大少爷多露露脸，如亨利先生预想的一样，老爷认为这样很危险，表示反对。
“Oh!” says Mr. Henry, very easily, “you need no longer keep this up with me. 亨利先生轻巧地说：“呵，你再也不用瞒我了，
I am as much in the secret as yourself.” 您知道的秘密我也知道。”
“In the secret?” says my lord. 老爷问道：“什么秘密？
“What do you mean, Henry? 亨利，你在说些什么？
I give you my word, I am in no secret from which you are excluded.” 我告诉你，我们没有任何事情瞒着你。”
The Master had changed countenance, and I saw he was struck in a joint of his harness. 大少爷大惊失色，我看到他简直是魂不附体。
“How?” says Mr. Henry, turning to him with a huge appearance of surprise. 亨利先生朝着大少爷，满脸惊讶地说：“我是怎么知道的？
“I see you serve your masters very faithfully; but I had thought you would have been humane enough to set your father’s mind at rest.” 你为你的主子忠心卖命，我还以为你没有丧尽天良，不会让老父亲为你担心呢。”
“What are you talking of? “你在说什么呢？
I refuse to have my business publicly discussed. 我拒绝在大庭广众之下，谈我的事情。
I order this to cease,” cries the Master very foolishly and passionately, and indeed more like a child than a man. 我命令你住嘴。”大少爷喊道，他看起来很傻，很激动，不像个大人，倒像个孩子。
“So much discretion was not looked for at your hands, I can assure you,” continued Mr. Henry. 亨利先生继续说：“我向你保证，你不用那么害怕，
“For see what my correspondent writes”—unfolding the paper—“‘It is, of course, in the interests both of the Government and the gentleman whom we may perhaps best continue to call Mr. Bally, to keep this understanding secret; but it was never meant his own family should continue to endure the suspense you paint so feelingly; and I am pleased mine should be the hand to set these fears at rest. 看看人家给我写了什么，”他打开信，读道，“当然了，这封信是关于政府和一个我们最好一直称作巴利少爷的绅士，这样有利于我们了解这个秘密。但这并不意味着他的家人也应当忍受这种疑虑，我很高兴能借我之手来给你们消除这种疑虑。
Mr. Bally is as safe in Great Britain as yourself.’” 巴利少爷在大不列颠和你一样安全。”
“Is this possible?” cries my lord, looking at his son, with a great deal of wonder and still more of suspicion in his face. 老爷喊道：“这是真的吗？”看着自己的儿子，满脸惊讶，更多的是疑虑。
“My dear father,” says the Master, already much recovered. “亲爱的父亲大人，”大少爷已缓过神来说道，
“I am overjoyed that this may be disclosed. “这个秘密公之于众，我反而更开心了。
My own instructions, direct from London, bore a very contrary sense, and I was charged to keep the indulgence secret from every one, yourself not excepted, and indeed yourself expressly named—as I can show in black and white unless I have destroyed the letter. 我直接从伦敦接到的指令与这完全不同，命令我必须对每一个人都隐瞒这个秘密，您也不例外，实际上是特别提到了您，我的父亲。我还没把那封信毁了，所以白纸黑字明摆着。
They must have changed their mind very swiftly, for the whole matter is still quite fresh; or rather, Henry’s correspondent must have misconceived that part, as he seems to have misconceived the rest. 因为命令下达不久，所以他们一定是很快就改变了想法。要么就是亨利的朋友如同误解其他的部分一样，也误解了那一部分。
To tell you the truth, sir,” he continued, getting visibly more easy, “I had supposed this unexplained favour to a rebel was the effect of some application from yourself; and the injunction to secrecy among my family the result of a desire on your part to conceal your kindness. 父亲，告诉您真相吧！”大少爷明显已放松很多，继续说，“对我这个叛乱分子给予不问缘由的宽容，我原以为是您周旋的结果；在家人之间继续保守这个秘密，是您不愿意公开您的善心。
Hence I was the more careful to obey orders.
It remains now to guess by what other channel indulgence can have flowed on so notorious an offender as myself; for I do not think your son need defend himself from what seems hinted at in Henry’s letter. 我现在还不知道究竟是何种渠道让我这个臭名昭著的罪犯得到赦免，因为我认为您的儿子不需要为亨利信中暗示的东西辩护。
I have never yet heard of a Durrisdeer who was a turncoat or a spy,” says he, proudly. 我从没听说过达里斯迪尔府出过叛徒或间谍。”他说这些话的时候很神气。
And so it seemed he had swum out of this danger unharmed; but this was to reckon without a blunder he had made, and without the pertinacity of Mr. Henry, who was now to show he had something of his brother’s spirit. 貌似他毫发无损地摆脱了危险；但是却忽略了他所犯的错误以及亨利先生的纠缠不休，此时他有点儿他哥哥的脾气了。
“You say the matter is still fresh,” says Mr. Henry. 亨利先生问道：“你说这件事刚发生。”
“It is recent,” says the Master, with a fair show of stoutness and yet not without a quaver. 大少爷坚定地、不带任何颤抖地回答道：“是最近发生的。”
“Is it so recent as that?” asks Mr. Henry, like a man a little puzzled, and spreading his letter forth again. 亨利先生又问道：“有那么近吗？”他有些困惑，把信又摊开。
In all the letter there was no word as to the date; but how was the Master to know that? 这封信里根本就没有任何关于日期的字眼，大少爷是如何知道日期的呢？
“It seemed to come late enough for me,” says he, with a laugh. 大少爷笑着说：“这封信看起来到得够晚了。”
And at the sound of that laugh, which rang false, like a cracked bell, my lord looked at him again across the table, and I saw his old lips draw together close. 听到那如同裂缝的铃铛般的假笑声，老爷再次看着桌子对面的大少爷，我看见老爷干瘪的嘴唇紧闭着。
“No,” said Mr. Henry, still glancing on his letter, “but I remember your expression. 亨利先生仍然盯着那封信，说道：“不晚，但我记着你说的话了。
You said it was very fresh.” 你说这件事刚发生。”
And here we had a proof of our victory, and the strongest instance yet of my lord’s incredible indulgence; for what must he do but interfere to save his favourite from exposure! 现在有证据表明我们获得了胜利，老爷对大少爷的纵容简直到了令人难以置信的程度；老爷必须插手此事，以免他最喜欢的儿子东窗事发。
“I think, Henry,” says he, with a kind of pitiful eagerness, “I think we need dispute no more. 老爷可怜巴巴地说：“亨利，我看我们别再吵了。
We are all rejoiced at last to find your brother safe; we are all at one on that; and, as grateful subjects, we can do no less than drink to the king’s health and bounty.” 看到你哥哥最后平安无事，我们都很开心，在这一点上我们都是一致的。说点儿让人开心的事吧，让我们一起为国王的健康和慷慨干杯吧。”
Thus was the Master extricated; but at least he had been put to his defence, he had come lamely out, and the attraction of his personal danger was now publicly plucked away from him. 就这样，虽然大少爷摆脱了危险，但至少他也被逼到进行自我辩护的份上，他的真面貌公之于众了，公众对他身处危险的同情，现在也没有了。
My lord, in his heart of hearts, now knew his favourite to be a Government spy; and Mrs. Henry (however she explained the tale) was notably cold in her behaviour to the discredited hero of romance. 老爷现在也从内心深处知道自己最疼爱的儿子是政府的间谍；亨利太太（不管她怎么解释这个故事）也明显地对这个名声败坏的风流公子冷漠多了。
Thus in the best fabric of duplicity, there is some weak point, if you can strike it, which will loosen all; and if, by this fortunate stroke, we had not shaken the idol, who can say how it might have gone with us at the catastrophe? 事物都有两面性，这个成功也有不好的方面，一着不慎，满盘皆输；如果一击不中，没有打破大少爷这个神话，那么他就能让我们自食恶果。
And yet at the time we seemed to have accomplished nothing. 我们似乎一无所获。
Before a day or two he had wiped off the ill-results of his discomfiture, and, to all appearance, stood as high as ever. 短短的一两天后，他就把窘迫带来的坏影响抹去了，与以前的形象一样高大了。
As for my Lord Durrisdeer, he was sunk in parental partiality; it was not so much love, which should be an active quality, as an apathy and torpor of his other powers; and forgiveness (so to mis-apply a noble word) flowed from him in sheer weakness, like the tears of senility. 至于达里斯迪尔老爷，他那份为人父母的偏爱根深蒂固，这倒不是他那份积极向上的爱，而是他的同情与萎靡不振作祟；原谅（不恰当地用一个褒义词）从他那脆弱中一涌而出，如同老人的泪水。
Mrs. Henry’s was a different case; and Heaven alone knows what he found to say to her, or how he persuaded her from her contempt. 而亨利太太则截然不同，只有老天爷知道大少爷对她说了些什么，怎样劝她别看不起他。
It is one of the worst things of sentiment, that the voice grows to be more important than the words, and the speaker than that which is spoken. 感情用事是一件最糟糕的事情，说话的语气比说的内容更加管用，说话的人比说的话更加管用。
But some excuse the Master must have found, or perhaps he had even struck upon some art to wrest this exposure to his own advantage; for after a time of coldness, it seemed as if things went worse than ever between him and Mrs. Henry. 大少爷一定是找了什么借口，或是耍了一些手段把间谍身份的暴露扭转为自己的优势，因为他和亨利太太之间经过一段冷漠过后，反而比以前更加肆无忌惮了。
They were then constantly together. 他俩整天腻在一起。
I would not be thought to cut one shadow of blame, beyond what is due to a half-wilful blindness, on that unfortunate lady; but I do think, in these last days, she was playing very near the fire; and whether I be wrong or not in that, one thing is sure and quite sufficient: Mr. Henry thought so. 对那个不幸的女人，我除了说她自欺欺人以外，不想对此有任何的谴责。但我坚信，在最近这些天里，她是在玩火自焚，不管我是对是错，有一件事是肯定的，显而易见的，那就是亨利先生也是这么想的。
The poor gentleman sat for days in my room, so great a picture of distress that I could never venture to address him; yet it is to be thought he found some comfort even in my presence and the knowledge of my sympathy. 可怜的人在我房里呆了好几天，我以前从来没敢想过他会如此沮丧，也从没想过他会因为我的陪伴和同情而得到一丝安慰。
There were times, too, when we talked, and a strange manner of talk it was; there was never a person named, nor an individual circumstance referred to; yet we had the same matter in our minds, and we were each aware of it. 我们有时候也聊天，但聊天的方式很奇怪，我们从不指名道姓，也从不谈某一件具体的事情，但我们彼此心照不宣。
It is a strange art that can thus be practised; to talk for hours of a thing, and never name nor yet so much as hint at it. 这是门很奇怪的艺术，我们聊几个小时，从不涉及人名，也不暗指某事。
And I remember I wondered if it was by some such natural skill that the Master made love to Mrs. Henry all day long (as he manifestly did), yet never startled her into reserve. 我还记得我那时疑惑是不是大少爷用这种天生的技能整天地向亨利太太示爱，（他做得一点儿都不避讳）却没有吓到她。
To show how far affairs had gone with Mr. Henry, I will give some words of his, uttered (as I have cause not to forget) upon the 26th of February, 1757. 为了表明亨利先生的心境，我把他在 1757 年 2 月 26 日（我有理由记住这个日子）说的话记录下来。
It was unseasonable weather, a cast back into Winter: windless, bitter cold, the world all white with rime, the sky low and gray the sea black and silent like a quarry-hole. 那天天气很反常，好像又回到了寒冬：无风，严寒，霜把大地染了一片白色，天空灰蒙蒙，云层很厚，大海像石洞一样乌黑、寂静。
Mr. Henry sat close by the fire, and debated (as was now common with him) whether “a man” should “do things,” whether “interference was wise,” and the like general propositions, which each of us particularly applied. 亨利先生靠着壁炉坐着，沉思着（现在他经常这样）“作为男人”是否应该“有所作为”、“插手是否明智”，我们俩分别提了几个问题。
I was by the window, looking out, when there passed below me the Master, Mrs. Henry, and Miss Katharine, that now constant trio. 我靠在窗边，向外望去，这时，大少爷、亨利太太和凯瑟琳小姐正从窗下走过，那段时间他们三人形影不离。
The child was running to and fro, delighted with the frost; the Master spoke close in the lady’s ear with what seemed (even from so far) a devilish grace of insinuation; and she on her part looked on the ground like a person lost in listening. 小姐跑来跑去，在霜雾中玩得很开心；大少爷与亨利太太亲密耳语，脸上带着（即使那么远，也能看清的）含沙射影的邪恶神情；亨利太太看着地面，好似全神贯注地听他说话。
I broke out of my reserve. 我不再有所保留。
“If I were you, Mr. Henry,” said I, “I would deal openly with my lord.” “亨利先生，如果我是您，”我说道，“我会在老爷面前把这层窗户纸捅穿。”
“Mackellar, Mackellar,” said he, “you do not see the weakness of my ground. 他说：“麦凯勒啊！麦凯勒！你没有看到我的弱点。
I can carry no such base thoughts to any one—to my father least of all; that would be to fall into the bottom of his scorn. 我不会对任何人采取这种卑劣的手段——尤其是不会对父亲那样；这样老爷会笑掉大牙的。
