The weakness of my ground,” he continued, “lies in myself, that I am not one who engages love. 我的弱点是”，他继续道，“根深蒂固的，我是一个得不到爱的人。
I have their gratitude, they all tell me that; I have a rich estate of it! 他们对我说，他们感激我，我有太多人的感激了！
But I am not present in their minds; they are moved neither to think with me nor to think for me. 但他们并不关心我，他们既不会跟我想的一样，也不为我考虑。
There is my loss!” 我彻底地输了！”
He got to his feet, and trod down the fire. 然后他站起身，踏着火。
“But some method must be found, Mackellar,” said he, looking at me suddenly over his shoulder; “some way must be found. 突然他看着我说：“麦凯勒，我们必须找些法子，必须找些法子。
I am a man of a great deal of patience—far too much—far too much. 我是个有耐心的人，极其、极其有耐心。
I begin to despise myself. 我开始蔑视我自个儿了。
And yet, sure, never was a man involved in such a toil!” 我肯定还从没有人像我这样陷入如此的折磨。”
He fell back to his brooding. 他再次陷入沉思。
“Cheer up,” said I. 我说：“振作起来！
“It will burst of itself.” 事情总会结束的！”
“I am far past anger now,” says he, which had so little coherency with my own observation that I let both fall. 他说：“我现在早已不生气了。”可这与我看到的截然不同，在此，我先不写这些了。
Chapter 5 第五章
Account of All that Passed on the Night on February 27th, 1757. 1757年2月27日夜全记录
On the evening of the interview referred to, the Master went abroad; he was abroad a great deal of the next day also, that fatal 27th; but where he went, or what he did, we never concerned ourselves to ask until next day. 就在我和亨利先生谈话的那天晚上，大少爷出门了。接下来一天，也就是要命的27号，他也出去了很久。直到第三天，我们才问了问他去了哪里以及做了什么。
If we had done so, and by any chance found out, it might have changed all. 如果我们早一点儿问了，并且碰巧发现了什么，事情会截然不同。
But as all we did was done in ignorance, and should be so judged, I shall so narrate these passages as they appeared to us in the moment of their birth, and reserve all that I since discovered for the time of its discovery. 但我们所做的一切都是在不明内情的情况下，这么说一点儿没错。因此，我将原原本本地讲述这些事情，它们是如何产生的，又是怎么结束的。
For I have now come to one of the dark parts of my narrative, and must engage the reader’s indulgence for my patron. 接下来我要记述的是最黑暗的一部分，同时也必须请读者们对我的主子抱着宽容的心态。
All the 27th that rigorous weather endured: a stifling cold; the folk passing about like smoking chimneys; the wide hearth in the hall piled high with fuel; some of the spring birds that had already blundered north into our neighbourhood, besieging the windows of the house or trotting on the frozen turf like things distracted. 27号，恶劣的天气持续了一整天：严寒让人窒息，行人嘴里呼出的气犹如烟筒；大厅的壁炉里加满了柴禾；一些失算已飞回北方的候鸟，被困在窗户上，或像热锅上的蚂蚁一样在上了冻的草皮上跳来跳去。
About noon there came a blink of sunshine, showing a very pretty, wintry, frosty landscape of white hills and woods, with Crail’s lugger waiting for a wind under the Craig Head, and the smoke mounting straight into the air from every farm and cottage. 中午时分，有了一丝阳光，山野林地，银装素裹，一片美丽的冬日霜雾景象，克雷尔船长的小帆船在头型角等待风向，以便起航，每个农场和村舍的炊烟直升天空。
With the coming of night, the haze closed in overhead; it fell dark and still and starless, and exceeding cold: a night the most unseasonable, fit for strange events. 夜幕降临，薄雾停滞，天色变黑，寂静无星，更加寒冷了：最反常的夜晚，容易发生不平常的事情。
Mrs. Henry withdrew, as was now her custom, very early. 亨利太太很早就离开了大厅，现在她经常那样。
We had set ourselves of late to pass the evening with a game of cards; another mark that our visitor was wearying mightily of the life at Durrisdeer; and we had not been long at this when my old lord slipped from his place beside the fire, and was off without a word to seek the warmth of bed. 我们想用打牌来消磨这个晚上，这也是大少爷厌倦达里斯迪尔生活的一个标志。牌还没打一会儿，老爷就一言不发地离开了炉旁，去享受温暖的被窝。
The three thus left together had neither love nor courtesy to share; not one of us would have sat up one instant to oblige another; yet from the influence of custom, and as the cards had just been dealt, we continued the form of playing out the round. 我、主子和大少爷留了下来。我们三个人之间，没有任何感情和礼节可言，没有一个会听从另一个的安排。但按照惯例，牌既然开始了，就得玩完一局。
I should say we were late sitters; and though my lord had departed earlier than was his custom, twelve was already gone some time upon the clock, and the servants long ago in bed. 首先，我得先声明我们三人都是夜猫子，虽然老爷离开大厅比往常要早，但过了午夜已有段时间了，仆人们早睡了。
Another thing I should say, that although I never saw the Master anyway affected with liquor, he had been drinking freely, and was perhaps (although he showed it not) a trifle heated. 第二呢，尽管我从没见大少爷喝醉过，可今晚他却开怀畅饮，或许（虽然他没表现出来）已有点儿醉意了。
Anyway, he now practised one of his transitions; and so soon as the door closed behind my lord, and without the smallest change of voice, shifted from ordinary civil talk into a stream of insult. 不管怎样，大少爷今晚有点儿不同往常。老爷离开后，门一关上，大少爷的声音没有任何变化，就从君子之谈变为一通谩骂。
“My dear Henry, it is yours to play,” he had been saying, and now continued: “It is a very strange thing how, even in so small a matter as a game of cards, you display your rusticity. 他一直这样说，现在又这么说道：“亲爱的亨利，轮到你出牌了。真奇怪，即使是玩牌这种小事，也能显示出你的粗俗。
You play, Jacob, like a bonnet laird, or a sailor in a tavern. 雅各布，你打牌既像个地主，又像个小酒馆的水手。
The same dulness, the same petty greed, CETTE LENTEUR D’HEBETE QUI ME FAIT RAGER; it is strange I should have such a brother. 这两者同样无趣，同样贪婪，你笨得气死人。我怎么会有你这样的弟弟呢？真奇怪！
Even Square-toes has a certain vivacity when his stake is imperilled; but the dreariness of a game with you I positively lack language to depict.” 榆木脑袋遇险时也有灵光的时候。可是和你打牌，真是闷死了，我都找不到词儿来形容了。”
Mr. Henry continued to look at his cards, as though very maturely considering some play; but his mind was elsewhere. 亨利先生继续看着自己的牌，好像是在思考怎样出牌，其实他的心思不在这里。
“Dear God, will this never be done?” cries the Master. “上帝啊！有完没完啊？”大少爷大声喊道，
“QUEL LOURDEAU! “真笨啊！
But why do I trouble you with French expressions, which are lost on such an ignoramus? 我怎么用法语了呢？你这个蠢物又听不懂！
A LOURDEAU, my dear brother, is as we might say a bumpkin, a clown, a clodpole: a fellow without grace, lightness, quickness; any gift of pleasing, any natural brilliancy: such a one as you shall see, when you desire, by looking in the mirror. 笨蛋，我亲爱的弟弟啊！你就是大家说的冬瓜脑袋、小丑、笨蛋。你照镜子的时候，看到的是一个没尊严、轻浮、笨拙的人，了无生趣，没有一丝灵光。
I tell you these things for your good, I assure you; and besides, Square-toes” (looking at me and stifling a yawn), “it is one of my diversions in this very dreary spot to toast you and your master at the fire like chestnuts. 我保证我这么说是为了你好，”他看着我，打了一个呵欠，又说，“在这儿打牌真没劲，只能在火炉旁边逗你和你的主子玩。
I have great pleasure in your case, for I observe the nickname (rustic as it is) has always the power to make you writhe. 我对你很感兴趣，因为我发现你的外号（尽管粗鄙）能够让你发狂。
But sometimes I have more trouble with this dear fellow here, who seems to have gone to sleep upon his cards. 但有时候这个家伙更让我不爽，他都快拿着牌睡着了。
Do you not see the applicability of the epithet I have just explained, dear Henry? 亲爱的亨利，难道你没有发现我刚刚解释的那些诨名对你很适用吗？
Let me show you. 让我来告诉你。
For instance, with all those solid qualities which I delight to recognise in you, I never knew a woman who did not prefer me—nor, I think,” he continued, with the most silken deliberation, “I think—who did not continue to prefer me.” 例如，虽然你有很多优点，但所有的女人都更加喜欢我，而不喜欢你，还有，”他如丝般缓缓地继续说道，“她们一直更喜欢我。”
Mr. Henry laid down his cards. 亨利先生放下牌。
He rose to his feet very softly, and seemed all the while like a person in deep thought. 他缓缓地站起身，好似陷入沉思。
“You coward!” he said gently, as if to himself. “你这个懦夫！”他温和地说道，好似对自己说的。
And then, with neither hurry nor any particular violence, he struck the Master in the mouth. 然后，他不慌不忙，不带丁点儿鲁莽地打了少爷一下，打在了嘴上。
The Master sprang to his feet like one transfigured; I had never seen the man so beautiful. 大少爷腾地跳起来，好像变了个人一样，我从没见过他如此潇洒。
“A blow!” he cried. “你打我！”他喊道，
“I would not take a blow from God Almighty!” “天皇老子也不敢打我！”
“Lower your voice,” said Mr. Henry. 亨利先生道：“小点儿声，
“Do you wish my father to interfere for you again?” 你想把父亲再次牵扯进来吗？”
“Gentlemen, gentlemen,” I cried, and sought to come between them. “两位先生，两位先生。”我喊道，设法给他们调停。
The Master caught me by the shoulder, held me at arm’s length, and still addressing his brother: “Do you know what this means?” said he. 大少爷抓着我肩膀，离我有一臂的距离，仍然和他弟弟说：“你知道这意味着什么吗？”
“It was the most deliberate act of my life,” says Mr. Henry. 亨利先生答道：“这是我一生做得最深思熟虑的事。”
“I must have blood, I must have blood for this,” says the Master. 大少爷说：“我一定要你血债血偿，血债血偿。”
“Please God it shall be yours,” said Mr. Henry; and he went to the wall and took down a pair of swords that hung there with others, naked. 亨利先生说道：“你这是自食其果。”然后他走到墙边，取下两柄剑，墙上挂着许多没入鞘的剑。
These he presented to the Master by the points. 亨利先生用那两柄剑指着大少爷。
“Mackellar shall see us play fair,” said Mr. Henry. “麦凯勒为我们作证，我们将公平决斗。”亨利先生说道，
“I think it very needful.” “我认为有必要这样做。”
“You need insult me no more,” said the Master, taking one of the swords at random. “你不用再侮辱我了，”大少爷说着，随意拿了其中一把剑，
“I have hated you all my life.” “我这辈子一直都恨你。”
“My father is but newly gone to bed,” said Mr. Henry. “父亲刚上床睡觉，”亨利先生说道，
“We must go somewhere forth of the house.” “我们得去房子前面。”
“There is an excellent place in the long shrubbery,” said the Master. 大少爷回道：“长灌木林里有个绝佳之地。”
“Gentlemen,” said I, “shame upon you both! 我说：“两位先生，你们太丢人了！
Sons of the same mother, would you turn against the life she gave you?” 亲兄弟，要互相残杀吗？”
“Even so, Mackellar,” said Mr. Henry, with the same perfect quietude of manner he had shown throughout. 亨利先生用他一直以来的那种平静语调说：“麦凯勒，即使是亲兄弟。”
“It is what I will prevent,” said I. 我答道：“我会阻止你们的”。
And now here is a blot upon my life. 这是我一生中的一个污点。
At these words of mine the Master turned his blade against my bosom; I saw the light run along the steel; and I threw up my arms and fell to my knees before him on the floor. 我说了这番话后，大少爷用剑指着我的肚子，我看到剑刃上闪着的寒光，便举起双手，在他面前双膝跪地。
“No, no,” I cried, like a baby. “不要，不要。”我像个孩子似的哭着说。
“We shall have no more trouble with him,” said the Master. “他不会给我们找麻烦了，”大少爷说，
“It is a good thing to have a coward in the house.” “有个胆小鬼在这儿，是件好事。”
“We must have light,” said Mr. Henry, as though there had been no interruption. 亨利先生若无其事地说：“我们需要点儿光亮”。
“This trembler can bring a pair of candles,” said the Master. 大少爷说：“这个胆小鬼可以拿着两根蜡烛。”
To my shame be it said, I was still so blinded with the flashing of that bare sword that I volunteered to bring a lantern. 说起来，真够丢脸的，那把明晃晃的剑让我有点儿目眩，我主动提议去拿个灯笼。
“We do not need a l-l-lantern,” says the Master, mocking me. “我们不需要灯……灯……灯笼，”大少爷嘲笑道吗，
“There is no breath of air. “那儿没风。
Come, get to your feet, take a pair of lights, and go before. 快，站起来，拿两根蜡烛，在前面带路。
I am close behind with this—” making the blade glitter as he spoke. 我拿着这个在后面紧跟着你”，他边说边晃着那把剑。
I took up the candlesticks and went before them, steps that I would give my hand to recall; but a coward is a slave at the best; and even as I went, my teeth smote each other in my mouth. 我拿起烛台，走在他们前面，我可以大喊救命，但一个胆小鬼最好还是乖乖的。我走路的时候，嘴里的牙齿在打战。
It was as he had said: there was no breath stirring; a windless stricture of frost had bound the air; and as we went forth in the shine of the candles, the blackness was like a roof over our heads. 正如大少爷所说，那里没风，无风的霜冻凝固了空气，我们在烛光下前行，黑暗如同房顶一样罩在我们头上。
Never a word was said; there was never a sound but the creaking of our steps along the frozen path. 我们谁也没有说话，除了踏在结了霜的路上的脚步声，一点儿声音也没有。
The cold of the night fell about me like a bucket of water; I shook as I went with more than terror; but my companions, bare-headed like myself, and fresh from the warm ball, appeared not even conscious of the change. 夜晚的寒冷如同一桶凉水泼在身上，我边走边吓得浑身哆嗦。可是我那两个同伴，一样没戴帽子，一样刚从温暖的大厅里出来，但他们好像没有意识到环境的改变。
“Here is the place,” said the Master. 大少爷说道：“就是这儿，
“Set down the candles.” 把蜡烛放下。”
I did as he bid me, and presently the flames went up, as steady as in a chamber, in the midst of the frosted trees, and I beheld these two brothers take their places. 我照他的吩咐做了，火苗在这寒霜满天的林地里，如同在屋里一样直直地朝上烧着。我看着这两兄弟各就各位。
“The light is something in my eyes,” said the Master. 大少爷说道：“我这边有点儿晃眼。”
“I will give you every advantage,” replied Mr. Henry, shifting his ground, “for I think you are about to die.” 亨利先生回复道：“因为你就要死了，所以我会满足你任何的条件。”于是就和他交换了位置。
He spoke rather sadly than otherwise, yet there was a ring in his voice. 虽然他的语调里满是悲伤，但声音依然很响亮。
“Henry Durie,” said the Master, “two words before I begin. 大少爷说：“亨利·迪里，开始前我先说两句。
You are a fencer, you can hold a foil; you little know what a change it makes to hold a sword! 你是个击剑手，虽说你会舞花剑，但你不知道怎样用剑来搏斗！
And by that I know you are to fall. 因此，我知道你要输。
But see how strong is my situation! 来看看我的处境多有利吧！
If you fall, I shift out of this country to where my money is before me. 如果你输了，我会离开这个国家，金钱在等着我呢。
If I fall, where are you? 如果我输了，你又能去哪儿呢？
My father, your wife—who is in love with me, as you very well know—your child even, who prefers me to yourself:—how will these avenge me! 父亲，还有你那爱着我的妻子（这你很清楚），甚至是你的女儿，比起你，也更喜欢我，他们都会为我报仇！
Had you thought of that, dear Henry?” 亲爱的亨利，你想过这些吗？”
He looked at his brother with a smile; then made a fencing-room salute. 大少爷微笑着看着他的弟弟，然后以击剑的礼节向他行礼。
Never a word said Mr. Henry, but saluted too, and the swords rang together. 亨利先生一言未发，也行了礼，接着他们打了起来。
I am no judge of the play; my head, besides, was gone with cold and fear and horror; but it seems that Mr. Henry took and kept the upper hand from the engagement, crowding in upon his foe with a contained and glowing fury. 虽然我不想对这场比赛有所评论，再加上我此时因为寒冷、害怕和恐惧，已没有了思绪。但可以看出亨利先生在这场比赛中主攻，他怒火中烧，向大少爷逼近。
Nearer and nearer he crept upon the man, till of a sudden the Master leaped back with a little sobbing oath; and I believe the movement brought the light once more against his eyes. 他离大少爷越来越近，突然大少爷往后跳去，嘴里小声诅咒着。我想这时他的眼睛又对着烛光了。
To it they went again, on the fresh ground; but now methought closer, Mr. Henry pressing more outrageously, the Master beyond doubt with shaken confidence. 他们打到一片新场地，两人相距更近了，亨利先生暴怒地加紧了进攻，毫无疑问，大少爷信心受挫。
For it is beyond doubt he now recognised himself for lost, and had some taste of the cold agony of fear; or he had never attempted the foul stroke. 因为大少爷已意识到自己快输了，也尝到了害怕的痛苦滋味，否则他不会用这卑鄙的一招。
I cannot say I followed it, my untrained eye was never quick enough to seize details, but it appears he caught his brother’s blade with his left hand, a practice not permitted. 我不敢说我看得懂击剑，我没经过击剑训练，所以我很难捕捉到细节，但大少爷用左手抓住了亨利先生的剑锋，这一招是犯规的。
Certainly Mr. Henry only saved himself by leaping on one side; as certainly the Master, lunging in the air, stumbled on his knee, and before he could move the sword was through his body. 亨利先生连忙跳向一旁，以求活命。大少爷扑了个空，绊倒在地，他来不及躲开，亨利的剑已穿胸而过。
I cried out with a stifled scream, and ran in; but the body was already fallen to the ground, where it writhed a moment like a trodden worm, and then lay motionless. 我惊声尖叫，跑到两人打斗的地方。大少爷已摔倒在地，他就像被人踩在脚下的虫子一样，抽搐了一会儿，就不动了。
“Look at his left hand.” said Mr. Henry. 亨利先生说：“看看他的左手。”
“It is all bloody,” said I. 我答道：“全是血。”
“On the inside?” said he. 他问道：“是手心里吗？”
“It is cut on the inside,” said I. 我答道：“手心被划伤了。”
“I thought so,” said he, and turned his back. 他说道：“如我所料，”然后转过身去。
I opened the man’s clothes; the heart was quite still, it gave not a flutter. 我解开大少爷的衣服，心脏已经沉寂，停止了跳动。
“God forgive us, Mr. Henry!” said I. “上帝宽恕我们！亨利先生！”我喊道，
“He is dead.” “他死了。”
“Dead?” he repeated, a little stupidly; and then with a rising tone, “Dead? dead?” says he, and suddenly cast his bloody sword upon the ground. “死了？”他有点儿傻傻地重复道，然后又提高声调说，“死了？死了？”他突然把血淋淋的剑扔在了地上。
“What must we do?” said I. 我问道：“我们怎么办？
“Be yourself, sir. 先生，冷静！
It is too late now: you must be yourself.” 事已至此，您得冷静啊！”
He turned and stared at me. 他转过身来，盯着我。
“Oh, Mackellar!” says he, and put his face in his hands. “噢！麦凯勒！”他说着，用双手捂住了脸。
I plucked him by the coat. 我给他披上外套，
“For God’s sake, for all our sakes, be more courageous!” said I. 说道：“看在上帝的份上，为了我们，勇敢一点儿！
“What must we do?” 我们得做点儿什么？”
He showed me his face with the same stupid stare. 他还是傻乎乎地盯着我。
“Do?” says he. “做什么？”他说。
And with that his eye fell on the body, and “Oh!” he cries out, with his hand to his brow, as if he had never remembered; and, turning from me, made off towards the house of Durrisdeer at a strange stumbling run. 说着他看着尸体，喊道：“天啊！”他用手摸着额头，好像不记得一样，背对我开始朝达里斯迪尔趔趔趄趄地狂奔。
I stood a moment mused; then it seemed to me my duty lay most plain on the side of the living; and I ran after him, leaving the candles on the frosty ground and the body lying in their light under the trees. 我站着想了一会儿，似乎照顾活着的那个才是我的职责。然后我跟在亨利先生后面跑，把蜡烛留在落霜的地上，把尸体留在树下的烛光里。
But run as I pleased, he had the start of me, and was got into the house, and up to the hall, where I found him standing before the fire with his face once more in his hands, and as he so stood he visibly shuddered. 不管我怎么追，他还是在我前面，奔进大厅，站在火炉旁，再次用手捂住脸，尽管他那样站着，但明显地看出他在发抖。
“Mr. Henry, Mr. Henry,” I said, “this will be the ruin of us all.” 我说：“亨利先生，亨利先生，这会把我们都给毁了的。”
“What is this that I have done?” cries he, and then looking upon me with a countenance that I shall never forget, “Who is to tell the old man?” he said. 他喊道：“我究竟做了什么？”然后用一种我永不会忘记的神情抬头看着我，问道，“谁去告诉老爷？”
The word knocked at my heart; but it was no time for weakness. 这句话沉重地敲打着我的心，但现在不是脆弱的时候。
I went and poured him out a glass of brandy. 我为他倒了一杯白兰地。
“Drink that,” said I, “drink it down.” “喝了它，把它喝光。”我说道。
I forced him to swallow it like a child; and, being still perished with the cold of the night, I followed his example. 我像强迫孩子似的逼他一口吞下。因为夜晚的寒冷突然袭上身来，我也像他那样喝了一杯。
“It has to be told, Mackellar,” said he. “麦凯勒，必须告诉大家，”他说，
“It must be told.” “必须告诉大家。”
And he fell suddenly in a seat—my old lord’s seat by the chimney-side—and was shaken with dry sobs. 他突然倒在一个椅子上——老爷靠近壁炉的椅子，并且全身颤抖地呜咽着，眼中没有泪水。
Dismay came upon my soul; it was plain there was no help in Mr. Henry. 沮丧袭上我的心头，很明显，亨利先生现在一点儿忙也帮不上。
“Well,” said I, “sit there, and leave all to me.” “好吧，”我说道，“您就坐在那儿，把一切都交给我吧。”
And taking a candle in my hand, I set forth out of the room in the dark house. 然后，我拿起一根蜡烛，离开那个房间，整座房子漆黑一片。
There was no movement; I must suppose that all had gone unobserved; and I was now to consider how to smuggle through the rest with the like secrecy. 一片寂静，我必须假设一切都没被发现，我考虑着怎样神不知鬼不觉地走到其他房间。
It was no hour for scruples; and I opened my lady’s door without so much as a knock, and passed boldly in. 现在没时间顾虑什么，我没有窍门就打开太太的房门，然后)鲁莽地进到房里。
“There is some calamity happened,” she cried, sitting up in bed. 她坐在床上喊道：“一定是发生了什么不好的事情。”
“Madam,” said I, “I will go forth again into the passage; and do you get as quickly as you can into your clothes. 我说：“夫人，我马上回到走廊去，您尽快穿好衣服。
There is much to be done.” 还有很多事情要做。”
She troubled me with no questions, nor did she keep me waiting. 她没问我任何问题，也没让我等太久。
Ere I had time to prepare a word of that which I must say to her, she was on the threshold signing me to enter. 我还没来得及想出怎么和她说，她已经站在门口示意我进去。
“Madam,” said I, “if you cannot be very brave, I must go elsewhere; for if no one helps me to-night, there is an end of the house of Durrisdeer.” 我说：“夫人，如果您不够勇敢的话，我就得去找别人了。因为今晚如果没有人帮助我，达里斯迪尔将遭遇灭顶之灾，”
“I am very courageous,” said she; and she looked at me with a sort of smile, very painful to see, but very brave too. 她答道：“我非常勇敢。”她含笑望着我，看到她这样，我很伤心，但也变得很大胆了。
“It has come to a duel,” said I. 我说：“发生了一场决斗。”
“A duel?” she repeated. 她重复道：“一场决斗？”
“A duel! “一场决斗！
Henry and—” 亨利和——
“And the Master,” said I. “和大少爷，”我说道，
“Things have been borne so long, things of which you know nothing, which you would not believe if I should tell. “这件事酝酿已久，您对此一无所知，我就算告诉您，您也不会相信。
But to-night it went too far, and when he insulted you—” 但今晚这件事做过头了，当他侮辱您的时候——”
“Stop,” said she. 她说：“停，
“He? 他？
Who?” 他是谁？”
“Oh! madam,” cried I, my bitterness breaking forth, “do you ask me such a question? “噢！夫人，”我的痛苦夺胸而出，喊道，“您怎么会问我这么一个问题呢？
Indeed, then, I may go elsewhere for help; there is none here!” 事实上，我不该来这儿寻求帮助，可是又没别的地方可去！”
“I do not know in what I have offended you,” said she. “我不知道怎么冒犯了你，”她说道，
“Forgive me; put me out of this suspense.” “但请你原谅我，告诉我这是怎么一回事。”
But I dared not tell her yet; I felt not sure of her; and at the doubt, and under the sense of impotence it brought with it, I turned on the poor woman with something near to anger. 但我不敢告诉她，我不相信她，由于对她的怀疑以及怀疑带来的无助，我对眼前这个可怜的女人有些生气。
“Madam,” said I, “we are speaking of two men: one of them insulted you, and you ask me which. 我说道：“夫人，我们谈到两个男人，其中一个侮辱了您，您问我是哪一个？
I will help you to the answer. 我会帮您找出答案。
With one of these men you have spent all your hours: has the other reproached you? 其中一个，您与他朝夕相处，那么是另一个冒犯了您吗？
To one you have been always kind; to the other, as God sees me and judges between us two, I think not always: has his love ever failed you? 您对其中一个一直温柔体贴；而对另一个，上帝可以作证，我认为不怎么好，难道是他的爱辜负了您吗？
To-night one of these two men told the other, in my hearing—the hearing of a hired stranger,—that you were in love with him. 今晚，其中一个告诉另一个，我听见他说——来自一个受雇佣的陌生人的听闻——您爱着他。
Before I say one word, you shall answer your own question: Which was it? 在我说之前，您自己能够找出答案：是谁侮辱了您？
Nay, madam, you shall answer me another: If it has come to this dreadful end, whose fault is it?” 不，夫人，您还是回答我另一个问题吧。事情到了这么可怕的地步，到底是谁的错呢？”
She stared at me like one dazzled. 她昏眩一般地盯着我。
“Good God!” she said once, in a kind of bursting exclamation; and then a second time in a whisper to herself: “Great God! “上帝啊！”她用惊讶的口气说了一次，然后又自言自语地说了一次，“上帝啊！”
—In the name of mercy, Mackellar, what is wrong?” she cried. 她哭喊道：“麦凯勒，你发发善心，到底发生了什么？
“I am made up; I can hear all.” 我准备好了，什么都能听。”
“You are not fit to hear,” said I. 我说：“您听不合适，
“Whatever it was, you shall say first it was your fault.” 不管是什么事，您应该知道那都是您的错。”
“Oh!” she cried, with a gesture of wringing her hands, “this man will drive me mad! 她双手拧着喊道：“啊！你快让我疯了！
Can you not put me out of your thoughts?” 你就不能不提我吗？”
“I think not once of you,” I cried. “我从没想过您，”我喊道，
“I think of none but my dear unhappy master.” “除了我那不幸福的主子，我谁也不想。”
“Ah!” she cried, with her hand to her heart, “is Henry dead?” 她把手放到胸口哭着说：“啊！亨利死了吗？”
“Lower your voice,” said I. “小点儿声，”我说道，
“The other.” “是另一个。”
I saw her sway like something stricken by the wind; and I know not whether in cowardice or misery, turned aside and looked upon the floor. 我看到她像被风吹似地晃来晃去，我不知道是因为害怕还是痛苦，我转过身看着地板。
“These are dreadful tidings,” said I at length, when her silence began to put me in some fear; “and you and I behove to be the more bold if the house is to be saved.” “这些可怕的消息，”她的沉默让我有些害怕，我最后说道，“如果要拯救这个家，您和我就得勇敢起来。”
Still she answered nothing. 她还是没有任何回应。
“There is Miss Katharine, besides,” I added: “unless we bring this matter through, her inheritance is like to be of shame.” 我又说道：“还有凯瑟琳小姐呢，除非我们把这件事情解决，否则她一辈子都会感到耻辱。”
I do not know if it was the thought of her child or the naked word shame, that gave her deliverance; at least, I had no sooner spoken than a sound passed her lips, the like of it I never heard; it was as though she had lain buried under a hill and sought to move that burthen. 我不知道是不是因为想到了她女儿，还是“耻辱”这个赤裸裸的词使她得到了解脱。我没说一句话，她发出了一个我不可能听得到的声音，就好像是她一直被埋在山下，而现在想摆脱重压一样。
And the next moment she had found a sort of voice. 接下来她终于开口说话了。
“It was a fight,” she whispered. “那是一场争斗，”她低声道，
“It was not—” and she paused upon the word. “不是——”她戛然而止。
“It was a fair fight on my dear master’s part,” said I. 我说：“对我亲爱的主子而言，那是场公平的争斗。
“As for the other, he was slain in the very act of a foul stroke.” 而对另一个而言，他是因为犯规才送命的。”
“Not now!” she cried. 她哭道：“现在别说这个！”
“Madam,” said I, “hatred of that man glows in my bosom like a burning fire; ay, even now he is dead. 我说：“夫人，对那个人的憎恨在我心中如火一样燃烧着，即使他现在死了。
God knows, I would have stopped the fighting, had I dared. 上帝知道，如果我有胆量，我应该阻止这场争斗。
It is my shame I did not. 可我没有那么做，是我的耻辱。
But when I saw him fall, if I could have spared one thought from pitying of my master, it had been to exult in that deliverance.” 但当我看到他倒地的瞬间，除了对我主子的深深同情之外，如果还有什么其他想法，那就是解脱所带来的兴奋。”
I do not know if she marked; but her next words were, “My lord?” 我不知道她是否听进去我说的话，但她接着说：“老爷呢？”
“That shall be my part,” said I. 我说：“那件事交给我”。
“You will not speak to him as you have to me?” she asked. 她问道：“你不会像对我说的那样对他说吧？”
“Madam,” said I, “have you not some one else to think of? 我说：“夫人，您就不能想想另一个人吗？
Leave my lord to me.” 把老爷交给我吧。”
“Some one else?” she repeated. 她重复道：“另一个人？”
“Your husband,” said I. 我说：“您丈夫。”
She looked at me with a countenance illegible. 她用不可名状的神情看着我。
“Are you going to turn your back on him?” “您会对他不理不睬吗？”
I asked. 我问道。
Still she looked at me; then her hand went to her heart again. 她还是看着我，接着把手又一次放到胸口。
“No,” said she. “不会。”她答道。
“God bless you for that word!” “您那么说，上帝会保佑您的！”
I said. 我说，
“Go to him now, where he sits in the hall; speak to him—it matters not what you say; give him your hand; say, ‘I know all;’—if God gives you grace enough, say, ‘Forgive me.’” “现在就去他那儿吧！他坐在大厅里，和他说说话，说什么不重要，支持他，和他说‘我都知道了’，如果上帝赐予您足够的仁慈，您再和他说‘原谅我’”。
“God strengthen you, and make you merciful,” said she. “上帝赐予你力量，赐予你仁慈，”她说道，
“I will go to my husband.” “我要去我丈夫那儿。”
“Let me light you there,” said I, taking up the candle. “让我给您照路吧。”我说着拿上了蜡烛。
“I will find my way in the dark,” she said, with a shudder, and I think the shudder was at me. 她说：“我能在黑暗中找到路的。”她战栗了一下，我觉得这是因我而起。
So we separated—she down stairs to where a little light glimmered in the hall-door, I along the passage to my lord’s room. 于是我们就分开了，她下楼去大厅了，大厅门口有一丝灯光在闪烁，而我沿着走廊去老爷的房间。
It seems hard to say why, but I could not burst in on the old man as I could on the young woman; with whatever reluctance, I must knock. 看起来很难说清原因，但我不能像闯进年轻的夫人的房间一样，闯进老爷的房间，不管多不情愿，我必须得敲门。
But his old slumbers were light, or perhaps he slept not; and at the first summons I was bidden enter. 人老了，睡觉轻了，或许是因为他根本就没睡，我敲了一下，他就吩咐我进去了。
He, too, sat up in bed; very aged and bloodless he looked; and whereas he had a certain largeness of appearance when dressed for daylight, he now seemed frail and little, and his face (the wig being laid aside) not bigger than a child’s. 他也是坐在床上，看上去很苍老，面无血色。虽然在白天穿戴整齐时，他看起来很高大，而现在看上去很脆弱、弱小，他的脸庞（如果不算假发的话）不比小孩子的大。
This daunted me; nor less, the haggard surmise of misfortune in his eye. 这把我吓坏了，而他眼神中流露出的不祥预感，同样让我感到害怕。
Yet his voice was even peaceful as he inquired my errand. 但是他的声音与平常吩咐我做事时一样平静。
I set my candle down upon a chair, leaned on the bed-foot, and looked at him. 我把蜡烛放到一把椅子上，倚在床脚，看着他。
“Lord Durrisdeer,” said I, “it is very well known to you that I am a partisan in your family.” 我说：“达里斯迪尔老爷，我是您家里忠实的下人，这一点您是知道的。”
“I hope we are none of us partisans,” said he. 他说：“我希望我们之间不要提什么下人了，
“That you love my son sincerely, I have always been glad to recognise.” 知道你忠心地爱着我的儿子，我一直很高兴。”
“Oh! my lord, we are past the hour of these civilities,” I replied. 我答复道：“噢！老爷，我们不用说这些客套话了。
“If we are to save anything out of the fire, we must look the fact in its bare countenance. 如果我们要挽救任何东西于水深火热之中，我们必须看到赤裸裸的事实真相。
A partisan I am; partisans we have all been; it is as a partisan that I am here in the middle of the night to plead before you. 身为下人，我一直忠心耿耿。正是出于忠诚，我才深夜前来，向您求助。
Hear me; before I go, I will tell you why.” 求您听我道来，在走之前我会告诉您原因的。”
“I would always hear you, Mr. Mackellar,” said he, “and that at any hour, whether of the day or night, for I would be always sure you had a reason. 他说：“麦凯勒先生，我一定洗耳恭听，不管何时，白天或黑夜，因为我相信你定有原因。
You spoke once before to very proper purpose; I have not forgotten that.” 你以前有次就说得合情合理，我还记着呢。”
“I am here to plead the cause of my master,” I said. 我说：“我来这儿是为主子求情的。
“I need not tell you how he acts. 我用不着说他的为人了。
You know how he is placed. 您也知道他的处境。
You know with what generosity, he has always met your other—met your wishes,” I corrected myself, stumbling at that name of son. 您知道他为了满足您另一个——您的愿望，是多么慷慨吗？”我改了口，差点儿说出他那个儿子的名字，
“You know—you must know—what he has suffered—what he has suffered about his wife.” “您知道，您必须知道，关于他妻子，他承受了，承受了什么。”
“Mr. Mackellar!” cried my lord, rising in bed like a bearded lion. 老爷喊道：“麦凯勒先生！”他像雄狮一样从床上站起来。
“You said you would hear me,” I continued. 我继续说道：“您答应过会听我说的。
“What you do not know, what you should know, one of the things I am here to speak of, is the persecution he must bear in private. 有件事您本该知道，却一直被蒙在鼓里，我今天不得不说，那就是他私底下遭受的迫害。
Your back is not turned before one whom I dare not name to you falls upon him with the most unfeeling taunts; twits him—pardon me, my lord—twits him with your partiality, calls him Jacob, calls him clown, pursues him with ungenerous raillery, not to be borne by man. 我不敢直呼其名的那个人无情地折磨亨利先生，折磨他——老爷，请您原谅我——仗着您的偏爱，折磨他，叫他雅各布，叫他小丑，开玩笑说他小气，是人都受不了。在我跟您说这些之前，您是不会改变对他们俩人的态度的。
And let but one of you appear, instantly he changes; and my master must smile and courtesy to the man who has been feeding him with insults; I know, for I have shared in some of it, and I tell you the life is insupportable. 而在您面前，他则立刻变脸，我的主子不得不对那个一直辱骂他的人强颜欢笑，以礼相待。因为我曾牵涉其中，所以我很清楚，我告诉您主子的生活中承受不了那些。
All these months it has endured; it began with the man’s landing; it was by the name of Jacob that my master was greeted the first night.” 这几个月来，一直是这样，自从那个人一上岸，他回来的第一晚，给主子的见面礼就是把他叫做雅各布。”
My lord made a movement as if to throw aside the clothes and rise. 老爷动了动，好似要把衣服扔在一边，站起来。
“If there be any truth in this—” said he. 他问：“你说的是真的吗？”
“Do I look like a man lying?” “我看起来像个会撒谎的人吗？”
I interrupted, checking him with my hand. 我插嘴道，用手阻止了他继续说下去。
“You should have told me at first,” he odd. 他又说道：“你早该告诉我这些。”
“Ah, my lord! indeed I should, and you may well hate the face of this unfaithful servant!” I cried. “天啊！老爷！我应该早告诉您，那您可能会非常厌恶我这个不忠心的仆人了！”我大声喊道。
“I will take order,” said he, “at once.” 他说：“我会改的，马上就改”。
And again made the movement to rise. 他再次动了动，要站起来。
Again I checked him. 我又一次制止了他。
“I have not done,” said I. 我说：“我没有那么做。
“Would God I had! 上帝啊！我早应该告诉您！
All this my dear, unfortunate patron has endured without help or countenance. 我那亲爱的、不幸的主子，一直无助地、不声不响地承受着。
Your own best word, my lord, was only gratitude. 老爷，您对他说的最好的话，就是感激。
Oh, but he was your son, too! 噢！他也是您的儿子啊！
He had no other father. 他只有您这一个父亲。
He was hated in the country, God knows how unjustly. 村子里人都恨他，老天知道这对他是多么不公平。
He had a loveless marriage. 他的婚姻里没有爱情。
He stood on all hands without affection or support—dear, generous, ill-fated, noble heart!” 他得不到爱，得不到支持，那是一颗不幸，但又珍贵、慷慨、高贵的心灵啊！”
“Your tears do you much honour and me much shame,” says my lord, with a palsied trembling. 老爷像中风似的颤抖着说：“你的泪水是你的荣耀，对我则是莫大的耻辱。
“But you do me some injustice. 但你却冤枉了我。
Henry has been ever dear to me, very dear. 亨利对我而言，一直珍贵，非常珍贵。
James (I do not deny it, Mr. Mackellar), James is perhaps dearer; you have not seen my James in quite a favourable light; he has suffered under his misfortunes; and we can only remember how great and how unmerited these were. 詹姆斯（麦凯勒先生，我不否认），詹姆斯对我而言，也许更加珍贵，你没有用十分欣赏的眼光看待我的詹姆斯。他遭受了很多不幸，我们应该知道这些不幸是多么严重、多么不应该。
And even now his is the more affectionate nature. 即使现在我还是更加喜欢他的个性。
But I will not speak of him. 但我并不想谈他。
All that you say of Henry is most true; I do not wonder, I know him to be very magnanimous; you will say I trade upon the knowledge? 你说的关于亨利的事情大多是真的。不用怀疑，我知道他心胸宽广，你可能要说我利用这一点？
It is possible; there are dangerous virtues: virtues that tempt the encroacher. 但他也可能有一些危险的品质：这种品质会诱人前来冒犯。
Mr. Mackellar, I will make it up to him; I will take order with all this. 麦凯勒先生，我要弥补他，我会改正这一切。
I have been weak; and, what is worse, I have been dull!” 我一直很脆弱，更糟糕的是，我一直很迟钝！”
“I must not hear you blame yourself, my lord, with that which I have yet to tell upon my conscience,” I replied. 我答复道：“老爷，我不想听到您自责，那样会让我良心不安。
“You have not been weak; you have been abused by a devilish dissembler. 您不脆弱，只是您被邪恶的伪君子利用了。
You saw yourself how he had deceived you in the matter of his danger; he has deceived you throughout in every step of his career. 您亲眼看到他是怎样利用他所处的危险欺骗了您，他生活中的每一步都欺骗了您。
I wish to pluck him from your heart; I wish to force your eyes upon your other son; ah, you have a son there!” 我希望把他从您的心中拽出来，我想强迫您关注您的另一个儿子。噢！毕竟，您还有一个儿子！”
“No, no” said he, “two sons—I have two sons.” 他说：“不，不，两个儿子，我有两个儿子。”
I made some gesture of despair that struck him; he looked at me with a changed face. 我做了一个绝望的手势，这让他很震惊，他看着我，脸色大变。
“There is much worse behind?” he asked, his voice dying as it rose upon the question. 他问道：“还有更糟糕的事情吗？”他问出这个问题，声音渐渐低下去。
“Much worse,” I answered. 我答道：“糟糕得很！
“This night he said these words to Mr. Henry: ‘I have never known a woman who did not prefer me to you, and I think who did not continue to prefer me.’” 今晚他对亨利先生说了这样一句话：‘我所认识的女人都喜欢我，而不喜欢你，而且她们一直更喜欢我。’”
“I will hear nothing against my daughter,” he cried; and from his readiness to stop me in this direction, I conclude his eyes were not so dull as I had fancied, and he had looked not without anxiety upon the siege of Mrs. Henry. 他喊道：“我不想听到任何不利于我儿媳的话。”他看着我让我住嘴，他的眼神并不如我想象的呆滞，看到亨利太太是争论的焦点，他焦虑万分。
“I think not of blaming her,” cried I. 我喊道：“我没有要责备她。
“It is not that. 事情不是这样的。
These words were said in my hearing to Mr. Henry; and if you find them not yet plain enough, these others but a little after: Your wife, who is in love with me!’” 这些话是我听到有人对亨利先生说的，如果您觉得这些话还不够清楚，接下来一句‘你老婆爱的人是我’可够清楚了！”
“They have quarrelled?” he said. 他问道：“他们吵架了？”
I nodded. 我点点头。
“I must fly to them,” he said, beginning once again to leave his bed. “我要马上去他们那儿。”他说着又开始想离开床。
“No, no!” “不要！不要！”
I cried, holding forth my hands. 我伸出双手阻止道。
“You do not know,” said he. 他说：“你不知道
“These are dangerous words.” 这些话很危险。”
“Will nothing make you understand, my lord?’ said I. 我说：“老爷，您还没明白吗？”
His eyes besought me for the truth. 他哀求地望着我寻求答案。
I flung myself on my knees by the bedside. 我在床边跪了下来。
“Oh, my lord,” cried I, “think on him you have left; think of this poor sinner whom you begot, whom your wife bore to you, whom we have none of us strengthened as we could; think of him, not of yourself; he is the other sufferer—think of him! “天啊！老爷，”我喊道，“想想那个您不管不顾的人吧！想想那个拜您所赐的可怜的人吧！您妻子给您生下来的人，我们都没有尽力关心他，为他想想吧！不要只为您自己考虑，他是另一个受难者，为他想想！
That is the door for sorrow—Christ’s door, God’s door: oh! it stands open. 那是痛苦之门——耶稣的门，上帝之门，天啊！门敞着呢！
Think of him, even as he thought of you. 像他为您着想那样，也为他着想吧。
‘WHO IS TO TELL THE OLD MAN?’—these were his words. ‘谁去告诉老爷？’这是他的原话。
It was for that I came; that is why I am here pleading at your feet.” 这就是我来这儿的原因，跪这儿求您的原因。”
“Let me get up,” he cried, thrusting me aside, and was on his feet before myself. 他喊道：“让我起来，”他一把推开我，站起来。
His voice shook like a sail in the wind, yet he spoke with a good loudness; his face was like the snow, but his eyes were steady and dry. 他的声音如风中的船帆一样颤抖着，但声音还是很响亮，他的脸苍白如纸，眼神平静，并没有流泪。
“Here is too much speech,” said he. 他说：“我们说得太多了，
“Where was it?” 地点在哪儿？”
“In the shrubbery,” said I. 我说：“在灌木林里。”
“And Mr. Henry?” he asked. 他问道：“亨利呢？”
And when I had told him he knotted his old face in thought. 我告诉他的时候，他眉头紧皱沉思着。
“And Mr. James?” says he. 他又问：“詹姆斯呢？”
“I have left him lying,” said I, “beside the candles.” 我答道：“我让他躺那儿了，躺在蜡烛旁边。”
“Candles?” he cried. “蜡烛？”他喊道，
And with that he ran to the window, opened it, and looked abroad. 说着他跑到窗边，打开窗，向外望去，
“It might be spied from the road.” “路上的行人会发现的。”
“Where none goes by at such an hour,” I objected. 我反驳道：“这个时候，谁去那儿啊！”
“It makes no matter,” he said. “那倒没关系。”他说道。
“One might. “但有一件，
Hark!” cries he. 听！”他喊道，
“What is that?” “那是什么？”
It was the sound of men very guardedly rowing in the bay; and I told him so. 那是一群人在海湾里小心地划船，我如实告诉他。
“The freetraders,” said my lord. 老爷道：“是走私贩。
“Run at once, Mackellar; put these candles out. 麦凯勒，快跑，去把那些蜡烛熄灭。
I will dress in the meanwhile; and when you return we can debate on what is wisest.” 我会穿好衣服，你回来的时候我们再讨论怎么做才是上策。”
I groped my way downstairs, and out at the door. 我摸索着下了楼，走出房门。
From quite a far way off a sheen was visible, making points of brightness in the shrubbery; in so black a night it might have been remarked for miles; and I blamed myself bitterly for my incaution. 隔着很远就看到一阵火光，灌木林里亮光点点。在这样漆黑的深夜里，方圆几里都能看到。我为我的疏忽而深深自责。
How much more sharply when I reached the place! 到事发地点的时候，我更加自责了！
One of the candlesticks was overthrown, and that taper quenched. 一个烛台被推翻了，烛芯也灭了。
The other burned steadily by itself, and made a broad space of light upon the frosted ground. 另一支蜡烛还燃烧着，照亮了一大片洒满银霜的地面。
All within that circle seemed, by the force of contrast and the overhanging blackness, brighter than by day. 在弥漫四周的黑暗的衬托下，烛光照到之处似乎比白昼还要明亮。
And there was the bloodstain in the midst; and a little farther off Mr. Henry’s sword, the pommel of which was of silver; but of the body, not a trace. 中央是一团血迹，远处是亨利先生的剑，剑柄是银色的。但尸体却已踪迹皆无。
My heart thumped upon my ribs, the hair stirred upon my scalp, as I stood there staring—so strange was the sight, so dire the fears it wakened. 我的心脏怦怦地敲着肋骨，寒毛悚立。我站那里，盯着这幅奇怪的画面，心中充满恐惧。
I looked right and left; the ground was so hard, it told no story. 我左右张望，地面很硬，看不出什么线索。
I stood and listened till my ears ached, but the night was hollow about me like an empty church; not even a ripple stirred upon the shore; it seemed you might have heard a pin drop in the county. 我一直站那里听着周围的声音，直到耳朵都疼了，夜晚像一个空教堂一样空空荡荡，海岸上无一丝波动，村子里有针掉到地上，好像都能听到似的。
I put the candle out, and the blackness fell about me groping dark; it was like a crowd surrounding me; and I went back to the house of Durrisdeer, with my chin upon my shoulder, startling, as I went, with craven suppositions. 我把蜡烛熄灭，黑暗降临，我摸索着前行，如同周围挤满了人，我回到达里斯迪尔家，头垂得低低的，心中十分害怕。
In the door a figure moved to meet me, and I had near screamed with terror ere I recognised Mrs. 门口有个人朝我走来，我差点儿害怕得尖叫起来，幸而认出来是亨利太太。
Henry.
“Have you told him?” says she. 她问道：“你告诉老爷了吗？”
“It was he who sent me,” said I. 我说：“就是他让我去的。
“It is gone. 不见了。
But why are you here?” 可是您怎么在这儿？”
“It is gone!” she repeated. 她重复道：“不见了！
“What is gone?” 什么不见了？”
“The body,” said I. “尸体，”我说道，
“Why are you not with your husband?” “您怎么没和您丈夫在一起？”
“Gone!” said she. 她说：“不见了！
“You cannot have looked. 你肯定没仔细看。
Come back.” 回去再看看！”
“There is no light now,” said I. 我说：“那儿现在没烛光了。
“I dare not.” 我不敢去。”
“I can see in the dark. 她说：“我在黑暗中能看清。
I have been standing here so long—so long,” said she. 我一直站在这儿，站了很长时间，
“Come, give me your hand.” 来，把手给我。”
We returned to the shrubbery hand in hand, and to the fatal place. 我们手牵手回到灌木林里，来到那个不祥的地方。
“Take care of the blood,” said I. 我说：“小心有血。”
“Blood?” she cried, and started violently back. “血？”她叫道，开始拼命地往后退。
“I suppose it will be,” said I. 我说：“我想应该有血迹。
“I am like a blind man.” 我现在就像个瞎子。”
“No!” said she, “nothing! 她说：“没有血迹，什么也没有！
Have you not dreamed?” 你不是在做梦吧？”
“Ah, would to God we had!” cried I. 我喊道：“天啊！我倒希望是在做梦！”
She spied the sword, picked it up, and seeing the blood, let it fall again with her hands thrown wide. 她看到了那把剑，把它捡了起来。当她看到剑上的血时，手张开来，剑掉了下去。
“Ah!” she cried. “啊！”她叫道。
And then, with an instant courage, handled it the second time, and thrust it to the hilt into the frozen ground. 接着，她立刻鼓起勇气，再次捡了起来，把它插进上了冻的地面。
“I will take it back and clean it properly,” says she, and again looked about her on all sides. “我要把它带回去，擦干净。”她说，然后看了看四周。
“It cannot be that he was dead?” she added. “他不可能死了”。她接着说道。
“There was no flutter of his heart,” said I, and then remembering: “Why are you not with your husband?” “他都没有心跳了，”我说，然后又想起问她，“您怎么没和您丈夫在一起？”
“It is no use,” said she; “he will not speak to me.” 她说：“那没有用，他不会和我说话的。”
“Not speak to you?” “不和您说话？”
I repeated. 我重复道，
“Oh! you have not tried.” “噢！您连试都没试。”
“You have a right to doubt me,” she replied, with a gentle dignity. 她略带庄重地回复道：“你有权利怀疑我”。
At this, for the first time, I was seized with sorrow for her. 此时此刻，我第一次为她感到痛苦。
“God knows, madam,” I cried, “God knows I am not so hard as I appear; on this dreadful night who can veneer his words? 我喊道：“夫人，老天知道，我不像看起来那样无情，在如此恐怖的夜晚，谁又能虚情假意呢？
But I am a friend to all who are not Henry Durie’s enemies.” 只要不是亨利·迪里的敌人，我就是他的朋友。”
“It is hard, then, you should hesitate about his wife,” said she. 她说：“那就难办了，你应该为他的妻子是不是你的朋友而犹豫一下。”
I saw all at once, like the rending of a veil, how nobly she had borne this unnatural calamity, and how generously my reproaches. 我一下子看清，就像揭去面纱一样，对这件不同寻常的灾难，她的表现是多么高尚，面对我的责难，又是多么大度。
“We must go back and tell this to my lord,” said I. 我说：“我们必须回去告诉老爷这一切。”
“Him I cannot face,” she cried. 她说：“我不敢面对他。”
“You will find him the least moved of all of us,” said I. 我说：“您会发现他是我们当中最平静的。”
“And yet I cannot face him,” said she. 她说：“那我也不敢面对他。”
“Well,” said I, “you can return to Mr. Henry; I will see my lord.” 我说：“好吧，您可以回亨利先生那儿，我去见老爷。”
As we walked back, I bearing the candlesticks, she the sword—a strange burthen for that woman—she had another thought. 我们往回走，我拿着烛台，她拿着剑，对那个女人来讲，这柄剑是个奇怪的重担，她另有打算。
“Should we tell Henry?” she asked. 她问道：“我们应该告诉亨利吗？”
“Let my lord decide,” said I. 我答道：“让老爷决定吧”。
My lord was nearly dressed when I came to his chamber. 我来到老爷寝室的时候，他快穿好衣服了。
He heard me with a frown. 他听我说完，眉头紧皱。
“The freetraders,” said he. “是走私贩，”他说，
“But whether dead or alive?” “可他是死是活呢？”
“I thought him—” said I, and paused, ashamed of the word. 我说：“我认为他——”我突然停住了，因内疚而不愿说出那个字。
“I know; but you may very well have been in error. “我知道，但你可能弄错了。
Why should they remove him if not living?” he asked. 如果他没活着，那些人为什么要弄走他呢？”他问道，
“Oh! here is a great door of hope. “啊！还大有希望。
It must be given out that he departed—as he came—without any note of preparation. 他一定是走了，像他回来一样，没有任何迹象。
We must save all scandal.” 我们必须阻止一切谣言。”
I saw he had fallen, like the rest of us, to think mainly of the house. 我发现他和我们一样，考虑的是这个家。
Now that all the living members of the family were plunged in irremediable sorrow, it was strange how we turned to that conjoint abstraction of the family itself, and sought to bolster up the airy nothing of its reputation: not the Duries only, but the hired steward himself. 由于全家陷入极度的悲伤之中，奇怪的是，我们都考虑到这个家，考虑到维护这个家族空洞的名望，不只是迪里家的人，还有我这个雇来的佣人。
“Are we to tell Mr. Henry?” “我们要告诉亨利先生吗？”
I asked him. 我问他。
“I will see,” said he. 他说：“我想想。
“I am going first to visit him; then I go forth with you to view the shrubbery and consider.” 我先去看看他，再和你去灌木林看看。”
We went downstairs into the hall. 我们下楼来到大厅。
Mr. Henry sat by the table with his head upon his hand, like a man of stone. 亨利先生坐在桌边，双手捧着脑袋，一动不动，像个石头人一样。
His wife stood a little back from him, her hand at her mouth; it was plain she could not move him. 他的妻子站在他后面不远处，手放在嘴上，很明显她的劝说没能打动亨利先生。
My old lord walked very steadily to where his son was sitting; he had a steady countenance, too, but methought a little cold. 老爷稳稳地走到他儿子坐的地方，他的神情也很平静，但我认为有点儿冷酷。
When he was come quite up, he held out both his hands and said, “My son!” 他走到亨利先生身边，伸出他的双手说道：“我的孩子！”
With a broken, strangled cry, Mr. Henry leaped up and fell on his father’s neck, crying and weeping, the most pitiful sight that ever a man witnessed. 亨利先生跳起来，趴到他父亲的肩上突然哭了，差点儿喘不过气，这真是最悲惨的景象。
“Oh! father,” he cried, “you know I loved him; you know I loved him in the beginning; I could have died for him—you know that! 他哭道：“啊！父亲，您知道我爱他，您知道我一直都爱他，我可以为他去死，您知道的！
I would have given my life for him and you. 为了他和您，我都可以付出生命。
Oh! say you know that. 噢！说您知道啊！
Oh! say you can forgive me. 噢！说您可以原谅我啊！
O father, father, what have I done—what have I done? 噢！父亲，父亲，我做了什么啊？我做了什么啊？
And we used to be bairns together!” and wept and sobbed, and fondled the old man, and clutched him about the neck, with the passion of a child in terror. 我们从小一块长大！”他如泣如诉，抚摸着这个老人，紧紧地搂着他的脖子，像个受惊的小孩一样。
And then he caught sight of his wife (you would have thought for the first time), where she stood weeping to hear him, and in a moment had fallen at her knees. 接着，他看见了自己的妻子（您第一次就应该想到），她站那里哭着听她丈夫说着，不一会儿，她跪了下来。
“And O my lass,” he cried, “you must forgive me, too! 他哭道：“噢！我的姑娘啊！你也要原谅我啊！
Not your husband—I have only been the ruin of your life. 我不配做你的丈夫，是我毁了你的一生。
But you knew me when I was a lad; there was no harm in Henry Durie then; he meant aye to be a friend to you. 但当我还是个孩子的时候，你就认识我了。那时亨利·迪里没有任何坏心眼，他本想作你的朋友。
It’s him—it’s the old bairn that played with you—oh, can ye never, never forgive him?” 是他，是曾陪你玩耍的、你年长的哥哥。噢！你永远都不会原谅他吗？”
Throughout all this my lord was like a cold, kind spectator with his wits about him. 老爷一直用他的智慧观察着，既冷静又慈祥。
At the first cry, which was indeed enough to call the house about us, he had said to me over his shoulder, “Close the door.” 亨利先生一哭，就足以把全家人都招到我们身旁，老爷回过头对我说：“把门关上。”
And now he nodded to himself. 现在，他点了点头。
“We may leave him to his wife now,”’ says he. “现在让他的妻子陪他吧，”他说道，
“Bring a light, Mr. Mackellar.” 麦凯勒先生，拿上根蜡烛。”
Upon my going forth again with my lord, I was aware of a strange phenomenon; for though it was quite dark, and the night not yet old, methought I smelt the morning. 在我和老爷再次去灌木林的时候，我意识到一个很奇怪的现象，虽然天还很黑，黑夜还没到尽头，我却感觉到了黎明的气息。
At the same time there went a tossing through the branches of the evergreens, so that they sounded like a quiet sea, and the air pulled at times against our faces, and the flame of the candle shook. 与此同时，那些常青树的树枝一阵颤动，听起来像平静的大海一样，风有时吹到我们脸上，烛光摇曳着。
We made the more speed, I believe, being surrounded by this bustle; visited the scene of the duel, where my lord looked upon the blood with stoicism; and passing farther on toward the landing-place, came at last upon some evidences of the truth. 我认为是周围的声音让我们加快了步伐，来到决斗的地方，老爷默默地看着血迹，然后向前走到登陆的地方，最终发现了蛛丝马迹。
For, first of all, where there was a pool across the path, the ice had been trodden in, plainly by more than one man’s weight; next, and but a little farther, a young tree was broken, and down by the landing-place, where the traders’ boats were usually beached, another stain of blood marked where the body must have been infallibly set down to rest the bearers. 因为，首先，路旁有个池塘，冰面被人踏过了，显然不止一个人；其次，稍远一些，有棵小树折断了，掉到登陆的地方，走私贩的船通常搁浅于此，血迹清楚地表明搬运尸体的人曾在此处放下尸体休息。
This stain we set ourselves to wash away with the sea-water, carrying it in my lord’s hat; and as we were thus engaged there came up a sudden moaning gust and left us instantly benighted. 我们用老爷的帽子，舀了些海水把血迹洗掉了。我们正忙着的时候，突然一阵狂风，把我们吓傻了。
“It will come to snow,” says my lord; “and the best thing that we could hope. 老爷道：“要下雪了，我们正希望那样呢。
Let us go back now; we can do nothing in the dark.” 我们现在就回去，这里一片漆黑，我们什么也做不了。”
As we went houseward, the wind being again subsided, we were aware of a strong pattering noise about us in the night; and when we issued from the shelter of the trees, we found it raining smartly. 我们往回走的时候，风又一次减弱了，黑夜里四周传来响亮的“啪嗒”声。当我们离开树林的遮护时，才发现雨下得很大。
Throughout the whole of this, my lord’s clearness of mind, no less than his activity of body, had not ceased to minister to my amazement. 在这整个过程中，老爷头脑清醒，身体矫健，还一直照顾着我。
He set the crown upon it in the council we held on our return. 我们回去的路上，更显示出他的老谋深算。
The freetraders had certainly secured the Master, though whether dead or alive we were still left to our conjectures; the rain would, long before day, wipe out all marks of the transaction; by this we must profit. 走私贩一定是救了大少爷，虽然我们还不知道他是死是活，雨水在天明以前会把所有的证据冲掉，这肯定对我们有利。
The Master had unexpectedly come after the fall of night; it must now he given out he had as suddenly departed before the break of day; and, to make all this plausible, it now only remained for me to mount into the man’s chamber, and pack and conceal his baggage. 天黑后，大少爷肯定神不知鬼不觉地来过这里，在天亮之前就突然离开。现在我只有去他的卧室藏好他的行李，才能使这一切显得合情合理。
True, we still lay at the discretion of the traders; but that was the incurable weakness of our guilt. 事实上，我们依然认为是那些走私贩掌握着大少爷的命运，对此我们难辞其咎。
I heard him, as I said, with wonder, and hastened to obey. 我惊讶地听着老爷的分析，但又立刻按他的吩咐做。
Mr. and Mrs. Henry were gone from the hall; my lord, for warmth’s sake, hurried to his bed; there was still no sign of stir among the servants, and as I went up the tower stair, and entered the dead man’s room, a horror of solitude weighed upon my mind. 亨利夫妇离开了大厅；老爷为了取暖，赶快钻进了被窝；仆人们依然没有任何躁动，我爬上楼梯，走进那个死人的房间，心中充满了独处的恐惧。
To my extreme surprise, it was all in the disorder of departure. 令我极其震惊的是，房间一片狼藉，好像主人准备离开似的。
Of his three portmanteaux, two were already locked; the third lay open and near full. 三个行李箱中，两个已锁好，第三个敞开着，快装满了。
At once there flashed upon me some suspicion of the truth. 我的头脑中立刻闪现出对真相的怀疑。
The man had been going, after all; he had but waited upon Crail, as Crail waited upon the wind; early in the night the seamen had perceived the weather changing; the boat had come to give notice of the change and call the passenger aboard, and the boat’s crew had stumbled on him dying in his blood. 他终究是走了，他只是在等克雷尔船长，而克雷尔船长在等风向。傍晚时分，水手们意识到天气的变化。船提示人们这一变化，让乘客登船，船员恰巧碰到躺在血泊之中奄奄一息的他。
Nay, and there was more behind. 不，还有很多真相。
This pre-arranged departure shed some light upon his inconceivable insult of the night before; it was a parting shot, hatred being no longer checked by policy. 这一有预谋的离开正好印证了今晚他对亨利先生难以置信的辱骂。那只是大少爷阴谋的一环，他终于可以无所顾忌地发泄仇恨了。
And, for another thing, the nature of that insult, and the conduct of Mrs. Henry, pointed to one conclusion, which I have never verified, and can now never verify until the great assize—the conclusion that he had at last forgotten himself, had gone too far in his advances, and had been rebuffed. 还有，那些辱骂的性质以及亨利太太的言行，得出一个结论，以前我从没有证实过，而且直到最后的审判之前都不能得到证实，这个结论就是他忘乎所以，得寸进尺，最终遭到了太太的拒绝。
It can never be verified, as I say; but as I thought of it that morning among his baggage, the thought was sweet to me like honey. 像我说的那样，这件事永远不可能得到证实，但那天早上看到房间里狼藉的行李，这想法倒是像吃了蜜一样甜呢！
Into the open portmanteau I dipped a little ere I closed it. 我在敞着的那个行李箱中翻了翻。
The most beautiful lace and linen, many suits of those fine plain clothes in which he loved to appear; a book or two, and those of the best, Caesar’s “Commentaries,” a volume of Mr. Hobbes, the “Henriade” of M. de Voltaire, a book upon the Indies, one on the mathematics, far beyond where I have studied: these were what I observed with very mingled feelings. 里面有最漂亮的蕾丝和亚麻，许多件他喜欢的衣服；一两本名著，有一本凯撒大帝的《高卢战记》、一卷霍布斯的著作、伏尔泰的《亨利亚德》、一本关于印度的书、一本数学书，都是我没读过的书；这就是我仔细观察到的一切。
But in the open portmanteau, no papers of any description. 但是在敞着箱子中，没有任何描述性的材料。
This set me musing. 这让我疑惑了。
It was possible the man was dead; but, since the traders had carried him away, not likely. 那个人可能已经死了；但是，由于走私贩把他弄走了，所以也可能没死。
It was possible he might still die of his wound; but it was also possible he might not. 他有可能受伤死去；但也可能没有。
And in this latter case I was determined to have the means of some defence. 我决定找出证据证明后一种可能性。
One after another I carried his portmanteaux to a loft in the top of the house which we kept locked; went to my own room for my keys, and, returning to the loft, had the gratification to find two that fitted pretty well. 我把他的行李箱一个个搬到房顶锁着的阁楼里，回到我自己的房间去拿钥匙，又回到阁楼，发现那两只皮箱可以打开，我很开心。
In one of the portmanteaux there was a shagreen letter-case, which I cut open with my knife; and thenceforth (so far as any credit went) the man was at my mercy. 其中一个箱子里有一个粗皮的信盒，我用刀子把它割开，从这时起，这个人就任由我摆布了。
Here was a vast deal of gallant correspondence, chiefly of his Paris days; and, what was more to the purpose, here were the copies of his own reports to the English Secretary, and the originals of the Secretary’s answers: a most damning series: such as to publish would be to wreck the Master’s honour and to set a price upon his life. 里面是他大量的信件，主要是他在巴黎时期的；更有价值的是他写给英格兰某国务大臣的副本以及国务大臣回信的原稿，这些可是重要的东西啊。如果公开这些信，大少爷的名誉会受损，而且还会有人悬赏捉拿他。
I chuckled to myself as I ran through the documents; I rubbed my hands, I sang aloud in my glee. 我看这些信时，不禁发笑，我跃跃欲试，开心地唱起歌来。
Day found me at the pleasing task; nor did I then remit my diligence, except in so far as I went to the window—looked out for a moment, to see the frost quite gone, the world turned black again, and the rain and the wind driving in the bay—and to assure myself that the lugger was gone from its anchorage, and the Master (whether dead or alive) now tumbling on the Irish Sea. 我还在忙于这一开心的事，天已亮了。我还乐此不疲地进行着，除了走到窗边向外望了一会儿，看到雾已散去，地面又恢复到黑乎乎的样子，海岸处风雨交加，相信走私贩已经起航了，大少爷（不管死活）正在爱尔兰海面上颠簸着。
It is proper I should add in this place the very little I have subsequently angled out upon the doings of that night. 现在是时候补充一下我那晚上忙活了一晚发掘出的事情了。
It took me a long while to gather it; for we dared not openly ask, and the freetraders regarded me with enmity, if not with scorn. 我花了好一会儿才把这些东西整理好，因为我不敢公开询问，走私贩们不是蔑视我，就是视我为仇家。
It was near six months before we even knew for certain that the man survived; and it was years before I learned from one of Crail’s men, turned publican on his ill-gotten gain, some particulars which smack to me of truth. 六个月后，我们才知道那个人活了下来。几年后，克雷尔的手下用不义之财开了一家酒馆，我从他那里打听到了一些真相。
It seems the traders found the Master struggled on one elbow, and now staring round him, and now gazing at the candle or at his hand which was all bloodied, like a man stupid. 经过大概是这样的，走私贩看到大少爷挣扎着用胳膊肘支撑着身体后，他们先是仔细地查看了四周，又仔细观察了蜡烛和他沾满鲜血的手，简直目瞪口呆。
Upon their coming, he would seem to have found his mind, bade them carry him aboard, and hold their tongues; and on the captain asking how he had come in such a pickle, replied with a burst of passionate swearing, and incontinently fainted. 他们来到后，他已恢复神智，请求他们把他抬到船上，还让他们不要说话，船长问他何以如此窘迫时，他开始咒骂，然后晕了过去。
They held some debate, but they were momently looking for a wind, they were highly paid to smuggle him to France, and did not care to delay. 他们为此争论了一番，他们那时正在等待风向，他们如果把他偷运到法国，能得到很多报酬，也不在乎耽搁一会儿了。
Besides which, he was well enough liked by these abominable wretches: they supposed him under capital sentence, knew not in what mischief he might have got his wound, and judged it a piece of good nature to remove him out of the way of danger. 除此之外，那些恶棍都挺喜欢他的。他们认为他遭到酷刑，不知他为何受伤，并且认为帮他脱离险境是件好事。
So he was taken aboard, recovered on the passage over, and was set ashore a convalescent at the Havre de Grace. 于是，他就被带上了船，在路上恢复神智了，船在格雷斯港靠岸，他身体也恢复了。
What is truly notable: he said not a word to anyone of the duel, and not a trader knows to this day in what quarrel, or by the hand of what adversary, he fell. 很明显，他没有对任何人提及那次决斗，时至今日，也没有一个走私贩知道他是卷入一个怎样的争斗，被一个怎样的对手打败的。
With any other man I should have set this down to natural decency; with him, to pride. 如果换作别人，我认为这是自然而然的事，而他则完全是虚荣心作祟。
He could not bear to avow, perhaps even to himself, that he had been vanquished by one whom he had so much insulted whom he so cruelly despised. 他可不能公然告诉别人，或是承认，他是被一个他侮辱和蔑视的人击败的。
Chapter 6 第六章
Summary of Events During the Master’s Second Absence. 大少爷二次出走的大事摘要
Of the heavy sickness which declared itself next morning I can think with equanimity, as of the last unmingled trouble that befell my master; and even that was perhaps a mercy in disguise; for what pains of the body could equal the miseries of his mind? 第二天早上，亨利先生病得很重，我对此可以平静地对待，就像对待上次主子所遇到的麻烦一样。相比之下，那未尝不是一件好事，因为肉体上的疼痛又怎能比得上心灵的痛苦呢？
Mrs. Henry and I had the watching by the bed. 亨利太太和我在床边照顾他。
My old lord called from time to time to take the news, but would not usually pass the door. 老爷一次次地让我们告诉他消息，但他不怎么走进主子的房间。
Once, I remember, when hope was nigh gone, he stepped to the bedside, looked awhile in his son’s face, and turned away with a gesture of the head and hand thrown up, that remains upon my mind as something tragic; such grief and such a scorn of sublunary things were there expressed. 我记得有一次，主子几乎要没希望的时候，老爷走到主子的床边，看了一会儿他儿子的脸庞，转过身，仰着头，挥着双臂，看起来十分悲惨，那是一副悲痛、疯狂的景象。
But the most of the time Mrs. Henry and I had the room to ourselves, taking turns by night, and bearing each other company by day, for it was dreary watching. 但大多时间只有亨利太太和我守在那间屋里，晚上轮流看护，白天两人一块儿，毕竟守护病人很枯燥。
Mr. Henry, his shaven head bound in a napkin, tossed fro without remission, beating the bed with his hands. 亨利先生，剃光的头上裹着围巾，不停地摇来摇去，双手捶打着床。
His tongue never lay; his voice ran continuously like a river, so that my heart was weary with the sound of it. 他一直不住嘴，声音如同溪流般不断地流淌，听到他的声音，我心痛不已。
It was notable, and to me inexpressibly mortifying, that he spoke all the while on matters of no import: comings and goings, horses—which he was ever calling to have saddled, thinking perhaps (the poor soul!) that he might ride away from his discomfort—matters of the garden, the salmon nets, and (what I particularly raged to hear) continually of his affairs, cyphering figures and holding disputation with the tenantry. 很明显，对我而言也是羞愧难当，他一直在说一些琐碎之事：来来往往、马匹（他曾吩咐过把马鞍备好），可能想（可怜的人啊！）骑着它能够从痛苦中逃脱；花园、鲑鱼网以及（听到后让我生气）他的风流韵事、无关紧要的数字、与佃户争论。
Never a word of his father or his wife, nor of the Master, save only for a day or two, when his mind dwelled entirely in the past, and he supposed himself a boy again and upon some innocent child’s play with his brother. 他只字未提他的父亲、妻子，还有大少爷，可是只过了一两天，他的思想完全沉浸到过去，他认为自己又成了小孩子，和他哥哥玩一些小孩子的游戏。
What made this the more affecting: it appeared the Master had then run some peril of his life, for there was a cry—“Oh! 更加感人的是：主子好像想起大少爷遇到危险，因为主子喊道：“天啊！
Jamie will be drowned—Oh, save Jamie!” which he came over and over with a great deal of passion. 詹姆斯会淹死的。天啊！救救詹姆斯！”亨利先生一遍遍地喊着，十分激动。
This, I say, was affecting, both to Mrs. Henry and myself; but the balance of my master’s wanderings did him little justice. 我认为这不管是对亨利太太，还是对我自己而言，都很感人，但是大少爷的胡言乱语对亨利先生而言，则不大公平。
It seemed he had set out to justify his brother’s calumnies; as though he was bent to prove himself a man of a dry nature, immersed in money-getting. 他好像要证明兄长的诽谤有理，好像要证明自己是个品行低劣、沉迷于攫取金钱的人。
Had I been there alone, I would not have troubled my thumb; but all the while, as I listened, I was estimating the effect on the man’s wife, and telling myself that he fell lower every day. 如果只是我自己在病房，我则不会自寻烦恼。然而，我在听的时候，一直在想这些话对他妻子的影响，并且认为他在他妻子心目中的形象江河日下。
I was the one person on the surface of the globe that comprehended him, and I was bound there should be yet another. 虽然我是这个世界唯一理解他的人，但我坚信会有其他人理解他的。
Whether he was to die there and his virtues perish: or whether he should save his days and come back to that inheritance of sorrows, his right memory: I was bound he should be heartily lamented in the one case, and unaffectedly welcomed in the other, by the person he loved the most, his wife. 不管是他死去、品质丧失，还是他活下去，回到那痛苦的日子，并且恢复记忆，我认为他一定会得到他的最爱——他的妻子真挚的痛惜以及真诚的欢迎。
Finding no occasion of free speech, I bethought me at last of a kind of documentary disclosure; and for some nights, when I was off duty and should have been asleep, I gave my time to the preparation of that which I may call my budget. 由于找不到时机与亨利太太谈谈，我想至少我能找一些隐秘的文件。轮到我休息的几个晚上，我本应睡觉，我却用那些时间来搜集资料，我称我的这种准备为“预案”。
But this I found to be the easiest portion of my task, and that which remained—namely, the presentation to my lady—almost more than I had fortitude to overtake. 然而准备资料却是最简单的部分，而我却没有勇气把这些资料呈给太太过目。
Several days I went about with my papers under my arm, spying for some juncture of talk to serve as introduction. 有好几天，我都把这些资料夹在胳肢窝下，寻求些谈话间隙，把这些资料交给太太。
I will not deny but that some offered; only when they did my tongue clove to the roof of my mouth; and I think I might have been carrying about my packet till this day, had not a fortunate accident delivered me from all my hesitations. 我不否认，确实有那么几次机会，可是我关键时刻掉链子，没有说出口。要不是有一个天降的机会让我不再犹豫，恐怕我时至今日还揣着这些东西呢。
This was at night, when I was once more leaving the room, the thing not yet done, and myself in despair at my own cowardice. 一天晚上，我正要走出那间房间，还是没有把东西给太太，我对自己的懦弱感到绝望。
“What do you carry about with you, Mr. Mackellar?” she asked. 太太问道：“麦凯勒先生，你拿的是什么？
“These last days, I see you always coming in and out with the same armful.” 过去几天，我一直看见你夹着这些东西进进出出。”
I returned upon my steps without a word, laid the papers before her on the table, and left her to her reading. 我一言不发地转过身，把这些文件放到她面前的桌子上，让她读读。
Of what that was, I am now to give you some idea; and the best will be to reproduce a letter of my own which came first in the budget and of which (according to an excellent habitude) I have preserved the scroll. 那些文件是些什么，我现在就谈谈，最好还是把一封我做预案前的信摆出来，（按照好习惯）我还保存着呢。
It will show, too, the moderation of my part in these affairs, a thing which some have called recklessly in question. 有些人不假思索地怀疑我在这些纠纷中扮演的角色，这封信也会说明我在这些事情中不偏不倚的态度。
“Durrisdeer.” 1757. 1757年于达里斯迪尔府
“HONOURED MADAM, 尊敬的夫人：
“I trust I would not step out of my place without occasion; but I see how much evil has flowed in the past to all of your noble house from that unhappy and secretive fault of reticency, and the papers on which I venture to call your attention are family papers, and all highly worthy your acquaintance. 我相信自己不是一个不守本分的人，可是现在，我发现守口如瓶的不良习惯给您高贵的家族带来了邪恶，我斗胆请您看的文件是家族文件，而且这些非常值得您一看。
“I append a schedule with some necessary observations, 我给一些重要的文件附加了一个目录。
“And am, 此致
“Honoured Madam, 敬礼
“Your ladyship’s obliged, obedient servant, 您忠诚的仆人
“EPHRAIM MACKELLAR. 伊弗雷姆·麦凯勒
“Schedule of Papers. 文件目录
“A. Scroll of ten letters from Ephraim Mackellar to the Hon. James Durie, Esq., by courtesy Master of Ballantrae during the latter’s residence in Paris: under dates ...” (follow the dates) … 第一卷：伊弗雷姆·麦凯勒写给旅居巴黎的、尊敬的詹姆斯·迪里先生，即巴伦特雷少爷的十封信：日期为（按照时间顺序）……
“Nota: to be read in connection with B. and C. 备注：与第二、三卷一起阅读。
“B. Seven original letters from the said Mr of Ballantrae to the said E. Mackellar, under dates ...” (follow the dates.) 第二卷：巴伦特雷少爷写给伊弗雷姆·麦凯勒的七封信原稿，日期为（按照时间顺序）……
“C. Three original letters from the Mr of Ballantrae to the Hon. Henry Durie, Esq., under dates ...” (follow the dates) … 第三卷：巴伦特雷少爷写给尊敬的亨利·迪里先生的三封信件原稿，日期为（按照时间顺序）……
“Nota: given me by Mr. Henry to answer: copies of my answers A 4, A 5, and A 9 of these productions. 备注：亨利先生命我回信，以下是我第四、五、九封回信的复写。
The purport of Mr. Henry’s communications, of which I can find no scroll, may be gathered from those of his unnatural brother. 我没有找到亨利先生回信的文稿，至于他的意图想法，可以从他不同寻常的哥哥的信件中总结出来。
“D. A correspondence, original and scroll, extending over a period of three years till January of the current year, between the said Mr of Ballantrae and—, Under Secretary of State; twenty-seven in all. 第四卷：巴伦特雷少爷与某国务大臣之间，到今年一月为止，时间跨度为三年的通信及其目录，共二十七封。
Nota: found among the Master’s papers.” 备注：在大少爷文件中找到的。
Weary as I was with watching and distress of mind, it was impossible for me to sleep. 看护亨利先生的劳累，加上心里的痛苦，使我难以入睡。
All night long I walked in my chamber, revolving what should be the issue, and sometimes repenting the temerity of my immixture in affairs so private; and with the first peep of the morning I was at the sick-room door. 一整晚，我在房中徘徊，脑海里一直想着事情会怎么样，后悔自己冒失地插手这么私密的事情。天刚一亮，我就站在病房门口了。
Mrs. Henry had thrown open the shutters and even the window, for the temperature was mild. 因为天气暖和，亨利太太撑起了百叶窗，甚至把窗户也打了开来。
She looked steadfastly before her; where was nothing to see, or only the blue of the morning creeping among woods. 她目光坚定地看着前方，其实什么也看不见，只有清晨一缕晨曦爬上树梢。
Upon the stir of my entrance she did not so much as turn about her face: a circumstance from which I augured very ill. 我走进去的声音并没有使她转过身，我认为这是一个不祥的兆头。
“Madam,” I began; and then again, “Madam;” but could make no more of it. 我开始叫了声“夫人”，然后又叫了声“夫人”，但也说不出别的话。
Nor yet did Mrs. Henry come to my assistance with a word. 亨利太太也没有任何答应。
In this pass I began gathering up the papers where they lay scattered on the table; and the first thing that struck me, their bulk appeared to have diminished. 这时候，我把散在桌子上的文件整理好，第一件让我惊讶的事情是好像少了些文件。
Once I ran them through, and twice; but the correspondence with the Secretary of State, on which I had reckoned so much against the future, was nowhere to be found. 我查了一遍又一遍，但国务大臣的信依然不见踪影，我是多么指望这些信未来有些作用。
I looked in the chimney; amid the smouldering embers, black ashes of paper fluttered in the draught; and at that my timidity vanished. 我看见烟筒里余火未尽，黑色的灰烬在穿堂风里挥动着，到此，我的胆怯消失殆尽。
“Good God, madam,” cried I, in a voice not fitting for a sick-room, “Good God, madam, what have you done with my papers?” 我喊道：“上帝啊！夫人，上帝啊！夫人，您把我的文件怎么了？”在病房里，我的音调可不大适合。
“I have burned them,” said Mrs. Henry, turning about. 亨利太太转过身说：“我烧了。
“It is enough, it is too much, that you and I have seen them.” 你和我所看到的已经足够了，其实是太多了。”
“This is a fine night’s work that you have done!” cried I. 我喊道：“您昨晚做得真是好啊！
“And all to save the reputation of a man that ate bread by the shedding of his comrades’ blood, as I do by the shedding of ink.” 就是为了拯救他的名誉，而他是个靠出卖兄弟谋生的家伙，就像我靠写字谋生一样。”
“To save the reputation of that family in which you are a servant, Mr. Mackellar,” she returned, “and for which you have already done so much.” 她回道：“麦凯勒先生，我这么做是为了拯救你作为仆人所服务的家族的荣誉。为此，你已经做了很多了。”
“It is a family I will not serve much longer,” I cried, “for I am driven desperate. 我又喊道：“我再也不为这样一个家族服务了，因为我已经绝望了。
You have stricken the sword out of my hands; you have left us all defenceless. 您已经把我的剑夺过去，我们现在没有任何防卫的武器。
I had always these letters I could shake over his head; and now—What is to do? 拿着这些信，我还可以威胁大少爷，可是现在，该怎么办？
We are so falsely situate we dare not show the man the door; the country would fly on fire against us; and I had this one hold upon him—and now it is gone—now he may come back to-morrow, and we must all sit down with him to dinner, go for a stroll with him on the terrace, or take a hand at cards, of all things, to divert his leisure! 我们不敢不让他进门，而且整个村子都会与我们为敌。我本来有他的把柄，可是现在把柄没了。他可能明天就回来，我们肯定会和他一起用餐，一起在房前散步，一起打牌，我们陪着他做这些事情帮他打发他时间。
No, madam! 不，夫人！
God forgive you, if He can find it in His heart; for I cannot find it in mine.” 上帝可以原谅您；但我没法原谅您。”
“I wonder to find you so simple, Mr. Mackellar,” said Mrs. Henry. 亨利太太说：“麦凯勒先生，没想到你这么幼稚。
“What does this man value reputation? 这个人在乎名誉吗？
But he knows how high we prize it; he knows we would rather die than make these letters public; and do you suppose he would not trade upon the knowledge? 但是他知道我们是多么珍视名誉，他知道我们宁死也不会把这些信件公之于众。你认为他不会利用这一点吗？
What you call your sword, Mr. Mackellar, and which had been one indeed against a man of any remnant of propriety, would have been but a sword of paper against him. 麦凯勒先生，你把它们称为你的剑，可是对一个一无所有的人而言，这也许只是一把纸做的剑。
He would smile in your face at such a threat. 他会对你的威胁嗤之以鼻。
He stands upon his degradation, he makes that his strength; it is in vain to struggle with such characters.” 他把自己的堕落看作是他的武器，和那种人争是徒劳的。”
She cried out this last a little desperately, and then with more quiet: “No, Mr. Mackellar; I have thought upon this matter all night, and there is no way out of it. 她略带绝望地喊出了这些话，然后更加安静地说：“麦凯勒先生，我想了一整晚，也没有想到任何办法。
Papers or no papers, the door of this house stands open for him; he is the rightful heir, forsooth! 不论有没有文件，这座房子的大门永远为他敞开，他是法定继承人。
If we sought to exclude him, all would redound against poor Henry, and I should see him stoned again upon the streets. 如果我们试图排挤他，都会对可怜的亨利不利，他又成了过街老鼠，人人喊打了。
Ah! if Henry dies, it is a different matter! 天啊！如果亨利死了，那就另当别论了！　
They have broke the entail for their own good purposes; the estate goes to my daughter; and I shall see who sets a foot upon it. 他们为了自己的利益，继承顺序就被打乱了，到时候房子会由我的女儿继承，我倒看看谁会插手此事。
But if Henry lives, my poor Mr. Mackellar, and that man returns, we must suffer: only this time it will be together.” 但是，可怜的麦凯勒先生，如果亨利活下来，那个人又回来，我们一定遭遇不幸，到那时真是祸不单行了。”
On the whole I was well pleased with Mrs. Henry’s attitude of mind; nor could I even deny there was some cogency in that which she advanced about the papers. 总体而言，对亨利太太的态度我感到欣慰，甚至不得不承认她关于这些文件的看法有些说服力。
“Let us say no more about it,” said I. 我说：“我们不要再说那个了。
“I can only be sorry I trusted a lady with the originals, which was an unbusinesslike proceeding at the best. 我只能说把这些原件交给一位女士，是我的错。这一着走得不好。
As for what I said of leaving the service of the family, it was spoken with the tongue only; and you may set your mind at rest. 至于我说再也不在这里工作只是说说而已，您可以放心了。
I belong to Durrisdeer, Mrs. Henry, as if I had been born there.” 亨利太太，我属于达里斯迪尔家，就像我生来就在这儿一样。”
I must do her the justice to say she seemed perfectly relieved; so that we began this morning, as we were to continue for so many years, on a proper ground of mutual indulgence and respect. 平心而论，她听到后，松了一口气。于是那天早上我们如同过去几年一样，相互包容，相互尊敬。
The same day, which was certainly prededicate to joy, we observed the first signal of recovery in Mr. Henry; and about three of the following afternoon he found his mind again, recognising me by name with the strongest evidences of affection. 那天一看就是快乐的一天，我们捕捉到亨利先生康复的第一个信号。第二天下午3点左右，他恢复了意识，带着明显的欢喜，认出了我是谁。
Mrs. Henry was also in the room, at the bedfoot; but it did not appear that he observed her. 亨利太太也在病房，她在床尾，但是他并没有注意到她。
And indeed (the fever being gone) he was so weak that he made but the one effort and sank again into lethargy. 他虽已退烧，但仍然很虚弱。有一次想挣扎起来，可是身体太虚弱了，很快又倒床上昏昏欲睡了。
The course of his restoration was now slow but equal; every day his appetite improved; every week we were able to remark an increase both of strength and flesh; and before the end of the month he was out of bed and had even begun to be carried in his chair upon the terrace. 他的恢复过程缓慢但平稳；胃口日益见好。每周体力以及精神都有所好转，月底前他可以下床，甚至开始坐着轮椅在阳台上晒太阳。
It was perhaps at this time that Mrs. Henry and I were the most uneasy in mind. 也许此时正是亨利太太和我心绪最不安的时刻。
Apprehension for his days was at an end; and a worse fear succeeded. 对他的担忧结束了，可是更大的恐惧袭来了。
Every day we drew consciously nearer to a day of reckoning; and the days passed on, and still there was nothing. 每天都离审判日更近一步，日子一天天过去，依然没有任何风吹草动。
Mr. Henry bettered in strength, he held long talks with us on a great diversity of subjects, his father came and sat with him and went again; and still there was no reference to the late tragedy or to the former troubles which had brought it on. 亨利先生恢复了力气，他和我们天南地北地聊天，他父亲来了，与他坐在一起，又走了。我们还是没有提到那场悲剧，以及造成那场悲剧的种种麻烦。
Did he remember, and conceal his dreadful knowledge? or was the whole blotted from his mind? 他是明明记得却故意隐藏那些可怕的记忆？还是他根本就不记得了呢？
This was the problem that kept us watching and trembling all day when we were in his company and held us awake at night when we were in our lonely beds. 白天看护他时,我们一直想着这个问题；晚上孤单地躺在床上时，这个问题也让我们失眠。
We knew not even which alternative to hope for, both appearing so unnatural and pointing so directly to an unsound brain. 我们甚至不知道该期望哪种情形，因为两种情形都极为不正常，都直接说明他的头脑出了问题。
Once this fear offered, I observed his conduct with sedulous particularity. 一旦有了这种担忧，我就更加仔细地观察他的行为。
Something of the child he exhibited: a cheerfulness quite foreign to his previous character, an interest readily aroused, and then very tenacious, in small matters which he had heretofore despised. 他有些举动像小孩子一样，表现出与以前性格截然不同的兴奋。对他以前嗤之以鼻的琐事现在变得很容易好奇，还很固执。
When he was stricken down, I was his only confidant, and I may say his only friend, and he was on terms of division with his wife; upon his recovery, all was changed, the past forgotten, the wife first and even single in his thoughts. 他病倒的时候，我是他唯一的伙伴，或许是唯一的朋友，他与他的妻子有些隔阂。他恢复健康后，一切都变了，过去的事情忘了，他的妻子在他心目中成了第一位的，甚至是唯一的。
He turned to her with all his emotions, like a child to its mother, and seemed secure of sympathy; called her in all his needs with something of that querulous familiarity that marks a certainty of indulgence; and I must say, in justice to the woman, he was never disappointed. 他的喜怒哀乐都向她倾诉，如同孩子对妈妈那样，好似寻求同情一样。他有任何需要都会叫她，语调里那种熟人间的不耐烦显示出了某种纵容。为了对那个女人的公平起见，我不得不说，她从没让他失望。
To her, indeed, this changed behaviour was inexpressibly affecting; and I think she felt it secretly as a reproach; so that I have seen her, in early days, escape out of the room that she might indulge herself in weeping. 事实上，这种行为的改变对她的影响无以言表。我认为她把这当作对她的羞辱，刚开始那些天，我看见她逃离病房，独自哭泣。
But to me the change appeared not natural; and viewing it along with all the rest, I began to wonder, with many head-shakings, whether his reason were perfectly erect. 但对我而言，这一改变却不同寻常。观察了他的改变后，我开始疑惑他是否丧失了理智，并且找到越来越多的否定答案。
As this doubt stretched over many years, endured indeed until my master’s death, and clouded all our subsequent relations, I may well consider of it more at large. 这一怀疑持续了数年，直到主子逝世，并且给后来我们之间的关系蒙上了一层阴影，我还是好好地考虑考虑。
When he was able to resume some charge of his affairs, I had many opportunities to try him with precision. 当他能够记起一些事情时，我有很多机会试试他是否恢复正常。
There was no lack of understanding, nor yet of authority; but the old continuous interest had quite departed; he grew readily fatigued, and fell to yawning; and he carried into money relations, where it is certainly out of place, a facility that bordered upon slackness. 他并不是缺少理解力，也不是没有自信心。但他以前那种好奇心已经没有了，他变得容易疲惫，呵欠连天，还在不恰当的时候谈到钱的问题时，有点儿吊儿郎当。
True, since we had no longer the exactions of the Master to contend against, there was the less occasion to raise strictness into principle or do battle for a farthing. 事实上，既然我们不用再同大少爷的勒索做斗争，就不必像原来那样循规蹈矩，也不必常常锱铢必较了。
True, again, there was nothing excessive in these relaxations, or I would have been no party to them. 当然，这种放松无可厚非，要不然我也不会那样做。
But the whole thing marked a change, very slight yet very perceptible; and though no man could say my master had gone at all out of his mind, no man could deny that he had drifted from his character. 但这一切都表明了一种变化，虽说细微，却也明显。尽管没人能说主子丧失理智，但也没有人能够否认他性情大变。
It was the same to the end, with his manner and appearance. 他的行为和举止都大为改变。
Some of the heat of the fever lingered in his veins: his movements a little hurried, his speech notably more voluble, yet neither truly amiss. 他血管里发烧的热度还没有褪尽：他的行动比以前匆忙，话也比以前多了不少，不过倒没有什么差错。
His whole mind stood open to happy impressions, welcoming these and making much of them; but the smallest suggestion of trouble or sorrow he received with visible impatience and dismissed again with immediate relief. 他整个人变得乐于接受快乐的事物，也乐于创造快乐。但对于麻烦或痛苦的事情却没有丝毫耐心，只要有人提及，他会马上避开，然后立即放松下来。
It was to this temper that he owed the felicity of his later days; and yet here it was, if anywhere, that you could call the man insane. 正是由于这种脾性，在他最后的时光中，他很开心。也正因如此，你可以说这个人疯了。
A great part of this life consists in contemplating what we cannot cure; but Mr. Henry, if he could not dismiss solicitude by an effort of the mind, must instantly and at whatever cost annihilate the cause of it; so that he played alternately the ostrich and the bull. 他的大部分生命都是用来思索我们不能解决的事情。但是亨利先生如果不能依赖心里的努力来排除孤独，一定会立即并且不惜一切代价消除产生孤独的原因。因此他要么逃避现实，要么勇敢面对。
It is to this strenuous cowardice of pain that I have to set down all the unfortunate and excessive steps of his subsequent career. 正是由于他对痛苦的胆怯，我必须为他的将来做好打算，尽管这些有点儿过分。
Certainly this was the reason of his beating McManus, the groom, a thing so much out of all his former practice, and which awakened so much comment at the time. 这就是他打了马夫麦克马纳斯的原因，这一举动与他以前的行为大相径庭，在当时也引起了很多争议。
It is to this, again, that I must lay the total lose of near upon two hundred pounds, more than the half of which I could have saved if his impatience would have suffered me. 也是因为这个，我必须赔偿接近两百镑的全部损失，如果他当时稍有耐心，我本来可以节省一多半。
But he preferred loss or any desperate extreme to a continuance of mental suffering. 但是比起心里承受的痛苦，他更加乐于损失钱财或任何绝望的极端行为。
All this has led me far from our immediate trouble: whether he remembered or had forgotten his late dreadful act; and if he remembered, in what light he viewed it. 这些都让我无暇顾及我们最紧迫的问题：他是否还记得他那恐怖的行径；如果他还记得，那他是怎样看待的。
The truth burst upon us suddenly, and was indeed one of the chief surprises of my life. 真相突然而至，绝对称得上我一生中最大的惊奇之一。
He had been several times abroad, and was now beginning to walk a little with an arm, when it chanced I should be left alone with him upon the terrace. 他离开房间好几次了，现在有人搀着能走点儿路，有时我会与他单独待在阳台上。
He turned to me with a singular furtive smile, such as schoolboys use when in fault; and says he, in a private whisper and without the least preface: “Where have you buried him?” 他朝着我鬼鬼祟祟地一笑，就像做错事的学生一样，悄悄地、直插主题地问我：“你把他埋在哪儿了？”
I could not make one sound in answer. 我惊得说不出一句话。
“Where have you buried him?” he repeated. 他重复道：“你把他埋在哪儿了？
“I want to see his grave.” 我想去看看他的墓。”
I conceived I had best take the bull by the horns. 我想还是铤而走险一回。
“Mr. Henry,” said I, “I have news to give that will rejoice you exceedingly. 我说：“亨利先生，我有个消息要告诉您，您一定非常开心。
In all human likelihood, your hands are clear of blood. 十有八九，您没有杀人。
I reason from certain indices; and by these it should appear your brother was not dead, but was carried in a swound on board the lugger. 我根据确凿的证据推断出来的，根据这些证据，您哥哥应该没有死，只是晕了过去，被走私贩运到海外了。
But now he may be perfectly recovered.” 现在他可能已经完全康复了。”
What there was in his countenance I could not read. 他脸上的表情，我无法看懂。
“James?” he asked. 他问道：“詹姆斯？”
“Your brother James,” I answered. 我答道：“您哥哥詹姆斯。
“I would not raise a hope that may be found deceptive, but in my heart I think it very probable he is alive.” 我并不是为了欺骗您，故意给您一线希望，但从心底里我认为他很可能还活着。”
“Ah!” says Mr. Henry; and suddenly rising from his seat with more alacrity than he had yet discovered, set one finger on my breast, and cried at me in a kind of screaming whisper, “Mackellar”—these were his words—“nothing can kill that man. 亨利先生“啊！”了一声，突然从座位上站起来，比以往更加高兴，手指戳着我的胸膛用尖叫着小声说：“麦凯勒，那个人是杀不死的。
He is not mortal. 他永不会死。
He is bound upon my back to all eternity—to all eternity!” says he, and, sitting down again, fell upon a stubborn silence. 他这辈子都要骑在我的脖子上，一辈子！”这是他的原话，说完后，他又坐下，突然变得沉默。
A day or two after, with the same secret smile, and first looking about as if to be sure we were alone, “Mackellar,” said he, “when you have any intelligence, be sure and let me know. 一两天后，他又带着那同样神秘的微笑，先是往四周看看是否就我们两个人，然后说：“麦凯勒，你得到任何消息，一定要让我知道。
We must keep an eye upon him, or he will take us when we least expect.” 我们必须注意他，要不他会在我们最不经意的时候回来袭击我们。”
“He will not show face here again,” said I. 我说：“他再也不会回来了。”
“Oh yes he will,” said Mr. Henry. 亨利先生说：“他会的，
“Wherever I am, there will he be.” 我在哪儿，他就会在哪儿。”
And again he looked all about him. 他再次向周围看看。
“You must not dwell upon this thought, Mr. Henry,” said I. 我说：“亨利先生，您一定不要这么想。”
“No,” said he, “that is a very good advice. “不，”他说，“这是很好的建议。
We will never think of it, except when you have news. 除非你得到什么消息，要不我们永远也不去想那件事。
And we do not know yet,” he added; “he may be dead.” 我们现在还不知道。”他又补充道，“他也许已经死了。”
The manner of his saying this convinced me thoroughly of what I had scarce ventured to suspect: that, so far from suffering any penitence for the attempt, he did but lament his failure. 他说的方式让我彻彻底底明白了，我以前想都不敢想。他不但一点儿也没有愧疚，竟然是对失败的惋惜。
This was a discovery I kept to myself, fearing it might do him a prejudice with his wife. 我没有把这个发现告诉任何人，害怕会引起他妻子对他产生偏见。
But I might have saved myself the trouble; she had divined it for herself, and found the sentiment quite natural. 但是我也许省了那个麻烦，她自己早已猜出，只是装作不知道而已。
Indeed, I could not but say that there were three of us, all of the same mind; nor could any news have reached Durrisdeer more generally welcome than tidings of the Master’s death. 事实上，我只能说，我们三个人想到一块儿了，传到达里斯迪尔的任何消息，没有能比大少爷的死讯更受我们欢迎了。
This brings me to speak of the exception, my old lord. 但有一个人例外，那就是老爷。
As soon as my anxiety for my own master began to be relaxed, I was aware of a change in the old gentleman, his father, that seemed to threaten mortal consequences. 我对主子的担忧一减少，我就意识到主子的父亲，老爷的改变，他好像不久于人世了。
His face was pale and swollen; as he sat in the chimney-side with his Latin, he would drop off sleeping and the book roll in the ashes; some days he would drag his foot, others stumble in speaking. 老爷脸色苍白，双颊肿胀。他坐在火炉边读书时，会睡着，书也滚到火堆里。他有时步履蹒跚，有时口齿不清。
The amenity of his behaviour appeared more extreme; full of excuses for the least trouble, very thoughtful for all; to myself, of a most flattering civility. 他的行为所带来的好处不胜枚举。只要给别人带来一点儿麻烦，他就满口抱歉；而对我，竟极尽谄媚之事。
One day, that he had sent for his lawyer and remained a long while private, he met me as he was crossing the hall with painful footsteps, and took me kindly by the hand. 一天，他派人去叫他的律师，自己呆了好长一会儿，他拖着沉重的步伐走过大厅时看见了我，然后和蔼地抓着我的手，
“Mr. Mackellar,” said he, “I have had many occasions to set a proper value on your services; and to-day, when I re-cast my will, I have taken the freedom to name you for one of my executors. “麦凯勒先生，”他说道，“我很多次说过你服侍得好。而今天我要修改遗嘱，我决定让你做一个见证人。
I believe you bear love enough to our house to render me this service.” 我相信你对我们这个家充满爱，一定会为我完成这个任务。”
At that very time he passed the greater portion of his days in chamber, from which it was often difficult to rouse him; seemed to have losst all count of years, and had several times (particularly on waking) called for his wife and for an old servant whose very gravestone was now green with moss. 那时候，老爷大部分时间都在房内度过，他的时间概念已经混乱了。有好几次（醒着的时候），他要找他的妻子和一位老仆人，而那个仆人的坟头早已布满了青苔。
If I had been put to my oath, I must have declared he was incapable of testing; and yet there was never a will drawn more sensible in every trait, or showing a more excellent judgment both of persons and affairs. 如果要我发誓的话，我一定说老爷已经没有能力来考验了；但也没有任何一封遗嘱会在各个方面都那么理智，不管是人还是事都处理得很好。
His dissolution, though it took not very long, proceeded by infinitesimal gradations. 老爷的病情逐渐恶化，不久之后就去世了。
His faculties decayed together steadily; the power of his limbs was almost gone, he was extremely deaf, his speech had sunk into mere mumblings; and yet to the end he managed to discover something of his former courtesy and kindness, pressing the hand of any that helped him, presenting me with one of his Latin books, in which he had laboriously traced my name, and in a thousand ways reminding us of the greatness of that loss which it might almost be said we had already suffered. 他的器官一起慢慢地老化；四肢丧失能力，耳聋，口齿不清。临终前，他又重拾以前那种彬彬有礼和和蔼可亲的态度，同任何帮助过他的人握手，送给我一本拉丁文的书，在那本书里，他费力找到了我的名字；并用各种方式提醒我们那场损失的惨重，关于那场损失，我们已经承受了很多。
To the end, the power of articulation returned to him in flashes; it seemed he had only forgotten the art of speech as a child forgets his lesson, and at times he would call some part of it to mind. 最后，他回光返照似的又能说话了。他就像一个忘记了功课的孩子一样，忘记了怎么讲话，有时却又会想起一些。
On the last night of his life he suddenly broke silence with these words from Virgil: “Gnatique pratisque, alma, precor, miserere,” perfectly uttered, and with a fitting accent. 他去世的那天晚上，他突然用维吉尔的话打破了沉默：“生生死死，生为了死，死了却了生。”他发音很清楚，就连重音都很准确。
At the sudden clear sound of it we started from our several occupations; but it was in vain we turned to him; he sat there silent, and, to all appearance, fatuous. 我们一听到这句清晰的话，都从各自忙活的事情中抽身。等我们跑到他身边时，已经晚了，他已经一声不吭了，模样傻乎乎的。
A little later he was had to bed with more difficulty than ever before; and some time in the night, without any more violence, his spirit fled. 稍后，他比以往更艰难地上床。那天晚上，没有任何挣扎，他就驾鹤西归了。
At a far later period I chanced to speak of these particulars with a doctor of medicine, a man of so high a reputation that I scruple to adduce his name. 很长一段时间后，我碰巧和医生谈到这些特殊情况，那位医生德高望重，我不敢说出他的名字。
By his view of it father and son both suffered from the affection: the father from the strain of his unnatural sorrows—the son perhaps in the excitation of the fever; each had ruptured a vessel on the brain, and there was probably (my doctor added) some predisposition in the family to accidents of that description. 那位医生认为父子俩得了同一种病：父亲悲伤过度，儿子高烧不退；俩人大脑血管破裂，（那位医生补充道）可能这个家族有得那种病的遗传基因。
