The father sank, the son recovered all the externals of a healthy man; but it is like there was some destruction in those delicate tissues where the soul resides and does her earthly business; her heavenly, I would fain hope, cannot be thus obstructed by material accidents. 父亲去世了，儿子表面上恢复了健康。但是内部脆弱的组织可能遭受了破坏，这些组织控制着正常生命的精神活动，而我认为这些组织不会因为有形的伤害而受损。
And yet, upon a more mature opinion, it matters not one jot; for He who shall pass judgment on the records of our life is the same that formed us in frailty. 然而从更加正确的角度看，这纯属无稽之谈。因为上帝不仅对我们的生命轨迹作出评判，而且正是他赋予了人性的弱点。
The death of my old lord was the occasion of a fresh surprise to us who watched the behaviour of his successor. 老爷死后，我们看到他的继承人的行为感到很吃惊。
To any considering mind, the two sons had between them slain their father, and he who took the sword might be even said to have slain him with his hand, but no such thought appeared to trouble my new lord. 任何有思想的人都会想到，老人是给两个儿子害死的，甚至可以说手握宝剑的人亲手杀死了他。但是，我的这位新爵爷却似乎没有这种想法。
He was becomingly grave; I could scarce say sorrowful, or only with a pleasant sorrow; talking of the dead with a regretful cheerfulness, relating old examples of his character, smiling at them with a good conscience; and when the day of the funeral came round, doing the honours with exact propriety. 他很庄重，符合他的身份；他不能说是悲伤，或只是悲伤中带着喜悦。谈到逝者，既悔恨又洒脱，带着善意的微笑谈论他的性格。葬礼那天，他的神情庄重得体。
I could perceive, besides, that he found a solid gratification in his accession to the title; the which he was punctilious in exacting. 还有，我能看出他对于继承这个爵位充满感激之情，他的继承理所当然。
And now there came upon the scene a new character, and one that played his part, too, in the story; I mean the present lord, Alexander, whose birth (17th July, 1757) filled the cup of my poor master’s happiness. 接着出现了一个新人物，他在这个故事中也有一席之地；我指的是小主子，亚历山大，他的出生（日期为1757年7月17日）令可怜的爵爷欣喜若狂。
There was nothing then left him to wish for; nor yet leisure to wish for it. 他的出生令爵爷心满意足，也无暇去奢望别的什么了。
Indeed, there never was a parent so fond and doting as he showed himself. 事实上，还没有任何父母像爵爷那样溺爱孩子。
He was continually uneasy in his son’s absence. 他一看不到儿子就心慌。
Was the child abroad? the father would be watching the clouds in case it rained. 孩子出门了时，爵爷就会抬头看天会不会下雨。
Was it night? he would rise out of his bed to observe its slumbers. 晚上，他会起床去看着孩子睡觉。
His conversation grew even wearyful to strangers, since he talked of little but his son. 和陌生人谈话时，也是开口闭口谈起儿子，令别人感觉枯燥无味。
In matters relating to the estate, all was designed with a particular eye to Alexander; and it would be:—“Let us put it in hand at once, that the wood may be grown against Alexander’s majority;” or, “This will fall in again handsomely for Alexander’s marriage.” 涉及房产的事情，他总是特别关照亚历山大。他会说：“我们买下来吧，等到亚历山大长大的时候，树木也就成材了。”或者说：“这给亚历山大结婚时用最好了。”
Every day this absorption of the man’s nature became more observable, with many touching and some very blameworthy particulars. 爵爷的痴迷日益明显，大多令人感动，但有些却引起争议。
Soon the child could walk abroad with him, at first on the terrace, hand in hand, and afterward at large about the policies; and this grew to be my lord’s chief occupation. 很快孩子就能和他一块儿出门了，起先是拉着手走上阳台，后来就在府邸四周走动。这也成了爵爷的主要任务。
The sound of their two voices (audible a great way off, for they spoke loud) became familiar in the neighbourhood; and for my part I found it more agreeable than the sound of birds. 街坊四邻都熟悉了他们的声音（很远都能听到，因为他们说话声很大）。在我看来，他们的谈话声比鸟鸣还悦耳动听。
It was pretty to see the pair returning, full of briars, and the father as flushed and sometimes as bemuddied as the child, for they were equal sharers in all sorts of boyish entertainment, digging in the beach, damming of streams, and what not; and I have seen them gaze through a fence at cattle with the same childish contemplation. 有时他们回家时，身上挂满了野蔷薇；有时父子俩满脸通红，浑身是泥，因为他俩玩小孩子们的游戏，在海滩上挖坑，在溪水中堆土，什么都干；有时我还看见他们在牛圈旁像小孩子一样注视着。
The mention of these rambles brings me to a strange scene of which I was a witness. 提到散步，让我想起一件亲眼所见的奇怪事。
There was one walk I never followed myself without emotion, so often had I gone there upon miserable errands, so much had there befallen against the house of Durrisdeer. 有那么一条路，我每次走在上面时都心事重重，去办的事情都不是好事，发生的许多事都不利于达里斯迪尔府。
But the path lay handy from all points beyond the Muckle Ross; and I was driven, although much against my will, to take my use of it perhaps once in the two months. 这条路是去马克罗斯最近的一条，虽然不情愿，但我还是决定走那条路，也许两个月才走一次。
It befell when Mr. Alexander was of the age of seven or eight, I had some business on the far side in the morning, and entered the shrubbery, on my homeward way, about nine of a bright forenoon. 那时亚历山大七八岁，我一大早就去远处办事，回来的时候经过灌木林，大约9点。
It was that time of year when the woods are all in their spring colours, the thorns all in flower, and the birds in the high season of their singing. 此时春意盎然，树木一片绿色，花朵遍地，鸟儿唱得正欢。
In contrast to this merriment, the shrubbery was only the more sad, and I the more oppressed by its associations. 与这种欢乐形成对比的是，灌木林则悲凉的多，而我因为它的悲凉更加忧郁。
In this situation of spirit it struck me disagreeably to hear voices a little way in front, and to recognise the tones of my lord and Mr. Alexander. 在这种气氛下，我听到前面不远处有说话声，吓我一跳，心情不爽，我听出那是爵爷和亚历山大先生的声音。
I pushed ahead, and came presently into their view. 我继续往前走，走进他们的视线。
They stood together in the open space where the duel was, my lord with his hand on his son’s shoulder, and speaking with some gravity. 他们站在发生那场决斗的一片空地上，爵爷把手放在他儿子的肩膀上，正在严肃地说着什么。
At least, as he raised his head upon my coming, I thought I could perceive his countenance to lighten. 当他抬起头看见我，我至少能从他的神情上猜出他在说什么。
“Ah!” says he, “here comes the good Mackellar. 他说：“啊！善良的麦凯勒来了。
I have just been telling Sandie the story of this place, and how there was a man whom the devil tried to kill, and how near he came to kill the devil instead.” 我正给桑迪讲关于这个地方的故事呢，有个魔鬼想杀死一个人，结果那个魔鬼却差点儿被那个人杀了。”
I had thought it strange enough he should bring the child into that scene; that he should actually be discoursing of his act, passed measure. 他带一个孩子来这里本来就够奇怪了，他竟然把他的所作所为讲出来，就更不可思议了。
But the worst was yet to come; for he added, turning to his son—“You can ask Mackellar; he was here and saw it.” 接下来是最糟糕的，他朝着他的儿子又说：“你可以问问麦凯勒，他当时在这儿亲眼看见了。”
“Is it true, Mr. Mackellar?” asked the child. 孩子问道：“麦凯勒先生，是真的吗？
“And did you really see the devil?” 你真的看见魔鬼了吗？”
“I have not heard the tale,” I replied; “and I am in a press of business.” 我答道：“我没有听说那个故事，我现在正忙着。”
So far I said a little sourly, fencing with the embarrassment of the position; and suddenly the bitterness of the past, and the terror of that scene by candle-light, rushed in upon my mind. 我情绪低落地搪塞着，心中充满了尴尬。刹那间，过去的痛苦以及对烛光照耀下景象的恐惧冲上心头。
I bethought me that, for a difference of a second’s quickness in parade, the child before me might have never seen the day; and the emotion that always fluttered round my heart in that dark shrubbery burst forth in words. 短短片刻之后，我意识到眼前的这个孩子从未目睹当日的情境。阴暗的灌木林中曾经多次激荡在我胸中的情绪，此时化作了话语。
“But so much is true,” I cried, “that I have met the devil in these woods, and seen him foiled here. 我喊道：“是真的，我在这片树林里看见了魔鬼，看见了他在这儿的挫败。
Blessed be God that we escaped with life—blessed be God that one stone yet stands upon another in the walls of Durrisdeer! 上帝保佑我们死里逃生，上帝保佑达里斯迪尔府依然屹立不倒！
And, oh! 天啊！
Mr. Alexander, if ever you come by this spot, though it was a hundred years hence, and you came with the gayest and the highest in the land, I would step aside and remember a bit prayer.” 亚历山大先生，如果您经过这个地方，即使一百年后，如果您来到这个地方，享受着快乐与荣誉，我也会站在一旁为您祈祷的。”
My lord bowed his head gravely. 爵爷神情严肃地点点头，
“Ah!” says he, “Mackellar is always in the right. 他说道：“哈！麦凯勒永远是对的。
Come, Alexander, take your bonnet off.” 亚历山大，来，把帽子摘下来。”
And with that he uncovered, and held out his hand. 他把孩子的帽子摘了下来，举着。
“O Lord,” said he, “I thank Thee, and my son thanks Thee, for Thy manifold great mercies. “主啊！”他说，“我感激您！我的儿子感激您！感激您的仁慈。
Let us have peace for a little; defend us from the evil man. 赐予我们平静，保护我们不受魔鬼的伤害。
Smite him, O Lord, upon the lying mouth!” 噢！主啊！惩罚他！惩罚那个骗子。”
The last broke out of him like a cry; and at that, whether remembered anger choked his utterance, or whether he perceived this was a singular sort of prayer, at least he suddenly came to a full stop; and, after a moment, set back his hat upon his head. 最后一声像是哭泣，不知是因为怒气哽咽，还是因为他只是把这作为一种祈祷，总之他突然停住了。过了一会儿，他又把帽子给他儿子戴上了。
“I think you have forgot a word, my lord,” said I. “爵爷，我想您忘了一句话，”我说，
“‘Forgive us our trespasses, as we forgive them that trespass against us. “‘请原谅我们的罪过，我们也原谅践踏我们的人。
For Thine is the kingdom, and the power, and the glory, for ever and ever. 您的天国无所不能，荣耀无比，永远永远。
Amen.’” 阿门。’”
“Ah! that is easy saying,” said my lord. 爵爷说道：“哈！那很简单，
“That is very easy saying, Mackellar. 麦凯勒，那很简单。
But for me to forgive! 让我原谅他人！
—I think I would cut a very silly figure if I had the affectation to pretend it.” 如果我会假装的话，那看起来会像个傻瓜。”
“The bairn, my lord!” said I, with some severity, for I thought his expressions little fitted for the care of children. 我神情严肃地说：“爵爷，孩子在这儿呢”，我认为在孩子面前，他的措辞不大适合。
“Why, very true,” said he. 他问道：“为什么？这是真事呀。
“This is dull work for a bairn. 对孩子来说，这很无聊。
Let’s go nesting.” 我们去掏鸟巢吧。”
I forget if it was the same day, but it was soon after, my lord, finding me alone, opened himself a little more on the same head. 我不记得是否还是那天，但不久，爵爷单独找我，敞开胸怀谈论了那个话题。
“Mackellar,” he said, “I am now a very happy man.” 他说：“麦凯勒，我现在很幸福。”
“I think so indeed, my lord,” said I, “and the sight of it gives me a light heart.” 我答道：“爵爷，的确是那样，看到您这么幸福，我就放心了。”
“There is an obligation in happiness—do you not think so?” says he, musingly. 他若有所思地说：“有了幸福，就要承担责任，你不那么认为吗？”
“I think so indeed,” says I, “and one in sorrow, too. 我答道：“我确实那么以为，身处痛苦，也是一样。
If we are not here to try to do the best, in my humble opinion the sooner we are away the better for all parties.” 如果我们不是尽力做到最好，以我愚见，还是尽早分开为妙。”
“Ay, but if you were in my shoes, would you forgive him?” asks my lord. 爵爷问道：“嗯，如果你站在我的立场，你会原谅他吗？”
The suddenness of the attack a little gravelled me. 爵爷突然的一招，让我有些无从招架。
“It is a duty laid upon us strictly,” said I. 我说：“那是摆在我们面前的责任。”
“Hut!” said he. 他说：“住嘴！
“These are expressions! 这些只是托词！
Do you forgive the man yourself?” 你会不会原谅他？”
“Well—no!” said I. 我说：“呃，不会！
“God forgive me, I do not.” 愿上帝宽恕我，我不会原谅他。”
“Shake hands upon that!” cries my lord, with a kind of joviality. 爵爷欣喜地喊道：“咱俩握握手吧！”
“It is an ill sentiment to shake hands upon,” said I, “for Christian people. 我说：“对基督徒来说，为这样的事情握手可是一种亵渎。
I think I will give you mine on some more evangelical occasion.” 我希望在更加符合教义的场合与您握手。”
This I said, smiling a little; but as for my lord, he went from the room laughing aloud. 我说这些话的时候，笑了一下，可是爵爷却是大笑着走出房间。
For my lord’s slavery to the child, I can find no expression adequate. 爵爷对这个孩子的纵容，我找不到恰当的表述。
He lost himself in that continual thought: business, friends, and wife being all alike forgotten, or only remembered with a painful effort, like that of one struggling with a posset. 孩子占据了他的思想，而工作、朋友和妻子都忘了，或是只有经过痛苦的努力才能记起来，就像喝牛乳酒一样。
It was most notable in the matter of his wife. 这在他的妻子身上体现得最明显。
Since I had known Durrisdeer, she had been the burthen of his thought and the loadstone of his eyes; and now she was quite cast out. 自从我认识达里斯迪尔一家人，她就是他心里的重担，吸引着他的目光，而现在她却被抛弃了。
I have seen him come to the door of a room, look round, and pass my lady over as though she were a dog before the fire. 我看见他走到房门口，四处张望，从夫人身边径直走过，好像她就是火炉边的一只小狗。
It would be Alexander he was seeking, and my lady knew it well. 夫人很清楚，他应该是在找亚历山大。
I have heard him speak to her so ruggedly that I nearly found it in my heart to intervene: the cause would still be the same, that she had in some way thwarted Alexander. 我听到他同她讲话时粗声粗气，以至于我都想去阻止。还是那个原因，她从某种意义上对亚历山大构成了威胁。
Without doubt this was in the nature of a judgment on my lady. 毫无疑问，这是对夫人品性的偏见。
Without doubt she had the tables turned upon her, as only Providence can do it; she who had been cold so many years to every mark of tenderness, it was her part now to be neglected: the more praise to her that she played it well. 毫无疑问，她的处境今非昔比，似乎这是上天的捉弄。以前，爵爷对她温柔多情，她却冷若冰霜；如今，轮到她受到冷落。想不到她竟能处之泰然，真是了不起。
An odd situation resulted: that we had once more two parties in the house, and that now I was of my lady’s. 奇怪的事情发生了：这个家又分成了两派，现在我站在夫人这边。
Not that ever I lost the love I bore my master. 不是我失去了对爵爷的爱。
But, for one thing, he had the less use for my society. 而是，第一，他不那么需要我和他做伴了。
For another, I could not but compare the case of Mr. Alexander with that of Miss Katharine; for whom my lord had never found the least attention. 第二，我不能把亚历山大先生和凯瑟琳小姐相提并论，因为爵爷对小姐根本就不关心。
And for a third, I was wounded by the change he discovered to his wife, which struck me in the nature of an infidelity. 第三，他对妻子态度的改变，我视之位为背叛，这让我很受伤。
I could not but admire, besides, the constancy and kindness she displayed. 此外，我不得不敬佩太太表现出的始终如一和温柔善良。
Perhaps her sentiment to my lord, as it had been founded from the first in pity, was that rather of a mother than a wife; perhaps it pleased her—if I may so say—to behold her two children so happy in each other; the more as one had suffered so unjustly in the past. 可能是因为她对爵爷的感情是出于同情，更像母子之情而非夫妻之意，发现这个让人感到遗憾；也可能因为她认为拥有两个孩子足够幸福；更可能的是她过去承受了那么多不公。
But, for all that, and though I could never trace in her one spark of jealousy, she must fall back for society on poor neglected Miss Katharine; and I, on my part, came to pass my spare hours more and more with the mother and daughter. 即使如此，我也没有发现她表现出一丝一毫的妒忌，她开始陪伴可怜的、备受冷落的凯瑟琳小姐。而我，则把越来越多的闲暇时间和这对母女共同度过。
It would be easy to make too much of this division, for it was a pleasant family, as families go; still the thing existed; whether my lord knew it or not, I am in doubt. 和普通家庭一样，这是幸福的一家人，把他们分成两派实在有些残忍；两派的存在却是事实；我疑惑爵爷到底知不知道。
I do not think he did; he was bound up so entirely in his son; but the rest of us knew it, and in a manner suffered from the knowledge. 我认为他不知道，因为他整个心思都用在他儿子身上。但其他的人都心知肚明，都为此感到痛苦。
What troubled us most, however, was the great and growing danger to the child. 然而，最让我们心烦的是孩子面临的严重危险，而且危险日益加重。
My lord was his father over again; it was to be feared the son would prove a second Master. 现在的爵爷就是当年的老爷，我们很担心亚历山大会成为第二个大少爷。
Time has proved these fears to have been quite exaggerate. 时间证明这种担心太多余了。
Certainly there is no more worthy gentleman to-day in Scotland than the seventh Lord Durrisdeer. 事实上，苏格兰当今没有比达里斯迪尔勋爵七世更绅士的人了。
Of my own exodus from his employment it does not become me to speak, above all in a memorandum written only to justify his father.... 由于我离开了，所以我不应该来讲这些，总之是以备忘录的形式在这里为他的父亲辩解……
[Editor’s Note. 编者注：
Five pages of Mr. Mackellar’s MS. are here omitted. 此处删除麦凯勒先生备忘录中的五页。
I have gathered from their perusal an impression that Mr. Mackellar, in his old age, was rather an exacting servant. 编者通过研读这五页，了解到麦凯乐先生在其晚年仍是一个称职的仆人。
Against the seventh Lord Durrisdeer (with whom, at any rate, we have no concern) nothing material is alleged. 至于达里斯迪尔勋爵七世（关于此人，我们没有任何关注）没有确切的材料。
—R. L. S.] ——罗伯特·路易斯·斯蒂文森
...But our fear at the time was lest he should turn out, in the person of his son, a second edition of his brother. ……但我们此时的担忧是以免爵爷的儿子成为他哥哥的翻版。
My lady had tried to interject some wholesome discipline; she had been glad to give that up, and now looked on with secret dismay; sometimes she even spoke of it by hints; and sometimes, when there was brought to her knowledge some monstrous instance of my lord’s indulgence, she would betray herself in a gesture or perhaps an exclamation. 夫人起先试图制定些规矩，但最后她欣然放弃了，现在她只是心里带着沮丧旁观。有时她讲话时会有暗示，有时她想到爵爷溺爱孩子的事情时，会下意识地做出手势或发出尖叫，从而暴露了自己的心迹。
As for myself, I was haunted by the thought both day and night: not so much for the child’s sake as for the father’s. 而我则日夜被这个想法萦绕着，倒不是为了孩子，而是为了孩子的父亲。
The man had gone to sleep, he was dreaming a dream, and any rough wakening must infallibly prove mortal. 爵爷去睡觉了，正做梦，怎样叫他都叫不醒。
That he should survive its death was inconceivable; and the fear of its dishonour made me cover my face. 很难想象他能活下来，这一屈辱带来的恐惧让我把脸埋在双手中。
It was this continual preoccupation that screwed me up at last to a remonstrance: a matter worthy to be narrated in detail. 这个思绪久久萦绕心头，终于令我无法容忍：这件事值得我细细道来。
My lord and I sat one day at the same table upon some tedious business of detail; I have said that he had lost his former interest in such occupations; he was plainly itching to be gone, and he looked fretful, weary, and methought older than I had ever previously observed. 一天，我和爵爷坐在同一张桌子前，做着枯燥的日常事务。我已经说过，他对这种工作已经丧失了兴趣。显然，他很急于走开，显得焦躁不安、疲惫不堪，比起以前也苍老了许多。
I suppose it was the haggard face that put me suddenly upon my enterprise. 我认为就是他那憔悴的面容让我直切主题。
“My lord,” said I, with my head down, and feigning to continue my occupation—“or, rather, let me call you again by the name of Mr. Henry, for I fear your anger and want you to think upon old times—” 我低着头，假装忙着工作说道：“爵爷，或者允许我再叫您亨利先生，我又怕这样称呼您，让您想起以前的事情。”
“My good Mackellar!” said he; and that in tones so kindly that I had near forsook my purpose. 他说：“善良的麦凯勒啊！”他的语调如此温柔，以至于我差点儿忘了自己的目的。
But I called to mind that I was speaking for his good, and stuck to my colours. 我心里想着我这么做是为了他好，然后言归正传。
“Has it never come in upon your mind what you are doing?” “您就没想过您在做什么吗？”
I asked. 我问道。
“What I am doing?” he repeated; “I was never good at guessing riddles.” 他重复道：“我在做什么？我从来不擅长猜谜语。”
“What you are doing with your son?” said I. 我说：“您和您的儿子在干什么？”
“Well,” said he, with some defiance in his tone, “and what am I doing with my son?” 他语调带着些挑衅地说：“哦，和我的儿子在干什么？”
“Your father was a very good man,” says I, straying from the direct path. 我拐弯抹角地说：“您的父亲是个非常好的人，
“But do you think he was a wise father?” 但您认为他是个明智的父亲吗？”
There was a pause before he spoke, and then: “I say nothing against him,” he replied. 他停顿了一会儿，然后答道：“我没说他不好。
“I had the most cause perhaps; but I say nothing.” 虽然我最有理由那么做，但我什么也没说。”
“Why, there it is,” said I. 我说：“为什么没那么做，这么说吧。
“You had the cause at least. 您至少有理由那样做啊！
And yet your father was a good man; I never knew a better, save on the one point, nor yet a wiser. 您父亲是个好人，我还没见过比他更好的人，就说这一点吧，其实也没见过比他更明智的。
Where he stumbled, it is highly possible another man should fail. 他跌倒的地方，其他人也非常有可能跌倒。
He had the two sons—” 他有两个儿子——”
My lord rapped suddenly and violently on the table. 爵爷突然重重地拍了一下桌子。
“What is this?” cried he. 他喊道：“这话是什么意思？
“Speak out!” 说出来！”
“I will, then,” said I, my voice almost strangled with the thumping of my heart. “接下来，我会说，”我心怦怦地跳，几乎窒息，说道，
“If you continue to indulge Mr. Alexander, you are following in your father’s footsteps. “如果您继续溺爱亚历山大先生的话，您就是步您父亲的后尘。
Beware, my lord, lest (when he grows up) your son should follow in the Master’s.” 醒醒吧，爵爷，不要让您的儿子（长大成人的时候）走大少爷的老路”。
I had never meant to put the thing so crudely; but in the extreme of fear, there comes a brutal kind of courage, the most brutal indeed of all; and I burnt my ships with that plain word. 我从没想过要把这件事情如此赤裸裸地讲出来，但害怕到了极点就变成了勇气，最大的勇气，说那些话的确是破釜沉舟了。
I never had the answer. 他永远也没有答复我。
When I lifted my head, my lord had risen to his feet, and the next moment he fell heavily on the floor. 当我抬起头时，爵爷已经站起来了，接着重重地摔倒在地板上。
The fit or seizure endured not very long; he came to himself vacantly, put his hand to his head, which I was then supporting, and says he, in a broken voice: “I have been ill,” and a little after: “Help me.” 这阵发作时间不长，他恢复了意识，但眼神呆滞，我正捧着他的头，他用手摸着脑袋，声音断断续续地说：“我病了。”过了一会儿又说：“救救我。”
I got him to his feet, and he stood pretty well, though he kept hold of the table. 我扶他站起来，虽然他不得不扶着桌子，但站得很稳。
“I have been ill, Mackellar,” he said again. 他又说道：“麦凯勒，我病了。
“Something broke, Mackellar—or was going to break, and then all swam away. 身体里不知什么坏了，麦凯勒，或者要坏了，接着就失去了意识。
I think I was very angry. 我想我是气晕了。
Never you mind, Mackellar; never you mind, my man. 没关系，麦凯勒。伙计，没关系。
I wouldnae hurt a hair upon your head. 我不会伤你一根毫毛。
Too much has come and gone. 发生了太多事情。
It’s a certain thing between us two. 这是我们之间的秘密。
But I think, Mackellar, I will go to Mrs. Henry—I think I will go to Mrs. Henry,” said he, and got pretty steadily from the room, leaving me overcome with penitence. 麦凯勒，但是我想我会去找亨利夫人，我想我会去找亨利夫人。”他说完就很稳当地离开了，留下我自己在那里愧疚。
Presently the door flew open, and my lady swept in with flashing eyes. 一会儿，门砰地一下打开了，夫人闯了进来，眼中充满了怒火。
“What is all this?” she cried. 她喊道：“这是怎么回事？
“What have you done to my husband? 你对我丈夫做了些什么？
Will nothing teach you your position in this house? 难道你不清楚你在这个家的地位吗？
Will you never cease from making and meddling?” 你就不能不惹是生非吗？”
“My lady,” said I, “since I have been in this house I have had plenty of hard words. 我说：“夫人，自从我在这儿工作，我遭受过很多辱骂。
For a while they were my daily diet, and I swallowed them all. 有段时间，那是家常便饭，我都忍气吞声。
As for to-day, you may call me what you please; you will never find the name hard enough for such a blunder. 至于今天，您可以随便骂我，关于我所犯的错，您怎么骂都不为过。
And yet I meant it for the best.” 但我本来是一片好意。”
I told her all with ingenuity, even as it is written here; and when she had heard me out, she pondered, and I could see her animosity fall. 我原原本本地告诉了她，和我在这里写的一样，她听完后，陷入了沉思，我能看出她的怒火消了下去。
“Yes,” she said, “you meant well indeed. 她说道：“是的，你本是好意。
I have had the same thought myself, or the same temptation rather, which makes me pardon you. 其实我也曾有过和你一样的想法，或者说，我也曾受到了同样的诱惑。正因如此，我才能够原谅你。
But, dear God, can you not understand that he can bear no more? 但是，上帝啊！您难道不明白他已经承受不起任何痛苦了吗？
He can bear no more!” she cried. 他承受不起了。”
“The cord is stretched to snapping. 她喊道：“绳子快崩断了。
What matters the future if he have one or two good days?” 他如果还能过一两天好日子，还管将来干什么？”
“Amen,” said I. 我说道：“阿门！
“I will meddle no more. 我再也不掺和了。
I am pleased enough that you should recognise the kindness of my meaning.” 您明白我是出自一番好意，我就心满意足了。”
“Yes,” said my lady; “but when it came to the point, I have to suppose your courage failed you; for what you said was said cruelly.” 夫人说：“是的，但说到这儿，我不得不说，你并不像自己想象的那样勇敢，你说话的方式未免过于残忍。”
She paused, looking at me; then suddenly smiled a little, and said a singular thing: “Do you know what you are, Mr. Mackellar? 她停下，看着我，然后突然笑了笑，说了一句话：“麦凯勒，你知道自己是谁吗？
You are an old maid.” 你是个老妈子。”
No more incident of any note occurred in the family until the return of that ill-starred man the Master. 直到那个邪恶的角色——大少爷回来，家里再也没有发生任何事情。
But I have to place here a second extract from the memoirs of Chevalier Burke, interesting in itself, and highly necessary for my purpose. 我得在这里再次摘取伯克骑士的回忆录，这本身很有意思，也非常符合我的目的。
It is our only sight of the Master on his Indian travels; and the first word in these pages of Secundra Dass. 这是我们唯一可以窥探大少爷印度之旅的地方，也是第一次提到塞孔拉德·戴斯。
One fact, it is to observe, appears here very clearly, which if we had known some twenty years ago, how many calamities and sorrows had been spared!—that Secundra Dass spoke English. 一个事实变得清晰起来，如果二十年前我们就知塞孔拉德·戴斯会说英语的话，那会避免多少灾难和痛苦啊！
Chapter 7 第七章
Adventure of Chevalier Burke in India. 伯克骑士印度奇遇
Extracted from his Memoirs. 摘自他的回忆录
...Here was I, therefore, on the streets of that city, the name of which I cannot call to mind, while even then I was so ill- acquainted with its situation that I knew not whether to go south or north. ……于是，我漫步在这个城市的大街小巷，连这个城市的名字都记不起来，我对这里的情况了解很少，南北都分不清。
The alert being sudden, I had run forth without shoes or stockings; my hat had been struck from my head in the mellay; my kit was in the hands of the English; I had no companion but the cipaye, no weapon but my sword, and the devil a coin in my pocket. 突然，我猛地惊醒，开始往前跑，鞋和袜子都没穿，帽子也被混乱的人群挤掉了，我的箱子还在那个英国人手里。除了印度兵，我没有其他同伴；除了我的剑，我没有其他武器，他妈的口袋里只剩一个银币了。
In short, I was for all the world like one of those calendars with whom Mr. Galland has made us acquainted in his elegant tales. 简而言之，发生在我身上的事简直就像加朗先生在他优雅的故事中描写的那些日子一样。
These gentlemen, you will remember, were for ever falling in with extraordinary incidents; and I was myself upon the brink of one so astonishing that I protest I cannot explain it to this day. 你会记得这些绅士们总是会遇上些稀奇百怪的事情，而我自己也差点儿遇上一件神奇的事，以至于到今天我都没法解释清楚。
The cipaye was a very honest man; he had served many years with the French colours, and would have let himself be cut to pieces for any of the brave countrymen of Mr. Lally. 那个印度兵非常诚实，他为法国人工作了很多年，而且愿意为了拉利先生勇敢的同胞们粉身碎骨。
It is the same fellow (his name has quite escaped me) of whom I have narrated already a surprising instance of generosity of mind—when he found Mr. de Fessac and myself upon the ramparts, entirely overcome with liquor, and covered us with straw while the commandant was passing by. 他的名字我没记住，他就是我之前说过的那个无比慷慨大方的人——那天我和德费萨克先生在城墙上喝得酩酊大醉，就在司令要经过的时候，他用稻草把我们盖住了。
I consulted him, therefore, with perfect freedom. 因此，我自然而然地向他请教。
It was a fine question what to do; but we decided at last to escalade a garden wall, where we could certainly sleep in the shadow of the trees, and might perhaps find an occasion to get hold of a pair of slippers and a turban. 问题是接下来该怎么办，但我们最终决定翻过一个花园的墙头，这样我们可以躺在树阴下睡觉，或许还可能捡到一双拖鞋、一块头巾。
In that part of the city we had only the difficulty of the choice, for it was a quarter consisting entirely of walled gardens, and the lanes which divided them were at that hour of the night deserted. 在城市的那片地区，唯一的难题就是选择哪一个花园，因为那一带都是住宅区，四面都有围墙，围墙之间的小巷到了晚上就无人通行了。
I gave the cipaye a back, and we had soon dropped into a large enclosure full of trees. 我让印度兵踩着我的背翻过墙去，很快我们就跳到一大片被围墙围着的树林中。
The place was soaking with the dew, which, in that country, is exceedingly unwholesome, above all to whites; yet my fatigue was so extreme that I was already half asleep, when the cipaye recalled me to my senses. 这地方到处都是露水，在那个国家，尤其是对白人来说，露水对健康是有害的。但是我实在是太累了，几乎昏昏欲睡，幸亏印度兵把我叫醒了。
In the far end of the enclosure a bright light had suddenly shone out, and continued to burn steadily among the leaves. 在树林的边缘，突然出现一道亮光，透过树叶不断闪耀着。
It was a circumstance highly unusual in such a place and hour; and, in our situation, it behoved us to proceed with some timidity. 在这个时间、这个地点出现这种情况极其不正常，而且这让我们前行的时候更加小心了。
The cipaye was sent to reconnoitre, and pretty soon returned with the intelligence that we had fallen extremely amiss, for the house belonged to a white man, who was in all likelihood English. 我让印度兵去前面侦察情况，他很快就带着情报回来,原来我们竟然误打误撞地闯进一个白人的房子里了,这个白人还可能是个英国人。
“Faith,” says I, “if there is a white man to be seen, I will have a look at him; for, the Lord be praised! there are more sorts than the one!” “确实，”我说，“如果真遇上一个白人，我倒要会会他。愿上帝保佑，白人也会有好坏之分！”
The cipaye led me forward accordingly to a place from which I had a clear view upon the house. 印度兵领着我往前走，到了一个能清楚看到那栋房子的地方。
It was surrounded with a wide verandah; a lamp, very well trimmed, stood upon the floor of it, and on either side of the lamp there sat a man, cross-legged, after the Oriental manner. 房子的四周是宽宽的走廊，走廊的地板上立着一盏装饰精美的灯，灯的两旁各坐着一个男人，像东方人那样盘着腿。
Both, besides, were bundled up in muslin like two natives; and yet one of them was not only a white man, but a man very well known to me and the reader, being indeed that very Master of Ballantrae of whose gallantry and genius I have had to speak so often. 而且，两个人都像本地人一样穿着印花布做的衣服。而且其中一个不仅是个白人，还是我与读者的老熟人，他就是我一直提到的那个勇敢聪明的巴伦特雷少爷。
Word had reached me that he was come to the Indies, though we had never met at least, and I heard little of his occupations. 我早就听说他到印度来了，尽管我们从未见过面，而且我也不太清楚他干的是哪一行。
But, sure, I had no sooner recognised him, and found myself in the arms of so old a comrade, than I supposed my tribulations were quite done. 但是，如果我马上认出他来，和他像老友一样拥抱一下，我想自己的苦难就要结束了吧。
I stepped plainly forth into the light of the moon, which shone exceeding strong, and hailing Ballantrae by name, made him in a few words master of my grievous situation. 我大大方方地走在明亮的月光下，大声叫着巴伦特雷的名字，让他了解我现在的艰难处境。
He turned, started the least thing in the world, looked me fair in the face while I was speaking, and when I had done addressed himself to his companion in the barbarous native dialect. 他淡定地转过身，在我说话的时候，他直直地看着我的脸。我一说完，他就叽里咕噜地用地方方言和他同伴说起话来。
The second person, who was of an extraordinary delicate appearance, with legs like walking canes and fingers like the stalk of a tobacco pipe,[1] now rose to his feet. 他的同伴看着非常瘦弱，双腿犹如两根拐杖，手指像烟斗柄。[1]此刻他站起身来。
“The Sahib,” says he, “understands no English language. “这位阁下，”他说道，“不懂英文。
I understand it myself, and I see you make some small mistake—oh! which may happen very often. 我自己懂，而且我听出来你犯了些小错误——噢，这是常有的事。
But the Sahib would be glad to know how you come in a garden.” 但是，这位阁下想知道你是怎么进到花园里来的。”
“Ballantrae!” “巴伦特雷！”
I cried, “have you the damned impudence to deny me to my face?” 我大声喊道，“你他娘的难道不认识我了？”
Ballantrae never moved a muscle, staring at me like an image in a pagoda. 巴伦特雷像佛塔中的神像一般，纹丝不动地盯着我看。
“The Sahib understands no English language,” says the native, as glib as before. “这位阁下不懂英语，”那个本地人还是像之前一样，油腔滑调地说，
“He be glad to know how you come in a garden.” 他想知道你是怎么进到花园里来的。”
“Oh! the divil fetch him,” says I. “噢，天杀的，”我说，
“He would be glad to know how I come in a garden, would he? “他想知道我是怎么进到花园里来的，是吗？
Well, now, my dear man, just have the civility to tell the Sahib, with my kind love, that we are two soldiers here whom he never met and never heard of, but the cipaye is a broth of a boy, and I am a broth of a boy myself; and if we don’t get a full meal of meat, and a turban, and slippers, and the value of a gold mohur in small change as a matter of convenience, bedad, my friend, I could lay my finger on a garden where there is going to be trouble.” 好吧，伙计，现在就劳驾你告诉那位阁下，我们是两个士兵，他从来没见过，也没听说过，不过印度兵是条好汉，我也是条好汉。而且，要是我们吃不到一顿丰盛的肉，拿不到一条头巾和一双拖鞋，还有换成零钱方便花的一个印度金币，那么我的朋友，我就告诉你，在这个花园里，凡是我的手指碰得到的地方，都会鸡犬不宁。”
They carried their comedy so far as to converse awhile in Hindustanee; and then says the Hindu, with the same smile, but sighing as if he were tired of the repetition, “The Sahib would be glad to know how you come in a garden.” 他们继续演着戏，用印度语交流了一会儿，然后那个印度人带着同样的微笑，叹了口气，仿佛厌倦了这种重复：“这位阁下想知道你们是怎么进到花园里来的。”
“Is that the way of it?” says I, and laying my hand on my sword- hilt I bade the cipaye draw. “就这样吗？”我说着，手握剑柄，同时也命令印度兵准备拔剑。
Ballantrae’s Hindu, still smiling, pulled out a pistol from his bosom, and though Ballantrae himself never moved a muscle I knew him well enough to be sure he was prepared. 巴伦特雷的印度伙伴仍然面带微笑，从胸口掏出一把手枪。尽管巴伦特雷自己纹丝不动，但是我对他太了解了，他肯定是有了充分的准备。
“The Sahib thinks you better go away,” says the Hindu. “这位阁下认为你们最好离开这里。”那个印度人说。
Well, to be plain, it was what I was thinking myself; for the report of a pistol would have been, under Providence, the means of hanging the pair of us. 坦白地说，我心里也是这么想的。上帝啊！他要是一开枪，我们俩就要被判死刑了。
“Tell the Sahib I consider him no gentleman,” says I, and turned away with a gesture of contempt. “你告诉那位阁下，我可觉得他一点儿都不像个绅士。”我说完，做了一个轻蔑的手势，转过身去了。
I was not gone three steps when the voice of the Hindu called me back. 我还没走出去三步，那个印度人就叫我回去。
“The Sahib would be glad to know if you are a dam low Irishman,” says he; and at the words Ballantrae smiled and bowed very low. “这位阁下想知道，你是不是个下贱的爱尔兰人。”他说。听到这话，巴伦特雷笑了，深深地鞠了一躬。
“What is that?” says I. “这是什么意思？”我问道。
“The Sahib say you ask your friend Mackellar,” says the Hindu. “这位阁下说，你可以去问你的朋友麦凯勒，”印度人说道，
“The Sahib he cry quits.” “阁下叫你们滚出去。”
“Tell the Sahib I will give him a cure for the Scots fiddle when next we meet,” cried I. “告诉那位阁下，下次我们见面的时候，我会想办法治治这个苏格兰骗子。”我喊道。
The pair were still smiling as I left. 我离开的时候，他们两人仍然面带笑意。
There is little doubt some flaws may be picked in my own behaviour; and when a man, however gallant, appeals to posterity with an account of his exploits, he must almost certainly expect to share the fate of Caesar and Alexander, and to meet with some detractors. 毫无疑问，我自身的行为并非完美无瑕。一个人，不管多么英勇，如果想通过描述自己的丰功伟绩而彪炳千秋，就必须承受凯撒和亚历山大同样的命运，也必然招致诋毁。
But there is one thing that can never be laid at the door of Francis Burke: he never turned his back on a friend.... 但是，有一件事是弗朗西斯·伯克从未遇到过的：他从来没有背叛过朋友……
(Here follows a passage which the Chevalier Burke has been at the pains to delete before sending me his manuscript. （下面是伯克骑士把他的手稿寄给我之前，费心删除的一段话。
Doubtless it was some very natural complaint of what he supposed to be an indiscretion on my part; though, indeed, I can call none to mind. 毫无疑问，他认为我办事鲁莽，这个想法并不是毫无根据的，尽管我自己想不出来有什么证据。
Perhaps Mr. Henry was less guarded; or it is just possible the Master found the means to examine my correspondence, and himself read the letter from Troyes: in revenge for which this cruel jest was perpetrated on Mr. Burke in his extreme necessity. 或许，亨利先生警惕性不高，又或者大少爷可能找到什么方法检查了我的信件，并且他亲自看了来自特鲁瓦的信。为了报复伯克先生，所以大少爷在最需要帮助的时候跟他开了个玩笑。
The Master, for all his wickedness, was not without some natural affection; I believe he was sincerely attached to Mr. Burke in the beginning; but the thought of treachery dried up the springs of his very shallow friendship, and his detestable nature appeared naked. 大少爷尽管心狠手辣，但并不是一个完全没有人性的人，我相信他一开始的时候对伯克先生是很真诚的。但是一想到背叛的事情，友情的源泉就枯竭了，况且还是非常浅薄的友情，他那可憎的本性也就显露无遗了。
—E. McK.) ——伊弗雷姆·麦凯勒）
[1] Note by Mr. Mackellar. [1]麦凯勒先生作的注释。
—Plainly Secundra Dass. ——简单地说，塞孔拉德·戴斯
—E. McK. ———伊弗雷姆·麦凯勒
Chapter 8 第八章
The Enemy in the House. 宿敌归来
It is a strange thing that I should be at a stick for a date—the date, besides, of an incident that changed the very nature of my life, and sent us all into foreign lands. 奇怪的是，我会为了一个日期感到为难——而且这个日子里发生的一件事彻底改变了我的生活，并把我们都送到了国外。
But the truth is, I was stricken out of all my habitudes, and find my journals very ill redd-up, [1] the day not indicated sometimes for a week or two together, and the whole fashion of the thing like that of a man near desperate. 但事实是，我自己的习惯完全被打乱了，我的日记被搞得乱七八糟，[1]有时一周或两周都没写日记，整个日记就像是一个濒临绝境的人写的。
It was late in March at least, or early in April, 1764. 那至少是1764年的三月下旬，或四月初的时候。
I had slept heavily, and wakened with a premonition of some evil to befall. 我睡得很沉，醒来的时候预感有什么坏事要发生了。
So strong was this upon my spirit that I hurried downstairs in my shirt and breeches, and my hand (I remember) shook upon the rail. 这种感觉无比强烈，于是我穿上衬衫和马裤就匆忙下楼，（我记得）我的手扶在栏杆上时抖了一下。
It was a cold, sunny morning, with a thick white frost; the blackbirds sang exceeding sweet and loud about the house of Durrisdeer, and there was a noise of the sea in all the chambers. 那是一个寒冷但晴朗的早晨，外面结了厚厚的白霜；画眉在达里斯迪尔府邸周围唱着非常甜美清脆的歌，所有的房间都能听到海浪的声音。
As I came by the doors of the hall, another sound arrested me—of voices talking. 当我经过大厅门口时，另一个声音吸引了我——谈话的声音。
I drew nearer, and stood like a man dreaming. 我靠近了点儿，像个梦游的人一样站在那里。
Here was certainly a human voice, and that in my own master’s house, and yet I knew it not; certainly human speech, and that in my native land; and yet, listen as I pleased, I could not catch one syllable. 这的确是人的声音，而且就在我主人的房子里，不过我听不出那个声音是谁的，肯定是当地人的口音，尽管我听得很欢，却连一个字都听不懂。
An old tale started up in my mind of a fairy wife (or perhaps only a wandering stranger), that came to the place of my fathers some generations back, and stayed the matter of a week, talking often in a tongue that signified nothing to the hearers; and went again, as she had come, under cloud of night, leaving not so much as a name behind her. 我想起一个古老的故事，几代人以前有个老妇人（或许只是一个流浪的陌生人）来到我的祖辈们生活的地方，呆了一周的样子，经常嘀嘀咕咕不知道说什么。后来，她趁着夜幕离开了，就如同来的时候一样，连个名字都没留下。
A little fear I had, but more curiosity; and I opened the hall-door, and entered. 我有点儿害怕，但更多的是好奇。我打开大厅的门，走了进去。
The supper-things still lay upon the table; the shutters were still closed, although day peeped in the divisions; and the great room was lighted only with a single taper and some lurching reverberation of the fire. 晚餐仍然摆在餐桌上，百叶窗仍然关着，尽管透过缝隙能隐约看到白天的亮光，照亮整个大房间的只有一根细蜡烛和火炉里反射的光。
Close in the chimney sat two men. 烟囱附近坐着两个人。
The one that was wrapped in a cloak and wore boots, I knew at once: it was the bird of ill omen back again. 一个披着斗篷、穿着皮靴，我立马认出来了：那个不祥的人又回来了。
Of the other, who was set close to the red embers, and made up into a bundle like a mummy, I could but see that he was an alien, of a darker hue than any man of Europe, very frailly built, with a singular tall forehead, and a secret eye. 另一个坐在红红的火苗附近，裹得跟木乃伊似的，我只能说他像个外星人，长得比任何欧洲人都要黑，身形消瘦，前额宽阔，还有一双诡秘的眼睛。
Several bundles and a small valise were on the floor; and to judge by the smallness of this luggage, and by the condition of the Master’s boots, grossly patched by some unscrupulous country cobbler, evil had not prospered. 地板上放着几捆东西和一个小箱子。行李不大，大少爷的靴子粗糙地打着补丁，大概是一个不太认真的乡村鞋匠给补的，从这些来看，邪恶的大少爷并没有飞黄腾达。
He rose upon my entrance; our eyes crossed; and I know not why it should have been, but my courage rose like a lark on a May morning. 我一进去，他站起身来，我们四目相交。我不知道情况为什么会这样，但是我的勇气就像五月清晨的百灵鸟一样腾空而起。
“Ha!” said I, “is this you?”—and I was pleased with the unconcern of my own voice. “哈，是您呀？”——我对自己的声音所表现出的冷淡很满意。
“It is even myself, worthy Mackellar,” says the Master. “正是我，尊敬的麦凯勒。”大少爷说道。
“This time you have brought the black dog visibly upon your back,” I continued. “显然，这次您带来了晦气。”我接着道。
“Referring to Secundra Dass?” asked the Master. “你说的是塞孔拉德·戴斯吗？”大少爷问道，
“Let me present you. “我来给你介绍一下。
He is a native gentleman of India.” 他是一位印度当地的绅士。”
“Hum!” said I. “哼！”我说道，
“I am no great lover either of you or your friends, Mr. Bally. “巴利先生，我对您和您的朋友都不是很待见。
But I will let a little daylight in, and have a look at you.” 不过我得让外面的光线进来一点儿，看看你们的样子。”
And so saying, I undid the shutters of the eastern window. 说着，我打开东边窗户的百叶窗。
By the light of the morning I could perceive the man was changed. 借着早晨的光线，我发现这个人有了一些变化。
Later, when we were all together, I was more struck to see how lightly time had dealt with him; but the first glance was otherwise. 后来，当我们都聚在一块的时候，我发觉时间并没有改变他多少，但是第一眼却给了我另一种感觉。
“You are getting an old man,” said I. “您老了。”我说道。
A shade came upon his face. 他的脸阴沉了下来。
“If you could see yourself,” said he, “you would perhaps not dwell upon the topic.” “如果你看看你自己，”他说，“你可能就不会这么说了。”
“Hut!” “啊哈！”
I returned, “old age is nothing to me. 我反驳道，“年老对于我来说不算什么。
I think I have been always old; and I am now, I thank God, better known and more respected. 我觉得自己一直就是老人。现在嘛，感谢上帝，我比以前懂的更多，更受尊敬。
It is not every one that can say that, Mr. Bally! 巴利先生，不是谁都能这么说的！
The lines in your brow are calamities; your life begins to close in upon you like a prison; death will soon be rapping at the door; and I see not from what source you are to draw your consolations.” 您额头上的皱纹表示你经历的不幸，您的生活正像监狱一般逼近您，死神很快就会来敲门，而且我看不出您将要去何处寻找安慰。”
Here the Master addressed himself to Secundra Dass in Hindustanee, from which I gathered (I freely confess, with a high degree of pleasure) that my remarks annoyed him. 此时，大少爷和塞孔拉德·戴斯用印度语说话，由此看来（坦白地说，我心里十分开心），我的话惹恼了他。
All this while, you may be sure, my mind had been busy upon other matters, even while I rallied my enemy; and chiefly as to how I should communicate secretly and quickly with my lord. 这个时候，你可能会觉得，甚至当我在挖苦我的对手的时候，我都在想着其他的事情，主要就是我应该怎么秘密快速地和爵爷联系上。
To this, in the breathing-space now given me, I turned all the forces of my mind; when, suddenly shifting my eyes, I was aware of the man himself standing in the doorway, and, to all appearance, quite composed. 就在现有的喘息之际，我调动了所有的脑细胞。突然，我眼睛一转，看到爵爷就站在门口，而且看起来非常镇定自若的样子。
He had no sooner met my looks than he stepped across the threshold. 他一碰上我的目光，就跨过门槛。
The Master heard him coming, and advanced upon the other side; about four feet apart, these brothers came to a full pause, and stood exchanging steady looks, and then my lord smiled, bowed a little forward, and turned briskly away. 大少爷听到他进来，走到另外一边，大概四英尺的距离。兄弟俩都停顿了一下，站在那里不动声色地互相打量着，接着爵爷笑了，稍微往前弯了弯腰，轻快地转过身来。
“Mackellar,” says he, “we must see to breakfast for these travellers.” “麦凯勒，”他说道，“我们得给这两位客人准备点儿早餐。”
It was plain the Master was a trifle disconcerted; but he assumed the more impudence of speech and manner. 很明显，大少爷有点儿仓皇失措，但言谈举止却表现得更加趾高气扬。
“I am as hungry as a hawk,” says he. “我饿坏了，”他说道，
“Let it be something good, Henry.” “亨利，给我们做点儿好吃的吧。”
My lord turned to him with the same hard smile. 爵爷带着同样生硬的微笑转向他。
“Lord Durrisdeer,” says he. “是达里斯迪尔勋爵。”他说道。
“Oh! never in the family,” returned the Master. “噢，在家里就不必这么称呼了吧。”大少爷回答道。
“Every one in this house renders me my proper title,” says my lord. “这个房子里的每个人都是用我的爵位来称呼我的，”爵爷说道，
“If it please you to make an exception, I will leave you to consider what appearance it will bear to strangers, and whether it may not be translated as an effect of impotent jealousy.” “如果破个例会让你高兴的话，那你自己想想看，这在外人面前会像什么样子，难道不会被看成一种无能为力的嫉妒么？”
I could have clapped my hands together with delight: the more so as my lord left no time for any answer, but, bidding me with a sign to follow him, went straight out of the hall. 我真是高兴得想拍手叫好，爵爷没等他回答，就示意让我跟着他，直接走出了大厅。
“Come quick,” says he; “we have to sweep vermin from the house.” “快点儿，”他说道，“我们必须将屋里的害虫扫地出门。”
And he sped through the passages, with so swift a step that I could scarce keep up with him, straight to the door of John Paul, the which he opened without summons and walked in. 于是他快速穿过走廊，步履轻快，我都快跟不上他了。他径直来到约翰·保罗的门口，招呼也没打就直接走了进去。
John was, to all appearance, sound asleep, but my lord made no pretence of waking him. 约翰似乎睡得很熟，不过爵爷没有假意叫醒他。
“John Paul,” said he, speaking as quietly as ever I heard him, “you served my father long, or I would pack you from the house like a dog. “约翰·保罗，”他以我听过最轻柔的声音说道：要不是你伺候了我父亲那么长时间，我会把你赶出这个房子，就像撵狗一样。
If in half an hour’s time I find you gone, you shall continue to receive your wages in Edinburgh. 如果你在半个小时内消失，你就去爱丁堡继续拿你的工资。
If you linger here or in St. Bride’s—old man, old servant, and altogether—I shall find some very astonishing way to make you smart for your disloyalty. 要是你留在这里或者圣布赖德——老人也好，老仆也罢——我会用一些意想不到的方式让你尝一尝背叛带来的苦果。
Up and begone. 起来吧，然后离开这儿。
The door you let them in by will serve for your departure. 从你放他们进来的那个门出去。
I do not choose my son shall see your face again.” 我不会让我的儿子再一次看到你。”
“I am rejoiced to find you bear the thing so quietly,” said I, when we were forth again by ourselves. “看到您处理事情这么镇定，我很高兴。”我们出来以后，我说道。
“Quietly!” cries he, and put my hand suddenly against his heart, which struck upon his bosom like a sledge. “镇定！”他大声叫道，然后突然把我的手放到他的胸口，他的心脏像大锤一样跳个不停。
At this revelation I was filled with wonder and fear. 一发现这个出乎意料的事实，我的心里一下充满了好奇和恐惧。
There was no constitution could bear so violent a strain—his least of all, that was unhinged already; and I decided in my mind that we must bring this monstrous situation to an end. 没有一个人能忍受如此强烈的紧张——至少对于一个已经精神错乱的人来说是这样的，我暗暗决定我们必须结束这种危险的境地。
“It would be well, I think, if I took word to my lady,” said I. “我觉得，如果我去给太太报个信，恐怕会好些。”我说道。
Indeed, he should have gone himself, but I counted—not in vain—on his indifference. 事实上，他本应该自己去的，但是我考虑到（并不是徒劳的）他的冷漠态度。
“Aye,” says he, “do. “对，”他说，“去吧。
I will hurry breakfast: we must all appear at the table, even Alexander; it must appear we are untroubled.” 我会赶紧弄好早餐：我们都得上桌吃饭，亚历山大也是一样。我们必须表现得像没有受到干扰一样。”
I ran to my lady’s room, and with no preparatory cruelty disclosed my news. 我跑到太太的房间，在她毫无准备的情况下，告诉她这个消息。
“My mind was long ago made up,” said she. “我早就下定决心了，”她说道，
“We must make our packets secretly to-day, and leave secretly to-night. “我们必须今天悄悄整理好行装，然后今晚秘密离开。
Thank Heaven, we have another house! 感谢老天，我们还有一处房子！
The first ship that sails shall bear us to New York.” 头班船会把我们带去纽约。”
“And what of him?” “那他怎么办？”
I asked. 我问道。
“We leave him Durrisdeer,” she cried. “就让他留在达里斯迪尔，”她大喊道，
“Let him work his pleasure upon that.” “让他在这享受自己当爵爷的乐趣吧。”
“Not so, by your leave,” said I. “不好意思，应该还不只这些，”我说道，
“There shall be a dog at his heels that can hold fast. “他身边应该还有一条忠实的狗紧紧看着他。
Bed he shall have, and board, and a horse to ride upon, if he behave himself; but the keys—if you think well of it, my lady—shall be left in the hands of one Mackellar. 他会有床睡，有饭吃，如果表现得规矩，还会有马骑。不过房子的钥匙——太太，您可以好好考虑一下——就留到我麦凯勒这里吧。
There will be good care taken; trust him for that.” 我会好好照管的，就相信我吧。”
“Mr. Mackellar,” she cried, “I thank you for that thought. “麦凯勒先生，”她说道，“谢谢你给我出的主意。
All shall be left in your hands. 所有的东西都会交给你。
If we must go into a savage country, I bequeath it to you to take our vengeance. 如果我们必须去一个野蛮的国度，我会委托你来执行我们的报复计划。
Send Macconochie to St. Bride’s, to arrange privately for horses and to call the lawyer. 赶紧派麦康纳基去圣布赖德，悄悄地安排马匹，然后把律师请过来。
My lord must leave procuration.” 爵爷必须留下委任状。”
At that moment my lord came to the door, and we opened our plan to him. 就在那个时候，爵爷刚好来到门边，我们把计划一五一十地告诉了他。
“I will never hear of it,” he cried; “he would think I feared him. “我绝不会听从你们这个计划的，”他喊道，“他会觉得我怕了他。
I will stay in my own house, please God, until I die. 上帝啊！我要呆在自己的房子里，直到我死去。
There lives not the man can beard me out of it. 这个世上还没人能把我赶出去。
Once and for all, here I am, and here I stay in spite of all the devils in hell.” 我就永远待在这儿，不管有什么妖魔鬼怪，我都不会走。”
I can give no idea of the vehemency of his words and utterance; but we both stood aghast, and I in particular, who had been a witness of his former self-restraint. 我完全不懂他的言辞和呐喊中的愤怒，但是我们都呆呆地站着，特别是我，曾经亲眼目睹了他之前的自我克制。
My lady looked at me with an appeal that went to my heart and recalled me to my wits. 太太别有深意地看了我一眼，我突然明白过来。
I made her a private sign to go, and when my lord and I were alone, went up to him where he was racing to and fro in one end of the room like a half-lunatic, and set my hand firmly on his shoulder. 我悄悄做了个手势让她离开，当爵爷和我单独呆着的时候，他像半疯似的来回踱步，我走上前，把手牢牢地按在他的肩膀上。
“My lord,” says I, “I am going to be the plain-dealer once more; if for the last time, so much the better, for I am grown weary of the part.” “爵爷，”我说道，“我还是坦白说吧，希望这是最后一次，因为我已经对这些感到厌烦了。”
“Nothing will change me,” he answered. “任何事情都不能改变我的想法，”他回答道，
“God forbid I should refuse to hear you; but nothing will change me.” “听听你的看法没什么不可以的，但是任何事情都不能改变我的想法。”
This he said firmly, with no signal of the former violence, which already raised my hopes. 他说这话的时候态度坚决，没有之前的激烈，这让我又有了一丝希望。
“Very well,” said I “I can afford to waste my breath.” “那好吧，”我说，“我浪费一点儿口舌也没关系。”
I pointed to a chair, and he sat down and looked at me. 我朝椅子指了指，他坐下来，看着我。
“I can remember a time when my lady very much neglected you,” said I. “我还记得有一阵子太太对您非常冷淡。”我说道。
“I never spoke of it while it lasted,” returned my lord, with a high flush of colour; “and it is all changed now.”’ “那个时候，我从来没有提起过，”爵爷脸红了，回答道，“不过现在情形全都改变了。”
“Do you know how much?” I said. “您知道改变了多少？” 我问，
“Do you know how much it is all changed? “您知道情形改变了多少吗？”
The tables are turned, my lord! 情形已经完全逆转了，爵爷啊！
It is my lady that now courts you for a word, a look—ay, and courts you in vain. 现在是太太求着您跟她说话，看她一眼——哎，可是您理都不理。
Do you know with whom she passes her days while you are out gallivanting in the policies? 您知道当您在别人家院子里跟别的女人调情的时候，是谁陪着太太吗？
My lord, she is glad to pass them with a certain dry old grieve[2] of the name of Ephraim Mackellar; and I think you may be able to remember what that means, for I am the more in a mistake or you were once driven to the same company yourself.” 是一个老的、不中用的仆人[2]，名字叫做伊弗雷姆·麦凯勒。我想您应该都记得那意味着什么，如果我没有说错的话，您一定会回到原来的伙伴身边的。”
“Mackellar!” cries my lord, getting to his feet. “麦凯勒！”爵爷站起来，大声嚷道，
“O my God, Mackellar!” “噢，天哪，麦凯勒！”
“It is neither the name of Mackellar nor the name of God that can change the truth,” said I; “and I am telling you the fact. “不管是麦凯勒还是上帝都无法改变这个事实，”我说道，“我跟您说的就是事实。
Now for you, that suffered so much, to deal out the same suffering to another, is that the part of any Christian? 您自己受过不少苦，但是现在却让别人遭受同样的痛苦，这难道是基督徒应该做的吗？
But you are so swallowed up in your new friend that the old are all forgotten. 但是您完全沉浸在新朋友的世界里，把老朋友都忘了。
They are all clean vanished from your memory. 他们彻底地从您的记忆里消失了。
And yet they stood by you at the darkest; my lady not the least. 虽然看不见他们，可是他们都默默地陪在您身边，特别是太太。
And does my lady ever cross your mind? 您心里想过太太吗？
Does it ever cross your mind what she went through that night?—or what manner of a wife she has been to you thenceforward?—or in what kind of a position she finds herself to-day? 您想过那天晚上她经历了什么吗？——或者从那以后，她该是一个怎样的妻子？——或者今天她又是什么样的心情？
Never. 从来没有。
It is your pride to stay and face him out, and she must stay along with you. 您呆在这儿，跟大少爷针锋相对，维护您的自尊心，太太就必须呆在您的身边。
Oh! my lord’s pride—that’s the great affair! 噢，爵爷的自尊心——那可是大事呀！
And yet she is the woman, and you are a great hulking man! 但是，她毕竟是个女人，而您却是个堂堂的大男人！
She is the woman that you swore to protect; and, more betoken, the own mother of that son of yours!” 她是您曾经发誓要保护的女人，更明白地说，她是你们儿子的母亲呀！”
“You are speaking very bitterly, Mackellar,” said he; “but, the Lord knows, I fear you are speaking very true. “麦凯勒，你说得太尖刻了，”他说，“不过，老天知道，恐怕你说的都是真的。
I have not proved worthy of my happiness. 我不配得到这样的幸福。
Bring my lady back.” 去把我的太太叫过来。”
My lady was waiting near at hand to learn the issue. 太太就在门外等着消息。
When I brought her in, my lord took a hand of each of us, and laid them both upon his bosom. 我领着她进来的时候，爵爷分别牵着我们的一只手，放到他的胸前。
“I have had two friends in my life,” said he. “我这一生有两个朋友，”他说道，
“All the comfort ever I had, it came from one or other. “是你们给了我所有的安慰。
When you two are in a mind, I think I would be an ungrateful dog—” 如果你们俩都这么想的话，那我真是个忘恩负义的家伙——”
He shut his mouth very hard, and looked on us with swimming eyes. 他紧闭着嘴，看着我们，眼含泪光。
“Do what ye like with me,” says he, “only don’t think—” “你们想怎么对我就怎么对我，”他说道，“只是不要以为——”
He stopped again. 他停顿了一下，
“Do what ye please with me: God knows I love and honour you.” “你们想怎么对我就怎么对我：上帝知道我是爱你们的，并且尊敬你们。”
And dropping our two hands, he turned his back and went and gazed out of the window. 他松开我们的手，转身走到窗户旁，凝视着窗外。
But my lady ran after, calling his name, and threw herself upon his neck in a passion of weeping. 太太走上去，喊着他的名字，扑到他的怀里哭了起来。
I went out and shut the door behind me, and stood and thanked God from the bottom of my heart. 我走出去，关上门，站在门口，由衷地感谢上帝。
At the breakfast board, according to my lord’s design, we were all met. 按照爵爷的意思，早餐时，我们都上桌吃饭。
The Master had by that time plucked off his patched boots and made a toilet suitable to the hour; Secundra Dass was no longer bundled up in wrappers, but wore a decent plain black suit, which misbecame him strangely; and the pair were at the great window, looking forth, when the family entered. 那时，大少爷已经脱了他那带有补丁的靴子，好好梳洗了一番。塞孔德拉·戴斯也脱下了裹着的长布条，穿着一套体面的黑色衣服，这衣服穿在他身上，看着有点儿奇怪。爵爷和夫人站在大大的窗户边，眼睛盯着前方。
They turned; and the black man (as they had already named him in the house) bowed almost to his knees, but the Master was for running forward like one of the family. 他们转过身，黑人（他们在屋子里这么称呼他的）来了一个近乎九十度的大鞠躬，但是大少爷已经像迎接家人一样飞快地迎上前了。
My lady stopped him, curtseying low from the far end of the hall, and keeping her children at her back. 太太拦住他，在大厅后面向他行了个屈膝礼，并把孩子们护在自己的身后。
My lord was a little in front: so there were the three cousins of Durrisdeer face to face. 爵爷站得稍微靠前：所以就是达里斯迪尔一家三个表兄妹面面相觑地站着。
The hand of time was very legible on all; I seemed to read in their changed faces a MEMENTO MORI; and what affected me still more, it was the wicked man that bore his years the handsomest. 岁月的痕迹在大家身上都很清晰。我似乎在他们沧桑的脸上读出了一句拉丁古训——人终有一死。更让我震惊的是，那个卑鄙的人在岁月的侵蚀下仍然英俊不已。
My lady was quite transfigured into the matron, a becoming woman for the head of a great tableful of children and dependents. 太太更是变成了一位家庭主妇，俨然就是一大帮孩子和仆人的头儿。
My lord was grown slack in his limbs; he stooped; he walked with a running motion, as though he had learned again from Mr. Alexander; his face was drawn; it seemed a trifle longer than of old; and it wore at times a smile very singularly mingled, and which (in my eyes) appeared both bitter and pathetic. 爵爷四肢的肌肉有些松弛，背有点儿驼，走起路来快速利落，好像又是从亚历山大先生那里学来的。他的脸紧绷着，似乎比以前长了点儿，有时候脸上还带着一丝奇怪的笑容，（可是在我眼中）显得痛苦和悲伤。
But the Master still bore himself erect, although perhaps with effort; his brow barred about the centre with imperious lines, his mouth set as for command. 但是大少爷依然站得笔直，也许只是努力撑着；眉心处长着几条专横的皱纹，嘴巴紧闭着像是在发号施令。
He had all the gravity and something of the splendour of Satan in the “Paradise Lost.” 他有着《失乐园》中撒旦所有的严肃、庄重和光彩。
I could not help but see the man with admiration, and was only surprised that I saw him with so little fear. 我忍不住看着他，内心充满了倾慕之情，奇怪的是，看到他竟然不怎么害怕。
But indeed (as long as we were at the table) it seemed as if his authority were quite vanished and his teeth all drawn. 但是，（只要我们坐在餐桌旁）他的威严好像完全消失了，戒备也没有了。
We had known him a magician that controlled the elements; and here he was, transformed into an ordinary gentleman, chatting like his neighbours at the breakfast-board. 一个我们认为是统治一切的魔术师摇身一变，成了一个普普通通的绅士，在早餐桌上像邻居似的聊天。
For now the father was dead, and my lord and lady reconciled, in what ear was he to pour his calumnies? 现在，老爷已经去世了，爵爷和太太也和好了，那他要跟谁去咬耳朵中伤别人呢？
It came upon me in a kind of vision how hugely I had overrated the man’s subtlety. 突然，我觉得自己好像大大高估了这个人的狡猾。
He had his malice still; he was false as ever; and, the occasion being gone that made his strength, he sat there impotent; he was still the viper, but now spent his venom on a file. 他仍然怀恨在心，跟以前一样虚伪，但是他恣意妄为的环境已经消失了，他只能无奈地坐在那里。虽然他还是那个像毒蛇一样的家伙，但是现在他的毒液却在锉刀上耗尽了。
Two more thoughts occurred to me while yet we sat at breakfast: the first, that he was abashed—I had almost said, distressed—to find his wickedness quite unavailing; the second, that perhaps my lord was in the right, and we did amiss to fly from our dismasted enemy. 吃早饭的时候，我又想到另外两件事：第一，若是大少爷发现自己的恶意无处发泄，他会局促不安，甚至可以说痛苦；第二，也许爵爷说得对，我们远离这个已经失势的敌人是不妥的。
But my poor man’s leaping heart came in my mind, and I remembered it was for his life we played the coward. 但是，一想到可怜的爵爷那激烈跳动的心脏，我才想起，正是替他的生命担忧，我们才成了胆小鬼。
When the meal was over, the Master followed me to my room, and, taking a chair (which I had never offered him), asked me what was to be done with him. 早餐结束后，大少爷跟着我来到我的房间，自己搬了一张椅子（我可从没招呼他坐），问我打算怎么招待他。
“Why, Mr. Bally,” said I, “the house will still be open to you for a time.” “怎么了，巴利先生，”我说道，“您还是可以在这里住一段时间的。”
“For a time?” says he. “一段时间？”他说道，
“I do not know if I quite take your meaning.” “我不太明白你的意思。”
“It is plain enough,” said I. “意思很明白了。”我说道，
“We keep you for our reputation; as soon as you shall have publicly disgraced yourself by some of your misconduct, we shall pack you forth again.” “我们接纳您是为了我们的名声考虑。一旦因为您的品行不端而在公众面前出丑的话，我们就要请你收拾东西走人了。”
“You are become an impudent rogue,” said the Master, bending his brows at me dangerously. 大少爷眉毛紧锁，恶狠狠地盯着我说：“你现在真是一个厚颜无耻的恶棍。”
“I learned in a good school,” I returned. “这是我在一个不错的学校学到的，”我回答道，
“And you must have perceived yourself that with my old lord’s death your power is quite departed. “而且您肯定也意识到了，老爷一死，您的权力也没有了。
I do not fear you now, Mr. Bally; I think even—God forgive me—that I take a certain pleasure in your company.” 巴利先生，我现在可不怕您了。我甚至觉得——上帝原谅我——有您的陪伴，我很开心。”
He broke out in a burst of laughter, which I clearly saw to be assumed. 他突然大笑起来，我一看就知道那是假装的。
“I have come with empty pockets,” says he, after a pause. “我回来可是两手空空呀。”停顿片刻，他说道。
“I do not think there will be any money going,” I replied. “现在家里估计也没钱了，”我回答道，
“I would advise you not to build on that.” “我建议您还是不要指望这个了。”
“I shall have something to say on the point,” he returned. “关于这一点，我有话要说。”他回答道。
“Indeed?” said I. “真的？”我说，
“I have not a guess what it will be, then.” “那我猜不出您想说什么。”
“Oh! you affect confidence,” said the Master. “噢！你这是假装自信，”大少爷说道，
“I have still one strong position—that you people fear a scandal, and I enjoy it.” “我仍然坚信一个观点——你们这些人害怕流言蜚语，但是我很享受。”
“Pardon me, Mr. Bally,” says I. “不好意思，巴利先生，”我说道，
“We do not in the least fear a scandal against you.” “我们可一点儿都不担心您的那些流言蜚语。”
He laughed again. 他又笑了起来。
“You have been studying repartee,” he said. “你现在可真是一直在学习妙语如珠的应变能力呀，”他说道，
“But speech is very easy, and sometimes very deceptive. “不过说话是挺容易的，而且有时候还非常具有欺骗性。
I warn you fairly: you will find me vitriol in the house. 我明明白白地警告你：你会看到我把这个家弄得鸡飞狗跳的。
You would do wiser to pay money down and see my back.” 你最好还是明智地把钱给我，让我离开这里。”
And with that he waved his hand to me and left the room. 说完，他挥了挥手，走出了房间。
A little after, my lord came with the lawyer, Mr. Carlyle; a bottle of old wine was brought, and we all had a glass before we fell to business. 过了一会儿，爵爷和律师卡莱尔先生一起进来了，还带着一瓶陈年老酒，我们先喝了一杯，然后就切入了正题。
The necessary deeds were then prepared and executed, and the Scotch estates made over in trust to Mr. Carlyle and myself. 我们把必要的契约书都准备好了，签了字，把苏格兰的房产转让给我和卡莱尔先生托管。
“There is one point, Mr. Carlyle,” said my lord, when these affairs had been adjusted, “on which I wish that you would do us justice. “卡莱尔先生，有一件事，”这些事情都处理完，爵爷说道，“我希望你能公正地对待我们。
This sudden departure coinciding with my brother’s return will be certainly commented on. 我的突然离开和我哥哥的回来撞到一起了，这肯定会招来流言蜚语。
I wish you would discourage any conjunction of the two.” 我希望你到时侯把这两件事区分开来。”
“I will make a point of it, my lord,” said Mr. Carlyle. “我会作出解释的，爵爷，”卡莱尔先生说道，
“The Mas-Bally does not, then, accompany you?” “大少——我是说巴利先生不会跟您一起离开吗？”
“It is a point I must approach,” said my lord. “这是我必须说清楚的一个问题，”爵爷说道，
“Mr. Bally remains at Durrisdeer, under the care of Mr. Mackellar; and I do not mean that he shall even know our destination.” “巴利先生会留在达里斯迪尔，由麦凯勒先生照顾。我的意思是，不要告诉他我们的去向。”
“Common report, however—” began the lawyer. “但是，纸是包不住火的——”律师说道。
“Ah! but, Mr. Carlyle, this is to be a secret quite among ourselves,” interrupted my lord. “啊！可是卡莱尔先生，这件事是我们三个人之间的秘密，”爵爷打断了他的话，
“None but you and Mackellar are to be made acquainted with my movements.” “除了你和麦凯勒，没有人会知道我的行踪。”
“And Mr. Bally stays here? “那巴利先生呆在这儿？
Quite so,” said Mr. Carlyle. 是这样的，”卡莱尔先生说道，
“The powers you leave—” “那您转交给我们的权力——”
Then he broke off again. 他突然停止说话，
“Mr. Mackellar, we have a rather heavy weight upon us.” “麦凯勒先生，那我们责任重大呀。”
“No doubt,” said I. “那是毫无疑问的。”我说道。
“No doubt,” said he. “想必，”他说道，
“Mr. Bally will have no voice?” “巴利先生没有发言权吧？”
“He will have no voice,” said my lord; “and, I hope, no influence. “他没有发言权，”爵爷说，“而且，我希望，你们不要受他影响。
Mr. Bally is not a good adviser.” 巴利先生提不出什么好建议。”
“I see,” said the lawyer. “我明白了，”律师说道，
“By the way, has Mr. Bally means?” “顺便问一下，巴利先生有什么打算吗？”
“I understand him to have nothing,” replied my lord. “据我所知，没有，”爵爷回答道，
“I give him table, fire, and candle in this house.” “我会把房子里的桌子、壁炉和蜡烛给他。”
“And in the matter of an allowance? “他的生活费呢？
If I am to share the responsibility, you will see how highly desirable it is that I should understand your views,” said the lawyer. 如果我要承担这个责任的话，那我就要完全理解您的想法，”律师说道，
“On the question of an allowance?” “他的生活费怎么弄？”
“There will be no allowance,” said my lord. “他没有生活费，”爵爷说道，
“I wish Mr. Bally to live very private. “我希望巴利先生过着默默无闻的生活。
We have not always been gratified with his behaviour.” 他的行为总是令我们不满意。”
“And in the matter of money,” I added, “he has shown himself an infamous bad husband. “在钱的问题上，”我补充道，“他可不是什么省钱的主儿。
Glance your eye upon that docket, Mr. Carlyle, where I have brought together the different sums the man has drawn from the estate in the last fifteen or twenty years. 卡莱尔先生，你看一下那份文件，这个男人在过去的15至20年间从房产中榨取的多项金额。
The total is pretty.” 总数不小呀。”
Mr. Carlyle made the motion of whistling. 卡莱尔先生做了个吹口哨的动作。
“I had no guess of this,” said he. “我可没料到这个情况，”他说道，
“Excuse me once more, my lord, if I appear to push you; but it is really desirable I should penetrate your intentions. “爵爷，如果我刚刚说话冒犯了您，请您谅解。但是，我还是要清楚地明白您的意思。
Mr. Mackellar might die, when I should find myself alone upon this trust. 麦凯勒先生可能会去世，到时候就是我一个人托管您的财产。
Would it not be rather your lordship’s preference that Mr. Bally should—ahem—should leave the country?” 阁下难道不希望巴利先生——呃哼——离开这个地方吗？”
My lord looked at Mr. Carlyle. 爵爷看着卡莱尔先生。
“Why do you ask that?” said he. “你为什么这么问呢？”他说道。
“I gather, my lord, that Mr. Bally is not a comfort to his family,” says the lawyer with a smile. “爵爷，我想着，巴利先生对于他的家人来说可不是个省油的灯。”律师笑着说道。
My lord’s face became suddenly knotted. 爵爷的脸突然扭曲起来。
“I wish he was in hell!” cried he, and filled himself a glass of wine, but with a hand so tottering that he spilled the half into his bosom. “但愿他去下地狱！”他大声喊道，接着给自己倒了一杯酒，一只手不断地颤抖，以至于撒了一半在胸前。
This was the second time that, in the midst of the most regular and wise behaviour, his animosity had spirted out. 这是他第二次在行为正常理智的情况下，心中的怨恨突然爆发出来。
It startled Mr. Carlyle, who observed my lord thenceforth with covert curiosity; and to me it restored the certainty that we were acting for the best in view of my lord’s health and reason. 一直在怀着好奇心偷偷观察爵爷的卡莱尔先生被吓了一跳，而我也更加确信我们这么做是为了爵爷的身心健康着想。
Except for this explosion the interview was very successfully conducted. 除了这突然的发作，谈话进行得很顺利。
No doubt Mr. Carlyle would talk, as lawyers do, little by little. 毫无疑问，卡莱尔先生说起话来有着律师的职业特点，有条不紊。
We could thus feel we had laid the foundations of a better feeling in the country, and the man’s own misconduct would certainly complete what we had begun. 这样，我们觉得给家乡留下的印象还不错，而这个男人自己的不检点行为肯定会完善我们已经开始的计划。
Indeed, before his departure, the lawyer showed us there had already gone abroad some glimmerings of the truth. 事实上，在他离开之前，律师告诉我们外面已经在传一些消息了。
“I should perhaps explain to you, my lord,” said he, pausing, with his hat in his hand, “that I have not been altogether surprised with your lordship’s dispositions in the case of Mr. Bally. “爵爷，或许我应该跟您解释一下，”他停顿了一下，手里拿着他的帽子，继续说道，“总之，我对于阁下您对巴利先生的处理方式并不感到十分惊讶。
Something of this nature oozed out when he was last in Durrisdeer. 上次他在达里斯迪尔的时候，有些事情就显露出来了。
There was some talk of a woman at St. Bride’s, to whom you had behaved extremely handsome, and Mr. Bally with no small degree of cruelty. 有传言说，您对圣布赖德的一个女人出手非常大方，而对巴利先生也没有一丝的不好。
There was the entail, again, which was much controverted. 现在还有争议的就是限定继承权。
In short, there was no want of talk, back and forward; and some of our wise-acres took up a strong opinion. 简单地说，外面有各种各样的传言，某些自作聪明的人态度还十分强硬。
I remained in suspense, as became one of my cloth; but Mr. Mackellar’s docket here has finally opened my eyes. 鉴于我的职业，我迟迟没有下判断；但是麦凯勒先生这里的文件终于让我看清了一切。
I do not think, Mr. Mackellar, that you and I will give him that much rope.” 麦凯勒先生，我觉得你和我都不会给他一丝希望的。”
The rest of that important day passed prosperously through. 那个重要的日子就这么顺利地过去了。
It was our policy to keep the enemy in view, and I took my turn to be his watchman with the rest. 我们的策略就是盯住我们的敌人，我和其他人轮流监视他。
I think his spirits rose as he perceived us to be so attentive, and I know that mine insensibly declined. 我觉得，当他意识到我们如此注意他的时候，他的情绪就高涨起来，而我的情绪却慢慢低落了。
What chiefly daunted me was the man’s singular dexterity to worm himself into our troubles. 让我胆怯的主要原因就是,这个人极其狡诈，能神不知鬼不觉地参与我们的事务。
You may have felt (after a horse accident) the hand of a bone-setter artfully divide and interrogate the muscles, and settle strongly on the injured place? （那次骑马事故之后）你可能感觉到了跌打医生的手是多么灵巧，可以摸索着区分不同的肌肉，然后用力把断骨接上！
It was so with the Master’s tongue, that was so cunning to question; and his eyes, that were so quick to observe. 大少爷的巧舌就是如此，可以巧妙地盘问；眼睛也是如此，可以敏捷地观察。
I seemed to have said nothing, and yet to have let all out. 我好像什么都没说，却让所有的消息都泄露了。
Before I knew where I was the man was condoling with me on my lord’s neglect of my lady and myself, and his hurtful indulgence to his son. 我还没明白是怎么回事，他就安慰我说爵爷整天就忽视我和太太，还纵容自己的儿子。
On this last point I perceived him (with panic fear) to return repeatedly. 在这个事情上，他一直不停地说，说得我都有点儿恐慌了。
The boy had displayed a certain shrinking from his uncle; it was strong in my mind his father had been fool enough to indoctrinate the same, which was no wise beginning: and when I looked upon the man before me, still so handsome, so apt a speaker, with so great a variety of fortunes to relate, I saw he was the very personage to captivate a boyish fancy. 这个男孩在他的伯伯面前总是畏畏缩缩的，我强烈地认为他的爸爸向一个还未懂事的孩子灌输同样的思想真是太愚蠢了。我看着眼前的大少爷，还是那么英俊潇洒，谈吐依然那么自如，又有那么多稀奇古怪的故事可以说，我想他一定能迷住那些想象力丰富的孩子们。
John Paul had left only that morning; it was not to be supposed he had been altogether dumb upon his favourite subject: so that here would be Mr. Alexander in the part of Dido, with a curiosity inflamed to hear; and there would be the Master, like a diabolical AEneas, full of matter the most pleasing in the world to any youthful ear, such as battles, sea-disasters, flights, the forests of the West, and (since his later voyage) the ancient cities of the Indies. 就在那天早上，约翰·保罗离开了，而他是不会对自己喜欢的话题缄默不语的。所以一方面，亚历山大就像迦太基女王狄多一样充满了好奇心；另外一方面，大少爷就像那个穷凶极恶的埃涅阿斯，有可以讲给年轻人听的世界上最有趣的故事，例如战争、海上灾难、大逃亡、西方森林以及（后来航行中的）印度古城。
How cunningly these baits might be employed, and what an empire might be so founded, little by little, in the mind of any boy, stood obviously clear to me. 我心里非常清楚，这些诱惑会怎样巧妙地被运用，并在任何一个男孩的心中一步步地建立起一个帝国。
There was no inhibition, so long as the man was in the house, that would be strong enough to hold these two apart; for if it be hard to charm serpents, it is no very difficult thing to cast a glamour on a little chip of manhood not very long in breeches. 只要这个人还呆在这个房子里，男孩就没法抵住他的诱惑。因为如果施魔法迷住狡猾的蛇比较困难的话，那要迷住一个刚穿起马裤不久、还没有什么男子汉气概的男孩就不是什么难事了。
I recalled an ancient sailor-man who dwelt in a lone house beyond the Figgate Whins (I believe, he called it after Portobello), and how the boys would troop out of Leith on a Saturday, and sit and listen to his swearing tales, as thick as crows about a carrion: a thing I often remarked as I went by, a young student, on my own more meditative holiday diversion. 我想起一个年老的水手，他住在费盖特岩石（我想他是根据波托贝洛给这个地方命名的）后面一栋孤零零的房子里。周六的时候，男孩们成群结队地走出利斯区，就像见到腐肉的乌鸦一样，聚集在水手旁听他讲故事。那时候我是个年轻学生，喜欢节假日独自出门冥想、消遣时光，每次经过那里的时候，都会看到这番景象。
Many of these boys went, no doubt, in the face of an express command; many feared and even hated the old brute of whom they made their hero; and I have seen them flee from him when he was tipsy, and stone him when he was drunk. 当然，许多孩子都听从他的命令，也有许多男孩把他当作英雄，但还是会害怕甚至憎恨这个老家伙。我看到他们会在水手东倒西歪的时候赶紧逃跑，在他酩酊大醉的时候朝他丢石子。
And yet there they came each Saturday! 但是，他们每个周六还是会来！
How much more easily would a boy like Mr. Alexander fall under the influence of a high-looking, high-spoken gentleman-adventurer, who should conceive the fancy to entrap him; and, the influence gained, how easy to employ it for the child’s perversion! 像亚历山大这样一个男孩，被一个风度翩翩、言谈高雅的绅士兼冒险家所吸引是再容易不过了。更何况大少爷还处心积虑地想引他落入陷阱，一旦成功了，要扭曲这个小孩的认识就易如反掌了！
I doubt if our enemy had named Mr. Alexander three times before I perceived which way his mind was aiming—all this train of thought and memory passed in one pulsation through my own—and you may say I started back as though an open hole had gaped across a pathway. 我们的敌人见过亚历山大三次之后，我就意识到大少爷心有所图了。当所有这些想法和记忆都浮现在我脑海中时，我不禁退了一步，就好像前方路上突然冒出一个大洞。
Mr. Alexander: there was the weak point, there was the Eve in our perishable paradise; and the serpent was already hissing on the trail. 亚历山大先生也有弱点，就像腐败堕落的伊甸园里的夏娃，毒蛇已经蠢蠢欲动了。
I promise you, I went the more heartily about the preparations; my last scruple gone, the danger of delay written before me in huge characters. 说真的，我非常积极地做着准备工作；我最后的一丝犹豫也消失了，实在是不能耽搁了，危险这两个大字赫然写在我面前。
From that moment forth I seem not to have sat down or breathed. 那个时刻起，我似乎就像没有坐下过，也没有呼吸过一般。
Now I would be at my post with the Master and his Indian; now in the garret, buckling a valise; now sending forth Macconochie by the side postern and the wood-path to bear it to the trysting-place; and, again, snatching some words of counsel with my lady. 现在，我一会儿要和大少爷和他的印度朋友呆在一起，一会儿又到阁楼上收拾行李箱，一会儿又派麦康纳基从侧门走丛林小路，把行李箱扛去会面的地点，一会儿又与太太说上几句话，跟她商量一下。
This was the VERSO of our life in Durrisdeer that day; but on the RECTO all appeared quite settled, as of a family at home in its paternal seat; and what perturbation may have been observable, the Master would set down to the blow of his unlooked-for coming, and the fear he was accustomed to inspire. 那天在达里斯迪尔府邸，我们背地里就是这么干的，而表面上大家都表现得很平静。在一个父权至上的家庭里，大少爷会将家里任何可以看到的混乱和不安归结于他自己突如其来的回家以及大家对他的恐惧。
Supper went creditably off, cold salutations passed and the company trooped to their respective chambers. 晚餐正常地结束了，大家冷冷地打了个招呼，就各自回房间了。
I attended the Master to the last. 我一直跟着大少爷。
We had put him next door to his Indian, in the north wing; because that was the most distant and could be severed from the body of the house with doors. 我们把他的房间安排在印度人的隔壁，在北侧，因为那里离正方正厅最远，门一关就完全隔开了。
I saw he was a kind friend or a good master (whichever it was) to his Secundra Dass—seeing to his comfort; mending the fire with his own hand, for the Indian complained of cold; inquiring as to the rice on which the stranger made his diet; talking with him pleasantly in the Hindustanee, while I stood by, my candle in my hand, and affected to be overcome with slumber. 我看出来，对于他的印度伙伴塞孔拉德·戴斯来说，他是一个友善的朋友或者一个好主人（不管是什么吧）——比如关心他呆得是否舒适；印度伙伴抱怨太冷的时候，亲自给他添炉火；印度人想吃米饭的时候就问我们有没有大米；跟他用印度语愉快地聊着天，而我就站在旁边，手里端着蜡烛，假装很瞌睡的样子。
At length the Master observed my signals of distress. 大少爷终于意识到我的痛苦了。
“I perceive,” says he, “that you have all your ancient habits: early to bed and early to rise. “我想，”他说，“你的老毛病一点儿没变：睡得早起得也早。
Yawn yourself away!” 去睡你的觉吧！”
Once in my own room, I made the customary motions of undressing, so that I might time myself; and when the cycle was complete, set my tinder-box ready, and blew out my taper. 我一回到房间，就像往常一样脱掉衣服，这样我可以把握好时间。事情整理好后，我准备好火绒匣，然后吹灭蜡烛。
The matter of an hour afterward I made a light again, put on my shoes of list that I had worn by my lord’s sick-bed, and set forth into the house to call the voyagers. 大约一个小时后，我又点亮蜡烛，换上当年在爵爷病床前穿过的那双鞋，然后来到正房叫他们要远航的人。
All were dressed and waiting—my lord, my lady, Miss Katharine, Mr. Alexander, my lady’s woman Christie; and I observed the effect of secrecy even upon quite innocent persons, that one after another showed in the chink of the door a face as white as paper. 所有的人都穿戴完毕，在那里等着——爵爷、太太、凯瑟琳小姐、亚历山大先生和太太的女仆克里斯蒂。透过门缝，我注意到那两个还不懂事的小孩脸色苍白、满脸神秘的样子。
We slipped out of the side postern into a night of darkness, scarce broken by a star or two; so that at first we groped and stumbled and fell among the bushes. 我们悄悄从侧门溜出去，外面夜色正浓，依稀看到一两颗星星。开始的时候我们只能在灌木丛中摸索着蹒跚前行，一不小心就可能会摔倒。
A few hundred yards up the wood-path Macconochie was waiting us with a great lantern; so the rest of the way we went easy enough, but still in a kind of guilty silence. 在丛林小路中走了几百码后，麦康纳基打着大灯笼在等着我们，所以接下来的路走得很轻松，只不过大家都保持着略带愧疚的沉默。
A little beyond the abbey the path debauched on the main road and some quarter of a mile farther, at the place called Eagles, where the moors begin, we saw the lights of the two carriages stand shining by the wayside. 过了教堂不远，小路就变成了大路，再往前走大约四分之一英里就到了一个叫伊格尔斯的地方，这里是沼泽地的边缘地带。我们看到两辆马车停在路旁，灯火通明。
Scarce a word or two was uttered at our parting, and these regarded business: a silent grasping of hands, a turning of faces aside, and the thing was over; the horses broke into a trot, the lamplight sped like Will- o’-the-Wisp upon the broken moorland, it dipped beyond Stony Brae; and there were Macconochie and I alone with our lantern on the road. 分别的时候我们都没说上几句话，只是无声地握了一下手，然后把脸转向旁边，就算告别了。拉车的马开始小跑起来，灯光像沼泽地上的鬼火忽明忽暗，消失在布雷石堆；只剩下麦康纳基和我打着灯笼站在路上。
There was one thing more to wait for, and that was the reappearance of the coach upon Cartmore. 我们还在等待一件事情，那就是等着马车重新出现在卡特莫上面。
It seems they must have pulled up upon the summit, looked back for a last time, and seen our lantern not yet moved away from the place of separation. 他们似乎在山顶上停了一会儿，回头看了最后一眼，见我们的灯笼还呆在刚刚离别的地方。
For a lamp was taken from a carriage, and waved three times up and down by way of a farewell. 一只灯笼从马车上被拿下来，来回动了三次，是在跟我们说再见。
And then they were gone indeed, having looked their last on the kind roof of Durrisdeer, their faces toward a barbarous country. 然后他们看了达里斯迪尔府邸的屋顶最后一眼，朝着一个野蛮的国度驶去。
I never knew before, the greatness of that vault of night in which we two poor serving-men—the one old, and the one elderly—stood for the first time deserted; I had never felt before my own dependency upon the countenance of others. 以前我都不知道，夜晚的苍穹是如此空旷辽阔。我们两个可怜的仆人站在那里——一个比一个老——我以前从未觉得如此孤单失落。
The sense of isolation burned in my bowels like a fire. 内心的孤独之感像火一样煎熬着我。
It seemed that we who remained at home were the true exiles, and that Durrisdeer and Solwayside, and all that made my country native, its air good to me, and its language welcome, had gone forth and was far over the sea with my old masters. 仿佛我们俩才是真正流落他乡的人，仿佛达里斯迪尔府邸和索尔韦海滨，所有这些属于我的家乡的东西、沁人心脾的空气以及悦耳的方言都随着爵爷漂洋过海，走远了。
The remainder of that night I paced to and fro on the smooth highway, reflecting on the future and the past. 那天晚上我一直在平坦的马路上来回踱步，思前想后。
My thoughts, which at first dwelled tenderly on those who were just gone, took a more manly temper as I considered what remained for me to do. 先先想到的是刚刚离开的爵爷一家，我有点儿伤感；然后一想到接下来要做的事情，我又多了点儿男子气概。
Day came upon the inland mountain-tops, and the fowls began to cry, and the smoke of homesteads to arise in the brown bosom of the moors, before I turned my face homeward, and went down the path to where the roof of Durrisdeer shone in the morning by the sea. 清晨的阳光从远处山顶上倾泻下来，鸟儿们开始歌唱，笼罩着沼泽地的褐色雾霭中升起了袅袅炊烟。我转过身，顺着小路朝着回家的方向走去。远处晨光笼罩着濒临海边的达里斯迪尔府邸的屋顶。
At the customary hour I had the Master called, and awaited his coming in the hall with a quiet mind. 我像往常一样叫醒大少爷，然后心态平和地等着他来大厅吃早餐。
He looked about him at the empty room and the three covers set. 他看了看空荡荡的房间和三套餐具。
“We are a small party,” said he. “就我们几个？”他说，
“How comes?” “怎么会这样？”
“This is the party to which we must grow accustomed,” I replied. “就我们几个，我们必须慢慢适应。”我回答道。
He looked at me with a sudden sharpness. 他突然用犀利的眼神看着我。
“What is all this?” said he. “这到底怎么回事？”他问道。
“You and I and your friend Mr. Dass are now all the company,” I replied. “现在只有您、我，还有戴斯先生一起做伴了，”我回答道，
“My lord, my lady, and the children, are gone upon a voyage.” “爵爷、太太，还有孩子们都旅行去了。”
“Upon my word!” said he. “哎呀，真没想到！”他说道，
“Can this be possible? “这怎么可能呢？
I have indeed fluttered your Volscians in Corioli! 那我不是反客为主了啊！
But this is no reason why our breakfast should go cold. 不过，不要让我们的早餐凉了。
Sit down, Mr. Mackellar, if you please”—taking, as he spoke, the head of the table, which I had designed to occupy myself—“and as we eat, you can give me the details of this evasion.” 赶紧坐下吧，麦凯勒先生，”说着，他在我本想给自己安排的首位坐了下来，“我们一边吃，你一边给我说说具体的情况吧。”
I could see he was more affected than his language carried, and I determined to equal him in coolness. 我可以看到他表现得比他说的话更加虚情假意，于是我决定以同样的冷淡来回应他。
“I was about to ask you to take the head of the table,” said I; “for though I am now thrust into the position of your host, I could never forget that you were, after all, a member of the family.” “我正要请您坐上席呢，”，我说道，“因为现在我虽然被推到主人这个位置，但我永远都不会忘记你也曾经是这个家庭的一员。”
For a while he played the part of entertainer, giving directions to Macconochie, who received them with an evil grace, and attending specially upon Secundra. 过了一会儿，他就扮演起主人的角色，对麦康诺基指手画脚，而麦康诺基非常不乐意地遵循他的命令照料塞孔拉德。
“And where has my good family withdrawn to?” he asked carelessly. “那么，我的善良的家人都去哪了？”大少爷漫不经心地问道。
“Ah! “啊！
Mr. Bally, that is another point,” said I. 巴利先生，那是另外一件事，”我答道，
“I have no orders to communicate their destination.” “我不能透露他们的目的地。”
“To me,” he corrected. “不能透露给我。”他纠正道。
“To any one,” said I. “谁都不能说。”我说道。
“It is the less pointed,” said the master; “C’EST DE BON TON: my brother improves as he continues. “这还差不多，”大少爷说道，“好极了！要是我的弟弟一直这样躲下去，那他可是会越过越好呀。
And I, dear Mr. Mackellar?” 那我呢？亲爱的麦凯勒先生。”
“You will have bed and board, Mr. Bally,” said I. “巴利先生，您会有的吃，有的睡，”我说，
“I am permitted to give you the run of the cellar, which is pretty reasonably stocked. “爵爷让我将地窖交给您掌管，那里物资充沛。
You have only to keep well with me, which is no very difficult matter, and you shall want neither for wine nor a saddle-horse.” 您只需要与我保持好关系，这也不是什么难事，您就可以有酒喝，有马骑。”
He made an excuse to send Macconochie from the room. 他找了个借口让麦康诺基离开屋子。
“And for money?” he inquired. “那钱呢？”他问道，
“Have I to keep well with my good friend Mackellar for my pocket-money also? “难道为了我的零花钱，我也要跟你搞好关系吗？
This is a pleasing return to the principles of boyhood.” 这就像回到了年少的时候。”
“There was no allowance made,” said I; “but I will take it on myself to see you are supplied in moderation.” “没有给您准备生活费，”我说，“但是我会酌情处理，保证您有适量的钱。”
“In moderation?” he repeated. “适量？”他重复道，
“And you will take it on yourself?” “你会酌情处理？”
He drew himself up, and looked about the hall at the dark rows of portraits. 他站起来，看着大厅周围黑暗中一排排家族先人的肖像。
“In the name of my ancestors, I thank you,” says he; and then, with a return to irony, “But there must certainly be an allowance for Secundra Dass?” he said. “我以列祖列宗的名义感谢你，”他说，然后又带着讽刺的口吻说道，“但是，塞孔拉德·戴斯也必须要有生活费。
“It in not possible they have omitted that?” 他们该不会把这个给忘了吧？”
“I will make a note of it, and ask instructions when I write,” said I. “我会记下这件事的，写信的时候跟他们请示一下。”我说道。
And he, with a sudden change of manner, and leaning forward with an elbow on the table—“Do you think this entirely wise?” 然后，他突然神色一变，把手肘撑在桌上，身体朝前倾：“你觉得这样做是完全明智的吗？”
“I execute my orders, Mr. Bally,” said I. “巴利先生，我只是在执行命令。”我说。
“Profoundly modest,” said the Master; “perhaps not equally ingenuous. “太谦虚了，”大少爷说，“只是还不够诚实。
You told me yesterday my power was fallen with my father’s death. 你昨天告诉我，我的权力随着父亲的去世衰落下来了。
How comes it, then, that a peer of the realm flees under cloud of night out of a house in which his fathers have stood several sieges? that he conceals his address, which must be a matter of concern to his Gracious Majesty and to the whole republic? and that he should leave me in possession, and under the paternal charge of his invaluable Mackellar? 那么，作为一家之主的弟弟怎么会在一夜之间逃离这个几代人苦心经营的家？而且还要隐瞒自己的去处，莫非是关系到国王，甚至整个国家的大事？还把我交给你这个位高权重的麦凯勒，像父亲一般管着我。
This smacks to me of a very considerable and genuine apprehension.” 对我来说，这似乎是一件让人非常忧虑的事。”
I sought to interrupt him with some not very truthful denegation; but he waved me down, and pursued his speech. 我本想打断他，违心地否认他所说的事实。但是他挥手示意我停下，然后继续他的演说。
“I say, it smacks of it,” he said; “but I will go beyond that, for I think the apprehension grounded. “我刚刚只说似乎，”他说，“其实事情远不止那样，我想担忧是有原因的。
I came to this house with some reluctancy. 我犹豫了好久才决定回到这里。
In view of the manner of my last departure, nothing but necessity could have induced me to return. 想到上一次的离家出走，这次我回来也是不得已。
Money, however, is that which I must have. 不过，钱，我是要定了。
You will not give with a good grace; well, I have the power to force it from you. 你不情愿给的话，那我有权力强迫你拿出来。
Inside of a week, without leaving Durrisdeer, I will find out where these fools are fled to. 一周之内，不用离开达里斯迪尔，我就会查出来这些蠢人都逃到哪里去了。
I will follow; and when I have run my quarry down, I will drive a wedge into that family that shall once more burst it into shivers. 我会跟踪他们，等我一找到他们，我就挑拨一下，这个家就会再一次分崩离析。
I shall see then whether my Lord Durrisdeer” (said with indescribable scorn and rage) “will choose to buy my absence; and you will all see whether, by that time, I decide for profit or revenge.” 我要看看那个时候达里斯迪尔爵爷（说到这时，带着轻蔑和愤怒）还会不会让我拿钱走人。你也会看看到那个时候我对你是奖励还是报复。”
I was amazed to hear the man so open. 这个人如此坦白，这让我很惊讶。
The truth is, he was consumed with anger at my lord’s successful flight, felt himself to figure as a dupe, and was in no humour to weigh language. 事实上，爵爷的成功出逃令他非常愤怒，他觉得自己被愚弄了，没有心情去考虑自己怎么说话了。
“Do you consider THIS entirely wise?” said I, copying his words. 我照着他的话，说道：“您真觉得这样做是明智的？”
“These twenty years I have lived by my poor wisdom,” he answered with a smile that seemed almost foolish in its vanity. “这20年来我就是靠着自己那一点点聪明才智活过来的。”他带着一丝自负又虚荣的笑容回答道。
“And come out a beggar in the end,” said I, “if beggar be a strong enough word for it.” “最后却成了一个乞丐，”我说，“好像连乞丐都不如。”
“I would have you to observe, Mr. Mackellar,” cried he, with a sudden imperious heat, in which I could not but admire him, “that I am scrupulously civil: copy me in that, and we shall be the better friends.” “我还想要你好好看看，麦凯勒先生，”他突然用一副蛮横的态度吼道，我不得不赞叹一下，“我是一个多么文明有教养的人：好好跟我学习一下，我们会成为好朋友的。”
Throughout this dialogue I had been incommoded by the observation of Secundra Dass. 在这个对话过程中，我被塞孔拉德·戴斯盯得全身不舒服。
Not one of us, since the first word, had made a feint of eating: our eyes were in each other’s faces—you might say, in each other’s bosoms; and those of the Indian troubled me with a certain changing brightness, as of comprehension. 从第一句话开始，我们都没有动筷子的迹象，只是盯着各自的脸——你可能会说，是盯着彼此的内心。而印度人好像听懂了一样，眼神忽闪忽闪的，这让我觉得烦心。
But I brushed the fancy aside, telling myself once more he understood no English; only, from the gravity of both voices, and the occasional scorn and anger in the Master’s, smelled out there was something of import in the wind. 但是我先把自己的胡思乱想放到一边，再次告诉自己他不懂英语，只是从我们两人严肃的声音以及大少爷偶尔轻蔑的语气和愤怒中嗅出了不寻常的信息。
For the matter of three weeks we continued to live together in the house of Durrisdeer: the beginning of that most singular chapter of my life—what I must call my intimacy with the Master. 接下来的三周里，我们继续同住在达里斯迪尔府邸：我的一生中最非凡的一章开始了——必须说的是，这是我与大少爷交往甚密的一个时期。
At first he was somewhat changeable in his behaviour: now civil, now returning to his old manner of flouting me to my face; and in both I met him half-way. 首先他的行为举止有点儿变幻莫测：时而彬彬有礼，时而故态复萌对我愚弄嘲笑一番，不管他的态度如何，我都态度温和。
Thanks be to Providence, I had now no measure to keep with the man; and I was never afraid of black brows, only of naked swords. 真是谢天谢地，我现在不需要与他保持距离了，我也不用害怕他的严肃的面容，只不过还真害怕他拿剑指着我。
So that I found a certain entertainment in these bouts of incivility, and was not always ill-inspired in my rejoinders. 于是，我在他粗鲁的言行中寻找到一些乐趣，有时候也能找到机会反击一下。
At last (it was at supper) I had a droll expression that entirely vanquished him. 最终（晚餐的时候），我的一个滑稽的表情彻底击败了他。
He laughed again and again; and “Who would have guessed,” he cried, “that this old wife had any wit under his petticoats?” 他一次又一次笑个不停。“谁会想到，”他大叫道，“这个唠叨的家伙还挺风趣的呢？”
“It is no wit, Mr. Bally,” said I: “a dry Scot’s humour, and something of the driest.” “这不是风趣，巴利先生，”我说，“这只是一个苏格兰人无聊的打趣，而且是最无聊的打趣。”
And, indeed, I never had the least pretension to be thought a wit. 的确，我从未想过自己是一个风趣的人。
From that hour he was never rude with me, but all passed between us in a manner of pleasantry. 从那以后，他不再对我粗鲁无礼了，我们之间的交往也更加愉快了。
One of our chief times of daffing[3] was when he required a horse, another bottle, or some money. 我们之间最搞笑的[3]就是他跟我要马匹、酒，或者钱的时候。
He would approach me then after the manner of a schoolboy, and I would carry it on by way of being his father: on both sides, with an infinity of mirth. 他就像小孩一般，而我就像他的爸爸一样：两个人都是很开心。
I could not but perceive that he thought more of me, which tickled that poor part of mankind, the vanity. 我只是发现他愈发地重视我，这让我的虚荣心——人类的弱点——得到一些满足。
He dropped, besides (I must suppose unconsciously), into a manner that was not only familiar, but even friendly; and this, on the part of one who had so long detested me, I found the more insidious. 此外，他和我慢慢熟稔起来，（我想应该是无意识的）甚至成为了好朋友。另外一方面，对于一个憎恨了我这么长时间的人，我越发觉得其中肯定有阴谋。
He went little abroad; sometimes even refusing invitations. 他很少出门，有时候甚至拒绝别人的邀请。
“No,” he would say, “what do I care for these thick-headed bonnet-lairds? “我不去，”他会说，“我可没把那些愚蠢的地主放在眼里。
