I will stay at home, Mackellar; and we shall share a bottle quietly, and have one of our good talks.” 麦凯勒，我就呆在家里，我们可以安安静静地喝酒，惬意地聊天。”
And, indeed, meal-time at Durrisdeer must have been a delight to any one, by reason of the brilliancy of the discourse. 的确，达里斯迪尔府邸的用餐对任何人来说都是一件愉快的事，大家谈得很投机。
He would often express wonder at his former indifference to my society. 他就以前对我的冷淡的态度常常表示惊诧。
“But, you see,” he would add, “we were upon opposite sides. “不过，你看，”他会继续说道，“以前我们视对方为敌人。
And so we are to-day; but let us never speak of that. 现在仍然是这样；我们还是不要说那个了。
I would think much less of you if you were not staunch to your employer.” 如果你不那么忠实地对你的主人，我还瞧不上你呢。”
You are to consider he seemed to me quite impotent for any evil; and how it is a most engaging form of flattery when (after many years) tardy justice is done to a man’s character and parts. 你会发现他似乎没法对着我胡作非为了。一个人的性格和才华终于在多年之后经历了正义的洗礼，这真令我感到欣慰。
But I have no thought to excuse myself. 但是我并不想为自己开脱。
I was to blame; I let him cajole me, and, in short, I think the watch-dog was going sound asleep, when he was suddenly aroused. 我是有责任的，我让他百般哄骗我。简而言之，我认为他就是一条熟睡的看门狗，突然醒了过来。
I should say the Indian was continually travelling to and fro in the house. 我想说，那个印度人一直在房间里走来走去。
He never spoke, save in his own dialect and with the Master; walked without sound; and was always turning up where you would least expect him, fallen into a deep abstraction, from which he would start (upon your coming) to mock you with one of his grovelling obeisances. 他从不说话，除了用方言跟大少爷交谈的时候。他走路无声，总是意外地冒出来，一副心不在焉的样子。等你发现他，他就会卑躬屈膝地鞠躬，好似在讥讽你。
He seemed so quiet, so frail, and so wrapped in his own fancies, that I came to pass him over without much regard, or even to pity him for a harmless exile from his country. 他看着如此安静、脆弱、始终沉浸在自己的遐想中，我每次经过他的时候，都不太注意他，更不用说为他无缘无故背井离乡感到可怜了。
And yet without doubt the creature was still eavesdropping; and without doubt it was through his stealth and my security that our secret reached the Master. 然而，毫无疑问，这个人总是偷听我们讲话。肯定是他偷偷摸摸的行动以及我的疏忽大意才让大少爷知道了我们的秘密。
It was one very wild night, after supper, and when we had been making more than usually merry, that the blow fell on me. 那是一个风雨交加的夜晚，晚饭后，我们玩得比平常都要尽兴，就在这时候，大少爷给了我当头一棒。
“This is all very fine,” says the Master, “but we should do better to be buckling our valise.” “一切都很好，”大少爷说，“不过我们得去收拾行李了。”
“Why so?” “为什么？”
I cried. 我问道，
“Are you leaving?” “您要走了吗？”
“We are all leaving to-morrow in the morning,” said he. “我们明天早上都要走。”他说，
“For the port of Glascow first, thence for the province of New York.” 先去格拉斯哥港口，然后去纽约。”
I suppose I must have groaned aloud. 我想我肯定大声哼哼了一句。
“Yes,” he continued, “I boasted; I said a week, and it has taken me near twenty days. “没错，”他继续道，“当时我宣称说只要一周，实际上却花了将近20天。
But never mind; I shall make it up; I will go the faster.” 但是没关系，我可以赶上去，我会快点儿赶路。”
“Have you the money for this voyage?” “您有钱出远门吗？”
I asked. 我问道。
“Dear and ingenuous personage, I have,” said he. “亲爱的坦诚又老实的先生，我有钱，”他说，
“Blame me, if you choose, for my duplicity; but while I have been wringing shillings from my daddy, I had a stock of my own put by against a rainy day. “你尽可以骂我言行不一。不过我一直在榨取父亲的钱的时候，也为自己存了点儿，未雨绸缪呢。
You will pay for your own passage, if you choose to accompany us on our flank march; I have enough for Secundra and myself, but not more—enough to be dangerous, not enough to be generous. 如果你想加入我们的队伍，就得自己掏钱了。我的钱只够我自己和塞孔拉德的路费——应付危险足够，但是要对你慷慨可不够。
There is, however, an outside seat upon the chaise which I will let you have upon a moderate commutation; so that the whole menagerie can go together—the house-dog, the monkey, and the tiger.” 不过我那辆马车外面有个座位，可以便宜点儿让你坐。这样整个鱼龙混杂的队伍——看门狗、猴子，还有老虎——就能一起走了。”
“I go with you,” said I. “我跟你们一起走。”我说道。
“I count upon it,” said the Master. “我就知道你会去，”大少爷说，
“You have seen me foiled; I mean you shall see me victorious. “你已经看过我潦倒的模样；我是说你也会看到我胜利的样子。
To gain that I will risk wetting you like a sop in this wild weather.” 为了达到目的，这样的天气里，恐怕你会被淋成落汤鸡的。”
“And at least,” I added, “you know very well you could not throw me off.” “至少，”我接着他的话说，“您非常清楚，您是没法把我丢下的。”
“Not easily,” said he. “不太容易，”他说，
“You put your finger on the point with your usual excellent good sense. “你跟往常一样，判断得挺准确。
I never fight with the inevitable.” 我从来不强求，而是顺其自然。”
“I suppose it is useless to appeal to you?” said I. “那么，劝您是没用的了？”我说。
“Believe me, perfectly,” said he. “完全正确。”他说。
“And yet, if you would give me time, I could write—” I began. “不过，如果再给我点儿时间的话，我会写信——”我说道。
“And what would be my Lord Durrisdeer’s answer?” asks he. “那达里斯迪尔爵爷的答案会是什么呢？”他问道。
“Aye,” said I, “that is the rub.” “呃，”我说，“这就是问题所在。”
“And, at any rate, how much more expeditions that I should go myself!” says he. “无论如何，我自己走的话还不知道要多走多少路呢！”他说，
“But all this is quite a waste of breath. 但是，现在这都是白费口舌了。
At seven to-morrow the chaise will be at the door. 明天7点马车会到门口等着。
For I start from the door, Mackellar; I do not skulk through woods and take my chaise upon the wayside—shall we say, at Eagles?” 麦凯勒，我会在大门口上车。我不会偷偷摸摸穿过树林然后到大路那边去上车的——比如说，在伊格尔斯？”
My mind was now thoroughly made up. 现在我完全下定决心了。
“Can you spare me quarter of an hour at St. Bride’s?” said I. “您能在圣布赖德等我一刻钟吗？”我说，
“I have a little necessary business with Carlyle.” 我还有点儿急事要找一下卡莱尔。”
“An hour, if you prefer,” said he. “如果你愿意的话，一个小时也行。”他说，
“I do not seek to deny that the money for your seat is an object to me; and you could always get the first to Glascow with saddle-horses.” “我还指望着收你的座位钱呢。要是你骑马到格拉斯哥，还会快些。”
“Well,” said I, “I never thought to leave old Scotland.” “那好吧，”我说，“我从来没想过要离开古老的苏格兰。”
“It will brisken you up,” says he. “这次旅行让你轻松活跃起来的。”他说道。
“This will be an ill journey for some one,” I said. “对某人来说，却是一次不幸的旅行。”我说，
“I think, sir, for you. “我想，先生，对您而言。”
Something speaks in my bosom; and so much it says plain—that this is an ill-omened journey.” 我的心中似乎有些预感，说白了，这是一次预示着不幸的旅行。”
“If you take to prophecy,” says he, “listen to that.” “如果你相信所谓的预言，”他说，“那你就听信这个吧。”
There came up a violent squall off the open Solway, and the rain was dashed on the great windows. 这时，索尔韦一带下起了暴风雨，雨珠打在大大的窗户上。
“Do ye ken what that bodes, warlock?” said he, in a broad accent: “that there’ll be a man Mackellar unco’ sick at sea.” 他带着很重的方言味儿说道：“预言家，你知道这预示着什么吗？有个叫麦凯勒的人要晕船。”
When I got to my chamber, I sat there under a painful excitation, hearkening to the turmoil of the gale, which struck full upon that gable of the house. 我走回自己的房间，坐在那里，又激动又痛苦，听着外面狂风乱作，撞击着房子的屋脊。
What with the pressure on my spirits, the eldritch cries of the wind among the turret-tops, and the perpetual trepidation of the masoned house, sleep fled my eyelids utterly. 我的情绪压抑，再加上角楼上怪异的风声以及这个石砖房屋永无休止的震颤，让我睡意全无。
I sat by my taper, looking on the black panes of the window, where the storm appeared continually on the point of bursting in its entrance; and upon that empty field I beheld a perspective of consequences that made the hair to rise upon my scalp. 我坐在烛光旁，看着窗户上黑乎乎的玻璃，暴风雨似乎正要从这里冲进来，我注视着那个空空的地方，心中有种不好的预感，不禁毛骨悚然。
The child corrupted, the home broken up, my master dead or worse than dead, my mistress plunged in desolation—all these I saw before me painted brightly on the darkness; and the outcry of the wind appeared to mock at my inaction. 孩子误入歧途，家庭支离破碎，爵爷死了，或者比死了更糟糕，太太孤独寂寥——所有这些都在黑暗中清晰地浮现在我的眼前，而且呼啸的狂风似乎在嘲笑我的无能。
[1] Ordered. [1]有序的。
[2] Land steward. [2]土财主。
[3] Fooling. [3]愚弄。
Chapter 9 第九章
Mr. Mackellar’s Journey with the Master. 麦凯勒与大少爷的旅程
The chaise came to the door in a strong drenching mist. 马车在滂沱大雨中来到门口。
We took our leave in silence: the house of Durrisdeer standing with dropping gutters and windows closed, like a place dedicate to melancholy. 我们安安静静地上车：达里斯迪尔府邸矗立在那里，顺着屋檐，流水如注，窗户紧闭，好像陷入了悲伤之中。
I observed the Master kept his head out, looking back on these splashed walls and glimmering roofs, till they were suddenly swallowed in the mist; and I must suppose some natural sadness fell upon the man at this departure; or was it some provision of the end? 我看到大少爷把头伸到外面，看着后面雨点溅击的墙壁和忽明忽暗的屋顶，直到它们突然淹没在雨雾中。在此离别时刻，我想大少爷一定觉得有点儿悲伤，要不就是预见了最后的结局？
At least, upon our mounting the long brae from Durrisdeer, as we walked side by side in the wet, he began first to whistle and then to sing the saddest of our country tunes, which sets folk weeping in a tavern, WANDERING WILLIE. 至少，在我们爬上达里斯迪尔府邸前长长的斜坡时，我们肩并肩在大雨里跋涉的时候，他先是吹着口哨，然后哼着最悲伤的那首曲调——《流浪的威利》。
The set of words he used with it I have not heard elsewhere, and could never come by any copy; but some of them which were the most appropriate to our departure linger in my memory. 他唱的歌词我没有听过，之后也没有再听过。不过有些话跟我们的离别特别契合，久久地徘徊在我的记忆中。
One verse began— 有一段的开头是这样的：
Home was home then, my dear, full of kindly faces, 亲爱的家乡，满是一张张亲切的面孔。
Home was home then, my dear, happy for the child. 亲爱的家乡，是孩子快乐的天堂。
And ended somewhat thus— 结尾好像是：
Now, when day dawns on the brow of the moorland, 此时，晨曦从荒野的尽头如约而至，
Lone stands the house, and the chimney-stone is cold. 这栋房子孤零零地立在那里，烟囱早已冰凉。
Lone let it stand, now the folks are all departed, 就让它孤零零地呆着吧，此刻乡亲们都已远走他乡，
The kind hearts, the true hearts, that loved the place of old. 那些真诚善良的人，对这个古老的地方有着深切的眷恋。
I could never be a judge of the merit of these verses; they were so hallowed by the melancholy of the air, and were sung (or rather “soothed”) to me by a master-singer at a time so fitting. 我无法评判这些歌词的好坏；它们在周围忧郁氛围的烘托下，显得如此神圣；由大少爷对我唱出来（更确切地说是抒发出来），是如此应时应景。
He looked in my face when he had done, and saw that my eyes watered. 他唱歌的时候看着我的脸，看到了我眼中的泪水。
“Ah! “啊！
Mackellar,” said he, “do you think I have never a regret?” 麦凯勒，”他说，“你觉得我从来没有任何遗憾和悔恨吗？”
“I do not think you could be so bad a man,” said I, “if you had not all the machinery to be a good one.” 我说：“如果把全部心思用在如何做一个好人上，我想您不是一个那么坏的人。”
“No, not all,” says he: “not all. “不，不是全部，”他说，“不是全部心思。
You are there in error. 你错了。
The malady of not wanting, my evangelist.” 我的福音传道士呀，学坏可用不上全部心思。”
But methought he sighed as he mounted again into the chaise. 但是，我发现他登上马车的时候，叹了口气。
All day long we journeyed in the same miserable weather: the mist besetting us closely, the heavens incessantly weeping on my head. 一整天下来，我们都在糟糕的天气中行路：雨雾严严实实地包围着我们，老天爷不停地在我的头顶伤心落泪。
The road lay over moorish hills, where was no sound but the crying of moor-fowl in the wet heather and the pouring of the swollen burns. 道路穿过荒山野岭，暴雨中除了野禽的叫声以及潺潺的溪水声外，寂寥无声。
Sometimes I would doze off in slumber, when I would find myself plunged at once in some foul and ominous nightmare, from the which I would awake strangling. 有时，我打个盹，会发现自己马上陷入一些残忍的噩梦中，就从窒息的感觉中醒来。
Sometimes, if the way was steep and the wheels turning slowly, I would overhear the voices from within, talking in that tropical tongue which was to me as inarticulate as the piping of the fowls. 有时候，路很陡峭，车轮转得很慢，我会无意间听到里面的谈话声，用的是热带地区的语言，在我听来，就像野鸟鸣叫的声音，一点儿都听不懂。
Sometimes, at a longer ascent, the Master would set foot to ground and walk by my side, mostly without speech. 有时候，马车爬了比较长的上坡路之后，大少爷会下车，走在我旁边，很多时候两人都默默不语。
And all the time, sleeping or waking, I beheld the same black perspective of approaching ruin; and the same pictures rose in my view, only they were now painted upon hillside mist. 一直以来，不论是睡觉还是走路，我都看到一种不幸的景象，感觉毁灭即将来临。这些同样的画面原来只是在我的脑海中出现，现在却是被刻画在山间迷雾中。
One, I remember, stood before me with the colours of a true illusion. 我记得，有这样一幅充满了色彩的幻想在我面前出现过。
It showed me my lord seated at a table in a small room; his head, which was at first buried in his hands, he slowly raised, and turned upon me a countenance from which hope had fled. 画面是这样的，爵爷坐在一间小房间的桌子旁，埋在手臂间的脑袋慢慢地抬起来，转向我，一副希望早已消逝的表情。
I saw it first on the black window-panes, my last night in Durrisdeer; it haunted and returned upon me half the voyage through; and yet it was no effect of lunacy, for I have come to a ripe old age with no decay of my intelligence; nor yet (as I was then tempted to suppose) a heaven-sent warning of the future, for all manner of calamities befell, not that calamity—and I saw many pitiful sights, but never that one. 在达里斯迪尔府邸最后的那个夜晚，我就在黑乎乎的窗户玻璃上看到了这个画面，在这次路途中它一直萦绕着我。不过这既不是精神病带来的幻觉，因为我虽已迈入老年，不过智力还算正常；也不是上天给我的指示（尽管我当时很想这么认为），因为即使各种各样的灾祸降临，但也不是那种灾祸——我看到过很多凄惨的场景，但从来不是那样的。
It was decided we should travel on all night; and it was singular, once the dusk had fallen, my spirits somewhat rose. 我们计划连夜赶路；奇怪的是，夜幕已降临，我的精神反而好起来了。
The bright lamps, shining forth into the mist and on the smoking horses and the hodding post-boy, gave me perhaps an outlook intrinsically more cheerful than what day had shown; or perhaps my mind had become wearied of its melancholy. 明亮的灯光穿透迷雾，照着呼着热气的马匹和赶马的伙计，或许给我一种比白天更加欢快的景象，又或者我的大脑已经厌烦了这种忧郁的气氛。
At least, I spent some waking hours, not without satisfaction in my thoughts, although wet and weary in my body; and fell at last into a natural slumber without dreams. 至少，尽管我的身体又湿又累，但我还是花了些时间用心去思考，很是满意；最后自然地进入无梦的沉睡中。
Yet I must have been at work even in the deepest of my sleep; and at work with at least a measure of intelligence. 然而，即使在深度睡眠的时候，我的脑子还是在运转，至少还有一点点理智在。
For I started broad awake, in the very act of crying out to myself 突然惊醒过来，我竟然不自觉地冲着自己大声叫道：
Home was home then, my dear, happy for the child, stricken to find in it an appropriateness, which I had not yesterday observed, to the Master’s detestable purpose in the present journey. 亲爱的家乡，是孩子快乐的天堂。我慢慢意识到这首歌与大少爷这次旅行可恶的目的刚好十分相符，而昨天我却没有发现这一点。
We were then close upon the city of Glascow, where we were soon breakfasting together at an inn, and where (as the devil would have it) we found a ship in the very article of sailing. 快到格拉斯哥城的时候，我们很快就在一家小酒馆吃上了早饭，而且刚好在那里发现有条船将要起航。
We took our places in the cabin; and, two days after, carried our effects on board. 我们在客舱里订了位置。两天后，我们的财物都装上了船。
Her name was the NONESUCH, a very ancient ship and very happily named. 这条船叫做“完美号”，非常老的一条船，名字也很好听。
By all accounts this should be her last voyage; people shook their heads upon the quays, and I had several warnings offered me by strangers in the street to the effect that she was rotten as a cheese, too deeply loaden, and must infallibly founder if we met a gale. 据说这可能是她的最后一次航行了；码头上的人们看着她摇摇头，街上的好几个路人都告诉我不要坐这条船，意思是这条船就像个奶酪一样千疮百孔了，装的货物又多，要是碰上大风，船肯定会沉没的。
From this it fell out we were the only passengers; the Captain, McMurtrie, was a silent, absorbed man, with the Glascow or Gaelic accent; the mates ignorant rough seafarers, come in through the hawsehole; and the Master and I were cast upon each other’s company. 结果是，船上就我们几个乘客。船长麦克默特里是个沉默寡言、一心干活的人，说话带着格拉斯哥或者盖尔语的口音。船员都是没什么文化的大老粗，一个个都是水手出身，大少爷只跟我谈得来。
THE NONESUCH carried a fair wind out of the Clyde, and for near upon a week we enjoyed bright weather and a sense of progress. “完美号”顺风驶出克莱德河，将近一周的时间，天气晴朗，船速很快。
I found myself (to my wonder) a born seaman, in so far at least as I was never sick; yet I was far from tasting the usual serenity of my health. 让我意想不到的是，我竟然觉得自己就是一个天生的水手，因为到现在我还没有晕船的感觉。不过，我也没觉得像往常那样心平气和。
Whether it was the motion of the ship on the billows, the confinement, the salted food, or all of these together, I suffered from a blackness of spirit and a painful strain upon my temper. 可能是船在海浪上的颠簸，狭窄的空间、带海腥味的食物，或者是所有这些都结合在一起，我感觉精神不振、情绪不定。
The nature of my errand on that ship perhaps contributed; I think it did no more; the malady (whatever it was) sprang from my environment; and if the ship were not to blame, then it was the Master. 可能是因为这趟差事闹的，不过这应该也不是主要原因。主要原因在于我所处的环境，如果不是这条船的问题，那就要怪大少爷了。
Hatred and fear are ill bedfellows; but (to my shame be it spoken) I have tasted those in other places, lain down and got up with them, and eaten and drunk with them, and yet never before, nor after, have I been so poisoned through and through, in soul and body, as I was on board the NONESUCH. 仇恨和恐惧都让我无法入睡。（虽然羞于启齿）但我在其他地方也体验过仇恨和恐惧，躺着的时候、起床的时候，还有吃饭喝水的时候。不过却从来没有像在“完美号”上这样，身心受到严重受影响。
I freely confess my enemy set me a fair example of forbearance; in our worst days displayed the most patient geniality, holding me in conversation as long as I would suffer, and when I had rebuffed his civility, stretching himself on deck to read. 我坦白地承认，我的敌人在克制方面给我树立了很好的榜样。在我们最艰难的日子里，他表现出了最大的耐心和亲切。只要我一难受，他就拉着我说话，而我对他的礼貌漠然置之，他只好躺在甲板上自己看书。
The book he had on board with him was Mr. Richardson’s famous CLARISSA! and among other small attentions he would read me passages aloud; nor could any elocutionist have given with greater potency the pathetic portions of that work. 他随身带的书是理查森先生的名作《克拉莉莎》。有时候他会大声念几段给我听，吸引我的注意，再有能力的演说家也不会把那部作品读得如此悲伤。
I would retort upon him with passages out of the Bible, which was all my library—and very fresh to me, my religious duties (I grieve to say it) being always and even to this day extremely neglected. 我会用《圣经》中的句子来回应他，那是我带的唯一一本书——抱歉地说，我总是没有时间去做礼拜，甚至到今天为止，我都彻底把这个给忽略了，书的内容对我来说很陌生。
He tasted the merits of the word like the connoisseur he was; and would sometimes take it from my hand, turn the leaves over like a man that knew his way, and give me, with his fine declamation, a Roland for my Oliver. 他却像行家一样品味其中的奥妙，有时候会把书从我手中夺过去，貌似很了解内容一样地翻着，然后再滔滔不绝地给我朗诵一段。
But it was singular how little he applied his reading to himself; it passed high above his head like summer thunder: Lovelace and Clarissa, the tales of David’s generosity, the psalms of his penitence, the solemn questions of the book of Job, the touching poetry of Isaiah—they were to him a source of entertainment only, like the scraping of a fiddle in a change- house. 但是他读的书却很少会运用到自己身上，就像夏日头顶瞬间即逝的雷声。登徒浪子和克拉莉莎、大卫的慷慨大度、他忏悔时唱的赞美诗、《约伯记》中严肃的问题，还有《以赛亚书》中感人的诗篇——这些对于他来说都只是娱乐的工具，就像小客栈里笛子的优美乐声。
This outer sensibility and inner toughness set me against him; it seemed of a piece with that impudent grossness which I knew to underlie the veneer of his fine manners; and sometimes my gorge rose against him as though he were deformed—and sometimes I would draw away as though from something partly spectral. 他这种外在的鉴赏能力和内在的坚韧让我很反感，我知道他彬彬有礼的举止下掩藏的是卑鄙粗鲁。有时候我会觉得他像一个畸形人一样令人厌恶——有时候他身上会有一种妖魔鬼怪般的气息，让我望而却步。
I had moments when I thought of him as of a man of pasteboard—as though, if one should strike smartly through the buckram of his countenance, there would be found a mere vacuity within. 有时候我觉得他就是纸板做的——就好像，只要有人优雅地轻戳他的外壳，就会发现只有空虚。
This horror (not merely fanciful, I think) vastly increased my detestation of his neighbourhood; I began to feel something shiver within me on his drawing near; I had at times a longing to cry out; there were days when I thought I could have struck him. 这种恐惧（我想并不是无中生有）大大加剧了我与他为邻的厌恶之感。他一接近我，我就会觉得全身战栗。有时候，我非常想大声喊出来，有些日子我真是想暴打他一顿。
This frame of mind was doubtless helped by shame, because I had dropped during our last days at Durrisdeer into a certain toleration of the man; and if any one had then told me I should drop into it again, I must have laughed in his face. 这种想法显然是由羞愧引起的，因为在我们呆在达里斯迪尔府邸的最后那段日子里，我对他百般容忍。如果还有人叫我那样忍耐，我肯定不会答应。
It is possible he remained unconscious of this extreme fever of my resentment; yet I think he was too quick; and rather that he had fallen, in a long life of idleness, into a positive need of company, which obliged him to confront and tolerate my unconcealed aversion. 他可能还没有觉察出我内心愤恨的烈火，不过我想他反应那么敏捷，可能早就看出我的厌恶，只不过长期的散漫懒惰的生活让他非常需要别人的陪伴，所以他不得不面对我，在我面前忍着。
Certain, at least, that he loved the note of his own tongue, as, indeed, he entirely loved all the parts and properties of himself; a sort of imbecility which almost necessarily attends on wickedness. 至少有一点可以肯定，他非常喜欢自己巧舌如簧。的确，他非常自负于自己的多才多艺和天赋，这是常常在邪恶之人身上会出现的愚蠢行为。
I have seen him driven, when I proved recalcitrant, to long discourses with the skipper; and this, although the man plainly testified his weariness, fiddling miserably with both hand and foot, and replying only with a grunt. 当我不愿听他说话时，他只好去找船长当他的听众。两人聊了很久，船长明确地表示了他的厌倦，难以忍受地拨弄手和脚，咕哝几声，算作回应。
After the first week out we fell in with foul winds and heavy weather. 一周过后，我们遇上了逆风的恶劣天气。
The sea was high. 海浪很大。
The NONESUCH, being an old-fashioned ship and badly loaden, rolled beyond belief; so that the skipper trembled for his masts, and I for my life. “完美号”本来就很破，还装了那么多货物，难以置信地摇晃着。船长扶着他的桅杆，双手在哆嗦，而我，也在为自己的生命担忧。
We made no progress on our course. 我们没有再往前行。
An unbearable ill-humour settled on the ship: men, mates, and master, girding at one another all day long. 一种让人难以承受的坏情绪在船上蔓延开来：水手、船员、船长，一个个整天嘲笑讥讽对方。
A saucy word on the one hand, and a blow on the other, made a daily incident. 这边一句粗话，那边揍上一拳，每天都是如此。
There were times when the whole crew refused their duty; and we of the afterguard were twice got under arms—being the first time that ever I bore weapons—in the fear of mutiny. 有时候所有船员集体罢工，我们这些船尾的乘客两次拿起了武器——这是我第一次手里拿着武器——以防发生叛乱。
In the midst of our evil season sprang up a hurricane of wind; so that all supposed she must go down. 就在这混乱不堪的时候，飓风来了。于是大家都以为船肯定得沉了。
I was shut in the cabin from noon of one day till sundown of the next; the Master was somewhere lashed on deck. 从那天中午到第二天日落，我一直呆在船舱内，大少爷则呆在甲板某处。
Secundra had eaten of some drug and lay insensible; so you may say I passed these hours in an unbroken solitude. 塞孔拉德不知吃了点儿什么药，躺在那里昏迷不醒。所以，你可以说我是在完全孤独的情况下度过那几个小时的。
At first I was terrified beyond motion, and almost beyond thought, my mind appearing to be frozen. 我先是被吓得没法动弹，几乎不能思考，思绪好像被冻结了。
Presently there stole in on me a ray of comfort. 过了一会儿，我突然得到了一丝安慰。
If the NONESUCH foundered, she would carry down with her into the deeps of that unsounded sea the creature whom we all so feared and hated; there would be no more Master of Ballantrae, the fish would sport among his ribs; his schemes all brought to nothing, his harmless enemies at peace. 如果“完美号”葬身大海，她将会把我们最害怕和憎恨的人送到大海的深处。世界上就再也没有巴伦特雷少爷了，海里的鱼会啃掉他的骨头，他的阴谋都会灰飞烟灭，他那些无辜的敌人就可以相安无事了。
At first, I have said, it was but a ray of comfort; but it had soon grown to be broad sunshine. 在前面我就说过，这只不过是一丝安慰而已。不久，太阳就出来了。
The thought of the man’s death, of his deletion from this world, which he embittered for so many, took possession of my mind. 我脑子里想的全是这个人的死亡，在他受尽磨难之后从这个世界消失。
I hugged it, I found it sweet in my belly. 我很享受这个想法，回想起来都觉得开心。
I conceived the ship’s last plunge, the sea bursting upon all sides into the cabin, the brief mortal conflict there, all by myself, in that closed place; I numbered the horrors, I had almost said with satisfaction; I felt I could bear all and more, if the NONESUCH carried down with her, overtook by the same ruin, the enemy of my poor master’s house. 我构思着这条船最后如何陷入水中，海水从四面八方涌入船舱，我自己一个人在那个密闭的空间里作临死前的思想斗争。我计算着内心的恐惧，但是可以说心里却感到愉快，我觉得只要“完美号”沉入大海，把可怜的主人家里这个敌人同样毁灭掉，我就能够承受所有，甚至更多的痛苦。
Towards noon of the second day the screaming of the wind abated; the ship lay not so perilously over, and it began to be clear to me that we were past the height of the tempest. 快到第二天中午的时候，风势渐渐弱了，并没有出现惊险翻船这一幕，我开始明白我们已经度过了风暴的高峰期。
As I hope for mercy, I was singly disappointed. 在我祈求上帝怜悯的时候，我又感到失望。
In the selfishness of that vile, absorbing passion of hatred, I forgot the case of our innocent shipmates, and thought but of myself and my enemy. 在憎恨的感情完全占据我的内心的时候，我完全忘了那些无辜的船员，只想到我自己和我的敌人。
For myself, I was already old; I had never been young, I was not formed for the world’s pleasures, I had few affections; it mattered not the toss of a silver tester whether I was drowned there and then in the Atlantic, or dribbled out a few more years, to die, perhaps no less terribly, in a deserted sick-bed. 就我自己而言，我已经老了。我从来没有年轻过，我不是为了享受世界的快乐而生的，我也没什么自己嗜好的东西。如果用抛掷硬币来决定我的生死，不管是被淹死在这里、葬身大西洋，还是苟延残喘多活几年，最后孤独地死在病榻上，对我来说都无所谓。
Down I went upon my knees—holding on by the locker, or else I had been instantly dashed across the tossing cabin—and, lifting up my voice in the midst of that clamour of the abating hurricane, impiously prayed for my own death. 我跪下来——双手紧抓着储物柜，要不然船舱一晃就会把我甩出去——在飓风退去的喧闹声中，我提高声音，祈祷上帝，让我死去。
“O God!” “上帝啊！”
I cried, “I would be liker a man if I rose and struck this creature down; but Thou madest me a coward from my mother’s womb. 我喊道，“如果我站起来把那个家伙打败，那我就是一个男子汉。但是我在娘胎里的时候，您就把我塑造成了一个胆小鬼。
O Lord, Thou madest me so, Thou knowest my weakness, Thou knowest that any face of death will set me shaking in my shoes. 啊，上帝！您把我弄成这样，您知道我的弱点，您知道我在面对任何死亡的时候，都会双腿颤抖。
But, lo! here is Thy servant ready, his mortal weakness laid aside. 但是，上帝！您的仆人已经准备将自己的生死置之度外了。
Let me give my life for this creature’s; take the two of them, Lord! take the two, and have mercy on the innocent!” 让我为了他献出生命吧。上帝！把我们两人都带走吧，怜悯一下那些无辜的人！”
In some such words as these, only yet more irreverent and with more sacred adjurations, I continued to pour forth my spirit. 接着，我带着诅咒的心情更加虔诚地祈祷，我继续倾吐心中积怨。
God heard me not, I must suppose in mercy; and I was still absorbed in my agony of supplication when some one, removing the tarpaulin cover, let the light of the sunset pour into the cabin. 上帝肯定没有听到我的祈祷，应该是上帝太仁慈了。有人将防水布揭开，日落余晖洒进船舱，而我仍然沉浸在自己痛苦的祈祷中。
I stumbled to my feet ashamed, and was seized with surprise to find myself totter and ache like one that had been stretched upon the rack. 我面带羞愧，踉踉跄跄地想站起来，却发现自己走路摇摇晃晃，而且全身酸痛，就像被钉在了绞刑架上一样。
Secundra Dass, who had slept off the effects of his drug, stood in a corner not far off, gazing at me with wild eyes; and from the open skylight the captain thanked me for my supplications. 塞孔拉德·戴斯已经从药效中醒过来了，他站在不远处的角落里，睁大眼睛盯着我。头顶的天窗也开着，船长感谢我的祈祷。
“It’s you that saved the ship, Mr. Mackellar,” says he. “麦凯勒先生，是你救了这只船。”他说，
“There is no craft of seamanship that could have kept her floating: well may we say, ‘Except the Lord the city keep, the watchmen watch in vain!’” “没有任何人的航海技术可以让她漂浮着。可以这么说，‘除非上帝眷顾这座城市，否则守护者只能白费力气。’”
I was abashed by the captain’s error; abashed, also, by the surprise and fear with which the Indian regarded me at first, and the obsequious civilities with which he soon began to cumber me. 船长的误解让我感到局促不安，同样令我感到不安的，还有印度人起先发现我时露出来的惊讶和恐惧，并且他很快开始谄媚地纠缠我。
I know now that he must have overheard and comprehended the peculiar nature of my prayers. 我知道现在他肯定偷听到了，而且理解了我祈祷的本意。
It is certain, of course, that he at once disclosed the matter to his patron; and looking back with greater knowledge, I can now understand what so much puzzled me at the moment, those singular and (so to speak) approving smiles with which the Master honoured me. 而且，他肯定马上跟他的主人报告了这件事。回过头来看以前的事情，我现在明白了为什么我当时如此困惑，还有大少爷表扬我时，脸上奇特而略带赞赏的微笑。
Similarly, I can understand a word that I remember to have fallen from him in conversation that same night; when, holding up his hand and smiling, “Ah! 同样，我理解了那天晚上他跟我交谈时说过的话。他拉着我的手，笑着说：“啊！
Mackellar,” said he, “not every man is so great a coward as he thinks he is—nor yet so good a Christian.” 麦凯勒！不是每个人都像自己想的那样是个胆小鬼——也不是每个人都如自己想的那样是个虔诚的基督徒。”
He did not guess how true he spoke! 他没有想到，这句话是何等真实！
For the fact is, the thoughts which had come to me in the violence of the storm retained their hold upon my spirit; and the words that rose to my lips unbidden in the instancy of prayer continued to sound in my ears: with what shameful consequences, it is fitting I should honestly relate; for I could not support a part of such disloyalty as to describe the sins of others and conceal my own. 事实就是，在对抗暴风雨时，我的那些想法都牢牢地印在我的脑海中。那些话就自发地在祈祷的时候脱口而出，然后传入我的耳中。我应该坦白地将祈祷导致的丢人后果讲出来，我不能忍受这样不忠的行为，隐瞒着自己的过错而去批评别人的罪恶。
The wind fell, but the sea hove ever the higher. 风势减弱了，但是海浪却越来越高。
All night the NONESUCH rolled outrageously; the next day dawned, and the next, and brought no change. 整个晚上，“完美号”都在大海中猛烈地颠簸着。第二天黎明和第三天都没有任何变化。
To cross the cabin was scarce possible; old experienced seamen were cast down upon the deck, and one cruelly mauled in the concussion; every board and block in the old ship cried out aloud; and the great bell by the anchor-bitts continually and dolefully rang. 从船舱的一头走到另一头都是不可能的事情。经验丰富的水手们趴在甲板上，一个被摔得太严重，脑震荡了。旧船上每块木板都在大声尖叫，锚缆柱旁的大钟不停地哀鸣。
One of these days the Master and I sate alone together at the break of the poop. 有一天，大少爷和我单独坐在船尾甲板结合处。
I should say the NONESUCH carried a high, raised poop. 不得不说，“完美号”的船尾甲板比较高。
About the top of it ran considerable bulwarks, which made the ship unweatherly; and these, as they approached the front on each side, ran down in a fine, old- fashioned, carven scroll to join the bulwarks of the waist. 四周有船舷，使得船无法抢风而行。船尾两侧的船舷雕饰精美，呈老式的漩涡状盘旋之下，与船身的船舷相连接。
From this disposition, which seems designed rather for ornament than use, it followed there was a discontinuance of protection: and that, besides, at the very margin of the elevated part where (in certain movements of the ship) it might be the most needful. 这种设计似乎没多大用处，只是装饰而已，接下来船体的保护就有些空隙了：除此之外，在隆起部分的边缘（特别是在船身颠簸时），这是非常必要的。
It was here we were sitting: our feet hanging down, the Master betwixt me and the side, and I holding on with both hands to the grating of the cabin skylight; for it struck me it was a dangerous position, the more so as I had continually before my eyes a measure of our evolutions in the person of the Master, which stood out in the break of the bulwarks against the sun. 就是我们正坐着的地方：我们双脚悬空，大少爷坐在我和船舷之间，我紧紧地握着天窗的栏杆，突然觉得这个地方很危险，特别是看到大少爷不断地在船上转来转去，阳光下的他显得特别突出。
Now his head would be in the zenith and his shadow fall quite beyond the NONESUCH on the farther side; and now he would swing down till he was underneath my feet, and the line of the sea leaped high above him like the ceiling of a room. 一会儿他头顶苍穹，影子落在“完美号”很远的那一边，一会儿他又摇摇晃晃地来到我的脚下，海平面就像天花板一样处在他的上方。
I looked on upon this with a growing fascination, as birds are said to look on snakes. 我慢慢地对这个景象越来越着迷，就像鸟儿被蛇迷住了一般。
My mind, besides, was troubled with an astonishing diversity of noises; for now that we had all sails spread in the vain hope to bring her to the sea, the ship sounded like a factory with their reverberations. 另外，我的脑海中充满了各式各样奇怪的声音，心烦意乱。现在我们将所有帆扬起来，希望船能乘风破浪，可是却白费劲。这条船就像一个机器轰鸣的工厂。
We spoke first of the mutiny with which we had been threatened; this led us on to the topic of assassination; and that offered a temptation to the Master more strong than he was able to resist. 我们先是谈论了之前的叛乱事件，然后由此联想到了暗杀这个话题，大少爷按捺不住心中的激动。
He must tell me a tale, and show me at the same time how clever he was and how wicked. 他一定要给我讲了一个故事，显示他是如何聪明的同时，又是如何邪恶。
It was a thing he did always with affectation and display; generally with a good effect. 他总是会声情并茂地炫耀这一类事，效果通常还不错。
But this tale, told in a high key in the midst of so great a tumult, and by a narrator who was one moment looking down at me from the skies and the next up from under the soles of my feet—this particular tale, I say, took hold upon me in a degree quite singular. 但是，在如此嘈杂喧闹的环境下讲这个故事，大少爷声调激昂，时而从天空向下俯视我，时而从我的脚下仰视我——我想说这个特别的故事的确让我觉得非同凡响。
“My friend the count,” it was thus that he began his story, “had for an enemy a certain German baron, a stranger in Rome. “我的一位伯爵朋友，”他这样开始他的故事，“在罗马跟一个陌生的德国男爵结下了梁子。
It matters not what was the ground of the count’s enmity; but as he had a firm design to be revenged, and that with safety to himself, he kept it secret even from the baron. 至于两人结怨是因为什么事就不清楚了，但是伯爵决心为自己复仇，并且要保证自己的安全。他对这一计划守口如瓶，甚至在男爵面前都不露声色。
Indeed, that is the first principle of vengeance; and hatred betrayed is hatred impotent. 事实上，那是复仇的第一原则；仇恨一旦显露出来，就不构成什么威胁了。
The count was a man of a curious, searching mind; he had something of the artist; if anything fell for him to do, it must always be done with an exact perfection, not only as to the result, but in the very means and instruments, or he thought the thing miscarried. 这个伯爵好奇心强，喜欢钻研，有点儿艺术家的感觉。若是让他做什么事情，那事情必须做得极其完美，不仅仅是结果，还有使用的方法和道具，否则他就会觉得事情没做好。
It chanced he was one day riding in the outer suburbs, when he came to a disused by-road branching off into the moor which lies about Rome. 碰巧有一天，他在郊区骑马的时候，来到一条通向罗马附近沼泽的废弃大道。
On the one hand was an ancient Roman tomb; on the other a deserted house in a garden of evergreen trees. 道路的一边是古罗马的墓地，另一边是长满了常青树的花园，院内有一座无人居住的房子。
This road brought him presently into a field of ruins, in the midst of which, in the side of a hill, he saw an open door, and, not far off, a single stunted pine no greater than a currant-bush. 不久，这条路带他到了一处废墟的中央，在山坡的一侧，他看到一扇开着的洞门，不远处，孤零零地立着一棵矮小的小松树，跟葡萄藤差不多。
The place was desert and very secret; a voice spoke in the count’s bosom that there was something here to his advantage. 这个地方杳无人迹而且十分隐秘，伯爵心中响起一个声音：这个地方肯定是个宝地。
He tied his horse to the pine- tree, took his flint and steel in his hand to make a light, and entered into the hill. 他把马拴在松树上，然后拿着打火石，点着了一个火把，进了山洞。
The doorway opened on a passage of old Roman masonry, which shortly after branched in two. 里面的走廊是古罗马时期的建筑，很快通道就分为两路。
The count took the turning to the right, and followed it, groping forward in the dark, till he was brought up by a kind of fence, about elbow-high, which extended quite across the passage. 伯爵走了右边那条道，在黑暗中摸索前进，直到他碰到一堵围墙，大约有手肘那么高，横着堵住了通道。
Sounding forward with his foot, he found an edge of polished stone, and then vacancy. 他用脚试探着往前走，发现有一块光滑的石头，石头另一边就是空的了。
All his curiosity was now awakened, and, getting some rotten sticks that lay about the floor, he made a fire. 他的好奇心全部被唤醒了，就捡了一些朽木，点了一堆火。
In front of him was a profound well; doubtless some neighbouring peasant had once used it for his water, and it was he that had set up the fence. 他的前面是一口深不见底的古井。多半是附近的哪个农民曾经从这取水，也是他砌了这堵围墙。
A long while the count stood leaning on the rail and looking down into the pit. 伯爵靠在栏杆上，站了很长时间，向井底望去。
It was of Roman foundation, and, like all that nation set their hands to, built as for eternity; the sides were still straight, and the joints smooth; to a man who should fall in, no escape was possible. 井下的基石是古罗马风格的，就像罗马所有设计师一样，将这个当作永恒的建造。井壁仍然挺直，接合处光滑，谁要是掉进去了，肯定爬不出来。
‘Now,’ the count was thinking, ‘a strong impulsion brought me to this place. ‘现在，’伯爵思考着，‘内心的冲动将我带到这个地方。
What for? what have I gained? why should I be sent to gaze into this well?’ when the rail of the fence gave suddenly under his weight, and he came within an ace of falling headlong in. 来干什么？我得到了什么？为什么我被送到这里看这口井？’这时，围墙上的栏杆在他的重压之下，突然咔嚓一声断了，他头往前一栽，差点儿掉了进去。
Leaping back to save himself, he trod out the last flicker of his fire, which gave him thenceforward no more light, only an incommoding smoke. 他吓得赶紧后退，踩灭了火堆上最后一丝火苗，周围没有其他亮光，只留下一阵恼人的烟雾。
‘Was I sent here to my death?’ says he, and shook from head to foot. ‘我是来这里送死的吗？’他说着，全身上下都颤抖起来。
And then a thought flashed in his mind. 突然，他的脑海中闪过一个念头。
He crept forth on hands and knees to the brink of the pit, and felt above him in the air. 他手和膝盖并用慢慢爬到古井的边缘，在他上方的空中摸索了一下。
The rail had been fast to a pair of uprights; it had only broken from the one, and still depended from the other. 栏杆紧紧地拴在一对立柱上；其中的一根立柱倒了，栏杆另一头还拴在立柱上。
The count set it back again as he had found it, so that the place meant death to the first comer, and groped out of the catacomb like a sick man. 伯爵将它扶起来，放归原位。这样谁要是来这里肯定会掉下去的。然后，他像个病人一样爬出了地下墓穴。
The next day, riding in the Corso with the baron, he purposely betrayed a strong preoccupation. 第二天，伯爵和男爵一起在科索骑马，他故意做出心不在焉的样子。
The other (as he had designed) inquired into the cause; and he, after some fencing, admitted that his spirits had been dashed by an unusual dream. （正如他所预计的那样），男爵就问他怎么回事。他有点儿含糊其辞，然后承认自己的心情被一个奇怪的梦搅乱了。
This was calculated to draw on the baron—a superstitious man, who affected the scorn of superstition. 这是故意设计的——男爵相信这些迷信东西，却假装对迷信不在乎。
Some rallying followed, and then the count, as if suddenly carried away, called on his friend to beware, for it was of him that he had dreamed. 他先是嘲笑了伯爵一番，然后伯爵就好似中邪了一样，叫他的朋友小心一点儿，因为他自己那天梦到的正是他。
You know enough of human nature, my excellent Mackellar, to be certain of one thing: I mean that the baron did not rest till he had heard the dream. 尊敬的麦凯勒，你也知道人的本性，总是喜欢对一件事情刨根问底。我的意思是，男爵要是没听到这个梦是不会罢休的。
The count, sure that he would never desist, kept him in play till his curiosity was highly inflamed, and then suffered himself, with seeming reluctance, to be overborne. 伯爵确定他是不会打消这个念头的，于是总是欲言又止，尽力挑起他的好奇心，然后装着不情愿的样子不得不说。
‘I warn you,’ says he, ’evil will come of it; something tells me so. ‘我提醒你一下，’他说道，‘有些事情告诉我，你的厄运要来了。
But since there is to be no peace either for you or me except on this condition, the blame be on your own head! 但是既然你我都被弄得不安宁，不过你却是罪魁祸首！
This was the dream:—I beheld you riding, I know not where, yet I think it must have been near Rome, for on your one hand was an ancient tomb, and on the other a garden of evergreen trees. 这个梦是这样的：我看到你骑着马，不知道要去哪里，不过我确定是在罗马附近，你的一边是一片古墓，另一边是一个长满常青树的花园。
Methought I cried and cried upon you to come back in a very agony of terror; whether you heard me I know not, but you went doggedly on. 我一直在大声叫你往回走，带着恐惧和痛苦，也不知道你听到了没有，可是你却固执地往前走。
The road brought you to a desert place among ruins, where was a door in a hillside, and hard by the door a misbegotten pine. 那条路将你带到一片荒芜的废墟中，山坡上有个洞门，洞口旁边有颗矮小的松树。
Here you dismounted (I still crying on you to beware), tied your horse to the pine-tree, and entered resolutely in by the door. 你在那里下马（我仍然大声喊着要你当心），把马拴在树上，然后坚决地从洞口进去了。
Within, it was dark; but in my dream I could still see you, and still besought you to hold back. 洞里漆黑一片，但是我在梦中还能看到你，大声喊着你回来。
You felt your way along the right-hand wall, took a branching passage to the right, and came to a little chamber, where was a well with a railing. 你靠着右面的墙壁摸索着前进，在一个岔路口往右边的通道走去，来到一个小房间，里面是栏杆围着的一口井。
At this—I know not why—my alarm for you increased a thousandfold, so that I seemed to scream myself hoarse with warnings, crying it was still time, and bidding you begone at once from that vestibule. 这个时候——不知道为什么我内心的担忧增加了千百倍，我的嗓子似乎都喊哑了，高喊着现在仍有时间，要你赶快离开那个地方。
Such was the word I used in my dream, and it seemed then to have a clear significancy; but to-day, and awake, I profess I know not what it means. 在梦里我就是这么喊叫的，但是这些话有着重大的含义；不过现在醒着的时候，我承认我完全不知道那是什么意思了。
To all my outcry you rendered not the least attention, leaning the while upon the rail and looking down intently in the water. 对于我的大喊大叫，你完全没有注意到，而是在栏杆上靠了一会儿，专注地往下看着井里的水。
And then there was made to you a communication; I do not think I even gathered what it was, but the fear of it plucked me clean out of my slumber, and I awoke shaking and sobbing. 然后你得到了什么指示，我不知道那是什么，但恐惧将我从睡梦中拉出来，我全身颤抖，还不停地哭着。
And now,’ continues the count, ‘I thank you from my heart for your insistency. 而且现在，’伯爵继续说道，‘我从心底感谢你的坚持。
This dream lay on me like a load; and now I have told it in plain words and in the broad daylight, it seems no great matter.’ 这个梦就像石头一样压着我喘不过气来。现在我在光天化日之下明明白白地说出来，好像没什么事了。’
—‘I do not know,’ says the baron. ——‘我不知道是怎么回事，’男爵说道，
‘It is in some points strange. ‘有些地方有点儿蹊跷。
A communication, did you say? 你说到什么指示，是吗？
Oh! it is an odd dream. 噢！这真是个奇怪的梦。
It will make a story to amuse our friends.’ 把这个当成故事告诉我们的朋友会很有趣的。’
—‘I am not so sure,’ says the count. ‘我不太确定这个故事是不是有趣，’伯爵说道，
‘I am sensible of some reluctancy. ‘不过我还是不太愿意说，
Let us rather forget it.’ 我们还是忘了它吧。’
—‘By all means,’ says the baron. ‘那好吧。’男爵说道。
And (in fact) the dream was not again referred to. 的确，两个人都没有提过这个梦。
Some days after, the count proposed a ride in the fields, which the baron (since they were daily growing faster friends) very readily accepted. 几天后，伯爵提议到田野上去骑马，男爵欣然接受了（因为他们的友谊与日俱增）。
On the way back to Rome, the count led them insensibly by a particular route. 在回罗马的路上，伯爵不知不觉地将他们带上了那条特别的路。
Presently he reined in his horse, clapped his hand before his eyes, and cried out aloud. 不一会儿，他勒住缰绳，在眼前拍了拍手，然后大声叫起来。
Then he showed his face again (which was now quite white, for he was a consummate actor), and stared upon the baron. 然后，他又露出脸来（脸色煞白，他真是一个技艺高超的演员），转过脸瞪着男爵。
‘What ails you?’ cries the baron. ‘你哪里不舒服？’男爵问道，
‘What is wrong with you?’ ‘你怎么啦？’
—‘Nothing,’ cries the count. ‘没事，’伯爵答道，
‘It is nothing. ‘没什么事。
A seizure, I know not what. 只是突然一阵不舒服，我也不知道怎么了。
Let us hurry back to Rome.’ 我们还是赶紧回罗马吧。’
But in the meanwhile the baron had looked about him; and there, on the left-hand side of the way as they went back to Rome, he saw a dusty by-road with a tomb upon the one hand and a garden of evergreen trees upon the other. 可就在这时，男爵看了看他的周围。在回罗马路上的左边，他看到一条满是灰尘的小道，一侧是一片墓地，另一侧是一个长满常青树的花园。
—‘Yes,’ says he, with a changed voice. ‘好吧，’他说道，声音为之一变，
‘Let us by all means hurry back to Rome. ‘我们还是赶紧回罗马吧。
I fear you are not well in health.’ 我担心你的身体不太舒服。’
—‘Oh, for God’s sake!’ cries the count, shuddering, ‘back to Rome and let me get to bed.’ ‘噢，上帝保佑！’伯爵叫道，全身颤抖，‘赶紧回罗马，让我睡上一觉。’
They made their return with scarce a word; and the count, who should by rights have gone into society, took to his bed and gave out he had a touch of country fever. 在往回赶的路上他们几乎没说话，伯爵按理应该去参加社交活动的，却说自己得了疟疾，去睡觉了。
The next day the baron’s horse was found tied to the pine, but himself was never heard of from that hour. 第二天，有人发现男爵的马拴在那棵松树上，他自己却再也没有出现。
—And, now, was that a murder?” says the Master, breaking sharply off. 现在，你看看，这是不是谋杀？”大少爷突然中止了这个故事。
“Are you sure he was a count?” “您确定他是一个伯爵？”
I asked. 我问道。
“I am not certain of the title,” said he, “but he was a gentleman of family: and the Lord deliver you, Mackellar, from an enemy so subtile!” “我不太确定他的爵位，”他说，“不过他出身贵族家庭。麦凯勒，愿上帝保佑你不要遇到这么狡猾的敌人！”
These last words he spoke down at me, smiling, from high above; the next, he was under my feet. 前面的话他是从上面俯视，笑着对我说的；而后面的话，是他从我的脚下仰视着我说的。
I continued to follow his evolutions with a childish fixity; they made me giddy and vacant, and I spoke as in a dream. 我带着小孩似的执著继续看着他不断变化的身影，这让我头晕目眩，心头空荡荡的，说起话来好似在梦中。
“He hated the baron with a great hatred?” “他非常恨那个男爵吗？”
I asked. 我问道。
His belly moved when the man came near him,” said the Master. “男爵一靠近，他就满肚子都是气。”大少爷说道。
“I have felt that same,” said I. “我也有同感。”我说道。
“Verily!” cries the Master. “那是当然。”大少爷叫道，
“Here is news indeed! “这的确是个新鲜事！
I wonder—do I flatter myself? or am I the cause of these ventral perturbations?” 我想知道——我这是在夸自己吗？或者我就是造成你内心不安的原因？”
He was quite capable of choosing out a graceful posture, even with no one to behold him but myself, and all the more if there were any element of peril. 虽然只有我一个人看着他，他却摆出一个相当优雅得体的姿势，要是碰到什么危险怎么办。
He sat now with one knee flung across the other, his arms on his bosom, fitting the swing of the ship with an exquisite balance, such as a featherweight might overthrow. 他跷着二郎腿，双臂抱在胸前，与船体的颠簸保持着微妙的平衡，好似一片羽毛就能掀翻他。
All at once I had the vision of my lord at the table, with his head upon his hands; only now, when he showed me his countenance, it was heavy with reproach. 突然，我好像看见爵爷坐在桌旁，脑袋埋在双手间，然后抬头，我看到他那带着责备的神情。
The words of my own prayer—I WERE LIKER A MAN IF I STRUCK THIS CREATURE DOWN—shot at the same time into my memory. 我祷告时说的话——如果我把这个人打倒，那我就是一个真的男子汉了——同时浮现在我的脑海里。
I called my energies together, and (the ship then heeling downward toward my enemy) thrust at him swiftly with my foot. 我集聚全身的能量，（这时船向我的敌人那边倾斜）迅速踢向他。
It was written I should have the guilt of this attempt without the profit. 应该说，我这么做是出于内疚，没有任何好处。
Whether from my own uncertainty or his incredible quickness, he escaped the thrust, leaping to his feet and catching hold at the same moment of a stay. 不知道是我不太果断，还是他的反应太快，大少爷一跳就避过了我这一脚，同时顺手抓住一根柱子。
I do not know how long a time passed by. 我不知道过了多久。
I lying where I was upon the deck, overcome with terror and remorse and shame: he standing with the stay in his hand, backed against the bulwarks, and regarding me with an expression singularly mingled. 我躺在甲板上，内心充满了恐惧、悔恨和羞耻。他站在那里，手里拿着那根柱子，背靠着船舷，用非常复杂的眼神注视着我。
At last he spoke. 终于他开口说话了。
“Mackellar,” said he, “I make no reproaches, but I offer you a bargain. “麦凯勒，”他说道，“我不责怪你，但是我有一个条件。
On your side, I do not suppose you desire to have this exploit made public; on mine, I own to you freely I do not care to draw my breath in a perpetual terror of assassination by the man I sit at meat with. 你呢，肯定不想把这个壮举宣扬出去；而我呢，坦白地说，我不想整天担心跟我同桌吃饭的人什么时候会杀了我。
Promise me—but no,” says he, breaking off, “you are not yet in the quiet possession of your mind; you might think I had extorted the promise from your weakness; and I would leave no door open for casuistry to come in—that dishonesty of the conscientious. 答应我——不会再这样做了，”他停了一下，继续道，“你还没有平静下来，你可能会以为我乘人之危强迫你答应的，我还是不要留下把柄让人家拿去诡辩——正直的人也会有不诚实的行为。
Take time to meditate.” 好好考虑一下吧。”
With that he made off up the sliding deck like a squirrel, and plunged into the cabin. 说完，他像松鼠一样逃到光滑的甲板上，走进船舱了。
About half an hour later he returned—I still lying as he had left me. 大约半小时过后，他回来了，看到我依然躺在那里。
“Now,’ says be, “will you give me your troth as a Christian, and a faithful servant of my brother’s, that I shall have no more to fear from your attempts?” “现在，”他说，“你可不可以作为一个虔诚的基督徒，作为我弟弟忠实的仆人，答应我你不会再铤而走险了？”
“I give it you,” said I. “我答应您。”我说道。
“I shall require your hand upon it,” says he. “那我们拉手为誓。”他说。
“You have the right to make conditions,” I replied, and we shook hands. “您有权利讲条件。”我回答道，于是我们拉了拉手。
He sat down at once in the same place and the old perilous attitude. 他又在同一个地方坐下来，还是之前那个危险的姿势。
“Hold on!” cried I, covering my eyes. “等等！”我叫道，用双手盖住眼睛，
“I cannot bear to see you in that posture. “我不忍心看着您那个姿势。
The least irregularity of the sea might plunge you overboard.” 随便一个海浪就会让您栽到水里去的。”
“You are highly inconsistent,” he replied, smiling, but doing as I asked. “你还真是反复无常呀，”他笑着回答道，但还是遵照我的话动了动，
“For all that, Mackellar, I would have you to know you have risen forty feet in my esteem. “麦凯勒，尽管如此，我还是想让你知道，你在我心中的地位又高了一点儿。
You think I cannot set a price upon fidelity? 你以为我不会奖赏忠诚的人？
But why do you suppose I carry that Secundra Dass about the world with me? 那你以为我为什么走到哪里都要带着塞孔拉德·戴斯？
Because he would die or do murder for me to- morrow; and I love him for it. 因为他随时都会为我死或者为我杀人，我就喜欢这一点。
Well, you may think it odd, but I like you the better for this afternoon’s performance. 好吧，你可能会觉得奇怪，但是因为你今天下午的表现，我更加喜欢你了。
I thought you were magnetised with the Ten Commandments; but no—God damn my soul!”—he cries, “the old wife has blood in his body after all! 原先我以为你是恪守摩西十诫，可实际却不是这样的，——他妈的！”他大声叫道，“想不到这个婆婆妈妈的老家伙身上还有点儿血气！
Which does not change the fact,” he continued, smiling again, “that you have done well to give your promise; for I doubt if you would ever shine in your new trade.” 可还是不能改变现实，”他又笑了，继续道，“你已经作出保证了，我倒是怀疑你下次行动的时候是不是能表现出色一些。”
“I suppose,” said I, “I should ask your pardon and God’s for my attempt. “我应该，”我说道，“请求您的原谅以及上帝的宽恕。
At any rate, I have passed my word, which I will keep faithfully. 不管怎样，我已经作出保证，而且我不会食言的。
But when I think of those you persecute—” I paused. 但是我一想起那些您害的人——”我停顿了一下。
“Life is a singular thing,” said he, “and mankind a very singular people. “人生各不相同，”他说道，“人类也各不相同。
You suppose yourself to love my brother. 你以为你爱我弟弟。
I assure you, it is merely custom. 但是我向你保证，那只是一种习惯。
Interrogate your memory; and when first you came to Durrisdeer, you will find you considered him a dull, ordinary youth. 好好回忆一下，当你初到达里斯迪尔府邸的时候，是不是把他当成一个傻子，一个平平凡凡的年轻人。
He is as dull and ordinary now, though not so young. 他现在还是一样傻，一样平凡，只不过不再年轻了。
Had you instead fallen in with me, you would to-day be as strong upon my side.” 要是你当时遇到的是我，那现在你同样会坚定地站在我身边。”
“I would never say you were ordinary, Mr. Bally,” I returned; “but here you prove yourself dull. “巴利先生，我永远不会说您是个平凡的人，”我回答道，“但是现在您却证明了自己是个傻子。
You have just shown your reliance on my word. 您刚刚相信了我说的话，
In other terms, that is my conscience—the same which starts instinctively back from you, like the eye from a strong light.” 也就是说，您相信了我的良心——就等于您找回了自己的良心，就像眼睛对强光的本能反应。”
“Ah!” says he, “but I mean otherwise. “啊！”他说道，“不过我的意思却不是这样。
I mean, had I met you in my youth. 我的意思是，要是我在年轻的时候认识你就好了。
You are to consider I was not always as I am to-day; nor (had I met in with a friend of your description) should I have ever been so.” 那样你就不会这么看我了，或者（如果遇上一个像你这样的朋友）我就不会是这个样子了。”
“Hut, Mr. Bally,” says I, “you would have made a mock of me; you would never have spent ten civil words on such a Square-toes.” “哈哈！巴利先生，”我说道，“您肯定是在嘲笑我。您从来没有在我这样一个古板的人身上用过10个好听的词。”
But he was now fairly started on his new course of justification, with which he wearied me throughout the remainder of the passage. 他还在喋喋不休地为自己辩解，没完没了，我都厌烦了。
No doubt in the past he had taken pleasure to paint himself unnecessarily black, and made a vaunt of his wickedness, bearing it for a coat-of-arms. 毫无疑问，他以前总是将自己丑化，夸大自己的邪恶，以此为乐，甚至以此为荣。
Nor was he so illogical as to abate one item of his old confessions. 他也不会不合逻辑地去减少曾经的忏悔了。
“But now that I know you are a human being,” he would say, “I can take the trouble to explain myself. “但是，现在我知道你也有人性，”他说，“我可以不厌其烦地为我自己辩解。
For I assure you I am human, too, and have my virtues, like my neighbours.” 因为我向你保证我也是一个人，也跟邻居一样有着自己的道德准则。”
I say, he wearied me, for I had only the one word to say in answer: twenty times I must have said it: “Give up your present purpose and return with me to Durrisdeer; then I will believe you.” 我就说，我都快被他烦死了，因为我只有一个回答：我肯定说了20遍了：“打消您现在的念头，跟我回达里斯迪尔，然后我就会相信您。”
Thereupon he would shake his head at me. 然后，他总是对我摇摇头。
“Ah! “啊！
Mackellar, you might live a thousand years and never understand my nature,” he would say. 麦凯勒！你可能活上千年都没法理解我的本性，”他说道，
“This battle is now committed, the hour of reflection quite past, the hour for mercy not yet come. “这场战争既然开始了，就容不得前思后想。
It began between us when we span a coin in the hall of Durrisdeer, now twenty years ago; we have had our ups and downs, but never either of us dreamed of giving in; and as for me, when my glove is cast, life and honour go with it.” 20年前，我们就在达里斯迪尔的大厅里掷硬币，开始了这场战争。我们都经历了起起落落，但都从来没有想过投降。至于我，只要我一投降，生命和荣誉就都灰飞烟灭了。”
“A fig for your honour!” “什么狗屁荣誉！”
I would say. 我会这么说，
“And by your leave, these warlike similitudes are something too high-sounding for the matter in hand. “恕我直言，用战争来比喻你们之间的事，这也太高调了。
You want some dirty money; there is the bottom of your contention; and as for your means, what are they? to stir up sorrow in a family that never harmed you, to debauch (if you can) your own nephew, and to wring the heart of your born brother! 您只是想要几个臭钱，这才是争夺的重点，至于采取什么手段，都无所谓了。对一个从未伤害过您的家庭带来伤痛，诱惑自己的亲侄子，让您自己的亲弟弟心如刀绞！
A footpad that kills an old granny in a woollen mutch with a dirty bludgeon, and that for a shilling-piece and a paper of snuff—there is all the warrior that you are.” 您就如同一个拦路贼，用一根脏兮兮的大头短棒杀害一个戴着毡帽的老奶奶，就为了抢一个先令和一卷鼻烟纸——这就是您所谓的英勇事迹？”
When I would attack him thus (or somewhat thus) he would smile, and sigh like a man misunderstood. 每当我这样（或者用类似的词语）痛斥他时，他会像被人误解了一样叹息、苦笑。
Once, I remember, he defended himself more at large, and had some curious sophistries, worth repeating, for a light upon his character. 我记得有一次，他长篇大论地为自己作奇怪的诡辩，为了展现他的个性，值得重复一下。
“You are very like a civilian to think war consists in drums and banners,” said he. “你就跟外面的平头百姓没啥区别，以为打仗就是战鼓加战旗，”他说道，
“War (as the ancients said very wisely) is ULTIMA RATIO. “（正如古人们的至理名言）战争是最终的手段。
When we take our advantage unrelentingly, then we make war. 当我们为捍卫自己的利益不择手段时，就可以开始战争。
Ah! 啊！
Mackellar, you are a devil of a soldier in the steward’s room at Durrisdeer, or the tenants do you sad injustice!” 麦凯勒，你是达里斯迪尔府邸管家屋里一个恶魔般的战士，要么就是那些佃户冤枉了你！”
“I think little of what war is or is not,” I replied. “我从来就没去想过战争什么的，”我回答道，
“But you weary me with claiming my respect. “但是，您总是想要得到我的尊重，我都烦了。
Your brother is a good man, and you are a bad one—neither more nor less.” 您的弟弟是个好人，而您是个坏蛋——就这么简单。”
“Had I been Alexander—” he began. “要是我是亚历山大——”他开始说道。
“It is so we all dupe ourselves,” I cried. “我们都在自欺欺人，”我大声说道，
“Had I been St. Paul, it would have been all one; I would have made the same hash of that career that you now see me making of my own.” “如果我是圣保罗，事情还不都一个样，我还是您现在看到的这个倒霉样。”
“I tell you,” he cried, bearing down my interruption, “had I been the least petty chieftain in the Highlands, had I been the least king of naked negroes in the African desert, my people would have adored me. “我告诉你，”他打断我的话，大声地说道，“如果我是苏格兰高地上一个小小的酋长，如果我是非洲沙漠里那些裸露的黑人中的一个首领，我的手下肯定会对我崇敬万分。
A bad man, am I? 我是个坏蛋？
Ah! but I was born for a good tyrant! 哈！但我天生就是个慈悲为怀的统治者！
Ask Secundra Dass; he will tell you I treat him like a son. 不信你去问问塞孔拉德·戴斯；他会告诉你，我待他就像对儿子一般。
Cast in your lot with me to-morrow, become my slave, my chattel, a thing I can command as I command the powers of my own limbs and spirit—you will see no more that dark side that I turn upon the world in anger. 不信你明天就试试做我的仆人、奴隶，像我的手脚和精神那样听我的使唤——你就看不到我在外人面前发火的阴暗面了。
I must have all or none. 要么我全赢，要么就输个一干二净。
But where all is given, I give it back with usury. 但是，如果付出了所有，我就会加倍索回。
I have a kingly nature: there is my loss!” 我有一种君王的性格：这就是我失败的原因！”
“It has been hitherto rather the loss of others,” I remarked, “which seems a little on the hither side of royalty.” “到目前为止，都还是对方受到损失，”我评论道，“您这君王这边似乎损失不大。”
“Tilly-vally!” cried he. “简直就是无稽之谈。”他喊道，
“Even now, I tell you, I would spare that family in which you take so great an interest: yes, even now—to- morrow I would leave them to their petty welfare, and disappear in that forest of cut-throats and thimble-riggers that we call the world. “甚至现在，我告诉你，我会放过那个你下了这么多功夫的家庭。是的，现在——明天，我就会让他们过自己的小日子，我自己会消失在充满刺客和坑蒙拐骗的森林中，也就是我们所说的人世间。
I would do it to-morrow!” says he. 明天开始，我就那么做！”他说道，
“Only—only—” “只要——只要——”
“Only what?” “只要什么？”
I asked. 我问道。
“Only they must beg it on their bended knees. “只要他们双膝跪地来求我。
I think in public, too,” he added, smiling. 要在大家面前跪下来，”他笑了笑，继续说道，
“Indeed, Mackellar, I doubt if there be a hall big enough to serve my purpose for that act of reparation.” “事实上，麦凯勒，我担心有没有那么大的大厅能让他们来赔礼道歉呢。”
“Vanity, vanity!” “虚荣啊，虚荣！”
I moralised. 我用说教式的口吻说道，
“To think that this great force for evil should be swayed by the same sentiment that sets a lassie mincing to her glass!” “想想，您那柔弱得只能让一个姑娘抿上一口小酒的力量怎么能撼动邪恶的强大力量呢！”
“Oh! there are double words for everything: the word that swells, the word that belittles; you cannot fight me with a word!” said he. “噢！任何事情都有两种说法：有夸大的，有贬低的，单靠一句话是没法打败我的！”他说道，
“You said the other day that I relied on your conscience: were I in your humour of detraction, I might say I built upon your vanity. “那天，你说你相信了我的良心：要是我和你一样喜欢诽谤的话，是不是可以说我相信了你的虚荣心。
It is your pretension to be UN HOMME DE PAROLE; ’tis mine not to accept defeat. 你冒充一个诚实守信的人；而我是一个不甘失败的人。
Call it vanity, call it virtue, call it greatness of soul—what signifies the expression? 不管是虚荣，还是美德，又或是心灵的伟大——只不过是一种表达方式而已？
But recognise in each of us a common strain: that we both live for an idea.” 但是，还是不得不承认我们之间有着共同点：我们都为一个信念活着。”
It will be gathered from so much familiar talk, and so much patience on both sides, that we now lived together upon excellent terms. 在双方进行过如此多不拘礼节的谈话，耗费了如此多的耐心之后，我们现在相处得非常融洽。
Such was again the fact, and this time more seriously than before. 而事实是，这次却跟以前不太一样。
Apart from disputations such as that which I have tried to reproduce, not only consideration reigned, but, I am tempted to say, even kindness. 除了我努力制造出来的争论外，更多的是互相体谅，甚至可以说是友好。
When I fell sick (as I did shortly after our great storm), he sat by my berth to entertain me with his conversation, and treated me with excellent remedies, which I accepted with security. 在经历大风暴之后，我生了一场病，大少爷坐在我床边跟我聊天，逗我开心，用各种药方给我治疗，我小心谨慎地接受了他的好意。
Himself commented on the circumstance. 他对这种情景颇有感触。
“You see,” says he, “you begin to know me better. “你看，你开始深入了解我了吧。”他说道，
A very little while ago, upon this lonely ship, where no one but myself has any smattering of science, you would have made sure I had designs upon your life. “几天前，在这个孤零零的船上，只有我对航海略知一二，你就以为我想害你。
And, observe, it is since I found you had designs upon my own, that I have shown you most respect. 看看吧，自从我发现你想加害于我的时候，我就对你敬意倍增。
You will tell me if this speaks of a small mind.” 你说这是不是说明了，是你思想狭隘。”
I found little to reply. 我不知如何应答。
In so far as regarded myself, I believed him to mean well; I am, perhaps, the more a dupe of his dissimulation, but I believed (and I still believe) that he regarded me with genuine kindness. 就我自己而言，我觉得他是好心的；或许我只是被他的伪装给骗了，但是我仍然愿意相信他待我是真诚的。
Singular and sad fact! so soon as this change began, my animosity abated, and these haunting visions of my master passed utterly away. 真是奇特而又让人悲伤的事实！这个变化一旦开始，我对他的憎恶就慢慢减弱了。爵爷那些难以忘怀的景象也完全消逝了。
So that, perhaps, there was truth in the man’s last vaunting word to me, uttered on the second day of July, when our long voyage was at last brought almost to an end, and we lay becalmed at the sea end of the vast harbour of New York, in a gasping heat, which was presently exchanged for a surprising waterfall of rain. 就这样到了7月2日，我们漫长的航行终于要结束了，我们静静地停靠在宽阔的纽约港，大少爷最后一次对我大大吹嘘了一番，其中也有一定的真实性。当时天气热得人喘不过气来，不久竟下了一场大雨。
I stood on the poop, regarding the green shores near at hand, and now and then the light smoke of the little town, our destination. 我站在船尾，看着眼前绿色的海滩，看着我们的目的地——不时被青烟缭绕的小镇。
And as I was even then devising how to steal a march on my familiar enemy, I was conscious of a shade of embarrassment when he approached me with his hand extended. 当我正想着如何先行一步，抢到这个熟悉的敌人前面时，大少爷伸出手，朝我走近，我感到很尴尬。
“I am now to bid you farewell,” said he, “and that for ever. “现在我要跟你道别了他说道，“是永别。
For now you go among my enemies, where all your former prejudices will revive. 因为现在你要回到我的敌人中间去了，你之前所有的偏见都会死灰复燃。
I never yet failed to charm a person when I wanted; even you, my good friend—to call you so for once—even you have now a very different portrait of me in your memory, and one that you will never quite forget. 如果我想收服一个人的话，我从来都不会失败。即使是你，我的朋友——让我最后一次这么称呼你——即使现在在你的记忆中，我与原来不一样了，不过将来你也不会忘记我的。
The voyage has not lasted long enough, or I should have wrote the impression deeper. 可惜这次航行的时间不够长，不然我会给你留下更深刻的印象。
But now all is at an end, and we are again at war. 但现在，一切都结束了，我们又要开战了。
Judge by this little interlude how dangerous I am; and tell those fools”—pointing with his finger to the town—“to think twice and thrice before they set me at defiance.” 通过这段小小的插曲，你就知道我是多么危险，去告诉那些笨蛋吧。”他指着那个小镇，“在他们蔑视我之前，记得三思而后行。”
Chapter 10 第十章
Passages at New York. 纽约往事
I have mentioned I was resolved to steal a march upon the Master; and this, with the complicity of Captain McMurtrie, was mighty easily effected: a boat being partly loaded on the one side of our ship and the Master placed on board of it, the while a skiff put off from the other, carrying me alone. 我曾经提到过我决心抢到大少爷前面，而这个计划也在麦克默特里船长的配合下轻而易举地实现了：我们的船一侧有一艘小船，船上载着部分货物，大少爷使用这艘船；同时，另一侧有一艘小艇，小艇就专门载着我一个人。
I had no more trouble in finding a direction to my lord’s house, whither I went at top speed, and which I found to be on the outskirts of the place, a very suitable mansion, in a fine garden, with an extraordinary large barn, byre, and stable, all in one. 我不费吹灰之力就以最快的速度找到了爵爷的住宅，宅子坐落在郊区，是一栋非常考究的府邸，里面有个漂亮的花园、一个集马车房以及牛棚与马厩为一体的大天棚。
It was here my lord was walking when I arrived; indeed, it had become his chief place of frequentation, and his mind was now filled with farming. 当我到达的时候，爵爷正在这里散步。事实上，这里已经成为他经常出入的主要地点，现在他脑子里装的全是农活。
I burst in upon him breathless, and gave him my news: which was indeed no news at all, several ships having outsailed the NONESUCH in the interval. 我急不可待地向他报告了我的消息，其实这早就算不上什么消息了，因为在这期间，已经有好几艘快于“完美号”到达了。
“We have been expecting you long,” said my lord; “and indeed, of late days, ceased to expect you any more. “我们已经等你好久了，”爵爷开口说道，“事实上，最近这些天，我们对你已经不抱任何期望了。
I am glad to take your hand again, Mackellar. 真高兴能再次见到你，麦凯勒。
I thought you had been at the bottom of the sea.” 我还以为你已经葬身海底了呢。”
“Ah! my lord, would God I had!” cried I. “啊！爵爷，上帝保佑，要是那样的话，”我大声喊道，
“Things would have been better for yourself.” “事情就对您有利多了。”
“Not in the least,” says he, grimly. “绝非如此。”他脸色阴沉地对我说，
“I could not ask better. “这已经是我能想到的最好的情况了。
There is a long score to pay, and now—at last—I can begin to pay it.” 那笔旧账我等了很长时间，现在我终于可以开始清算了。”
I cried out against his security. 我又大声地反对，怕爵爷有危险。
“Oh!” says he, “this is not Durrisdeer, and I have taken my precautions. “哦！”他说，“这里可不是达里斯迪尔，并且我已经做好了防范措施。
His reputation awaits him; I have prepared a welcome for my brother. 他已经臭名远扬了，我准备好怎样迎接我哥哥了。
Indeed, fortune has served me; for I found here a merchant of Albany who knew him after the ’45 and had mighty convenient suspicions of a murder: some one of the name of Chew it was, another Albanian. 事实上，命运还是垂怜于我的；我在这里认识了一位奥尔巴尼商人，他是在1745年以后认识我那哥哥的，这个商人怀疑他与一桩谋杀案有关，被害者也住在奥尔巴尼，名字叫丘之类的。
No one here will be surprised if I deny him my door; he will not be suffered to address my children, nor even to salute my wife: as for myself, I make so much exception for a brother that he may speak to me. 因此如果我不让他进我家门，这里没有人会惊讶；我不会允许他接触我的孩子，也不许跟我的妻子打招呼，至于我自己，我将念在兄弟之情上允许他同我讲话。
I should lose my pleasure else,” says my lord, rubbing his palms. 不然我会失去不少乐趣。”爵爷搓着手说道。
Presently he bethought himself, and set men off running, with billets, to summon the magnates of the province. 他沉思了一会儿后，派人带着请帖火速去邀请地方名流。
I cannot recall what pretext he employed; at least, it was successful; and when our ancient enemy appeared upon the scene, he found my lord pacing in front of his house under some trees of shade, with the Governor upon one hand and various notables upon the other. 我记不清爵爷是以什么借口发出的请帖，但邀请的人悉数到来。当我们的宿敌出现的时候，爵爷正在屋前树阴下踱步，身边一边是州长一边是各界名流。
My lady, who was seated in the verandah, rose with a very pinched expression and carried her children into the house. 起初坐在走廊上的太太露出痛苦的表情，接着她起身将孩子们带进屋子里。
The Master, well dressed and with an elegant walking-sword, bowed to the company in a handsome manner and nodded to my lord with familiarity. 大少爷衣冠楚楚，身佩宝剑，彬彬有礼地向众人鞠躬，亲切地向爵爷点头。
My lord did not accept the salutation, but looked upon his brother with bended brows. 爵爷并没有理会，只是皱着眉头看着他的兄长。
“Well, sir,” says he, at last, “what ill wind brings you hither of all places, where (to our common disgrace) your reputation has preceded you?” “好吧，先生，”最后，爵爷说道，“是什么邪风把你吹到这来了啊？（让我们觉得很丢脸的是）在你到之前，大家已经久仰你的大名了。”
“Your lordship is pleased to be civil,” said the Master, with a fine start. “那爵爷你可就太客气了。”大少爷淡然地说道。
“I am pleased to be very plain,” returned my lord; “because it is needful you should clearly understand your situation. “我很乐意跟你坦诚，”爵爷回道，“因为我觉得你有必要认清你现在的处境。
At home, where you were so little known, it was still possible to keep appearances; that would be quite vain in this province; and I have to tell you that I am quite resolved to wash my hands of you. 在家乡，你的劣迹不为众人所知，你可以抛头露面；但在这里你那一套可行不通。我得告诉你，我决心与你断绝一切关系。
You have already ruined me almost to the door, as you ruined my father before me;—whose heart you also broke. 你几乎毁了我的一辈子，在我之前你还毁了我的父亲——他的心被你伤透了。
Your crimes escape the law; but my friend the Governor has promised protection to my family. 你的罪行可以逃脱法律的严惩，但我的这位州长朋友已经许诺保护我的家庭。
Have a care, sir!” cries my lord, shaking his cane at him: “if you are observed to utter two words to any of my innocent household, the law shall be stretched to make you smart for it.” 你得小心了，先生！”爵爷边用手杖在他面前晃动，边厉声喝道，“如果有人发现你跟我家里的任何人说话，哪怕是只有两个字，法律都绝不会饶恕你的。”
“Ah!” says the Master, very slowly. “哦！”大爷缓缓说道，
“And so this is the advantage of a foreign land! “这就是生活在国外的好处！
These gentlemen are unacquainted with our story, I perceive. 看来，这几位先生还不了解我们的故事。
They do not know that I am the Lord Durrisdeer; they do not know you are my younger brother, sitting in my place under a sworn family compact; they do not know (or they would not be seen with you in familiar correspondence) that every acre is mine before God Almighty—and every doit of the money you withhold from me, you do it as a thief, a perjurer, and a disloyal brother!” 他们并不知道我才是真正的达里斯迪尔爵爷；更不知道我的弟弟是凭着一张家庭内部打赌的字据才坐上了原本属于我的位置，他们还不知道你拥有的每一寸土地、你拒绝支付给我的每个子儿都本该属于我，你的行径堪比小偷、骗子、叛徒！”
“General Clinton,” I cried, “do not listen to his lies. “克林顿将军，”我高声喊道，“别听他胡说八道。
I am the steward of the estate, and there is not one word of truth in it. 我是那个家族的管家，我确信他说的没一句真话。
The man is a forfeited rebel turned into a hired spy: there is his story in two words.” 这个人先是个暴乱分子，之后又去当了间谍，他的全部经历用这两个词概括最合适不过了。”
It was thus that (in the heat of the moment) I let slip his infamy. 就这样（在关键时刻）我在无意中透露了他的丑陋行径。
“Fellow,” said the Governor, turning his face sternly on the Master, “I know more of you than you think for. “伙计，”州长转过脸严肃地看着大少爷，说道，“我比你想象的更了解你。
We have some broken ends of your adventures in the provinces, which you will do very well not to drive me to investigate. 你在这一带的所作所为我们都已经有所了解，你最好不要让我再深入调查下去。
There is the disappearance of Mr. Jacob Chew with all his merchandise; there is the matter of where you came ashore from with so much money and jewels, when you were picked up by a Bermudan out of Albany. 比如雅克布·楚先生以及他的全部货物都到哪去了；你被一艘从奥尔巴尼出发的百慕大帆船救起的时候竟带着这么多的钱财珠宝，你究竟是从哪里弄来的？
Believe me, if I let these matters lie, it is in commiseration for your family and out of respect for my valued friend, Lord Durrisdeer.” 相信我，我对这些事情放任不管，完全是出于对你的家庭的怜悯以及看在我的朋友、尊敬的达里斯迪尔爵爷的面子上。”
There was a murmur of applause from the provincials. 那些地方名流也小声嘀咕着表示赞同。
“I should have remembered how a title would shine out in such a hole as this,” says the Master, white as a sheet: “no matter how unjustly come by. “想不到如此偏僻的地方对一个爵爷也这么膜拜，”大少爷脸色苍白地说道，“也不管他是通过怎样不法的手段得来这个头衔的。
It remains for me, then, to die at my lord’s door, where my dead body will form a very cheerful ornament.” 现在我只有死在爵爷的门前，让他拿我这具死尸去装点门面吧！”
“Away with your affectations!” cries my lord. “别再假装了！”爵爷吼道，
“You know very well I have no such meaning; only to protect myself from calumny, and my home from your intrusion. “你很清楚我并没有这个意思；我只是不想被你污蔑，不想我的家庭被你骚扰罢了。
I offer you a choice. 我给你个选择。
Either I shall pay your passage home on the first ship, when you may perhaps be able to resume your occupations under Government, although God knows I would rather see you on the highway! 要么我给你回家的路费，你赶紧坐最早的船离开，那样你还可以继续去政府供职，尽管我宁愿看你在公路上走着！
Or, if that likes you not, stay here and welcome! 要么，如果你不愿意的话，欢迎你留在这里！
I have inquired the least sum on which body and soul can be decently kept together in New York; so much you shall have, paid weekly; and if you cannot labour with your hands to better it, high time you should betake yourself to learn. 我将支付给你在纽约最基本的生活费；这就是你能获得的全部，按周领取；如果你不能通过劳动改善生活，你就该专心学着点儿。
The condition is—that you speak with no member of my family except myself,” he added. 这一切唯一的条件是——不许你同我们家除了我之外的任何人说话！”爵爷又加了一句。
I do not think I have ever seen any man so pale as was the Master; but he was erect and his mouth firm. 我想自己从来没看过像大少爷这么苍白的脸；尽管脸色苍白，但他站得笔直，双唇紧闭。
“I have been met here with some very unmerited insults,” said he, “from which I have certainly no idea to take refuge by flight. “我在这里受到了一些非常不当的侮辱，”他说道，“为了这个我也决意留下来。
Give me your pittance; I take it without shame, for it is mine already—like the shirt upon your back; and I choose to stay until these gentlemen shall understand me better. 给我你说的少得可怜的生活费；我拿着的话也不羞愧，因为这一切原本都属于我，比如说你身上的衬衣；我选择留下来，直到这些先生们能进一步了解我的为人。
Already they must spy the cloven hoof, since with all your pretended eagerness for the family honour, you take a pleasure to degrade it in my person.” 或许他们已经看出了你的破绽，既然你这么看重家族的荣誉，你又为何要侮辱我呢？”
“This is all very fine,” says my lord; “but to us who know you of old, you must be sure it signifies nothing. “你说的一切听起来都不错，”爵爷说道，“但你一定明白，对于非常了解你的过去的我们来说，这一切不会起任何作用。
You take that alternative out of which you think that you can make the most. 你决定留下来无非是想得到更多的好处。
Take it, if you can, in silence; it will serve you better in the long run, you may believe me, than this ostentation of ingratitude.” 那你就拿上这些钱，别说话，从长远上看，这总比你在大庭广众之下显露自己的忘恩负义要好得多。”
“Oh, gratitude, my lord!” cries the Master, with a mounting intonation and his forefinger very conspicuously lifted up. “哦，爵爷，那可太感激了！”大少爷举起食指，提高了声调说，
“Be at rest: it will not fail you. “放心好了，不会让你失望的。
It now remains that I should salute these gentlemen whom we have wearied with our family affairs.” 另外我得向几位先生致歉，拿我们自己家的家务事来打扰各位，抱歉了！”
And he bowed to each in succession, settled his walking-sword, and took himself off, leaving every one amazed at his behaviour, and me not less so at my lord’s. 他逐一向各位名流鞠躬，整了整佩剑，扬长而去。在场的每个人都对他的举动感到惊讶，而我则是对爵爷的行为也感到同样诧异。
We were now to enter on a changed phase of this family division. 我们眼下进入了这个家庭纠纷的变化阶段。
The Master was by no manner of means so helpless as my lord supposed, having at his hand, and entirely devoted to his service, an excellent artist in all sorts of goldsmith work. 大少爷并没有像爵爷想象的那么无助，他身边有一个忠心耿耿的奴仆，对各种金匠手艺无一不通。
With my lord’s allowance, which was not so scanty as he had described it, the pair could support life; and all the earnings of Secundra Dass might be laid upon one side for any future purpose. 由于爵爷的仁慈，每周给予的生活费并不仅仅是他先前描述的那么少，足够他们主仆俩生活之需，而塞昆德拉·达斯的日常收入可能都存起来以备将来之需。
That this was done, I have no doubt. 这些事情我确信无疑。
It was in all likelihood the Master’s design to gather a sufficiency, and then proceed in quest of that treasure which he had buried long before among the mountains; to which, if he had confined himself, he would have been more happily inspired. 很可能是大少爷想积蓄点儿盘缠，将来到那深山老林里把以前埋藏起来的财宝取出来；如果他乐天知命，别无旁骛，他本可以更快乐，更受到鼓舞。
But unfortunately for himself and all of us, he took counsel of his anger. 但不幸的是，他时常发火。
The public disgrace of his arrival—which I sometimes wonder he could manage to survive—rankled in his bones; he was in that humour when a man—in the words of the old adage—will cut off his nose to spite his face; and he must make himself a public spectacle in the hopes that some of the disgrace might spatter on my lord. 人们视他的到来为一种耻辱，他对此怨恨入骨，有时我在想他是否能生存下去，用一句老话说，他现在是因为要一时泄愤而伤害自己，为了赌一口气把自己弄得声名扫地。他目的恐怕是故意把自己搞得臭名远扬，这样就自然而然地殃及池鱼，损毁爵爷的名声。
He chose, in a poor quarter of the town, a lonely, small house of boards, overhung with some acacias. 他选了位于小镇穷人区的一间偏僻的小木板屋作为居住地，小屋旁边有几棵刺槐树。
It was furnished in front with a sort of hutch opening, like that of a dog’s kennel, but about as high as a table from the ground, in which the poor man that built it had formerly displayed some wares; and it was this which took the Master’s fancy and possibly suggested his proceedings. 前面有一个笼口，像是个狗屋，但有一张餐桌那么高，当初那个穷主人建这个笼子可能是用来摆摊，这一切却正合大少爷的心意，大概与他的行为很是符合。
It appears, on board the pirate ship he had acquired some quickness with the needle—enough, at least, to play the part of tailor in the public eye; which was all that was required by the nature of his vengeance. 看起来他在海盗船上学了些针线活，至少足够他在众人面前扮演裁缝的角色，这也是他复仇心的表现。
A placard was hung above the hutch, bearing these words in something of the following disposition: 他在笼子上方悬挂着一块招牌，上面写着：
James Durie, 詹姆斯·迪里，
Formerly Master of Ballantrae. 原巴伦特雷大少爷。
Clothes Neatly Clouted. 缝补旧衣如翻新。
Secundra Dass, 塞昆德拉·达斯，
Decayed Gentleman of India. 没落的印度绅士。
Fine Goldsmith Work. 金工巧匠。
Underneath this, when he had a job, my gentleman sat withinside tailor-wise and busily stitching. 有活的时候，大少爷在屋子里像个裁缝一样忙着做他的针线活。
I say, when he had a job; but such customers as came were rather for Secundra, and the Master’s sewing would be more in the manner of Penelope’s. 当然我是说当他有活的时候；但是到这里来的顾客大多是来找塞昆德拉·达斯的。大少爷的缝纫只是装装样子而已。
He could never have designed to gain even butter to his bread by such a means of livelihood: enough for him that there was the name of Durie dragged in the dirt on the placard, and the sometime heir of that proud family set up cross-legged in public for a reproach upon his brother’s meanness. 如果大少爷想靠他的针线活维持生计的话，他恐怕连块黄油都买不出来。他装样子的真正用意是冲着那块招牌上的迪里家族的姓氏，想要玷污它，大少爷有时候还以骄傲的家族继承人的身份在公众面前跷着二郎腿来谴责爵爷的吝啬无情。
And in so far his device succeeded that there was murmuring in the town and a party formed highly inimical to my lord. 就这一点而言，他的策略成功了，小镇里议论纷纷，甚而形成了一个与爵爷敌对的组织。
My lord’s favour with the Governor laid him more open on the other side; my lady (who was never so well received in the colony) met with painful innuendoes; in a party of women, where it would be the topic most natural to introduce, she was almost debarred from the naming of needle-work; and I have seen her return with a flushed countenance and vow that she would go abroad no more. 爵爷与州长的亲密关系也成为众人议论的话题；而太太（本来在殖民地就不受欢迎），也遭到了非议；女人聚在一起无非是说些针线活计之类的事情，但太太却并不擅长针线。有一次我看见她红着脸回到家里，并且发誓以后再也不出门了。
In the meanwhile my lord dwelled in his decent mansion, immersed in farming; a popular man with his intimates, and careless or unconscious of the rest. 此时的爵爷生活在舒适的府邸里，专心农事，热情好客，对其他的事情却充耳不闻。
He laid on flesh; had a bright, busy face; even the heat seemed to prosper with him; and my lady—in despite of her own annoyances—daily blessed Heaven her father should have left her such a paradise. 一段时间下来，他的身体渐渐发福，虽忙碌却容光焕发，甚至身上散发的热量好像也多了起来；虽然太太也有自己的烦恼，但她很感激上帝让父亲给她留下了这么好的生活。
She had looked on from a window upon the Master’s humiliation; and from that hour appeared to feel at ease. 当看到窗外大少爷的落魄样子，她会越发感觉到自己生活的美好。
I was not so sure myself; as time went on, there seemed to me a something not quite wholesome in my lord’s condition. 尽管不是很确定，但随着时间的流逝，我感觉到爵爷的状态有些不对。
Happy he was, beyond a doubt, but the grounds of this felicity were wont; even in the bosom of his family he brooded with manifest delight upon some private thought; and I conceived at last the suspicion (quite unworthy of us both) that he kept a mistress somewhere in the town. 毋庸置疑，他表面上快快乐乐，但这快乐的缘由却令人捉摸不透；即便是在家人面前他的快乐中似乎也藏着不为人知的秘密。我最后怀疑他是不是在镇上某个地方找了个情妇（这种怀疑对我俩都很不值）。
Yet he went little abroad, and his day was very fully occupied; indeed, there was but a single period, and that pretty early in the morning, while Mr. Alexander was at his lesson-book, of which I was not certain of the disposition. 然而他几乎不出门，整天忙忙碌碌的。实际上只有清晨那一会儿，亚历山大少爷上课的时候，我不知道他的行踪。
It should be borne in mind, in the defence of that which I now did, that I was always in some fear my lord was not quite justly in his reason; and with our enemy sitting so still in the same town with us, I did well to be upon my guard. 我心生疑虑，害怕爵爷并不是那样理智；毕竟我们的敌人就住在同一个镇上，我要做好防卫。
Accordingly I made a pretext, had the hour changed at which I taught Mr. Alexander the foundation of cyphering and the mathematic, and set myself instead to dog my master’s footsteps. 因此，我找了个借口把辅导亚历山大少爷算术基础和数学的时间作了变动，这样我就能对爵爷进行跟踪以了解事情的原委。
Every morning, fair or foul, he took his gold-headed cane, set his hat on the back of his head—a recent habitude, which I thought to indicate a burning brow—and betook himself to make a certain circuit. 每天早上，不管天气如何，爵爷总是拿着那根金头手杖，帽子搭在后脑勺上——这是最近才养成的习惯，我觉得他这样做是为了显露那两道漂亮的浓眉，然后出去走上一圈。
At the first his way was among pleasant trees and beside a graveyard, where he would sit awhile, if the day were fine, in meditation. 开始他是在浓郁的树丛中散步，如果赶上好天气，他会在墓地旁坐上一会儿，沉思片刻。
Presently the path turned down to the waterside, and came back along the harbour-front and past the Master’s booth. 之后他转到水边，绕道港口前面经过大少爷的货摊。
As he approached this second part of his circuit, my Lord Durrisdeer began to pace more leisurely, like a man delighted with the air and scene; and before the booth, half-way between that and the water’s edge, would pause a little, leaning on his staff. 路过此地时，达里斯迪尔爵爷就会显得格外地悠闲，仿佛全身心陶醉在如画的山水之中。爵爷总会倚着手杖在小木屋和海边中间停留一小会儿。
It was the hour when the Master sate within upon his board and plied his needle. 此时此刻，屋中的大少爷淡然坐在案几前忙于针线活。
So these two brothers would gaze upon each other with hard faces; and then my lord move on again, smiling to himself. 因此，两兄弟经常面色阴沉四目相对；之后爵爷便满心欢喜地继续前行。
It was but twice that I must stoop to that ungrateful necessity of playing spy. 有那么两次我偷偷跟踪了爵爷。
I was then certain of my lord’s purpose in his rambles and of the secret source of his delight. 那之后，我才对爵爷散步的目的和快乐的秘密恍然大悟。
Here was his mistress: it was hatred and not love that gave him healthful colours. 这就是他的情妇的秘密：他那红润的面色不是由于爱情的滋润，而是由于愤怒的宣泄。
Some moralists might have been relieved by the discovery; I confess that I was dismayed. 一些道德家了解这一切后可能会如释重负，而我承认我感到惊讶。
I found this situation of two brethren not only odious in itself, but big with possibilities of further evil; and I made it my practice, in so far as many occupations would allow, to go by a shorter path and be secretly present at their meeting. 我觉得这两兄弟的情形不仅令人憎恶，而且可能酿成大祸；我一有空闲便会抄近路，在他们相遇的地方偷偷观察他们。
Coming down one day a little late, after I had been near a week prevented, I was struck with surprise to find a new development. 有那么一个礼拜我有事儿没去，接下来的一天我去得稍微晚了点儿，我惊讶地发现情况有了进展。
I should say there was a bench against the Master’s house, where customers might sit to parley with the shopman; and here I found my lord seated, nursing his cane and looking pleasantly forth upon the bay. 我应该说过大少爷的木屋旁边有条凳子，客人们可以坐在这里谈生意，此时爵爷坐在凳子上，一边玩弄着手中的手杖，一边悠闲自得地观赏着海滨的风光。
Not three feet from him sate the Master, stitching. 大少爷坐在离爵爷不到三英尺的地方，做着针线活。
Neither spoke; nor (in this new situation) did my lord so much as cut a glance upon his enemy. 两人谁也没言语；（在这种新情境下）爵爷对自己的死敌连瞥一眼都没有。
He tasted his neighbourhood, I must suppose, less indirectly in the bare proximity of person; and, without doubt, drank deep of hateful pleasures. 我个人觉得爵爷是在有意欣赏着旁边这个人的苦难，毫无疑问，他自己深陷在宣泄仇恨的快乐中。
He had no sooner come away than I openly joined him. 在他起身的时候我凑上前。
“My lord, my lord,” said I, “this is no manner of behaviour.” 爵爷啊，爵爷，”我说道，“这样做似乎不合适啊。”
“I grow fat upon it,” he replied; and not merely the words, which were strange enough, but the whole character of his expression, shocked me. “我乐此不疲呢。”他回答道。不仅仅是他的话，连他的表情都是那么怪异，这使我很震惊。
“I warn you, my lord, against this indulgency of evil feeling,” said I. “爵爷，我提醒您，要远离这种邪恶放纵的感觉。”我说，
“I know not to which it is more perilous, the soul or the reason; but you go the way to murder both.” “我也不清楚您的灵魂和理智到底哪个处于更加岌岌可危的状态，但这样下去你这两方面都会受到伤害。”
“You cannot understand,” said he. “你不会理解我的。”他说道，
“You had never such mountains of bitterness upon your heart.” “你的内心从来没有经历过这样的苦楚。”
“And if it were no more,” I added, “you will surely goad the man to some extremity.” “如果仅此而已，”我接道，“您肯定会将他逼入绝境的。”
“To the contrary; I am breaking his spirit,” says my lord. “恰恰相反，我要摧毁他的灵魂。”爵爷说道。
Every morning for hard upon a week my lord took his same place upon the bench. 差不多一个礼拜，爵爷每天早上都坐在那条板凳上。
It was a pleasant place, under the green acacias, with a sight upon the bay and shipping, and a sound (from some way off) of marines singing at their employ. 这地方风景着实不错，在青青的刺槐树下可以看到海岸和船舶，（远处）还会时不时传来水手的劳动号子。
Here the two sate without speech or any external movement, beyond that of the needle or the Master biting off a thread, for he still clung to his pretence of industry; and here I made a point to join them, wondering at myself and my companions. 兄弟俩坐在这里无言以对，也没有任何其他明显动作，除了大少爷仍然装出一副忙碌的样子，埋头于他的针线活，不时地咬断线头；我加入他们的行列，并且同时诧异于我自己以及这两兄弟的举动。
If any of my lord’s friends went by, he would hail them cheerfully, and cry out he was there to give some good advice to his brother, who was now (to his delight) grown quite industrious. 如果爵爷的朋友路过，爵爷肯定会高兴地跟他们打招呼，嚷着说在这里是给自己的兄弟一些意见，还要夸兄长现在已经变得非常勤劳（他对此感到很高兴）。
And even this the Master accepted with a steady countenance; what was in his mind, God knows, or perhaps Satan only. 而此时大少爷总是不动声色，恐怕只有上帝，或许撒旦才知道他心里到底是怎么想的。
All of a sudden, on a still day of what they call the Indian Summer, when the woods were changed into gold and pink and scarlet, the Master laid down his needle and burst into a fit of merriment. 在一个他们称为印第安夏天的日子里，森林变成了金黄色、淡红色以及猩红色，大少爷突然放下了手中的针线，变得欣喜若狂。
I think he must have been preparing it a long while in silence, for the note in itself was pretty naturally pitched; but breaking suddenly from so extreme a silence, and in circumstances so averse from mirth, it sounded ominously on my ear. 我想他肯定为此默默准备了很长时间，因为这一切本身是那么自然；但突然一切戛然停止恢复平静，周围的气氛顿时来了个大转变，我的耳畔似乎响起了不祥的警告。
“Henry,” said he, “I have for once made a false step, and for once you have had the wit to profit by it. “亨利，”他说，“我曾经走错了一步，也让你占了便宜。
The farce of the cobbler ends to-day; and I confess to you (with my compliments) that you have had the best of it. 今天就让这场闹剧结束吧，让我恭维你两句，我承认你成功了。
Blood will out; and you have certainly a choice idea of how to make yourself unpleasant.” 这也是实实在在的话；在怎样招人讨厌这方面你确实是高人一等。”
Never a word said my lord; it was just as though the Master had not broken silence. 爵爷一言未发，就如大少爷从没有打破那份平静一样。
“Come,” resumed the Master, “do not be sulky; it will spoil your attitude. ”嗨！”大少爷接着说，“别这么绷着脸，这会影响你的态度。
You can now afford (believe me) to be a little gracious; for I have not merely a defeat to accept. （相信我）你现在可以更和蔼点儿，因为我并不是向你认输。
I had meant to continue this performance till I had gathered enough money for a certain purpose; I confess ingenuously, I have not the courage. 我曾经打算在我赚够钱以前一直这样，但坦白地讲，我并没有勇气坚持下去。
You naturally desire my absence from this town; I have come round by another way to the same idea. 你自然是很希望我赶紧离开这个小镇，我也有这样的想法。
And I have a proposition to make; or, if your lordship prefers, a favour to ask.” 如果你允许的话，在这里我想有个请求。
“Ask it,” says my lord. “有什么话就说吧。”爵爷说道。
“You may have heard that I had once in this country a considerable treasure,” returned the Master; “it matters not whether or no—such is the fact; and I was obliged to bury it in a spot of which I have sufficient indications. “你可能听说过以前我在这个国家有一大笔财宝，”大少爷回答道，“不管你信或者不信——这都是个事实，而我在埋藏财宝的地方做了标记。
To the recovery of this, has my ambition now come down; and, as it is my own, you will not grudge it me.” 为了取回宝藏我打算重回故地。既然这是我自己的事情，你也没必要嫉妒我。”
“Go and get it,” says my lord. “去取你的宝藏吧。”爵爷说道，
“I make no opposition.” “我没有意见。”
“Yes,” said the Master; “but to do so, I must find men and carriage. “那好，”大少爷说道，“不过要这么做的话，我必须找几个助手和一些运输工具。
The way is long and rough, and the country infested with wild Indians. 路途漫漫且艰险，到处都是野蛮的印第安人。
Advance me only so much as shall be needful: either as a lump sum, in lieu of my allowance; or, if you prefer it, as a loan, which I shall repay on my return. 只要提前给我这些需要的东西就行了：就算是一次性支付我的生活费；或者，如果你愿意的话，也可以算是借给我的，等我回来的时候自然会还给你。
And then, if you so decide, you may have seen the last of me.” 如果你同意的话，这将是你最后一次见到我。”
My lord stared him steadily in the eyes; there was a hard smile upon his face, but he uttered nothing. 爵爷一动不动地盯着他；脸上露出勉强的笑容，但他仍然沉默不语。
“Henry,” said the Master, with a formidable quietness, and drawing at the same time somewhat back—“Henry, I had the honour to address you.” “亨利，”大少爷神情异常平静，身体往后倒退了几步说，“亨利，我很高兴能跟你谈话。”
“Let us be stepping homeward,” says my lord to me, who was plucking at his sleeve; and with that he rose, stretched himself, settled his hat, and still without a syllable of response, began to walk steadily along the shore. “我们回去吧。”爵爷对正拉他袖口的我我说道，并站起身，伸了个懒腰，整理了下帽子，始终没有回复大少爷一个字，就沿着河岸坚定地走开了。
I hesitated awhile between the two brothers, so serious a climax did we seem to have reached. 我在兄弟俩之间犹豫了一会儿，事情竟到了如此严峻的地步。
