But the Master had resumed his occupation, his eyes lowered, his hand seemingly as deft as ever; and I decided to pursue my lord. 然而大少爷继续低下眼皮做他的活计，手一如既往的灵活，于是我决计去追赶爵爷。
“Are you mad?” “您疯了吗？”
I cried, so soon as I had overtook him. 我追上他后大喊，
“Would you cast away so fair an opportunity?” “您怎么能轻易放掉这么好的一个机会？”
“Is it possible you should still believe in him?” inquired my lord, almost with a sneer. “难道他这种人还值得你去相信吗？”爵爷讥笑道。
“I wish him forth of this town!” “我希望他离开这个地方。”
I cried. 我大声说道，
“I wish him anywhere and anyhow but as he is.” “只要不在这儿，随便在哪儿都行。”
“I have said my say,” returned my lord, “and you have said yours. “我已经把我想说的说完了，”爵爷回答道，“你也表达了自己的想法。
There let it rest.” 这事先放一放吧。”
But I was bent on dislodging the Master. 但我还是倾向于让大少爷远离我们。
That sight of him patiently returning to his needlework was more than my imagination could digest. 看到他耐心地继续做着针线活，我真是无法想象。
There was never a man made, and the Master the least of any, that could accept so long a series of insults. 从来没有一个男人，特别是像大少爷这样的人，能忍受这么长时间的侮辱。
The air smelt blood to me. 我在空气里嗅出了血腥味。
And I vowed there should be no neglect of mine if, through any chink of possibility, crime could be yet turned aside. 我发誓，如果有任何可能可以避免他们犯罪的话，我是绝对不会坐视不管的。
That same day, therefore, I came to my lord in his business room, where he sat upon some trivial occupation. 因此，那一天，我来到爵爷处理事务的房间，他正坐在那里处理一些琐事。
“My lord,” said I, “I have found a suitable investment for my small economies. “爵爷，”我说道，“我给我那微薄的积蓄找了个合适的投资方式。
But these are unhappily in Scotland; it will take some time to lift them, and the affair presses. 但不幸的是，钱存在苏格兰，取出来的话需要些时间，但时间紧迫。
Could your lordship see his way to advance me the amount against my note?” 我想爵爷是否能先借点儿钱给我，等我的钱到了马上奉还？”
He read me awhile with keen eyes. 他用敏锐的眼睛紧盯着我看了一会儿。
“I have never inquired into the state of your affairs, Mackellar,” says he. “麦凯勒，我从来不打听你的私事，”他说，
“Beyond the amount of your caution, you may not be worth a farthing, for what I know.” “但据我所知，你除了办事谨慎外没有一点儿存款。”
“I have been a long while in your service, and never told a lie, nor yet asked a favour for myself,” said I, “until to-day.” 我说：“爵爷，我伺候您很久了，从没说过谎，今天之前也没有请求您帮助过我什么。”
“A favour for the Master,” he returned, quietly. “给大少爷帮忙。”爵爷静静地回答，
“Do you take me for a fool, Mackellar? “你是拿我当傻子吗，麦凯勒？
Understand it once and for all, I treat this beast in my own way; fear nor favour shall not move me; and before I am hoodwinked, it will require a trickster less transparent than yourself. 你给我听明白了，对付那个畜生我自有办法，没有什么能让我动摇，别想用软的硬的那一套来糊弄我，想耍我的话，你还嫩了点儿。
I ask service, loyal service; not that you should make and mar behind my back, and steal my own money to defeat me.” 我雇佣你干活，按我的意思做事，不是让你在我背后玩把戏，拿我的钱去坏我的事。”
“My lord,” said I, “these are very unpardonable expressions.” “爵爷，”我说，“您说得太过分了。”
“Think once more, Mackellar,” he replied; “and you will see they fit the fact. “你再想想，麦凯勒，”他回答说，“你会发现这就是事实。
It is your own subterfuge that is unpardonable. 是你自己耍的花招让人无法原谅。
Deny (if you can) that you designed this money to evade my orders with, and I will ask your pardon freely. 只要保证这笔钱的用途不违背我的意思（如果你能的话），那么我随时可以向你道歉。
If you cannot, you must have the resolution to hear your conduct go by its own name.” 否则，你就做好思想准备，为自己的行为承担一切后果。”
“If you think I had any design but to save you—” I began. “难道您就不认为我做的一切是为了您好？”我开口道。
“Oh! my old friend,” said he, “you know very well what I think! “哦！我的老朋友，”爵爷说道，“你很是了解我的心思！
Here is my hand to you with all my heart; but of money, not one rap.” 我衷心地向你表示感谢，来握握手；但至于钱，那是一个子儿也没有。”
Defeated upon this side, I went straight to my room, wrote a letter, ran with it to the harbour, for I knew a ship was on the point of sailing; and came to the Master’s door a little before dusk. 这个计划失败后，我径直走回房间写了封信，然后匆忙赶到港口，因为我知道有一艘船即将起航。在天黑之前，我去找到了大少爷。
Entering without the form of any knock, I found him sitting with his Indian at a simple meal of maize porridge with some milk. 我没有敲门便直接走进了木屋，大少爷正跟那个印度人一起喝着简单的玉米粥，还有少许牛奶。
The house within was clean and poor; only a few books upon a shelf distinguished it, and (in one corner) Secundra’s little bench. 屋子里简陋而整洁，只有小书架上搁着的几本书才显出些许不俗，塞昆德拉的小板凳则摆在屋子的一角。
“Mr. Bally,” said I, “I have near five hundred pounds laid by in Scotland, the economies of a hard life. “巴利先生，”我说道，“我在苏格兰差不多有五百镑，是我清贫一生的所有积蓄。
A letter goes by yon ship to have it lifted. 我已经在那边船上送了封信，准备把钱取出来。
Have so much patience till the return ship comes in, and it is all yours, upon the same condition you offered to my lord this morning.” 请您耐心等待，等船回来的时候，那些钱就全都是您的，条件就是您早上对爵爷的那些许诺。”
He rose from the table, came forward, took me by the shoulders, and looked me in the face, smiling. 他从餐桌上站起来，走到我跟前，抓住我的肩膀，看着我的脸微笑。
“And yet you are very fond of money!” said he. “你对钱财那么爱惜！”他说道，
“And yet you love money beyond all things else, except my brother!” “但对你来说，我的弟弟比钱更重要！”
“I fear old age and poverty,” said I, “which is another matter.” “我攒钱是为了养老防穷，”我说道，“这个完全是另一回事。”
“I will never quarrel for a name. “我才不会为些虚名与人争执。
Call it so,” he replied. 你想怎么说就怎么说吧，”大少爷回答道，
“Ah! “噢！
Mackellar, Mackellar, if this were done from any love to me, how gladly would I close upon your offer!” 麦凯勒啊，麦凯勒啊，如果你做这一切是出于对我的情谊，对你伸出的援手我该多么高兴！”
“And yet,” I eagerly answered—“I say it to my shame, but I cannot see you in this poor place without compunction. “不过，”我急切地说道，“看到您在这种寒酸的地方我真是良心不安呐，虽然这让我很羞愧。
It is not my single thought, nor my first; and yet it’s there! 我不是第一次也不止一次这么想，但它就是存在！
I would gladly see you delivered. 您能离开这儿我会感到很高兴。
I do not offer it in love, and far from that; but, as God judges me—and I wonder at it too!—quite without enmity.” 我这么做可不是出于什么情谊，绝对不是；但上帝作证——我自己也弄不清楚！——但至少没什么恶意。”
“Ah!” says he, still holding my shoulders, and now gently shaking me, “you think of me more than you suppose. “啊！”他仍然紧紧地抓着我的肩膀，轻轻地摇晃了几下，说道，“我在你心中的地位比你想的要高。
‘And I wonder at it too,’” he added, repeating my expression and, I suppose, something of my voice. ‘我自己也弄不清楚’。”他重复着我刚才的话，似乎也学着我刚才的腔调。
“You are an honest man, and for that cause I spare you.” “你是个老实人，就凭这一点我饶了你。”
“Spare me?” “饶了我？”
I cried. 我喊道。
“Spare you,” he repeated, letting me go and turning away. “对，饶了你。”他又重复了一遍，然后松开我，转过身去。
And then, fronting me once more. 过了一会儿，他又转身面对着我。
“You little know what I would do with it, Mackellar! “麦凯勒，你根本不知道我要用这笔钱做什么！
Did you think I had swallowed my defeat indeed? 你认为我就这样束手认输了吗？
Listen: my life has been a series of unmerited cast-backs. 听着：我这一辈子可真算是命途多舛。
That fool, Prince Charlie, mismanaged a most promising affair: there fell my first fortune. 那个傻瓜查利王子把一件非常有前景的事给搅黄了：这是我第一次倒霉。
In Paris I had my foot once more high upon the ladder: that time it was an accident; a letter came to the wrong hand, and I was bare again. 而在巴黎我本有机会平步青云，结果恰好出了意外，信寄错了地址，我再次倒了霉。
A third time, I found my opportunity; I built up a place for myself in India with an infinite patience; and then Clive came, my rajah was swallowed up, and I escaped out of the convulsion, like another AEneas, with Secundra Dass upon my back. 第三次，在印度又逮到一个好机会。我非常耐心地在印度逐渐获得了自己的地位，结果克莱夫来了，我的首领被吞并了，我在慌乱中侥幸逃生，像勇士埃涅阿斯一样带着塞昆德拉·达斯四处流浪。
Three times I have had my hand upon the highest station: and I am not yet three-and-forty. 我还不到43岁却已经有三次机会，差点儿能得到最高的地位。
I know the world as few men know it when they come to die—Court and camp, the East and the West; I know where to go, I see a thousand openings. 许多人活了一辈子也没有像我一样对这个世界了解得这么清楚——从王宫到军营，从东方到西方；我知道应该怎么走，在我面前有上千条道路可走。
I am now at the height of my resources, sound of health, of inordinate ambition. 现在正是我智谋超人、体力充沛、雄心勃勃的时候。
Well, all this I resign; I care not if I die, and the world never hear of me; I care only for one thing, and that I will have. 然而，我放弃所有一切，不在乎生死，不在乎是否会被世人铭记，我只对一样事情感兴趣，而且我很快会拥有它。
Mind yourself; lest, when the roof falls, you, too, should be crushed under the ruins.” 请你千万小心，免得房顶倒下来砸碎脑袋。”
As I came out of his house, all hope of intervention quite destroyed, I was aware of a stir on the harbour-side, and, raising my eyes, there was a great ship newly come to anchor. 我走出大少爷的木屋，所有原本想调和他们兄弟间关系的愿望都破灭了，港口那边传来一阵喧哗，举目望去，一条大船刚刚抛下锚。
It seems strange I could have looked upon her with so much indifference, for she brought death to the brothers of Durrisdeer. 这艘船给达里斯迪尔兄弟俩彻底带来了死亡通知书，可奇怪的是，我对它并没有多大感觉。
After all the desperate episodes of this contention, the insults, the opposing interests, the fraternal duel in the shrubbery, it was reserved for some poor devil in Grub Street, scribbling for his dinner, and not caring what he scribbled, to cast a spell across four thousand miles of the salt sea, and send forth both these brothers into savage and wintry deserts, there to die. 在经过相互争辩、彼此侮辱、利益对立以及灌木丛里的生死决斗这些令人绝望的情节后，还是让伦敦格拉布街上穷困潦倒的墨客越过四千里的盐海施下咒语，把这俩兄弟送到寒冷的蛮横之地去处死吧。这些墨客为了吃饭而写作，对自己写的东西毫不关心。
But such a thought was distant from my mind; and while all the provincials were fluttered about me by the unusual animation of their port, I passed throughout their midst on my return homeward, quite absorbed in the recollection of my visit and the Master’s speech. 但是当时我还没有想那么远；异常喧腾的港口吸引了不少出来看热闹的当地人，我在拥挤的人群中穿行，赶着回家，心里不断地想起刚刚拜访大少爷的场景以及他说过的话。
The same night there was brought to us from the ship a little packet of pamphlets. 当天晚上，那艘船送来了一个装着很多小册子的包裹。
The next day my lord was under engagement to go with the Governor upon some party of pleasure; the time was nearly due, and I left him for a moment alone in his room and skimming through the pamphlets. 第二天爵爷应邀与州长一起参加宴会。时间紧迫，我就走了出去，让他一个人在屋里浏览那些小册子。
When I returned, his head had fallen upon the table, his arms lying abroad amongst the crumpled papers. 当我返回的时候，他的头栽在桌子上，手臂摊开压在揉皱了的纸上。
“My lord, my lord!” “爵爷，爵爷！”
I cried as I ran forward, for I supposed he was in some fit. 我边喊边朝他跑去，以为他是突发某种疾病。
He sprang up like a figure upon wires, his countenance deformed with fury, so that in a strange place I should scarce have known him. 他像个提线木偶一般突然跳起来，脸因为愤怒而抽搐变形，要是换个地方，我简直要认不出他来了。
His hand at the same time flew above his head, as though to strike me down. 他的手举过头顶，似乎想要将我击倒。
“Leave me alone!” he screeched, and I fled, as fast as my shaking legs would bear me, for my lady. “离我远点儿！”他尖叫道。我拖着两条颤抖的双腿赶忙往外跑，去找太太。
She, too, lost no time; but when we returned, he had the door locked within, and only cried to us from the other side to leave him be. 太太没有任何耽搁就跟我往爵爷房间走去；但是当我们到达的时候，爵爷已经从里面把门反锁上了，隔着门大吼着让我们离他远点儿。
We looked in each other’s faces, very white—each supposing the blow had come at last. 我和太太面面相觑，脸色苍白——我们俩都认为预料中的灾祸降临了。
“I will write to the Governor to excuse him,” says she. “我得写信给州长替爵爷致歉，说明他不能参加宴会了。”太太说道，
“We must keep our strong friends.” “这么强势的朋友我们可不能得罪了。”
But when she took up the pen, it flew out of her fingers. 可当她提起笔时，却怎么都拿不住。
“I cannot write,” said she. “我写不了。”她说道，
“Can you?” “你来吧。”
“I will make a shift, my lady,” said I. “我尽力而为吧，太太。”我回答道。
She looked over me as I wrote. 我写信的时候她一直盯着我。
“That will do,” she said, when I had done. 当信终于写完后，她说道：“这样就可以了。
“Thank God, Mackellar, I have you to lean upon! 谢天谢地，麦凯勒，我还可以指望你！
But what can it be now? 可现在这究竟是怎么回事呢？
What, what can it be?” 这一切到底怎么了？”
In my own mind, I believed there was no explanation possible, and none required; it was my fear that the man’s madness had now simply burst forth its way, like the long-smothered flames of a volcano; but to this (in mere mercy to my lady) I durst not give expression. 在我看来，这种事没法解释，也不需要解释。我担心爵爷的疯魔又犯了，就像长期压抑的火山一下爆发出来一样，然而关于这些（出于对太太的怜悯），我并没有说出口。
“It is more to the purpose to consider our own behaviour,” said I. “我想我们最好考虑一下我们该做点儿什么。”我说道，
“Must we leave him there alone?” “难道就这样对他不管不顾？”
“I do not dare disturb him,” she replied. “我可不敢去打扰他。”太太回答道，
“Nature may know best; it may be Nature that cries to be alone; and we grope in the dark. “也许是天意；也许是天意让他独处，我们只能在黑暗中摸索。
Oh yes, I would leave him as he is.” 我看我们还是随他去吧。”
“I will, then, despatch this letter, my lady, and return here, if you please, to sit with you,” said I. “太太，那我想这就去送这封信，如果你愿意的话，等我回来陪您守在这儿。”我说道。
“Pray do,” cries my lady. “去吧。”太太说道。
All afternoon we sat together, mostly in silence, watching my lord’s door. 整个下午我们几乎都默默地坐在那里，望着爵爷的门。
My own mind was busy with the scene that had just passed, and its singular resemblance to my vision. 刚才的情景在我脑中不断闪现，与我以前看到的何其相似。
I must say a word upon this, for the story has gone abroad with great exaggeration, and I have even seen it printed, and my own name referred to for particulars. 在这里我不得不提一下，这个故事经过演绎已经传到了国外，我也看过出版发行的文字，一些细节还提及我的名字。
So much was the same: here was my lord in a room, with his head upon the table, and when he raised his face, it wore such an expression as distressed me to the soul. 这部分是这样描写的：爵爷在屋里，头枕在桌子上，当他抬起头时，脸上写满了令我痛苦万分的表情。
But the room was different, my lord’s attitude at the table not at all the same, and his face, when he disclosed it, expressed a painful degree of fury instead of that haunting despair which had always (except once, already referred to) characterised it in the vision. 但是事实上，房间里的情景与这些描写不同，爵爷伏在桌上的姿势不尽相同，他露出表情时显现的是那种痛苦不堪的愤怒，而不是我经常（除了上述已经提及的一次）见到的绝望神色。
There is the whole truth at last before the public; and if the differences be great, the coincidence was yet enough to fill me with uneasiness. 这就是全部真相。如果与事实相差太远的话，这种巧合也足以让我焦躁不安。
All afternoon, as I say, I sat and pondered upon this quite to myself; for my lady had trouble of her own, and it was my last thought to vex her with fancies. 整个下午，我坐在那里苦想冥思；太太有她自己的烦恼，我不想用自己的胡思乱想去烦她。
About the midst of our time of waiting, she conceived an ingenious scheme, had Mr. Alexander fetched, and bid him knock at his father’s door. 就在我们苦苦等待的时候，她突发奇想，把亚历山大少爷叫了过来，让他去敲他爸爸的门。
My lord sent the boy about his business, but without the least violence, whether of manner or expression; so that I began to entertain a hope the fit was over. 爵爷打发孩子去干活，但是不论举止还是言语，都不带一丝的烦躁；因此我开始暗自希望爵爷的疯魔已经过去了。
At last, as the night fell and I was lighting a lamp that stood there trimmed, the door opened and my lord stood within upon the threshold. 最后，夜幕降临，我点上了灯，拨了拨灯芯，此时门突然开了，爵爷站在门口。
The light was not so strong that we could read his countenance; when he spoke, methought his voice a little altered but yet perfectly steady. 灯光太暗我们看不清他的表情，他说话的时候虽然有些改变，但还算是平稳。
“Mackellar,” said he, “carry this note to its destination with your own hand. “麦凯勒，”他说道，“你亲自把这封信送到目的地。
It is highly private. 这是绝密。
Find the person alone when you deliver it.” 一定要亲自交到收信人手里。”
“Henry,” says my lady, “you are not ill?” “亨利，”夫人问道，“你没生病吧？”
“No, no,” says be, querulously, “I am occupied. “没有，没有，”爵爷愠怒地说道，“我很忙。
Not at all; I am only occupied. 我没病，我只是有点儿忙罢了。
It is a singular thing a man must be supposed to be ill when he has any business! 难道男人有点儿事情就是生病了吗！
Send me supper to this room, and a basket of wine: I expect the visit of a friend. 把晚饭送到我房间来，另加一壶酒，有个朋友要来访。
Otherwise I am not to be disturbed.” 就不要用其他的事情来打搅我了。”
And with that he once more shut himself in. 说完这些话，他又把自己关进屋子里。
The note was addressed to one Captain Harris, at a tavern on the portside. 那封信是送给码头附近的一家酒馆里一个叫哈里斯船长的人。
I knew Harris (by reputation) for a dangerous adventurer, highly suspected of piracy in the past, and now following the rude business of an Indian trader. 我听闻哈里斯是个亡命之徒，以前干过海盗，现在又跟一个印第安商人做些不法勾当。
What my lord should have to say to him, or he to my lord, it passed my imagination to conceive: or yet how my lord had heard of him, unless by a disgraceful trial from which the man was recently escaped. 爵爷怎么会跟他有联系呢，他跟爵爷又有何干系，我实在想不出这其中的奥妙，再说爵爷又是怎么结识他的呢？除非是他近期受审的时候突然畏罪潜逃才让爵爷对他有所耳闻。
Altogether I went upon the errand with reluctance, and from the little I saw of the captain, returned from it with sorrow. 总之我跑这趟差事百般无奈、很不情愿，看到船长本人后，我感到很难过。
I found him in a foul-smelling chamber, sitting by a guttering candle and an empty bottle; he had the remains of a military carriage, or rather perhaps it was an affectation, for his manners were low. 我在一个臭气熏天的小屋里找到了哈里斯船长，他坐在忽明忽暗的烛光下，旁边立着一个空酒瓶；他身上还保留着些许军人气质，或者根本就是装模作样，因为他的行为极为卑劣。
“Tell my lord, with my service, that I will wait upon his lordship in the inside of half an hour,” says he, when he had read the note; and then had the servility, pointing to his empty bottle, to propose that I should buy him liquor. 有劳你替我告诉爵爷，我将在半小时内前去拜访。”当他看完信后，说道。然后他卑微地指了指他的空酒瓶，示意我给他买些酒。
Although I returned with my best speed, the Captain followed close upon my heels, and he stayed late into the night. 虽然我以最快的速度往回赶，船长仍能紧跟在后面，他跟爵爷一直呆到深夜。
The cock was crowing a second time when I saw (from my chamber window) my lord lighting him to the gate, both men very much affected with their potations, and sometimes leaning one upon the other to confabulate. 雄鸡二次报晓的时候，我（从我的房间窗户）看到爵爷提着灯将船长送到门外，两人都有点儿醉醺醺的，还不时交头接耳聊上几句。
Yet the next morning my lord was abroad again early with a hundred pounds of money in his pocket. 第二天一早，爵爷兜里揣着一百英镑又出门去了。
I never supposed that he returned with it; and yet I was quite sure it did not find its way to the Master, for I lingered all morning within view of the booth. 我估计他一个子儿也带不回来，我也确定这笔钱肯定到不了大少爷手里，因为我在大少爷那间木屋附近转悠了一早上。
That was the last time my Lord Durrisdeer passed his own enclosure till we left New York; he walked in his barn, or sat and talked with his family, all much as usual; but the town saw nothing of him, and his daily visits to the Master seemed forgotten. 那是我们离开纽约前爵爷最后一次走出府邸，他像往常一样时而漫步到仓房里去，时而坐在屋里跟家人聊天，只不过镇里的人再也没见到过爵爷，而每天去大少爷门口的习惯似乎也被忘掉了。
Nor yet did Harris reappear; or not until the end. 哈里斯也没再来过；或许只是还没到时候。
I was now much oppressed with a sense of the mysteries in which we had begun to move. 现在我心里总觉得压抑，因为整件事情正向一个不可知的方向发展。
It was plain, if only from his change of habitude, my lord had something on his mind of a grave nature; but what it was, whence it sprang, or why he should now keep the house and garden, I could make no guess at. 单从爵爷生活习惯上的改变就不难看出，他心里装着一些非常严重的事情，但到底是什么，从何而起，或者他为什么一直闷在屋子和花园里，我根本无从知晓。
It was clear, even to probation, the pamphlets had some share in this revolution; I read all I could find, and they were all extremely insignificant, and of the usual kind of party scurrility; even to a high politician, I could spy out no particular matter of offence, and my lord was a man rather indifferent on public questions. 很显然，爵爷的巨大变化与那些小册子有关。我把我能找到的传单看了个遍，发现里面几乎都是些琐事，无非是些党派间相互攻击之类的污言秽语；在我看来，即便是政界大佬对于这些传单都会毫不在意，更何况爵爷是一个对这些公众问题毫不感兴趣的人。
The truth is, the pamphlet which was the spring of this affair, lay all the time on my lord’s bosom. 但事实是，这些小册子成了这一系列事情的起源，时刻萦绕在爵爷的心间。
There it was that I found it at last, after he was dead, in the midst of the north wilderness: in such a place, in such dismal circumstances, I was to read for the first time these idle, lying words of a Whig pamphleteer declaiming against indulgency to Jacobites:- “Another notorious Rebel, the M-r of B-e, is to have his Title restored,” the passage ran. 当爵爷最后被抛尸北部荒野的时候，在那种阴沉凄凉的地方和场合，我第一次看到了那些荒诞不经的闲言碎语，都是辉格党人攻击詹姆斯二世子孙的保皇派言论。文章这样写道：“另一个臭名昭著的叛乱分子就是企图恢复自己爵位的巴伦特雷少爷。
“This Business has been long in hand, since he rendered some very disgraceful Services in Scotland and France. 这件事情由来已久，因为他在苏格兰和法国做了些龌龊的事情。
His Brother, L-D D-R, is known to be no better than himself in Inclination; and the supposed Heir, who is now to be set aside, was bred up in the most detestable Principles. 而他的弟弟，达里斯迪尔爵爷性情比巴伦特雷少爷好不到哪儿去；原先准备继承爵位，后来又被废黜的巴兰特拉少爷生来就是在这样可憎的信念教条下长大成人的。
In the old Phrase, it is SIX OF THE ONE AND HALF A DOZEN OF THE OTHER; but the Favour of such a Reposition is too extreme to be passed over.” 用句古话说，他兄弟俩是半斤八两。但是巴伦特雷少爷重新恢复爵位的事太过分，怎么能行。”
A man in his right wits could not have cared two straws for a tale so manifestly false; that Government should ever entertain the notion, was inconceivable to any reasoning creature, unless possibly the fool that penned it; and my lord, though never brilliant, was ever remarkable for sense. 凡是智力正常的人都不会在意错误如此明显的故事；政府居然插手此事，任何有理智的人都不会接受，除非是那个捏造这些传言的傻子；而爵爷本身虽然不是绝顶聪明，但素以思维理性为人所称赞。
That he should credit such a rodomontade, and carry the pamphlet on his bosom and the words in his heart, is the clear proof of the man’s lunacy. 但他对这样的胡言乱语竟然深信不疑，他深信其中的内容，把小册子揣进怀里，把内容铭记在心头，这一切很明确地表明他已精神失常。
Doubtless the mere mention of Mr. Alexander, and the threat directly held out against the child’s succession, precipitated that which had so long impended. 显然小册子里提到了亚历山大少爷，并威吓声称反对其世袭爵位，这加深了长期聚集在他心头的忧思。
Or else my master had been truly mad for a long time, and we were too dull or too much used to him, and did not perceive the extent of his infirmity. 或者，爵爷已经精神错乱很长时间，但因为我们太愚笨或跟他过于熟悉，没有察觉到他病情的严重性。
About a week after the day of the pamphlets I was late upon the harbour-side, and took a turn towards the Master’s, as I often did. 在收到那些小册子后大约一周，我在海边待到很晚才像往常一样转身向大少爷的小屋走去。
The door opened, a flood of light came forth upon the road, and I beheld a man taking his departure with friendly salutations. 屋门敞开着，一束光照在路上，我看见一个人正彬彬有礼地告别。
I cannot say how singularly I was shaken to recognise the adventurer Harris. 当我认出这个是哈里斯船长的时候，我大惊失色。
I could not but conclude it was the hand of my lord that had brought him there; and prolonged my walk in very serious and apprehensive thought. 我确信他是爵爷派过来的，于是我放慢了脚步，陷入沉思之中。
It was late when I came home, and there was my lord making up his portmanteau for a voyage. 当我到家的时候已经很晚了，爵爷正在为出远门打点行李。
“Why do you come so late?” he cried. “怎么回来得这么晚？”他高声喊道，
“We leave to-morrow for Albany, you and I together; and it is high time you were about your preparations.” “我们两人明天去奥尔巴尼，你也得抓紧时间准备准备。”
“For Albany, my lord?” “去奥尔巴尼，爵爷？”
I cried. 我喊出了声，
“And for what earthly purpose?” “到底是去那儿干什么啊？”
“Change of scene,” said he. “换个景色看看。”他说道。
And my lady, who appeared to have been weeping, gave me the signal to obey without more parley. 太太好像刚刚哭过，她示意我照办，不要回嘴。
She told me a little later (when we found occasion to exchange some words) that he had suddenly announced his intention after a visit from Captain Harris, and her best endeavours, whether to dissuade him from the journey, or to elicit some explanation of its purpose, had alike proved unavailing. 稍后（我俩找了个时机交谈了几句）她告诉我爵爷是去了哈里斯船长那里一趟后突然宣布这次旅行的，她无论是极力劝阻爵爷取消这次旅行，还是询问此行目的，都徒劳无功。
Chapter 11 第十一章
The Journey in the Wilderness. 涉足蛮荒
We made a prosperous voyage up that fine river of the Hudson, the weather grateful, the hills singularly beautified with the colours of the autumn. 我们沿着美丽的哈得孙河乘船旅行，一路上秋高气爽、山明水秀、秋色盎然。
At Albany we had our residence at an inn, where I was not so blind and my lord not so cunning but what I could see he had some design to hold me prisoner. 在奥尔巴尼我们找了家小旅馆住了下来，我不是瞎子，爵爷也并非狡诈无比，我能看出他想把我关在旅馆里不让我出去。
The work he found for me to do was not so pressing that we should transact it apart from necessary papers in the chamber of an inn; nor was it of such importance that I should be set upon as many as four or five scrolls of the same document. 他让我做的工作并不急，我们完全可以在旅馆房间里面写完必要的文件后再去做；同时工作也不是非常重要，根本不需要我把同一份文件誊写四五份。
I submitted in appearance; but I took private measures on my own side, and had the news of the town communicated to me daily by the politeness of our host. 我表面上没有异议。但暗地里我却有自己的一套做法，我每天从殷勤好客的老板那里打听镇里的动静。
In this way I received at last a piece of intelligence for which, I may say, I had been waiting. 就这样，我终于收到了一条我等待已久的消息。
Captain Harris (I was told) with “Mr. Mountain, the trader,” had gone by up the river in a boat. 哈里斯船长（据说）与商人芒廷先生乘船去了河的上游。
I would have feared the landlord’s eye, so strong the sense of some complicity upon my master’s part oppressed me. 我很害怕房东的眼神，爵爷与其他人共谋的想法折磨着我。
But I made out to say I had some knowledge of the Captain, although none of Mr. Mountain, and to inquire who else was of the party. 尽管对芒廷先生一无所知，我撒谎说我知道船长的事，以打听他们同行的还有谁。
My informant knew not; Mr. Mountain had come ashore upon some needful purchases; had gone round the town buying, drinking, and prating; and it seemed the party went upon some likely venture, for he had spoken much of great things he would do when he returned. 我并没有得到其同行人的信息，只知道芒廷先生是去采购必需品的。他在城里又是买东西又是吃饭、喝酒、吹牛皮，看起来这伙人像是要去冒险，因为他曾说等他回来了以后要做很多大事。
No more was known, for none of the rest had come ashore, and it seemed they were pressed for time to reach a certain spot before the snow should fall. 再没有其他信息，因为其他的人还没有上岸，看起来他们急着赶路，要在下雪前赶到某个地点去。
And sure enough, the next day, there fell a sprinkle even in Albany; but it passed as it came, and was but a reminder of what lay before us. 果然，第二天，连奥尔巴尼都下了场小雪。但是雪刚落地就化了，这只是提醒人们大雪即将到来。
I thought of it lightly then, knowing so little as I did of that inclement province: the retrospect is different; and I wonder at times if some of the horror of there events which I must now rehearse flowed not from the foul skies and savage winds to which we were exposed, and the agony of cold that we must suffer. 当时我对这地方了解不多，对这场小雪也没怎么在意，现在回想起来可就不同了；我有时怀疑那些骇人听闻的事件是不是恶劣天气、狂风和严寒造成的，当时，我们深受其苦。
The boat having passed by, I thought at first we should have left the town. 他们的船从这里经过，起初我还以为我们会动身离开小镇。
But no such matter. 但我们根本就没走。
My lord continued his stay in Albany where he had no ostensible affairs, and kept me by him, far from my due employment, and making a pretence of occupation. 爵爷继续呆在奥尔巴尼，无所事事却假装忙碌，他让我留在身边陪着他，这可不是我应该做的。
It is upon this passage I expect, and perhaps deserve, censure. 这段时间我受到责难，或许是我咎由自取。
I was not so dull but what I had my own thoughts. 我还没有笨到完全没有一点儿自己的想法。
I could not see the Master entrust himself into the hands of Harris, and not suspect some underhand contrivance. 我相信大少爷对哈里斯绝不是深信不疑，更不可能与其肝胆相照。
Harris bore a villainous reputation, and he had been tampered with in private by my lord; Mountain, the trader, proved, upon inquiry, to be another of the same kidney; the errand they were all gone upon being the recovery of ill-gotten treasures, offered in itself a very strong incentive to foul play; and the character of the country where they journeyed promised impunity to deeds of blood. 哈里斯声名狼藉，私下里听任爵爷的摆布；至于商人芒廷，打听后我知道他一样也不是什么好东西。他们奔着一大笔不义之财而去，这本身就容易使人产生歹意，更何况他们前去的那个国度对流血冲突根本没有法律惩罚。
Well: it is true I had all these thoughts and fears, and guesses of the Master’s fate. 好吧，我对大少爷的命运的确有些顾虑、担忧和猜测。
But you are to consider I was the same man that sought to dash him from the bulwarks of a ship in the mid-sea; the same that, a little before, very impiously but sincerely offered God a bargain, seeking to hire God to be my bravo. 但是那个想把他从船舷上踢到大海中的人也是我；同样，不久前，我认真但很不恭敬地跟上帝作了一笔交易，试图使上帝听我使唤。
It is true again that I had a good deal melted towards our enemy. 诚然，我对这个敌人的许多偏见和仇恨都消逝了。
But this I always thought of as a weakness of the flesh and even culpable; my mind remaining steady and quite bent against him. 但我总觉得这是血肉之躯的弱点使然，纵然这是不对的，而我内心深处对他的敌意却是一点儿没变。
True, yet again, that it was one thing to assume on my own shoulders the guilt and danger of a criminal attempt, and another to stand by and see my lord imperil and besmirch himself. 诚然，我身上总是有些罪恶感和谋杀未遂的恐慌，这是一回事，但看着爵爷即将身处险境、名声扫地却袖手旁观又是另外一回事。
But this was the very ground of my inaction. 然而这却是我不采取行动的理由。
For (should I anyway stir in the business) I might fail indeed to save the Master, but I could not miss to make a byword of my lord. 因为如果我在这件事情上做一点儿手脚，恐怕不仅救不了大少爷，还会遭到爵爷的怪罪。
Thus it was that I did nothing; and upon the same reasons, I am still strong to justify my course. 因此我什么也没做。基于同样的原因，我觉得自己这样做无可厚非。
We lived meanwhile in Albany, but though alone together in a strange place, had little traffic beyond formal salutations. 在这期间，我们孤零零地呆在奥尔巴尼这个陌生的地方，除了礼节性的寒暄外别无其他交往。
My lord had carried with him several introductions to chief people of the town and neighbourhood; others he had before encountered in New York: with this consequence, that he went much abroad, and I am sorry to say was altogether too convivial in his habits. 爵爷经人引荐结识了镇里及附近的头面人物，有的人他在纽约就已经遇见过了，因此他经常外出，自然而然养成了好吃好喝的习惯。
I was often in bed, but never asleep, when he returned; and there was scarce a night when he did not betray the influence of liquor. 当他回来时，我常常躺在床上难以入眠。他没有一晚上不是满身酒气回来的。
By day he would still lay upon me endless tasks, which he showed considerable ingenuity to fish up and renew, in the manner of Penelope’s web. 白天他仍会给我安排一大堆没完没了的任务，干完了又要我重新来一遍，就像是永远完不成的工作。
I never refused, as I say, for I was hired to do his bidding; but I took no pains to keep my penetration under a bushel, and would sometimes smile in his face. 对于这样的要求，我从不拒绝，就像我说的那样，我被雇佣就是要听从他的使唤，不过我也不总是装作无动于衷，有时冲他笑一笑。
“I think I must be the devil and you Michael Scott,” I said to him one day. “爵爷，看来您是把我当驴子推磨使啊。”一天，我对他说，
“I have bridged Tweed and split the Eildons; and now you set me to the rope of sand.” “尽让我做一些徒劳无功的事情，这简直是白白浪费时间。”
He looked at me with shining eyes, and looked away again, his jaw chewing, but without words. 他目光炯炯地看着我，又把头扭了过去，下颌动了动，但并没做声。
“Well, well, my lord,” said I, “your will is my pleasure. “好吧，好吧，爵爷，”我说道，“只要您愿意，我随时乐意效劳。
I will do this thing for the fourth time; but I would beg of you to invent another task against to-morrow, for by my troth, I am weary of this one.” 我会第四遍做这件事做，但请您明天想儿点别的活吧，我都快腻了。”
“You do not know what you are saying,” returned my lord, putting on his hat and turning his back to me. “你这是在说些什么。”爵爷回答道，戴上帽子，转过身去，
“It is a strange thing you should take a pleasure to annoy me. “你以惹怒我为乐，这真是件怪事。
A friend—but that is a different affair. 朋友嘛——那是另一回事。
It is a strange thing. 这真是件怪事。
I am a man that has had ill-fortune all my life through. 我这个人一生倒霉。
I am still surrounded by contrivances. 始终被人算计。
I am always treading in plots,” he burst out. 总是钻进别人的圈套。”他大声喊了起来，
“The whole world is banded against me.” “整个世界都联合起来跟我作对。”
“I would not talk wicked nonsense if I were you,” said I; “but I will tell you what I WOULD do—I would put my head in cold water, for you had more last night than you could carry.” “如果我是您的话，绝不会说这些没理智的话，”我说道，“但我要告诉您我会怎么做——我会把头伸到冷水里清醒一下，因为昨晚您又喝多了。”
“Do ye think that?” said he, with a manner of interest highly awakened. “是吗？”他突然来了很高的兴致，说道，
“Would that be good for me? “那样管用吗？
It’s a thing I never tried.” 我从来没有试过。”
“I mind the days when you had no call to try, and I wish, my lord, that they were back again,” said I. “我想您以前不需要这么做，我希望您能像以前一样。”我说道，
“But the plain truth is, if you continue to exceed, you will do yourself a mischief.” “但目前的状况是，如果您继续酗酒，最终只会害了自己。”
“I don’t appear to carry drink the way I used to,” said my lord. “现在我不像以前那样喝酒了。”爵爷说道，
“I get overtaken, Mackellar. “在喝酒这件事上，我是有点儿过头了，麦凯勒。
But I will be more upon my guard.” 但以后我会多加注意的。”
“That is what I would ask of you,” I replied. “这也是我对您的请求。”我回答道，
“You are to bear in mind that you are Mr. Alexander’s father: give the bairn a chance to carry his name with some responsibility.” “您应该在心中铭记您是亚历山大的父亲：也应该学着对他有一定的责任心。”
“Ay, ay,” said he. “是啊，是啊。”爵爷说道，
“Ye’re a very sensible man, Mackellar, and have been long in my employ. “你是个明白人，麦凯勒，你也服侍我多年了。
But I think, if you have nothing more to say to me I will be stepping. 但我想，如果你没有其他事情想对我说的话，我这就要走了。
If you have nothing more to say?” he added, with that burning, childish eagerness that was now so common with the man. 你还有什么想说的吗？”他脸上露出孩子气的急切神情，近来他总是这样。
“No, my lord, I have nothing more,” said I, dryly enough. “没了，爵爷。我没什么要说的了。”我无精打采地说道。
“Then I think I will be stepping,” says my lord, and stood and looked at me fidgeting with his hat, which he had taken off again. “那我想我要走了，”爵爷起身看着我，在手中把玩着又摘下的帽子，说道，
“I suppose you will have no errands? “我想你没有什么事了。
No? 是吧？
I am to meet Sir William Johnson, but I will be more upon my guard.” 我要去拜访威廉·约翰逊先生，但我会比以前更注意的。”
He was silent for a time, and then, smiling: “Do you call to mind a place, Mackellar—it’s a little below Engles—where the burn runs very deep under a wood of rowans. 他沉默了一会儿，然后笑着说：“麦凯勒，你还记得一个地方吗？——它就在恩格里斯下面一点点，有一片花楸，花楸下有一条深溪流过。
I mind being there when I was a lad—dear, it comes over me like an old song! 我记得我小时候常去那玩，现在回想起来就像一首老歌！
—I was after the fishing, and I made a bonny cast. 我在那里捕鱼，每次都会捕到很多。
Eh, but I was happy. 哎，当时的我是多么快活。
I wonder, Mackellar, why I am never happy now?” 麦凯勒，我在想为什么我现在快乐不起来呢？”
“My lord,” said I, “if you would drink with more moderation you would have the better chance. “爵爷，”我说道，“如果您喝酒时多一点儿节制的话，您就会更容易快乐起来。
It is an old byword that the bottle is a false consoler.” 有句俗话说得好，举杯消愁愁更愁。”
“No doubt,” said he, “no doubt. “对，”他说道，“对。
Well, I think I will be going.” 我想我该动身了。”
“Good-morning, my lord,” said I. “早安，爵爷。”我说道。
“Good-morning, good-morning,” said he, and so got himself at last from the apartment. “早安，早安。”他回道，最终离开了客店。
I give that for a fair specimen of my lord in the morning; and I must have described my patron very ill if the reader does not perceive a notable falling off. 我提到这些主要是为了说明爵爷早上的精神状况，如果你没有察觉到爵爷精神异常的话，你肯定以为我在诋毁他。
To behold the man thus fallen: to know him accepted among his companions for a poor, muddled toper, welcome (if he were welcome at all) for the bare consideration of his title; and to recall the virtues he had once displayed against such odds of fortune; was not this a thing at once to rage and to be humbled at? 看看他是如何没落的吧：他结识的人把他作为一个可怜的酒鬼，如果说人家还跟他交往的话，那完全是看在他所谓的爵位头衔的面子上。现在回想起他以前与命运斗争时展现的优点和美德，再看看现在的他，岂不可气，岂不悲哉？
In his cups, he was more expensive. 酒场上，他可真是豪爽。
I will give but the one scene, close upon the end, which is strongly marked upon my memory to this day, and at the time affected me almost with horror 现在我只说一个例子，至今我记忆犹新，那一次几乎将我吓昏，所以印象格外深刻。
I was in bed, lying there awake, when I heard him stumbling on the stair and singing. 我当时躺在床上，当我听到他唱着歌蹒跚上楼的时候，我依旧没有睡意。
My lord had no gift of music, his brother had all the graces of the family, so that when I say singing, you are to understand a manner of high, carolling utterance, which was truly neither speech nor song. 爵爷真是没有音乐细胞，而他哥哥却集整个家族的魅力于一身，所以我说他上楼时唱歌，你可以理解为我的恭维，其实纯粹是扯开嗓门瞎嚷嚷，说话不像说话，唱歌不像唱歌。
Something not unlike is to be heard upon the lips of children, ere they learn shame; from those of a man grown elderly, it had a strange effect. 他唱出的东西像是小孩在不知何为羞耻的年纪所唱的，而从这种老年人嘴里发出，那真是不知多么别扭。
He opened the door with noisy precaution; peered in, shading his candle; conceived me to slumber; entered, set his light upon the table, and took off his hat. 他噼里啪啦地推开门，往里看了看，遮住烛光；以为我睡着了，他便走了进来，把蜡烛放在桌子上，摘下帽子。
I saw him very plain; a high, feverish exultation appeared to boil in his veins, and he stood and smiled and smirked upon the candle. 我看他看得非常清楚，一副热血沸腾、欣喜若狂的样子，站在那里望着蜡烛一个劲地傻笑。
Presently he lifted up his arm, snapped his fingers, and fell to undress. 过了一会，他抬起胳膊，弹了弹手指，开始脱衣服。
As he did so, having once more forgot my presence, he took back to his singing; and now I could hear the words, which were those from the old song of the TWA CORBIES endlessly repeated: 他做这一切的时候，又似乎忘记了我的存在，又开始唱起他的歌。现在我听清了歌词，是一首叫《两只乌鸦》的老歌，他没完没了地重复那一句歌词：
“And over his banes when they are bare “不久他只剩下白骨，
The wind sall blaw for evermair!” 任风永远吹荡。”
I have said there was no music in the man. 我说过这个人没有一点儿音乐细胞。
His strains had no logical succession except in so far as they inclined a little to the minor mode; but they exercised a rude potency upon the feelings, and followed the words, and signified the feelings of the singer with barbaric fitness. 他的曲调中没有一点儿逻辑连贯性，仅有些许小调的味道，但那声音有一种粗犷的豪情，与歌词一道加深了唱歌者野性的情感。
He took it first in the time and manner of a rant; presently this ill-favoured gleefulness abated, he began to dwell upon the notes more feelingly, and sank at last into a degree of maudlin pathos that was to me scarce bearable. 开始时他大声唱着，整个一副酒徒咆哮的样子。不久这股狂喜的劲头稍减，他又开始深思，投入更多感情，最后竟然陷入悲怆和伤感，我几乎都要承受不了了。
By equal steps, the original briskness of his acts declined; and when he was stripped to his breeches, he sat on the bedside and fell to whimpering. 此时，他的动作不再是那么敏捷，他坐在床边，边脱衣服边啜泣。
I know nothing less respectable than the tears of drunkenness, and turned my back impatiently on this poor sight. 我知道酒徒的眼泪一文不值，于是我厌烦地转身，不愿再看到这幅情景。
But he had started himself (I am to suppose) on that slippery descent of self-pity; on the which, to a man unstrung by old sorrows and recent potations there is no arrest except exhaustion. 不过我想他开始忘却刚才的自怨自艾，这对于一个饱含悲伤、如今沉醉酒场的人来说，仅有的安慰便是身体的疲劳。
His tears continued to flow, and the man to sit there, three parts naked, in the cold air of the chamber. 他继续老泪横流，赤裸着大部分身体，坐在冰冷的房间中。
I twitted myself alternately with inhumanity and sentimental weakness, now half rising in my bed to interfere, now reading myself lessons of indifference and courting slumber, until, upon a sudden, the QUANTUM MUTATUS AB ILLO shot into my mind; and calling to remembrance his old wisdom, constancy, and patience, I was overborne with a pity almost approaching the passionate, not for my master alone but for the sons of man. 我时而责怪自己心肠太硬，时而又为自己的感情脆弱而惭愧，时而从床上起身想去照顾他，时而又警告自己不必多管闲事，赶快睡觉。这样翻来覆去，直到突然我思绪万千，回想起他以前的睿智、忠贞和耐心，万分悲伤涌上心头，不仅仅是为爵爷一人，而是替全人类感到惋惜。
At this I leaped from my place, went over to his side and laid a hand on his bare shoulder, which was cold as stone. 想到这点，我从床上爬起来走到他身边，把手轻轻搭在他赤裸的肩膀上，他的肩膀就像石头一样冰冷。
He uncovered his face and showed it me all swollen and begrutten[1] like a child’s; and at the sight my impatience partially revived. 他抬起头露出脸，有点儿肿胀，挂着泪痕，像个孩子，看到这一幕我又有点儿不耐烦了。
“Think shame to yourself,” said I. “你自己想想，不害臊吗？”我说，
“This is bairnly conduct. “小孩子才这样呢。
I might have been snivelling myself, if I had cared to swill my belly with wine. 如果我喝多了酒，恐怕也会泪流满面。
But I went to my bed sober like a man. 但我还是会像个男人那样好好地上床睡觉。
Come: get into yours, and have done with this pitiable exhibition.” 去吧，去您的床上躺下，别再哭哭啼啼。”
“Oh, Mackellar,” said he, “my heart is wae!” “哦，麦凯勒，”他说道，“我心里难受啊！”
“Wae?” cried I. “难受？”我喊道，
“For a good cause, I think. “我想这是个不错的理由。
What words were these you sang as you came in? 您进来时唱的什么歌啊？
Show pity to others, we then can talk of pity to yourself. 替别人伤心，那我们谈谈让您自己伤心的事吧。
You can be the one thing or the other, but I will be no party to half-way houses. 不管您是这样还是那样的事，我都不会半路去打岔。
If you’re a striker, strike, and if you’re a bleater, bleat!” 该伤心的您就伤心，该高兴的您就高兴！”
“Cry!” cries he, with a burst, “that’s it—strike! that’s talking! “伤心！”他突然大声说道，“就是我们谈论的那种伤心！
Man, I’ve stood it all too long. 伙计，我忍受这事很久了。
But when they laid a hand upon the child, when the child’s threatened”—his momentary vigour whimpering off—“my child, my Alexander!”—and he was at his tears again. 但这牵涉到孩子，威胁到孩子，”说到这里，他泣不成声，“我的儿子，我的亚历山大！”又开始泪流满面。
I took him by the shoulders and shook him. 我抓住他的肩膀摇了摇。
“Alexander!” said I. “亚历山大！”我说，
“Do you even think of him? “您还会想到他？
Not you! 不会吧！
Look yourself in the face like a brave man, and you’ll find you’re but a self-deceiver. 勇敢地看看您自己吧，您会发现自己就是在自欺欺人。
The wife, the friend, the child, they’re all equally forgot, and you sunk in a mere log of selfishness.” 妻子、朋友、孩子，您都统统忘掉了，沉醉在自我中不能自拔。”
“Mackellar,” said he, with a wonderful return to his old manner and appearance, “you may say what you will of me, but one thing I never was—I was never selfish.” “麦凯勒，”他说道，又回到以前的那副神态，“你怎么说我都可以，但有一样我永远不承认——我从来都不自私。”
“I will open your eyes in your despite,” said I. “我要让您睁开眼看看您是多么自私，”我说道，
“How long have we been here? and how often have you written to your family? “我们来这儿多久了？您给家里写过几封信？
I think this is the first time you were ever separate: have you written at all? 我想这是您第一次离家在外吧，您根本就没写信。
Do they know if you are dead or living?” 他们知道您是活着还是死了？”
I had caught him here too openly; it braced his better nature; there was no more weeping, he thanked me very penitently, got to bed and was soon fast asleep; and the first thing he did the next morning was to sit down and begin a letter to my lady: a very tender letter it was too, though it was never finished. 我说到了他的痛处，也唤醒了他的良知。他没有再哭泣，非常真诚地感激我，然后上床，很快便睡了过去。他第二天早上做的第一件事便是坐下给太太写了封信——一封缠绵悱恻的信，只是有点儿长，没有写完。
Indeed all communication with New York was transacted by myself; and it will be judged I had a thankless task of it. 事实上，所有与纽约家里的联系都是我一手操办的，这纯属吃力不讨好的工作。
What to tell my lady and in what words, and how far to be false and how far cruel, was a thing that kept me often from my slumber. 至于爵爷信中跟太太说了什么，怎样的措辞，怎样的虚情假意，怎样的严词责备，这一切都让我晚上辗转反侧地思考。
All this while, no doubt, my lord waited with growing impatiency for news of his accomplices. 在这期间，爵爷无疑在翘首等待他那几个同伙的消息。
Harris, it is to be thought, had promised a high degree of expedition; the time was already overpast when word was to be looked for; and suspense was a very evil counsellor to a man of an impaired intelligence. 哈里斯长途跋涉应该不是问题，但预定的时间过去了却依旧没有任何消息。对一个智力受损的人来说，这样悬而未决的事对他的精神真是一种折磨。
My lord’s mind throughout this interval dwelled almost wholly in the Wilderness, following that party with whose deeds he had so much concern. 爵爷脑中整天想的都是些远方的蛮荒之地，还有就是那几个与他利益相关的同伙。
He continually conjured up their camps and progresses, the fashion of the country, the perpetration in a thousand different manners of the same horrid fact, and that consequent spectacle of the Master’s bones lying scattered in the wind. 他不停地想象着他们扎营的情况及进程、当地的风土人情、与这件可怕的事情相关的上千种犯罪的方式以及大少爷在那片土地上抛尸露骨的悲惨场景。
These private, guilty considerations I would continually observe to peep forth in the man’s talk, like rabbits from a hill. 跟我谈话时，我能看到他流露出的各种私底下的罪恶想法，这些想法就像是山里的野兔那样多。
And it is the less wonder if the scene of his meditations began to draw him bodily. 不难想象，这些想法开始影响到他的身体健康。
It is well known what pretext he took. 他找了个众所周知的借口。
Sir William Johnson had a diplomatic errand in these parts; and my lord and I (from curiosity, as was given out) went in his company. 威廉·约翰逊爵士要到那些地方进行外交访问，爵爷和我则是他的陪同（爵爷称自己是出于好奇）。
Sir William was well attended and liberally supplied. 威廉爵士受到了热情款待，人们送来了丰盛的物品。
Hunters brought us venison, fish was taken for us daily in the streams, and brandy ran like water. 猎人们给我们带来了鹿肉，河里的鱼也是每天都往我们这里送，白兰地更是像流水般涌来。
We proceeded by day and encamped by night in the military style; sentinels were set and changed; every man had his named duty; and Sir William was the spring of all. 我们像行军一样，白天赶路，晚上安营扎寨，安排了轮换岗哨，各司其职，威廉爵士则统筹全局。
There was much in this that might at times have entertained me; but for our misfortune, the weather was extremely harsh, the days were in the beginning open, but the nights frosty from the first. 这一切有时还会让我觉得有兴致，但不幸的是天气极其恶劣，白天晴朗温暖，晚上却是冰霜覆盖。
A painful keen wind blew most of the time, so that we sat in the boat with blue fingers, and at night, as we scorched our faces at the fire, the clothes upon our back appeared to be of paper. 绝大部分时间寒风刺骨，我们坐在船上，手指都冻紫了。晚上我们紧紧贴着火堆，后背的衣服单薄得像张纸片。
A dreadful solitude surrounded our steps; the land was quite dispeopled, there was no smoke of fires, and save for a single boat of merchants on the second day, we met no travellers. 沿途了无人烟，荒凉得让人害怕，直到第二天才遇到一艘载有商人的船，除此以外别无他人。
The season was indeed late, but this desertion of the waterways impressed Sir William himself; and I have heard him more than once express a sense of intimidation. 这个季节实在太晚了，水路的荒凉也使威廉爵士本人感触颇多，我听到他不止一次倾诉心中的恐惧。
“I have come too late, I fear; they must have dug up the hatchet;” he said; and the future proved how justly he had reasoned. “恐怕我来得太晚了，他们多半已经开战了。”他说道。以后的事证明他当时的判断是多么准确。
I could never depict the blackness of my soul upon this journey. 这次旅行，我心头上的阴郁是难以言表的。
I have none of those minds that are in love with the unusual: to see the winter coming and to lie in the field so far from any house, oppressed me like a nightmare; it seemed, indeed, a kind of awful braving of God’s power; and this thought, which I daresay only writes me down a coward, was greatly exaggerated by my private knowledge of the errand we were come upon. 我对这些不寻常的事物本来就没有多少追寻的情怀：看着冬天到来，却在荒郊野地里呆着，这一切对我来说犹如噩梦，似乎是在挑战上帝的权威。而这种想法把我自己贬低成了懦夫胆小鬼，再说我心里知道了此行的目的，所以更是羞愧难当。
I was besides encumbered by my duties to Sir William, whom it fell upon me to entertain; for my lord was quite sunk into a state bordering on PERVIGILIUM, watching the woods with a rapt eye, sleeping scarce at all, and speaking sometimes not twenty words in a whole day. 一路上我还要按爵爷吩咐抽空去伺候和陪伴威廉爵士，因为爵爷正处在失眠的边缘，他凝视着这片树林，几乎不睡觉，一天总共说不了二十个字。
That which he said was still coherent; but it turned almost invariably upon the party for whom he kept his crazy lookout. 而他说的话也还算明晰，只是内容离不开他担心的事情。
He would tell Sir William often, and always as if it were a new communication, that he had “a brother somewhere in the woods,” and beg that the sentinels should be directed “to inquire for him.” 他经常跟威廉爵士提起“有一个哥哥在树林里”之类的话，每次提起却总像是第一次说，继而请求派出哨兵去“寻找哥哥”。
“I am anxious for news of my brother,” he would say. 他会说：“我很想知道我哥哥的消息。”
And sometimes, when we were under way, he would fancy he spied a canoe far off upon the water or a camp on the shore, and exhibit painful agitation. 有时候我们赶路时，他会想象地说自己看见远处水面上有一叶扁舟，或者河边有一个帐篷，同时显出一副痛苦难熬的样子。
It was impossible but Sir William should be struck with these singularities; and at last he led me aside, and hinted his uneasiness. 让我难以置信的是，威廉爵士对这样的小事情也体察入微，最后把我叫过去，委婉地表达了他的不安和关切。
I touched my head and shook it; quite rejoiced to prepare a little testimony against possible disclosures. 我搔了搔脑袋，又摇了摇头，然后很乐意做好准备，以防发现大少爷的踪迹。
“But in that case,” cries Sir William, “is it wise to let him go at large?” “如果真找到他的话，”威廉爵士说，“放他走算不算明智呢？”
“Those that know him best,” said I, “are persuaded that he should be humoured.” “那些最了解他的人，”我说道，“都认为该放任他不管。
“Well, well,” replied Sir William, “it is none of my affairs. “好吧，好吧，”威廉爵士回答说，“这可不关我的事。
But if I had understood, you would never have been here.” 如果早知道，我就不会让你们俩来了。”
Our advance into this savage country had thus uneventfully proceeded for about a week, when we encamped for a night at a place where the river ran among considerable mountains clothed in wood. 就这样，我们在蛮荒之地行进了一个礼拜，一路无事，直到一天晚上，我们在一处河边扎了营，河水在附近树木茂盛的山脉中穿行。
The fires were lighted on a level space at the water’s edge; and we supped and lay down to sleep in the customary fashion. 我们在河边一处平坦的地方生起了篝火。吃过晚饭，大家便像往常一样躺下睡觉。
It chanced the night fell murderously cold; the stringency of the frost seized and bit me through my coverings so that pain kept me wakeful; and I was afoot again before the peep of day, crouching by the fires or trotting to and for at the stream’s edge, to combat the aching of my limbs. 这天夜里格外冷，霜冻穿透铺盖。我被冻得浑身发疼，实在睡不着，没等天亮就爬了起来，时而在火堆旁趴着，时而沿着河岸猛跑一阵，以减轻四肢的疼痛。
At last dawn began to break upon hoar woods and mountains, the sleepers rolled in their robes, and the boisterous river dashing among spears of ice. 天终于破晓，阳光开始洒满冰霜覆盖的山脉和树林，众人穿上长袍，湍急的河流在冰凌丛中前行。
I stood looking about me, swaddled in my stiff coat of a bull’s fur, and the breath smoking from my scorched nostrils, when, upon a sudden, a singular, eager cry rang from the borders of the wood. 我裹着硬挺的牛皮衣服，起身环顾四周，热乎乎的鼻孔里直往外冒白气。忽然树林边沿传来一声急促的惊叫。
The sentries answered it, the sleepers sprang to their feet; one pointed, the rest followed his direction with their eyes, and there, upon the edge of the forest and betwixt two trees, we beheld the figure of a man reaching forth his hands like one in ecstasy. 哨兵闻声而去，睡觉的人也都跳了起来。一个人指着方向，其余的人顺着他指的方向看去，只见在森林边缘的两棵树中间有一个人影伸出手来，像是欣喜若狂的样子。
The next moment he ran forward, fell on his knees at the side of the camp, and burst in tears. 紧接着，那个人跑了过来，跑到帐篷面前跪了下来，放声大哭。
This was John Mountain, the trader, escaped from the most horrid perils; and his fist word, when he got speech, was to ask if we had seen Secundra Dass. 原来是商人芒廷，看起来他刚从最令人害怕的危险中逃生，而他开口的第一句话便是问我们是否看到过赛昆德拉·达斯。
“Seen what?” cries Sir William. “看到什么？”威廉爵士喊道。
“No,” said I, “we have seen nothing of him. “不，”我说，“我们没看见他。
Why?” 怎么了？”
“Nothing?” says Mountain. “没看到过？”芒廷说，
“Then I was right after all.” “那我算是猜对了。”
With that he struck his palm upon his brow. 说着他用手拍了拍眉头。
“But what takes him back?” he cried. “但他是怎么活过来的？”他喊道，
“What takes the man back among dead bodies. “是什么把他从死人堆里救活了？
There is some damned mystery here.” 这真是太神奇了。”
This was a word which highly aroused our curiosity, but I shall be more perspicacious, if I narrate these incidents in their true order. 这句话深深引起了我们的好奇心，但我觉得我还是按时间顺序描述发生的一切比较明智。
Here follows a narrative which I have compiled out of three sources, not very consistent in all points: 我从三个方面叙述，其中的某些细节难免有些矛盾：
FIRST, a written statement by Mountain, in which everything criminal is cleverly smuggled out of view; 首先，芒廷的一份书面声明，其中违法犯罪的情节都被巧妙地删除了；
SECOND, two conversations with Secundra Dass; 其次，与赛昆德拉·达斯的两次谈话；
and THIRD, many conversations with Mountain himself, in which he was pleased to be entirely plain; for the truth is he regarded me as an accomplice. 最后，与芒廷本人的多次谈话，谈话中他很愿意坦诚相对，可能他把我当成自己人了。
Narrative of the Trader, Mountain. 商人芒廷的叙述
The crew that went up the river under the joint command of Captain Harris and the Master numbered in all nine persons, of whom (if I except Secundra Dass) there was not one that had not merited the gallows. 船长哈里斯和大少爷一行九人在他们两个的领导下沿河而上，这些人中我想除了赛昆德拉·达斯之外，其余都是十恶不赦的罪犯。
From Harris downward the voyagers were notorious in that colony for desperate, bloody-minded miscreants; some were reputed pirates, the most hawkers of rum; all ranters and drinkers; all fit associates, embarking together without remorse, upon this treacherous and murderous design. 哈里斯和其他航行者，个个在这片土地上都是出了名的恶棍、亡命之徒，杀人不眨眼。有的甚至是响当当的海盗，有的干过非法卖酒的投机生意；个个是疯汉和醉鬼，都是一丘之貉，这次结伴同行完全是趟不要命的勾当，但他们却义无反顾。
I could not hear there was much discipline or any set captain in the gang; but Harris and four others, Mountain himself, two Scotchmen—Pinkerton and Hastie—and a man of the name of Hicks, a drunken shoemaker, put their heads together and agreed upon the course. 我想象不出这样的一群人能有什么纪律性或者称职的头领。不过哈里斯和另外四个人——芒廷本人、两个苏格兰人平克顿和黑斯蒂，还有一个常常喝醉的鞋匠希克斯秘密地凑在一块商量了一条前行路线。
In a material sense, they were well enough provided; and the Master in particular brought with him a tent where he might enjoy some privacy and shelter. 就物质条件而言，他们给养充足，大少爷还特意随身带了一个小帐篷，可以独自在里面享受一点儿隐私和保护。
Even this small indulgence told against him in the minds of his companions. 即便是这点儿特权也让同伴们满腹牢骚。
But indeed he was in a position so entirely false (and even ridiculous) that all his habit of command and arts of pleasing were here thrown away. 事实上，大少爷在这支队伍里的位置完全不当，甚至有些荒谬，那些发号施令的习惯和笼络人心的手段在这里都不适用。
In the eyes of all, except Secundra Dass, he figured as a common gull and designated victim; going unconsciously to death; yet he could not but suppose himself the contriver and the leader of the expedition; he could scarce help but so conduct himself and at the least hint of authority or condescension, his deceivers would be laughing in their sleeves. 除了赛昆德拉·达斯，在其他的同伙眼中，他只是个受人愚弄的傻瓜，天生的倒霉蛋，死都不知道怎么死的。他很自然地把他自己当作这次探险的策划者和领导者，言谈举止之间也显出高人一等的架势，然而随行人总是暗地里嘲笑他。
I was so used to see and to conceive him in a high, authoritative attitude, that when I had conceived his position on this journey, I was pained and could have blushed. 我很轻易地就想象出他那副高高在上的态度，而当我设想他在这次旅行中的地位时，我感到心痛惭愧。
How soon he may have entertained a first surmise, we cannot know; but it was long, and the party had advanced into the Wilderness beyond the reach of any help, ere he was fully awakened to the truth. 出发多久他才意识到自己的处境，我们并不知道。但出发后很久，当队伍进入蛮荒之地、无可求助的时候，他才完全体会到自己的真实处境。
It fell thus. 事情的经过是这样的。
Harris and some others had drawn apart into the woods for consultation, when they were startled by a rustling in the brush. 哈里斯和其他一些人躲到树林里密谋的时候，无意中听到树丛中有沙沙的响声，不禁大吃一惊。
They were all accustomed to the arts of Indian warfare, and Mountain had not only lived and hunted, but fought and earned some reputation, with the savages. 他们熟知印第安人的战争手法，而且芒廷不仅跟那些野蛮人一起生活、打猎，还与他们打过仗，立过战功。
He could move in the woods without noise, and follow a trail like a hound; and upon the emergence of this alert, he was deputed by the rest to plunge into the thicket for intelligence. 他能在丛林中悄无声息地移动，像猎狗一样寻找踪迹。听出危险信号后，其他人把前去密林深处察看的任务交给了他。
He was soon convinced there was a man in his close neighbourhood, moving with precaution but without art among the leaves and branches; and coming shortly to a place of advantage, he was able to observe Secundra Dass crawling briskly off with many backward glances. 不一会他就确定他附近有人，在树叶和树枝中间移动，虽然小心翼翼却没什么技巧。芒廷很快抵达有利的地形，他看到赛昆德拉·达斯敏捷地往前爬，不时回头看看。
At this he knew not whether to laugh or cry; and his accomplices, when he had returned and reported, were in much the same dubiety. 看到这个，他不知该哭还是该笑，当他回去把这件事向同伴说了以后，其他人顿时觉得可疑。
There was now no danger of an Indian onslaught; but on the other hand, since Secundra Dass was at the pains to spy upon them, it was highly probable he knew English, and if he knew English it was certain the whole of their design was in the Master’s knowledge. 印第安人偷袭的警报解除了，但另一方面，由于赛昆德拉·达斯费尽心思监视他们，那他很可能听得懂英语，如果他懂英语，那大少爷也会知晓他们的全部计划。
There was one singularity in the position. 不过他们也有个不为人知的优势。
If Secundra Dass knew and concealed his knowledge of English, Harris was a proficient in several of the tongues of India, and as his career in that part of the world had been a great deal worse than profligate, he had not thought proper to remark upon the circumstance. 赛昆德拉·达斯知晓英语却隐藏事实，但哈里斯也通晓好几种印度语，因为他在印度的那些年极其放荡荒淫，所以对他这一段经历也就避而不谈。
Each side had thus a spy-hole on the counsels of the other. 这样一来，两边都能互相探听对方消息。
The plotters, so soon as this advantage was explained, returned to camp; Harris, hearing the Hindustani was once more closeted with his master, crept to the side of the tent; and the rest, sitting about the fire with their tobacco, awaited his report with impatience. 解释完自己的优势后，他们回到宿营地，哈里斯听到赛昆德拉向他的主子汇报后，又匍匐爬到帐篷的一侧偷听，其他人则照旧围坐在火堆边吸烟，耐心等待他的汇报。
When he came at last, his face was very black. 最后回来的时候，他脸色铁青。
He had overheard enough to confirm the worst of his suspicions. 他听到的内容足以印证他们的设想。
Secundra Dass was a good English scholar; he had been some days creeping and listening, the Master was now fully informed of the conspiracy, and the pair proposed on the morrow to fall out of line at a carrying place and plunge at a venture in the woods: preferring the full risk of famine, savage beasts, and savage men to their position in the midst of traitors. 赛昆德拉·达斯是个英语通，经过几天的秘密监视偷听，大少爷已经完全掌握了他们的阴谋。大少爷和赛昆德拉决定第二天故意掉在队伍的最后面，等船靠岸的时候钻到密林里，宁愿忍受饥饿，冒着被野兽吃、被野人杀的危险，也不与这伙叛徒为伍。
What, then, was to be done? 那接下来该怎么办？
Some were for killing the Master on the spot; but Harris assured them that would be a crime without profit, since the secret of the treasure must die along with him that buried it. 一些人主张当场把他杀了，而哈里斯说服他们那是没什么好处的犯罪，因为宝藏的秘密将随大少爷的死去而一起被埋葬。
Others were for desisting at once from the whole enterprise and making for New York; but the appetising name of treasure, and the thought of the long way they had already travelled dissuaded the majority. 其他人主张就地散伙，马上回纽约，但宝藏的诱惑以及一路来受的苦难让他们不肯罢休。
I imagine they were dull fellows for the most part. 我想他们大都是笨蛋。
Harris, indeed, had some acquirements, Mountain was no fool, Hastie was an educated man; but even these had manifestly failed in life, and the rest were the dregs of colonial rascality. 哈里斯实际上确实有点儿见识，芒廷也不傻，黑斯蒂可以算是个知识分子，可这几个在社会上都吃不开，其余几个只不过是下层社会的渣滓。
The conclusion they reached, at least, was more the offspring of greed and hope, than reason. 他们所下的结论完全不是理智的结果，而是侥幸和贪婪的产物。
It was to temporise, to be wary and watch the Master, to be silent and supply no further aliment to his suspicions, and to depend entirely (as well as I make out) on the chance that their victim was as greedy, hopeful, and irrational as themselves, and might, after all, betray his life and treasure. 他们决定先放任和秘密监视大少爷，摆出疲惫不堪的样子。他们在一起的时候尽量保持沉默，避免再使他起疑心，我想这也完全取决于他们的对手是否同他们一样贪婪、侥幸、不理智以及最终是否会把宝藏的秘密说出去。
Twice in the course of the next day Secundra and the Master must have appeared to themselves to have escaped; and twice they were circumvented. 第二天，赛昆德拉和大少爷在途中曾两次试图逃跑，都被拦住了。
The Master, save that the second time he grew a little pale, displayed no sign of disappointment, apologised for the stupidity with which he had fallen aside, thanked his recapturers as for a service, and rejoined the caravan with all his usual gallantry and cheerfulness of mien and bearing. 大少爷除了第二次被拦住的时候面色有点儿苍白外，没有显出任何失望的表情，他为自己迷路的愚蠢行为道歉，还感谢监视他的人帮忙把他找回来，然后继续以以前的豪气和精神加入到队伍中。
But it is certain he had smelled a rat; for from thenceforth he and Secundra spoke only in each other’s ear, and Harris listened and shivered by the tent in vain. 不过他肯定起了疑心，因为打那以后他和赛昆德拉只是贴着耳朵咕哝过几句，而哈里斯在帐篷外什么也听不到，还冻得要死。
The same night it was announced they were to leave the boats and proceed by foot, a circumstance which (as it put an end to the confusion of the portages) greatly lessened the chances of escape. 当天晚上，大伙宣布弃舟而行，这样可以减少水陆交叉时的混乱，同样这也极大减少了逃跑的机会。
And now there began between the two sides a silent contest, for life on the one hand, for riches on the other. 现在两边开始了无言的战斗，一边为了生命，一边为了财富。
They were now near that quarter of the desert in which the Master himself must begin to play the part of guide; and using this for a pretext of persecution, Harris and his men sat with him every night about the fire, and laboured to entrap him into some admission. 他们现在接近沙漠地区，大少爷需要亲自做向导。以此为借口，哈里斯和他的同伙每天晚上同大少爷一起坐在火堆旁，努力骗他说出秘密。
If he let slip his secret, he knew well it was the warrant for his death; on the other hand, he durst not refuse their questions, and must appear to help them to the best of his capacity, or he practically published his mistrust. 如果大少爷说出了秘密，他很清楚这将极大威胁到自己的生命。另一方面，他不敢拒绝他们的问题，还要装作努力答复对方的样子，不然他就等于公开暴露了自己对同伴的不信任。
And yet Mountain assures me the man’s brow was never ruffled. 芒廷告诉我，大少爷的眉头从没皱过一下。
He sat in the midst of these jackals, his life depending by a thread, like some easy, witty householder at home by his own fire; an answer he had for everything—as often as not, a jesting answer; avoided threats, evaded insults; talked, laughed, and listened with an open countenance; and, in short, conducted himself in such a manner as must have disarmed suspicion, and went near to stagger knowledge. 他坐在豺狼之间，命悬一线，但他还是那样悠闲自得，妙语连珠，仿佛一屋之主端坐在自家的炉火前拉家常：有问必答，而且答案风趣幽默，对方威胁，他就回避；对方侮辱，他就装傻，沉着冷静地说着、笑着、听着。总之，他的言谈举止丝毫不能引起别人的猜疑，而且滴水不漏。
Indeed, Mountain confessed to me they would soon have disbelieved the Captain’s story, and supposed their designated victim still quite innocent of their designs; but for the fact that he continued (however ingeniously) to give the slip to questions, and the yet stronger confirmation of his repeated efforts to escape. 芒廷坦诚地说，他们那伙人几乎怀疑船长是在撒谎，要不是大少爷一再回避（尽管很圆滑）他们的问题，并多次企图逃跑，他们还真以为这个替死鬼对他们的阴谋仍然是浑然不知呢。
The last of these, which brought things to a head, I am now to relate. 现在我来说下事情恶化的经过。
And first I should say that by this time the temper of Harris’s companions was utterly worn out; civility was scarce pretended; and for one very significant circumstance, the Master and Secundra had been (on some pretext) deprived of weapons. 首先我得说一下，此时哈里斯等人的脾气都被磨光了，大伙很少装出客套，一个重要的情况是，大少爷和赛昆德拉的武器被他们以某些借口剥夺了。
On their side, however, the threatened pair kept up the parade of friendship handsomely; Secundra was all bows, the Master all smiles; and on the last night of the truce he had even gone so far as to sing for the diversion of the company. 然而，另一方面，被胁迫的那俩还是那样大大方方地友好相处，赛昆德拉还是见人就低头哈腰，大少爷还是逢人便笑脸相迎。在双方友好的最后一个晚上，他甚至还给大伙唱歌消遣。
It was observed that he had also eaten with unusual heartiness, and drank deep, doubtless from design. 他看起来吃饭吃得津津有味，酒也喝得尽兴，但毫无疑问，这一切都有他的深意。
At least, about three in the morning, he came out of the tent into the open air, audibly mourning and complaining, with all the manner of a sufferer from surfeit. 大约凌晨3点，大少爷走出帐篷，大声地哀鸣和抱怨，一副饮食过度的样子。
For some while, Secundra publicly attended on his patron, who at last became more easy, and fell asleep on the frosty ground behind the tent, the Indian returning within. 过了一会，赛昆德拉当着众人安抚他的主人，大少爷也终于宽慰了些，慢慢在帐篷后面冰霜覆盖的地上睡着了，那个印度人则返回到帐篷里头。
Some time after, the sentry was changed; had the Master pointed out to him, where he lay in what is called a robe of buffalo: and thenceforth kept an eye upon him (he declared) without remission. 过了一段时间后，开始换岗，放哨的告诉接班的同伙，大少爷就睡在那块牛皮毯子里头，并叮嘱他千万要小心看着点儿。
With the first of the dawn, a draught of wind came suddenly and blew open one side the corner of the robe; and with the same puff, the Master’s hat whirled in the air and fell some yards away. 破晓时分，一股风突然刮来，掀起毯子的一角，也将大少爷的帽子吹了起来，落到好几米远的地方。
The sentry thinking it remarkable the sleeper should not awaken, thereupon drew near; and the next moment, with a great shout, informed the camp their prisoner was escaped. 岗哨想大少爷怎么还没醒，于是上前察看，接着岗哨大惊失色，赶紧跟帐篷里的人报告说大少爷逃跑了。
He had left behind his Indian, who (in the first vivacity of the surprise) came near to pay the forfeit of his life, and was, in fact, inhumanly mishandled; but Secundra, in the midst of threats and cruelties, stuck to it with extraordinary loyalty, that he was quite ignorant of his master’s plans, which might indeed be true, and of the manner of his escape, which was demonstrably false. 大少爷撇下印度人，这让印度人起初也大惊失色，这位奴仆走过去替主子偿命，他遭到了惨无人道的毒打。然而赛昆德拉在恐吓与折磨中宁死不屈，始终一口咬定他对主子的计划毫不知情。这也可能是实情，但他说主子怎么逃跑的事他一点儿也不知情，那就明显是撒谎了。
Nothing was therefore left to the conspirators but to rely entirely on the skill of Mountain. 这时，除了完全依赖芒廷跟踪的本领外，他们无计可施。
The night had been frosty, the ground quite hard; and the sun was no sooner up than a strong thaw set in. 晚上下了霜，路面非常硬，太阳马上就出来了，霜也会很快化掉。
It was Mountain’s boast that few men could have followed that trail, and still fewer (even of the native Indians) found it. 芒廷说很少有人能嗅出这样的行迹，即使土著印第安人也很少能找到它。
The Master had thus a long start before his pursuers had the scent, and he must have travelled with surprising energy for a pedestrian so unused, since it was near noon before Mountain had a view of him. 等到他们寻找到线索的时候，大少爷已经跑了很久了。作为一位不习惯走长路的人，他一定使尽了全力，因为当芒廷看见他的时候，已经是中午了。
At this conjuncture the trader was alone, all his companions following, at his own request, several hundred yards in the rear; he knew the Master was unarmed; his heart was besides heated with the exercise and lust of hunting; and seeing the quarry so close, so defenceless, and seeming so fatigued, he vain-gloriously determined to effect the capture with his single hand. 此时芒廷只身一人，他的同伙还在后面几百米。他知道大少爷手无寸铁，自己跑了这么久以后热血沸腾，打猎的念头涌上心头。看到猎物近在咫尺，毫无反抗之力，看起来疲惫不堪，芒廷英雄之气顿发，决定只手将其俘获。
A step or two farther brought him to one margin of a little clearing; on the other, with his arms folded and his back to a huge stone, the Master sat. 他又前行走一两步，到了一块视野开阔之地，能清晰地看到大少爷叉着双手背靠大石，正坐着休息。
It is possible Mountain may have made a rustle, it is certain, at least, the Master raised his head and gazed directly at that quarter of the thicket where his hunter lay; “I could not be sure he saw me,” Mountain said; “he just looked my way like a man with his mind made up, and all the courage ran out of me like rum out of a bottle.” 可能芒廷不小心弄出了些响声，大少爷抬起头，直勾勾地看着芒廷隐藏的那片树林。芒廷说：“我不确定他是否看到了我，反正他一直坦然自若地朝我这个方向看，我原先的勇气像泄气的皮球一样荡然无存。”
And presently, when the Master looked away again, and appeared to resume those meditations in which he had sat immersed before the trader’s coming, Mountain slunk stealthily back and returned to seek the help of his companions. 过了一会大少爷转过头去，似乎又陷入了先前的沉思，芒廷悄无声息地缩了回去，招手示意同伙帮忙。
And now began the chapter of surprises, for the scout had scarce informed the others of his discovery, and they were yet preparing their weapons for a rush upon the fugitive, when the man himself appeared in their midst, walking openly and quietly, with his hands behind his back. 意想不到的事情发生了，芒廷刚把自己的发现告诉同伙，正准备好手中的武器想来个突然袭击，却没料到大少爷就把双手搭在背后大模大样地朝他们走了过来。
“Ah, men!” says he, on his beholding them. 一看到他们，大少爷就说道：“嗨，大伙！
“Here is a fortunate encounter. 幸会，幸会。
Let us get back to camp.” 咱们回营地吧。”
Mountain had not mentioned his own weakness or the Master’s disconcerting gaze upon the thicket, so that (with all the rest) his return appeared spontaneous. 芒廷没有向同伙提及自己临阵胆怯以及大少爷看着林子时那令人害怕的眼神的细节，所以大伙都认为他是自觉地返回目的地。
For all that, a hubbub arose; oaths flew, fists were shaken, and guns pointed. 尽管如此，还是引起了骚乱和不满，众人挥舞着拳头，用枪口指着俘虏。
“Let us get back to camp,” said the Master. “我们返回营地吧，”大少爷说，
“I have an explanation to make, but it must be laid before you all. “我有话要说，但必须当着所有人的面说。
And in the meanwhile I would put up these weapons, one of which might very easily go off and blow away your hopes of treasure. 所以我想你们还是收起武器吧，否则任何一件不小心走火，你们的宝藏梦将随之破灭。
I would not kill,” says he, smiling, “the goose with the golden eggs.” 要是我的话，我可不会杀了会下金蛋的母鸡。”大少爷笑着说道。
The charm of his superiority once more triumphed; and the party, in no particular order, set off on their return. 那高人一头的气势又一次发挥了作用，于是队伍开始三三两两地往回走。
By the way, he found occasion to get a word or two apart with Mountain. 期间，他找到机会单独与芒廷说了几句话。
“You are a clever fellow and a bold,” says he, “but I am not so sure that you are doing yourself justice. “你是个聪明人，又有胆识，”他说，“但我不知道你这么做是否合适。
I would have you to consider whether you would not do better, ay, and safer, to serve me instead of serving so commonplace a rascal as Mr. Harris. 我希望你考虑下，跟着我是不是比跟着哈里斯那种流氓无赖要好、要安全。
Consider of it,” he concluded, dealing the man a gentle tap upon the shoulder, “and don’t be in haste. 考虑下吧，”他说完，然后拍了拍他的肩膀，又说，“用不着那么着急回答。
Dead or alive, you will find me an ill man to quarrel with.” 是死是活，你总会明白的，我向来不喜欢与人争论。”
When they were come back to the camp, where Harris and Pinkerton stood guard over Secundra, these two ran upon the Master like viragoes, and were amazed out of measure when they were bidden by their comrades to “stand back and hear what the gentleman had to say.” 当他们回到营地时，哈里斯和平克顿正看守着赛昆德拉，当看到大少爷时，他们就像泼妇一样扑上前去。当被同伙喊着“退后，听听这位绅士怎么说。”时，他们极其惊讶。
The Master had not flinched before their onslaught; nor, at this proof of the ground he had gained, did he betray the least sufficiency. 大少爷面对刚才凶猛的举动没有任何退缩，现在他可找了个护身符，他对众人心平气和。
“Do not let us be in haste,” says he. “别那么急嘛，”他说，
“Meat first and public speaking after.” “咱们先吃饭而后开会。”
With that they made a hasty meal: and as soon as it was done, the Master, leaning on one elbow, began his speech. 接着他们仓促地吃了饭，刚吃完饭，大少爷就用手撑着脑袋，开始说话。
He spoke long, addressing himself to each except Harris, finding for each (with the same exception) some particular flattery. 他说了很多，除了哈里斯之外，他同每个人说话，少不了一番恭维。
He called them “bold, honest blades,” declared he had never seen a more jovial company, work better done, or pains more merrily supported. 他称大伙是“豪爽诚实的侠士”，宣称自己还从未见过这样如此有活力、活干得这么好、这么能分担苦难的一支队伍。
“Well, then,” says he, “some one asks me, Why the devil I ran away? “那么，对了，”他说，“如果有人问我，我到底为什么跑？
But that is scarce worth answer, for I think you all know pretty well. 这个问题不值得回答，因为我想你们都知道答案。
But you know only pretty well: that is a point I shall arrive at presently, and be you ready to remark it when it comes. 你们很了解这事，稍后我也将提到，到时候你们再准备好好评论下。
There is a traitor here: a double traitor: I will give you his name before I am done; and let that suffice for now. 我们队伍中间有个叛徒，一个双重叛徒，等我说故事之前我会告诉你们他的名字，现在说这些就足够了。
But here comes some other gentleman and asks me, ‘Why, in the devil, I came back?’ 可是现在又会有兄弟问我：我到底又为啥回来了？
Well, before I answer that question, I have one to put to you. 好吧，在我回答这个问题之前，我倒有一个问题想问各位。
It was this cur here, this Harris, that speaks Hindustani?” cries he, rising on one knee and pointing fair at the man’s face, with a gesture indescribably menacing; and when he had been answered in the affirmative, “Ah!” says he, “then are all my suspicions verified, and I did rightly to come back. 这个问题就是这条癞皮狗，就是这个哈里斯会说印度语吗？”说着他站起身，气势汹汹地指着那个人的脸。当他得到了肯定的回答后，他说，“啊哈！那么我所有的猜想就都成立了，我现在返回来也算是明智的。
Now, men, hear the truth for the first time.” 那么，兄弟们，让我跟你们说下你们所不知道的真相吧。”
Thereupon he launched forth in a long story, told with extraordinary skill, how he had all along suspected Harris, how he had found the confirmation of his fears, and how Harris must have misrepresented what passed between Secundra and himself. 他说着，开始亮出自己编造故事的独门绝活，口若悬河地讲着自己如何怀疑哈里斯已久，又是怎么证实自己的担忧，估计哈里斯会怎样歪曲他自己和赛昆德拉之间的谈话。
At this point he made a bold stroke with excellent effect. 说到这里，他果敢的举止开始有了出奇的效果。
“I suppose,” says he, “you think you are going shares with Harris; I suppose you think you will see to that yourselves; you would naturally not think so flat a rogue could cozen you. “我想，”他说道，“众位兄弟还以为可以与哈里斯分享宝藏吧，还以为这事肯定会落到自己头上了吧，还以为这么一个臭名昭著的骗子不会骗你们吧！
But have a care! 兄弟们注意了！
These half idiots have a sort of cunning, as the skunk has its stench; and it may be news to you that Harris has taken care of himself already. 这种半傻子更是狡猾奸诈，就像臭鼬会放臭气那样。可能你们还不知道吧，哈里斯已经为自己安排好了。
Yes, for him the treasure is all money in the bargain. 对的，对他来说这次寻找的宝藏只是交易的一部分。
You must find it or go starve. 对你们来说寻找宝藏是唯一出路，否则回去就要挨饿。
But he has been paid beforehand; my brother paid him to destroy me; look at him, if you doubt—look at him, grinning and gulping, a detected thief!” 可动身之前，我弟弟就给了哈里斯一大笔钱，要他害死我，如果你怀疑的话，看看他那德行——刚才还狰狞地笑，这回没词了，整个一个被人逮住的贼！”
Thence, having made this happy impression, he explained how he had escaped, and thought better of it, and at last concluded to come back, lay the truth before the company, and take his chance with them once more: persuaded as he was, they would instantly depose Harris and elect some other leader. 说到这，他兴高采烈地把自己所知的内情说了一遍，他解释自己如何逃脱，如何前思后想后决定把真相公之于众，然后跟大伙一起碰碰运气——如果能说服大家的话，那么大家就会立刻废除哈里斯，另选其他领导人。
“There is the whole truth,” said he: “and with one exception, I put myself entirely in your hands. “这就是全部真相，”他说道，“只要满足我一个条件，我就把自己和其他的一切交到兄弟们手里。
What is the exception? 条件是什么呢？
There he sits,” he cried, pointing once more to Harris; “a man that has to die! 就是坐在那儿的他，”大少爷用手指着哈里斯喊道，“这个人必须死！
Weapons and conditions are all one to me; put me face to face with him, and if you give me nothing but a stick, in five minutes I will show you a sop of broken carrion, fit for dogs to roll in.” 用武器或者其他方式，我都不在乎。让他跟我面对面，即便是给我一根棍子，五分钟之内我也会将他打成一堆肉酱，一摊喂狗的臭肉。”
It was dark night when he made an end; they had listened in almost perfect silence; but the firelight scarce permitted any one to judge, from the look of his neighbours, with what result of persuasion or conviction. 直到深夜他才结束讲话；大伙默默地听着，但是火光太暗，谁也无法看清楚周围人的表情，也无法看清楚大伙是否相信了大少爷的话。
Indeed, the Master had set himself in the brightest place, and kept his face there, to be the centre of men’s eyes: doubtless on a profound calculation. 而大少爷自己坐在最明亮的地方，把自己暴露在众目睽睽之下，显然他在苦苦思索些什么。
Silence followed for awhile, and presently the whole party became involved in disputation: the Master lying on his back, with his hands knit under his head and one knee flung across the other, like a person unconcerned in the result. 沉默了一会儿后，大伙开始七嘴八舌地议论起来；大少爷仰卧在那里，手搭在头下，两腿交叉，像个对结果毫不关心的局外人。
And here, I daresay, his bravado carried him too far and prejudiced his case. 此时，我敢说，他虚张声势过了头，这样反而对他不利。
At least, after a cast or two back and forward, opinion settled finally against him. 一来二去之后，最后大家得出的结论是不信任他。
It’s possible he hoped to repeat the business of the pirate ship, and be himself, perhaps, on hard enough conditions, elected leader; and things went so far that way, that Mountain actually threw out the proposition. 可能他想重演海盗船上的把戏，让大伙推举他为头儿吧。而事情真的向这个方向发展，芒廷提出另选头头。
But the rock he split upon was Hastie. 不过他提出的人选是黑斯蒂。
This fellow was not well liked, being sour and slow, with an ugly, glowering disposition, but he had studied some time for the church at Edinburgh College, before ill conduct had destroyed his prospects, and he now remembered and applied what he had learned. 这个家伙不怎么受欢迎，有点儿迂腐和愚笨，人缘差，脾气暴躁，不过他曾在爱丁堡大学学过几天神学，只不过不务正业毁了他的前程，现在正是他施展自己所学的时候了。
Indeed he had not proceeded very far, when the Master rolled carelessly upon one side, which was done (in Mountain’s opinion) to conceal the beginnings of despair upon his countenance. 他还没怎么开始说话，大少爷就心不在焉似地转过身去，芒廷认为他是在掩饰脸上失望的表情。
Hastie dismissed the most of what they had heard as nothing to the matter: what they wanted was the treasure. 黑斯蒂觉得大少爷说的大部分都与正题无关：他们想要的只是宝藏。
All that was said of Harris might be true, and they would have to see to that in time. 有关哈里斯的故事也可能是对的，他们以后该多防备着他点儿。
But what had that to do with the treasure? 但这与宝藏又有什么关系呢？
They had heard a vast of words; but the truth was just this, that Mr. Durie was damnably frightened and had several times run off. 他们听说了很多的事，但事实无非是迪里先生吓破了胆而多次企图逃跑。
Here he was—whether caught or come back was all one to Hastie: the point was to make an end of the business. 大少爷不管是被抓了回来还是自己回来，这对黑斯蒂而言都是一样，那就是这样的事决不允许再发生。
As for the talk of deposing and electing captains, he hoped they were all free men and could attend their own affairs. 对于撤销和选举头头的事，他希望他们都是自由人，能管好自己的事情就行了。
That was dust flung in their eyes, and so was the proposal to fight Harris. 有了头头，那他就成了众人眼里不爽的人物，同哈里斯决斗的事情也不可行。
“He shall fight no one in this camp, I can tell him that,” said Hastie. “我会跟他说，在这个帐篷里他不能同任何人打架，”黑斯蒂说，
“We had trouble enough to get his arms away from him, and we should look pretty fools to give them back again. “我们好不容易才解除了他的武器，现在把武器还给他，我们岂不是太蠢了。
But if it’s excitement the gentleman is after, I can supply him with more than perhaps he cares about. 不过如果这位绅士想找点儿刺激，我会多给他点儿，多到他受不了。
For I have no intention to spend the remainder of my life in these mountains; already I have been too long; and I propose that he should immediately tell us where that treasure is, or else immediately be shot. 因为我无意在这深山老林中度过余生，现在就已经受够了，我建议他立刻告诉我们宝藏在哪，否则我们就立刻杀了他。”
And there,” says he, producing his weapon, “there is the pistol that I mean to use.” 说着，他掏出了武器，说道，“对，就是用这把枪。”
“Come, I call you a man,” cries the Master, sitting up and looking at the speaker with an air of admiration. “来吧，我拿你当个男子汉。”大少爷高声喊道，他坐起来，用钦佩的眼光看着说话的人。
“I didn’t ask you to call me anything,” returned Hastie; “which is it to be?” “我可没让你拿我当什么，”黑斯蒂回答道，“你究竟想怎么样？”
“That’s an idle question,” said the Master. “这真是个愚蠢的问题。”大少爷说，
“Needs must when the devil drives. “被恶魔逼迫的时候就该采取行动。
The truth is we are within easy walk of the place, and I will show it you to-morrow.” 其实宝藏离这儿可就不远了，明天我就可以指给你看。”
With that, as if all were quite settled, and settled exactly to his mind, he walked off to his tent, whither Secundra had preceded him. 说完这些话，似乎一切都定了下来，一切都按他的想法来，大少爷走向自己的帐篷，赛昆德拉走在他的前头。
I cannot think of these last turns and wriggles of my old enemy except with admiration; scarce even pity is mingled with the sentiment, so strongly the man supported, so boldly resisted his misfortunes. 除了钦佩，我对自己的夙敌最后的挣扎没有别的想法，甚至没有多少同情，他在不幸面前是那么坚强，那么不屈。
Even at that hour, when he perceived himself quite lost, when he saw he had but effected an exchange of enemies, and overthrown Harris to set Hastie up, no sign of weakness appeared in his behaviour, and he withdrew to his tent, already determined (I must suppose) upon affronting the incredible hazard of his last expedient, with the same easy, assured, genteel expression and demeanour as he might have left a theatre withal to join a supper of the wits. 即便是在他完全不知所以的时候，在他好不容易把哈里斯拉下马却发现树立了新的敌人黑斯蒂的时候，他的言行举止也没有显出丝毫软弱。他进了帐篷，我想他肯定已经决意孤注一掷做最后的拼搏了。他依旧显出一副轻松、自信、彬彬有礼的神态，仿佛刚离开剧院要去参加智者的聚会呢。
But doubtless within, if we could see there, his soul trembled. 不过我们确定无疑的是，如果我们能看到的话，他的心肯定是在砰砰乱跳。
Early in the night, word went about the camp that he was sick; and the first thing the next morning he called Hastie to his side, and inquired most anxiously if he had any skill in medicine. 前半夜，帐篷里传出话说他病了，第二天一大早他把黑斯蒂叫到他身边，焦急地问他会不会治病。
As a matter of fact, this was a vanity of that fallen divinity student’s, to which he had cunningly addressed himself. 事实上，凡是学神学的人不懂也要装着懂医术，像黑斯蒂这种堕落的神学院学生更不例外。
Hastie examined him; and being flattered, ignorant, and highly auspicious, knew not in the least whether the man was sick or malingering. 黑斯蒂给他查了查，说了些奉承、宽慰的吉祥话，但对大少爷到底是真病了还是装病却无从知晓。
In this state he went forth again to his companions; and (as the thing which would give himself most consequence either way) announced that the patient was in a fair way to die. 他走出去把这些情况跟同伙说了一下，反正不管哪种情况都会给他带来很大的麻烦，他便说这个病人可能要死了。
“For all that,” he added with an oath, “and if he bursts by the wayside, he must bring us this morning to the treasure.” “不管怎么样，”他诅咒说，“就算是死在路上，他今天早上也一定得带我们去找到宝藏。”
But there were several in the camp (Mountain among the number) whom this brutality revolted. 然而队伍里有几个人，包括芒廷在内，对这种粗暴的行为表示不满。
They would have seen the Master pistolled, or pistolled him themselves, without the smallest sentiment of pity; but they seemed to have been touched by his gallant fight and unequivocal defeat the night before; perhaps, too, they were even already beginning to oppose themselves to their new leader: at least, they now declared that (if the man was sick) he should have a day’s rest in spite of Hastie’s teeth. 如果大少爷被枪杀或者自杀，他们不会有半点儿同情心，只是他们被头天晚上大少爷的勇气以及竞选头目失败的过程所感动，也或许他们开始抵触新头目，反正他们表示如果这个人确实病了，不管黑斯蒂怎么说，他都应该让病人休息一天。
The next morning he was manifestly worse, and Hastie himself began to display something of humane concern, so easily does even the pretence of doctoring awaken sympathy. 第二天早上，大少爷病情明显恶化，黑斯蒂本人也开始展现些许人性关怀，即便是假装的医生，他也会容易产生怜悯之心。
The third the Master called Mountain and Hastie to the tent, announced himself to be dying, gave them full particulars as to the position of the cache, and begged them to set out incontinently on the quest, so that they might see if he deceived them, and (if they were at first unsuccessful) he should be able to correct their error. 第三天，大少爷把芒廷和黑斯蒂叫到自己的帐篷内，跟他们说自己快要死了，把宝藏埋藏地点详尽地告诉他们，并请求他们立刻去努力寻找，这样他们就能知道他有没有说谎，如果他们开始时没找到，他还可以帮助他们修正。
But here arose a difficulty on which he doubtless counted. 但这样一来就出现了一个麻烦，他谁也信不过。
None of these men would trust another, none would consent to stay behind. 这些人谁也不信谁，没人愿意留在这里照顾他。
On the other hand, although the Master seemed extremely low, spoke scarce above a whisper, and lay much of the time insensible, it was still possible it was a fraudulent sickness; and if all went treasure-hunting, it might prove they had gone upon a wild-goose chase, and return to find their prisoner flown. 另一方面，虽然大少爷看起来极度虚弱，说起话来声音极其微弱，大部分时间躺在那里没有知觉，可他仍有在装病的可能，如果所有人都去寻找宝藏，可能会徒劳无功，反而让大少爷逃跑。
They concluded, therefore, to hang idling round the camp, alleging sympathy to their reason; and certainly, so mingled are our dispositions, several were sincerely (if not very deeply) affected by the natural peril of the man whom they callously designed to murder. 于是他们最后决定就在营地四周转悠，借口不忍心扔下病人，现在很多人又开始不忍心看着那个原先要被他们谋害的人就这样死去。
In the afternoon, Hastie was called to the bedside to pray: the which (incredible as it must appear) he did with unction; about eight at night, the wailing of Secundra announced that all was over; and before ten, the Indian, with a link stuck in the ground, was toiling at the grave. 当天下午，黑斯蒂被叫去做祈祷，他竟然虚情假意地做了，大约晚上8点左右，赛昆德拉的哭声宣告一切都结束了。10点之前，那个印度人已经在地上插了个火把，开始辛苦挖墓穴。
Sunrise of next day beheld the Master’s burial, all hands attending with great decency of demeanour; and the body was laid in the earth, wrapped in a fur robe, with only the face uncovered; which last was of a waxy whiteness, and had the nostrils plugged according to some Oriental habit of Secundra’s. 第二天太阳升起的时候，大少爷的尸体入了墓，大家纷纷来帮忙，表情肃穆。尸体放在墓穴中，裹着一块绒毛的长袍，只露出一张惨白如蜡的脸，鼻孔也按照赛昆德拉东方人的传统用塞子塞住了。
No sooner was the grave filled than the lamentations of the Indian once more struck concern to every heart; and it appears this gang of murderers, so far from resenting his outcries, although both distressful and (in such a country) perilous to their own safety, roughly but kindly endeavoured to console him. 没过多久，墓穴填满了土，赛昆德拉的哭声再一次震撼着周围每一个人的心灵。看起来这群杀人凶手非但没有对他的哭声不满，反而用粗俗却温暖的话语安慰他，虽然哭声会危及他们自身的安全。
But if human nature is even in the worst of men occasionally kind, it is still, and before all things, greedy; and they soon turned from the mourner to their own concerns. 然而如果最穷凶极恶的人也有善良时候的话，那么贪婪则是人类永恒不变的劣行；他们不一会儿就从悲伤中转到他们自己所关心的事情上来。
The cache of the treasure being hard by, although yet unidentified, it was concluded not to break camp; and the day passed, on the part of the voyagers, in unavailing exploration of the woods, Secundra the while lying on his master’s grave. 虽然宝藏还没有确定位置，但就在附近。他们决定不撤营，白天在树林里徒劳奔波，而赛昆德拉则躺在主人墓地上。
That night they placed no sentinel, but lay altogether about the fire, in the customary woodman fashion, the heads outward, like the spokes of a wheel. 晚上他们不设防，像樵夫一样一起围在火堆旁，头朝外围了一圈，像车轮辐条一样。
Morning found them in the same disposition; only Pinkerton, who lay on Mountain’s right, between him and Hastie, had (in the hours of darkness) been secretly butchered, and there lay, still wrapped as to his body in his mantle, but offering above that ungodly and horrific spectacle of the scalped head. 早上起来，他们还是在相同的位置上，只是躺在芒廷右边、黑斯蒂左边的平克顿在晚上被人给偷偷杀了。那具尸体仍然裹着一件斗篷，只是脑袋上的头皮被割走了，令人毛骨悚然。
The gang were that morning as pale as a company of phantoms, for the pertinacity of Indian war (or to speak more correctly, Indian murder) was well known to all. 那天早上，队伍像一群鬼一样面色苍白，因为他们深知印第安人战争，或者准确地说印第安人的杀戮绝对不是闹着玩的。
But they laid the chief blame on their unsentinelled posture; and fired with the neighbourhood of the treasure, determined to continue where they were. 他们把主要责任归咎为没有设岗哨，于是便在宝藏附近鸣枪示威，他们决心留在这里。
Pinkerton was buried hard by the Master; the survivors again passed the day in exploration, and returned in a mingled humour of anxiety and hope, being partly certain they were now close on the discovery of what they sought, and on the other hand (with the return of darkness) were infected with the fear of Indians. 平克顿就埋在大少爷附近，幸存下来的人白天继续搜索，回到营地时希望中又带着几分焦虑，一方面确信他们现在离发现宝藏不远了，另一方面回来时天已经暗下来，时刻感受到印第安人带来的恐惧。
Mountain was the first sentry; he declares he neither slept nor yet sat down, but kept his watch with a perpetual and straining vigilance, and it was even with unconcern that (when he saw by the stars his time was up) he drew near the fire to awaken his successor. 芒廷是第一个站岗的，他宣称自己始终没有睡着或者坐下，一直紧紧盯着，保持十分的警觉。他抬头看了看天上的繁星，知道他站岗的时间过去了，他走进火堆叫醒接班的同伙。
This man (it was Hicks the shoemaker) slept on the lee side of the circle, something farther off in consequence than those to windward, and in a place darkened by the blowing smoke. 这个人是鞋匠希克斯，他睡在背风的地方，比那些睡在顺风方向的人离火堆稍远一点儿，那里正好被烟雾笼罩，一片漆黑。
Mountain stooped and took him by the shoulder; his hand was at once smeared by some adhesive wetness; and (the wind at the moment veering) the firelight shone upon the sleeper, and showed him, like Pinkerton, dead and scalped. 芒廷停下来，抓着他的肩膀，立刻感觉到自己手上黏糊糊的，恰好风向变了，火光照在希克斯身上，芒廷发现他已经死了，和平克顿一样，也被人割走了头皮。
