It was clear they had fallen in the hands of one of those matchless Indian bravos, that will sometimes follow a party for days, and in spite of indefatigable travel, and unsleeping watch, continue to keep up with their advance, and steal a scalp at every resting-place. 很明显，他们落入了那些无人能敌的印第安暴徒手里，那些人有时会连续好几天跟踪一群人，然后不管是连续赶路还是彻夜不眠的守候，都会连续出击，在每个休息的地方都可能剥去被跟踪人的头皮。
Upon this discovery, the treasure-seekers, already reduced to a poor half dozen, fell into mere dismay, seized a few necessaries, and deserting the remainder of their goods, fled outright into the forest. 意识这一点，仅存的六个寻宝人吓得魂飞魄散，除了少数必需品外把其他东西全扔了，匆忙跑进树林。
Their fire they left still burning, and their dead comrade unburied. 他们留下的火堆还在燃烧，撇下的同伴尸体也没顾得上掩埋。
All day they ceased not to flee, eating by the way, from hand to mouth; and since they feared to sleep, continued to advance at random even in the hours of darkness. 他们白天不再逃窜，在路上吃点儿随身带的东西，晚上因为害怕不敢睡觉，他们就摸黑赶路。
But the limit of man’s endurance is soon reached; when they rested at last it was to sleep profoundly; and when they woke, it was to find that the enemy was still upon their heels, and death and mutilation had once more lessened and deformed their company. 但是这样他们很快到了耐力的极限，他们刚坐下休息就很快睡着了，当他们醒来时发现，敌人仍在追赶他们，又有同伴惨遭杀害和肢解。
By this they had become light-headed, they had quite missed their path in the wilderness, their stores were already running low. 到了这个地步，他们已经被弄得晕头转向，在丛林中彻底迷了路，随身携带的东西也所剩无几。
With the further horrors, it is superfluous that I should swell this narrative, already too prolonged. 由于说到这里故事已经很长了，至于那些更恐怖的细节就不详细说明了。
Suffice it to say that when at length a night passed by innocuous, and they might breathe again in the hope that the murderer had at last desisted from pursuit, Mountain and Secundra were alone. 单说有一晚安全过去了，仅剩下芒廷和赛昆德拉两人，他们觉得谋杀者终于停止了追杀，这才松了口气。
The trader is firmly persuaded their unseen enemy was some warrior of his own acquaintance, and that he himself was spared by favour. 芒廷坚信他们看不见的敌人一定是他的熟人，因为喜欢他才没有杀他。
The mercy extended to Secundra he explains on the ground that the East Indian was thought to be insane; partly from the fact that, through all the horrors of the flight and while others were casting away their very food and weapons, Secundra continued to stagger forward with a mattock on his shoulder, and partly because, in the last days and with a great degree of heat and fluency, he perpetually spoke with himself in his own language. 这份怜悯之心也延伸到了赛昆德拉身上，因为他们一定以为这个来自东方的印度人已经疯了，可能是因为经历过惊吓，其他人逃跑时把粮食和武器都扔了，而赛昆德拉却始终肩扛着一把锄头跟着跌跌撞撞地跑，或者可能因为最后几天他兴奋地用家乡话自言自语，喋喋不休。
But he was sane enough when it came to English. 而他说英语的时候，却一直很理智。
“You think he will be gone quite away?” he asked, upon their blest awakening in safety. 醒来时发现自己没事，他马上问道：“你觉得他们走远了吗？”
“I pray God so, I believe so, I dare to believe so,” Mountain had replied almost with incoherence, as he described the scene to me. 芒廷跟我描述说，当时他几乎是结结巴巴地回答说：“但愿上帝保佑，我想他们走了。”
And indeed he was so much distempered that until he met us, the next morning, he could scarce be certain whether he had dreamed, or whether it was a fact, that Secundra had thereupon turned directly about and returned without a word upon their footprints, setting his face for these wintry and hungry solitudes, along a path whose every stage was mile-stoned with a mutilated corpse. 事实上，遇到我们之前他都是精神恍惚，第二天早上他几乎都不知道自己是在做梦还是真事。他看到赛昆德拉顺着他们的足迹返身而去，不辞而别，不惧严寒和饥饿，毅然走上留有同伴尸骨的路。
[1] Tear-marked. [1]满面泪痕
Chapter 12 第十二章
The Journey in the Wilderness (continued). 涉足蛮荒（续）
Mountain’s story, as it was laid before Sir William Johnson and my lord, was shorn, of course, of all the earlier particulars, and the expedition described to have proceeded uneventfully, until the Master sickened. 芒廷呈现在威廉·约翰逊爵士和爵爷面前的故事，当然所有的早期故事细节都经过了一些修剪，他描述的远征在大少爷病倒前都是平安无事。
But the latter part was very forcibly related, the speaker visibly thrilling to his recollections; and our then situation, on the fringe of the same desert, and the private interests of each, gave him an audience prepared to share in his emotions. 后面的部分相互间很牵强，显然是他有些记忆模糊。我们现在处于同一片蛮荒之地的边缘，再加上各个人的私心，这让芒廷的听众与他产生了共鸣。
For Mountain’s intelligence not only changed the world for my Lord Durrisdeer, but materially affected the designs of Sir William Johnson. 芒廷的聪明才智不仅改变了达里斯迪尔爵爷的看法，也大大影响到威廉爵士的计划。
These I find I must lay more at length before the reader. 我觉得我必须将更多的事实呈现给读者。
Word had reached Albany of dubious import; it had been rumoured some hostility was to be put in act; and the Indian diplomatist had, thereupon, sped into the wilderness, even at the approach of winter, to nip that mischief in the bud. 有些谣言已经传到了奥尔巴尼，说有人要采取报复行动，这位印第安外交官威廉爵士于是不顾严寒，进入到蛮荒之地以防止报复行动的发生。
Here, on the borders, he learned that he was come too late; and a difficult choice was thus presented to a man (upon the whole) not any more bold than prudent. 当他到达边界的时候，他发现已经来晚了，于是艰难的抉择落到了这个勇敢审慎的人身上。
His standing with the painted braves may be compared to that of my Lord President Culloden among the chiefs of our own Highlanders at the ’forty-five; that is as much as to say, he was, to these men, reason’s only speaking trumpet, and counsels of peace and moderation, if they were to prevail at all, must prevail singly through his influence. 他跟那些涂脸的印第安勇士站在一起就好比1745年库勒登总督跟苏格兰高原的起义首领在一起。也就是说，他是那些人当中有理性，懂得休战与和平的人。如果他们获胜的话，也肯定是受到他的影响。
If, then, he should return, the province must lie open to all the abominable tragedies of Indian war—the houses blaze, the wayfarer be cut off, and the men of the woods collect their usual disgusting spoil of human scalps. 如果他回到城里，那个省将重演无休止的战争悲剧——焚烧房屋、抢劫旅客、到森林里割活人头皮等。
On the other side, to go farther forth, to risk so small a party deeper in the desert, to carry words of peace among warlike savages already rejoicing to return to war: here was an extremity from which it was easy to perceive his mind revolted. 另一方面，那么几个人的队伍要深入蛮荒之地，去给重新开战而欢欣鼓舞的野蛮人传递和平的福音，他内心对这种计划的反对是可想而知的。
“I have come too late,” he said more than once, and would fall into a deep consideration, his head bowed in his hands, his foot patting the ground. 威廉爵士不止一次地说：“我来得太晚了。”然后头埋入双手中，陷入沉思，脚拍打着地面。
At length he raised his face and looked upon us, that is to say upon my lord, Mountain, and myself, sitting close round a small fire, which had been made for privacy in one corner of the camp. 最后他抬起头看着我们——围坐在火堆旁的爵爷、芒廷和我，这一切秘密发生在帐篷的一角。
“My lord, to be quite frank with you, I find myself in two minds,” said he. “爵爷，坦白说，我自己左右为难，”威廉爵士说，
“I think it very needful I should go on, but not at all proper I should any longer enjoy the pleasure of your company. “一方面我觉得非常有必要继续前行，另一方面，跟你们在一起我体会不到丝毫的乐趣。
We are here still upon the water side; and I think the risk to southward no great matter. 现在我们还在水边，再往南走也没有多大风险。
Will not yourself and Mr. Mackellar take a single boat’s crew and return to Albany?” 你和麦凯勒就不能另外单独乘船回奥尔巴尼吗？”
My lord, I should say, had listened to Mountain’s narrative, regarding him throughout with a painful intensity of gaze; and since the tale concluded, had sat as in a dream. 我想说，刚才爵爷听着芒廷的故事，一边直瞪瞪地看着他。直到故事讲完了，他好像还在梦里。
There was something very daunting in his look; something to my eyes not rightly human; the face, lean, and dark, and aged, the mouth painful, the teeth disclosed in a perpetual rictus; the eyeball swimming clear of the lids upon a field of blood-shot white. 他的表情中带有些令人畏缩的东西，一些不像正常人的东西。他的脸又黑又瘦，略显苍老，嘴角痛苦地颤抖，张着嘴露出牙齿，眼珠在充了血的眼白中间转悠。
I could not behold him myself without a jarring irritation, such as, I believe, is too frequently the uppermost feeling on the sickness of those dear to us. 我自己痛苦地看着他，我觉得就像是看到自己的亲人患病时的感觉。
Others, I could not but remark. 有一些事我不得不提及。
were scarce able to support his neighbourhood—Sir William eviting to be near him, Mountain dodging his eye, and, when he met it, blenching and halting in his story. 其他人都不敢离他太近，威廉爵士尽量避开他，芒廷讲故事时眼神闪躲，看到爵爷的时候也是吞吞吐吐。
At this appeal, however, my lord appeared to recover his command upon himself. 听到威廉爵士的建议，爵爷似乎一下子恢复了知觉。
“To Albany?” said he, with a good voice. 他声音和蔼地说：“回奥尔巴尼？”
“Not short of it, at least,” replied Sir William. “总不能到别的地方去吧，”威廉爵士回答说，
“There is no safety nearer hand.” “这里很不安全。”
“I would be very sweir [1] to return,” says my lord. “就这么回去，我很不甘心[1]，”爵爷说，
“I am not afraid—of Indians,” he added, with a jerk. “我不害怕印第安人。”说到印第安人，爵爷停顿了一下。
“I wish that I could say so much,” returned Sir William, smiling; “although, if any man durst say it, it should be myself. “这样的话我可不敢说，”威廉爵士笑着回答说，“即便有人敢这么说，我也不敢。
But you are to keep in view my responsibility, and that as the voyage has now become highly dangerous, and your business—if you ever had any,” says he, “brought quite to a conclusion by the distressing family intelligence you have received, I should be hardly justified if I even suffered you to proceed, and run the risk of some obloquy if anything regrettable should follow.” 但是你得从我的责任角度看看，现在路途越来越艰险，如果你有自己的目的的话，你也打听到了你哥哥的消息，目的算是达到了。我没有任何理由让你继续前行，要是你有个三长两短的话，我可是会内心有愧啊。”
My lord turned to Mountain. 爵爷转向芒廷。
“What did he pretend he died of?” he asked. “他是怎么假装死的？”他问道。
“I don’t think I understand your honour,” said the trader, pausing like a man very much affected, in the dressing of some cruel frost-bites. 商人芒廷，一副被冻伤严重侵袭的模样，停顿了一下说道：“我想我不明白您的意思，先生。”
For a moment my lord seemed at a full stop; and then, with some irritation, “I ask you what he died of. 爵爷沉默了好久不出声，然后微怒地说：“我是问你他怎么死的。
Surely that’s a plain question,” said he. 多明白的问题啊。”
“Oh! “噢！
I don’t know,” said Mountain. 我不知道，”芒廷回答说，
“Hastie even never knew. “连黑斯蒂都不知道。
He seemed to sicken natural, and just pass away.” 他看起来好像很自然地得了病，然后就死掉了。”
“There it is, you see!” concluded my lord, turning to Sir William. 爵爷转身面对威廉爵士，总结说：“看看，这就是了。”
“Your lordship is too deep for me,” replied Sir William. 威廉爵士回答说：“你的话我理解不了。”
“Why,” says my lord, “this in a matter of succession; my son’s title may be called in doubt; and the man being supposed to be dead of nobody can tell what, a great deal of suspicion would be naturally roused.” “为什么？”爵爷说，“这可是关系到继承权的大事，我儿子将来继承的爵位可能引起争议，大家都不知道他是怎么死的，很自然地就会有很多怀疑产生、谣言就会满天飞。”
“But, God damn me, the man’s buried!” cried Sir William. “真是活见鬼！那个人已经被埋掉了！”威廉爵士说。
“I will never believe that,” returned my lord, painfully trembling. “我才不相信那些话。”爵爷痛苦地颤抖着说。
“I’ll never believe it!” he cried again, and jumped to his feet. 他跳起来，又喊道：“我永远不相信！”
“Did he LOOK dead?” he asked of Mountain. 他问芒廷说：“他看起来死掉了吗？”
“Look dead?” repeated the trader. “看起来死了？”芒廷说，
“He looked white. “他面色苍白。
Why, what would he be at? 还能怎么了？
I tell you, I put the sods upon him.” 我告诉您，我亲手把他给埋了。”
My lord caught Sir William by the coat with a hooked hand. 爵爷伸出手抓住威廉爵士的衣裳。
“This man has the name of my brother,” says he, “but it’s well understood that he was never canny.” 他说：“这个人名义上是我哥哥，可他从来不食人间烟火。”
“Canny?” says Sir William. 威廉爵士说：“不食人间烟火？
“What is that?” 那是什么？”
“He’s not of this world,” whispered my lord, “neither him nor the black deil that serves him. “他不是这个世界上的人，”爵爷喃喃说道，“那个伺候他的黑鬼也是一路货色。
I have struck my sword throughout his vitals,” he cried; “I have felt the hilt dirl [2] on his breastbone, and the hot blood spirt in my very face, time and again, time and again!” he repeated, with a gesture indescribable. 我曾经把宝剑刺进他的要害，我握着剑柄的手都感觉到剑在他的胸骨里咯吱响，那滚烫的热血喷了我一脸，一次又一次，一次又一次，”他重复着这句话，做了个难以言表的动作。
“But he was never dead for that,” said he, and I sighed aloud. “他却怎么都死不了。”他说。听到这话，我大声叹着气。
“Why should I think he was dead now? “现在我怎么会相信他死掉了呢？
No, not till I see him rotting,” says he. 不，除非我亲眼看着他的尸体腐烂。”他说。
Sir William looked across at me with a long face. 威廉爵士拉长脸看着我。
Mountain forgot his wounds, staring and gaping. 芒廷也忘掉了他的伤口，瞪着眼，张着嘴。
“My lord,” said I, “I wish you would collect your spirits.” “爵爷，”我说道，“我觉得您还是冷静点儿好。”
But my throat was so dry, and my own wits so scattered, I could add no more. 然而我的喉咙干涩，心乱如麻，再也说不出什么来。
“No,” says my lord, “it’s not to be supposed that he would understand me. “不，”爵爷说，“或许他理解不了我的意思。
Mackellar does, for he kens all, and has seen him buried before now. 可麦凯勒你能理解，因为你知道这一切，也曾看到过这个人被埋。
This is a very good servant to me, Sir William, this man Mackellar; he buried him with his own hands—he and my father—by the light of two siller candlesticks. 威廉爵士，麦凯勒这个人可是个不错的管家，他与家父一起亲手埋的那人，借着两个银烛台的烛光。
The other man is a familiar spirit; he brought him from Coromandel. 那个奴仆是那家伙从印度的科罗曼德尔带回来的。
I would have told ye this long syne, Sir William, only it was in the family.” 威廉爵士，这我早就该告诉你，只是怕家丑外扬才没有说。”
These last remarks he made with a kind of a melancholy composure, and his time of aberration seemed to pass away. 说到最后几句时，他哀伤中带着冷静，似乎刚才那种神情恍惚的状态已然消逝。
“You can ask yourself what it all means,” he proceeded. “你问问自己这意味着什么，”他继续说道，
“My brother falls sick, and dies, and is buried, as so they say; and all seems very plain. “他们说我哥哥病倒了，死了，然后埋了，这一切都是这样平淡无奇。
But why did the familiar go back? 可是那个印度奴仆为什么要原路返回呢？
I think ye must see for yourself it’s a point that wants some clearing.” 我想这一点需要你亲自弄清楚。”
“I will be at your service, my lord, in half a minute,” said Sir William, rising. “爵爷，我过会儿再来陪你。”威廉爵士站起身说道。
“Mr. Mackellar, two words with you;” and he led me without the camp, the frost crunching in our steps, the trees standing at our elbow, hoar with frost, even as on that night in the Long Shrubbery. 他领我走出帐篷，对我说：“麦凯勒，我有两句话想对你说。” 我们脚下的霜冻嘎吱嘎吱地响，树枝擦着我们的手肘，上面布满霜，这像极了当年兄弟俩在灌木林里决斗的那个晚上。
“Of course, this is midsummer madness,” said Sir William, as soon as we were gotten out of bearing. 我们走到个别人听不到的地方，威廉爵士说：“真是荒谬！”
“Why, certainly,” said I. “唷! 这是当然的，”我说，
“The man is mad. “因为那个人疯了。
I think that manifest.” 我想这是显而易见的。”
“Shall I seize and bind him?” asked Sir William. “难道我们该把他抓起来绑住吗？”威廉爵士问道，
“I will upon your authority. “这事由你做主，
If these are all ravings, that should certainly be done.” 如果他真的疯了的话，我们就真得这么干。”
I looked down upon the ground, back at the camp, with its bright fires and the folk watching us, and about me on the woods and mountains; there was just the one way that I could not look, and that was in Sir William’s face. 我低下头看了看地面，又回头看看帐篷，里面的火很旺，人们看着我们。我向四周看了看，瞅了瞅树林和山脉，只有一个地方不敢看，那就是威廉爵士的脸。
“Sir William,” said I at last, “I think my lord not sane, and have long thought him so. “威廉爵士，”我最后说，“我是觉得我的爵爷不正常，其实我早就有这个想法了。
But there are degrees in madness; and whether he should be brought under restraint—Sir William, I am no fit judge,” I concluded. 但是疯也有个限度，至于该不该把他监禁起来，这个我可说不好。”我总结道。
“I will be the judge,” said he. “那我来判断好了，”他说，
“I ask for facts. “我需要证据。
Was there, in all that jargon, any word of truth or sanity? 是不是他的胡言乱语里还是有那么一两句实话的？
Do you hesitate?” 你在犹豫？”
he asked. 他问道：
“Am I to understand you have buried this gentleman before?” 我能理解为你以前埋过那位绅士吗？”
“Not buried,” said I; and then, taking up courage at last, “Sir William,” said I, “unless I were to tell you a long story, which much concerns a noble family (and myself not in the least), it would be impossible to make this matter clear to you. “没埋过，”我答道，然后终于鼓足了勇气说，“威廉爵士，除非我跟您说一个很长的故事，这牵扯到一个贵族家庭和我个人，不然您弄不清这件事。
Say the word, and I will do it, right or wrong. 您说句话吧，不管对错我都会遵命。
And, at any rate, I will say so much, that my lord is not so crazy as he seems. 不管怎么样，我只能说爵爷没他看上去那样疯狂。
This is a strange matter, into the tail of which you are unhappily drifted.” 这件事本身就很蹊跷，而您又提及到了他的痛处。”
“I desire none of your secrets,” replied Sir William; “but I will be plain, at the risk of incivility, and confess that I take little pleasure in my present company.” “我无意打听你们的秘密，”威廉爵士回答说，“但是坦白说，也很不客气地说，跟今天这几位在一起我没有多大兴致。”
“I would be the last to blame you,” said I, “for that.” 我说：“我绝不会为这个去责怪您的。”
“I have not asked either for your censure or your praise, sir,” returned Sir William. 威廉爵士回答说：“先生，我可没有要求你发表褒贬评论呢。
“I desire simply to be quit of you; and to that effect, I put a boat and complement of men at your disposal.” 我只是想跟你们分开，为此我还为你们准备了一条船和几个助手呢。”
“This is fairly offered,” said I, after reflection. 我思考了一阵后，说：“那真是太感谢了。
“But you must suffer me to say a word upon the other side. 但您可得帮我在爵爷那边说句话。
We have a natural curiosity to learn the truth of this affair; I have some of it myself; my lord (it is very plain) has but too much. 我们对这件事的真相一直比较好奇，我们掌握了一部分，很显然爵爷知道的更多。
The matter of the Indian’s return is enigmatical.” 那个印度人返回去真是令人匪夷所思。”
“I think so myself,” Sir William interrupted, “and I propose (since I go in that direction) to probe it to the bottom. “我自己也这么觉得，”威廉爵士插话说，“因为我也往那个方向走，我建议去弄个究竟。
Whether or not the man has gone like a dog to die upon his master’s grave, his life, at least, is in great danger, and I propose, if I can, to save it. 不管那个印度人会不会像一条狗一样去他主人墓前殉葬，反正他的生命危在旦夕，我建议咱们去尽最大努力挽救他。
There is nothing against his character?” 这个人有什么劣迹没有？”
“Nothing, Sir William,” I replied. 我回答说：“没有。”
“And the other?” he said. 他说：“那你家大少爷呢？”
“I have heard my lord, of course; but, from the circumstances of his servant’s loyalty, I must suppose he had some noble qualities.” 他又接着说，“我从爵爷那听说过一些，不过既然他的仆人对他这么忠诚，我想他还是有些可贵品质的。”
“You must not ask me that!” “这样的问题您可不要问我！”
I cried. 我说道，
“Hell may have noble flames. “地狱里也有好的东西。
I have known him a score of years, and always hated, and always admired, and always slavishly feared him.” 我认识他这么多年了，我一直那么恨他，可也佩服他、害怕他。”
“I appear to intrude again upon your secrets,” said Sir William, “believe me, inadvertently. “好像我又在探寻你们的秘密似的，”威廉爵士说，“相信我，我不是有意的。
Enough that I will see the grave, and (if possible) rescue the Indian. 我只要看到那个坟墓的话就足够了，如果可能的话就救下那个印度人。
Upon these terms, can you persuade your master to return to Albany?” 如果满足了这些条件，能说服你家爵爷回奥尔巴尼吗？”
“Sir William,” said I, “I will tell you how it is. “威廉爵士，”我说，“我告诉您这究竟是怎么回事。
You do not see my lord to advantage; it will seem even strange to you that I should love him; but I do, and I am not alone. 你没有看到爵爷的优点，也许您听起来会感到诧异，喜欢他的人可不止我一个。
If he goes back to Albany, it must be by force, and it will be the death-warrant of his reason, and perhaps his life. 如果他回到奥尔巴尼，那他肯定是受了胁迫，那样的话，他的理智，甚至是他的生命也就宣告完结。
That is my sincere belief; but I am in your hands, and ready to obey, if you will assume so much responsibility as to command.” 这是我的真实想法，但如果您愿意承担责任的话，我会听您的，我也做好了服从命令的准备。”
“I will have no shred of responsibility; it is my single endeavour to avoid the same,” cried Sir William. “我可没有任何责任，我唯一想做的就是回避责任，”威廉爵士说道，
“You insist upon following this journey up; and be it so! “你坚持继续这趟旅行，那就跟着吧！
I wash my hands of the whole matter.” 我才不管这事呢。”
With which word, he turned upon his heel and gave the order to break camp; and my lord, who had been hovering near by, came instantly to my side. 说着这些话，威廉爵士转身下令拔营，刚才一直在帐篷旁边转悠的爵爷立刻来到我的身边。
“Which is it to be?” said he. 他问：“他刚才怎么说？”
“You are to have your way,” I answered. “按照您的想法做吧，”我回答说，
“You shall see the grave.” “您会看到那个人的坟墓的。”
The situation of the Master’s grave was, between guides, easily described; it lay, indeed, beside a chief landmark of the wilderness, a certain range of peaks, conspicuous by their design and altitude, and the source of many brawling tributaries to that inland sea, Lake Champlain. 大少爷的墓地位于两个路标之间，很好辨认。其实就在这荒野的主要标志旁边，有连绵的高山，有好几条流入内海尚普兰湖的大川小溪都发源于此。
It was therefore possible to strike for it direct, instead of following back the blood-stained trail of the fugitives, and to cover, in some sixteen hours of march, a distance which their perturbed wanderings had extended over more than sixty. 因此我们完全可以抄近路，而不必沿着那条沾染那群亡命之徒的血迹的路绕来绕去。这段路程他们走了六十多个小时，而我们抄近路只走了十六个小时。
Our boats we left under a guard upon the river; it was, indeed, probable we should return to find them frozen fast; and the small equipment with which we set forth upon the expedition, included not only an infinity of furs to protect us from the cold, but an arsenal of snow-shoes to render travel possible, when the inevitable snow should fall. 我们把船只停放在河边的一个哨卡附近。当我们回来的时候，船估计已经冻住了。我们带些随身物品开始了探险，不仅包括御寒用的大量皮毛，还包括一大堆雪鞋，下雪的时候穿着行走可以更方便些。
Considerable alarm was manifested at our departure; the march was conducted with soldierly precaution, the camp at night sedulously chosen and patrolled; and it was a consideration of this sort that arrested us, the second day, within not many hundred yards of our destination—the night being already imminent, the spot in which we stood well qualified to be a strong camp for a party of our numbers; and Sir William, therefore, on a sudden thought, arresting our advance. 我们出发时已经出现了些令人害怕的警报，我们长途跋涉过程中采取了军队远征的某些防御措施，晚上的帐篷搭建在精心选定的地方，设置了岗哨。第二天，在离目的地两三百码的地方，为了谨慎起见，我们停止了前行，这时天已经快黑了。我们站的地方正适合我们这么多人的队伍宿营，威廉爵士因此突然叫停了我们前进的脚步。
Before us was the high range of mountains toward which we had been all day deviously drawing near. 我们前面是大片的山脉，队伍沿着崎岖的山道走了一整天还没有到山脚下。
From the first light of the dawn, their silver peaks had been the goal of our advance across a tumbled lowland forest, thrid with rough streams, and strewn with monstrous boulders; the peaks (as I say) silver, for already at the higher altitudes the snow fell nightly; but the woods and the low ground only breathed upon with frost. 从看见清晨的第一缕阳光起，银色的山峰就成了我们越过低地后的目标，那个低地里树木茂盛，溪流湍急，怪石崚峋。山顶是银色的，因为海拔高，每天夜里山顶几乎都会下雪，而低地里的树木和地面只是稍稍染上了一点儿白霜。
All day heaven had been charged with ugly vapours, in the which the sun swam and glimmered like a shilling piece; all day the wind blew on our left cheek barbarous cold, but very pure to breathe. 整个白天天空里充满着云雾，太阳看起来像个遨游其中的银币。寒风吹在我们的左脸颊上让我们疼痛难忍，不过空气呼吸起来倒是清新凉爽。
With the end of the afternoon, however, the wind fell; the clouds, being no longer reinforced, were scattered or drunk up; the sun set behind us with some wintry splendour, and the white brow of the mountains shared its dying glow. 黄昏时分，风停了，聚集的云层碎裂成无数的云朵，有的渐渐变淡而消失。太阳落山了，带着冬日的光芒，白皑皑的山尖上还挂着瞬息即逝的晚霞。
It was dark ere we had supper; we ate in silence, and the meal was scarce despatched before my lord slunk from the fireside to the margin of the camp; whither I made haste to follow him. 吃晚饭时天已经黑了，我们沉默无语地吃着，爵爷胡乱吃了几口饭便悄然离开火堆走向营地边缘，而我犹豫着是否跟他过去。
The camp was on high ground, overlooking a frozen lake, perhaps a mile in its longest measurement; all about us, the forest lay in heights and hollows; above rose the white mountains; and higher yet, the moon rode in a fair sky. 营地位于高地上，可以俯瞰差不多有一英里长、结着冰的湖。我们周围，森林高低错落，一抬头就能看见白茫茫的高山，更高的天空上挂着一轮明月。
There was no breath of air; nowhere a twig creaked; and the sounds of our own camp were hushed and swallowed up in the surrounding stillness. 这地方没有一丝风，没有树枝的嘎吱声，营地的声音也被旷野的寂静给吞噬了。
Now that the sun and the wind were both gone down, it appeared almost warm, like a night of July: a singular illusion of the sense, when earth, air, and water were strained to bursting with the extremity of frost. 现在太阳下山，风也停了，似乎暖和了起来，像是七月的夜晚：这是一种幻觉，因为大地、空气和流水随着霜冻的降临都静止了。
My lord (or what I still continued to call by his loved name) stood with his elbow in one hand, and his chin sunk in the other, gazing before him on the surface of the wood. 爵爷（我依然用他喜欢的方式称呼他）站在那里，一只手撑着下巴，另一只手托着这只手的手肘，直瞪瞪地看着前面的树林。
My eyes followed his, and rested almost pleasantly upon the frosted contexture of the pines, rising in moonlit hillocks, or sinking in the shadow of small glens. 我的目光随着他注视的地方游走，定格在洒满月光的山冈和山谷中沾满霜的松针上。
Hard by, I told myself, was the grave of our enemy, now gone where the wicked cease from troubling, the earth heaped for ever on his once so active limbs. 我对自己说，前面不远处就是我们敌人的坟墓，他如今再也不能为非作歹了，他那曾经灵活的四肢上压满了黄土。
I could not but think of him as somehow fortunate to be thus done with man’s anxiety and weariness, the daily expense of spirit, and that daily river of circumstance to be swum through, at any hazard, under the penalty of shame or death. 我想或许这对他也是一种幸运，毕竟不用再忍受人世间的焦虑和疲惫，不再遭受日复一日的精神折磨，不再经受外界的风吹雨打，不再为耻辱和死亡的威胁而担惊受怕。
I could not but think how good was the end of that long travel; and with that, my mind swung at a tangent to my lord. 我想大少爷长途跋涉能有个这样的结果真的很不错，想到这一点，我的思绪又回到爵爷身上。
For was not my lord dead also? a maimed soldier, looking vainly for discharge, lingering derided in the line of battle? 爵爷不也是死了吗？一个伤残的老兵，徒劳地追寻着解脱，在战壕中忍辱偷生。
A kind man, I remembered him; wise, with a decent pride, a son perhaps too dutiful, a husband only too loving, one that could suffer and be silent, one whose hand I loved to press. 我记得他是个好人，睿智又豪气十足，对父亲尽职尽孝，对妻子百般怜爱，能默默承受痛苦，跟我亲密无间。
Of a sudden, pity caught in my windpipe with a sob; I could have wept aloud to remember and behold him; and standing thus by his elbow, under the broad moon, I prayed fervently either that he should be released, or I strengthened to persist in my affection. 一瞬间，怜悯之心让我喉咙发痒，一想到看到他我就想放声大哭，于是在皎洁的月光下我这样站在他身边，真诚地祈祷他能解脱，对他的感情也始终不渝。
“Oh God,” said I, “this was the best man to me and to himself, and now I shrink from him. “上帝啊，”我说，“他是个大好人，而现在我要离开他了。
He did no wrong, or not till he was broke with sorrows; these are but his honourable wounds that we begin to shrink from. 他没做什么错事，只是过分悲伤时才可能冒犯过您，我们将要远离他，仅仅是因为他那些荣耀的伤疤。
Oh, cover them up, oh, take him away, before we hate him!” 啊，请您盖上他的伤疤吧，在我们对他产生憎恨之前将他带走！”
I was still so engaged in my own bosom, when a sound broke suddenly upon the night. 我正沉浸在内心的祈祷中，忽然一阵声音传出，打破了静夜。
It was neither very loud, nor very near; yet, bursting as it did from so profound and so prolonged a silence, it startled the camp like an alarm of trumpets. 声音不是很大，也不是很近，然而在如此漫长寂静的黑夜中突然爆发出来，像是军营里吹起了冲锋的号角那样，整个营地的人都吓醒了。
Ere I had taken breath, Sir William was beside me, the main part of the voyagers clustered at his back, intently giving ear. 没等我喘息，威廉爵士已经到了我们身边，其他人都跟在他身后，细心倾听。
Methought, as I glanced at them across my shoulder, there was a whiteness, other than moonlight, on their cheeks; and the rays of the moon reflected with a sparkle on the eyes of some, and the shadows lying black under the brows of others (according as they raised or bowed the head to listen) gave to the group a strange air of animation and anxiety. 我回头瞥了他们一眼，他们脸颊上显现出一种白色，不同于月光，月光仅从某几个人的眼里倒映出来，另外一些人在移动脑袋仔细聆听的时候，眉毛下面出现丝丝阴影与不安。
My lord was to the front, crouching a little forth, his hand raised as for silence: a man turned to stone. 爵爷在最前面，屈膝上前，他举起手示意安静，像个石头人一样。
And still the sounds continued, breathlessly renewed with a precipitate rhythm. 响声继续着，而且随着急促的节奏不停地改变。
Suddenly Mountain spoke in a loud, broken whisper, as of a man relieved. 突然芒廷打破了沉寂，那口气如释重负。
“I have it now,” he said; and, as we all turned to hear him, “the Indian must have known the cache,” he added. “我现在知道了。”他嘀咕道。我们转向他听着，他继续说：“那个印度人肯定知道埋藏宝藏的地方，
“That is he—he is digging out the treasure.” 这肯定是他在挖宝藏呢。”
“Why, to be sure!” exclaimed Sir William. “你怎么这么肯定，”威廉爵士大叫道，
“We were geese not to have supposed so much.” “我们怎么蠢到没想到这一点。”
“The only thing is,” Mountain resumed, “the sound is very close to our old camp. 芒廷继续说：“我只知道这个声音应该非常接近我们以前的宿营地。
And, again, I do not see how he is there before us, unless the man had wings!” 不过他怎么跑我们前头去了，除非他有翅膀会飞！”
“Greed and fear are wings,” remarked Sir William. “贪婪和恐惧就是翅膀，”威廉爵士说，
“But this rogue has given us an alert, and I have a notion to return the compliment. “不过这个混蛋倒是给我们提了个醒，我有个主意，给他来个以牙还牙。
What say you, gentlemen, shall we have a moonlight hunt?” 先生们，我们来个月下追捕怎么样？”
It was so agreed; dispositions were made to surround Secundra at his task; some of Sir William’s Indians hastened in advance; and a strong guard being left at our headquarters, we set forth along the uneven bottom of the forest; frost crackling, ice sometimes loudly splitting under foot; and overhead the blackness of pine-woods, and the broken brightness of the moon. 大家一致同意。布置好对正在挖宝藏的赛昆德拉进行包围的任务后，威廉爵士手下的几个印度人一马当先，一个强壮的守卫留在营地，我们沿着崎岖不平的树林行进，脚下的冰霜时不时发出轻微的碎裂声，头上的月亮也没有了光华，松树林里一片黑暗。
Our way led down into a hollow of the land; and as we descended, the sounds diminished and had almost died away. 我们下山来到了一片开阔地，我们往下走的时候，那个声音越来越弱，最后几乎消失了。
Upon the other slope it was more open, only dotted with a few pines, and several vast and scattered rocks that made inky shadows in the moonlight. 对面的山坡更加开阔，只有零星的几棵松树，几块巨石稀稀拉拉地在月光下留下墨黑的阴影。
Here the sounds began to reach us more distinctly; we could now perceive the ring of iron, and more exactly estimate the furious degree of haste with which the digger plied his instrument. 我们站在这里，声音清晰可辨，我们能清楚地看到锄头形成的圆圈，更清楚地感受到那正在挖地的人的情绪。
As we neared the top of the ascent, a bird or two winged aloft and hovered darkly in the moonlight; and the next moment we were gazing through a fringe of trees upon a singular picture. 当我们到了坡顶时，一两只鸟被惊飞，在月光下盘旋。紧接着，透过树林我们眼前出现了一幅奇特的景象。
A narrow plateau, overlooked by the white mountains, and encompassed nearer hand by woods, lay bare to the strong radiance of the moon. 白色的山峰下面有块狭长的高地，四周林木环绕，沐浴在月光下。
Rough goods, such as make the wealth of foresters, were sprinkled here and there upon the ground in meaningless disarray. 山里人用的各种物品洒落在地上，一片狼藉。
About the midst, a tent stood, silvered with frost: the door open, gaping on the black interior. 高地中间有个挂满冰霜的帐篷，门敞着，里面黑洞洞的。
At the one end of this small stage lay what seemed the tattered remnants of a man. 高地的另一头躺着一个像碎裂人形的东西。
Without doubt we had arrived upon the scene of Harris’s encampment; there were the goods scattered in the panic of flight; it was in yon tent the Master breathed his last; and the frozen carrion that lay before us was the body of the drunken shoemaker. 毫无疑问，这是当初哈里斯的营地，地上乱七八糟的都是他们当时仓皇逃跑时扔下的东西。就是在这个帐篷里大少爷喘完了最后一口气，而眼前的那具尸体就是那个醉酒的鞋匠。
It was always moving to come upon the theatre of any tragic incident; to come upon it after so many days, and to find it (in the seclusion of a desert) still unchanged, must have impressed the mind of the most careless. 回顾过去的悲惨场景，总是让人百感交集，多少天过去了，这与世隔绝的荒漠中的景象依然如故，看到这些，即使最冷酷的心灵都会颤抖。
And yet it was not that which struck us into pillars of stone; but the sight (which yet we had been half expecting) of Secundra ankle deep in the grave of his late master. 然而，令我们震惊的并不是这些，而是事先有所猜测却又预料得不十分精确的情形：赛昆德拉站在齐膝深的墓穴里——大少爷的墓穴。
He had cast the main part of his raiment by, yet his frail arms and shoulders glistered in the moonlight with a copious sweat; his face was contracted with anxiety and expectation; his blows resounded on the grave, as thick as sobs; and behind him, strangely deformed and ink-black upon the frosty ground, the creature’s shadow repeated and parodied his swift gesticulations. 他几乎脱了个精光，瘦弱的双臂和肩膀在月光下闪着汗珠，脸上满是焦急和期盼，掘地的声音在墓穴里回响，微弱得像是有人小声哭泣。他那漆黑的身影映射在后面结冻的地表上，随着他飞快的动作来回晃动。
Some night birds arose from the boughs upon our coming, and then settled back; but Secundra, absorbed in his toil; heard or heeded not at all. 我们的到来惊起几只夜鸟飞出枝头，很快又安静了下来，赛昆德拉专注于自己的工作中，丝毫也没有听到或察觉到。
I heard Mountain whisper to Sir William, “Good God! it’s the grave! 我听到芒廷轻声对威廉爵士说：“天啊，天啊，他是在挖墓穴！
He’s digging him up!” 他要把他的主子给挖出来！”
It was what we had all guessed, and yet to hear it put in language thrilled me. 这一点我们所有人都猜到了，可是听到他说出来，我还是吓了一跳。
Sir William violently started. 威廉爵士猛地大喝一声。
“You damned sacrilegious hound!” he cried. 他喊道：“你这可恶的疯狗！
“What’s this?” 你在干什么？”
Secundra leaped in the air, a little breathless cry escaped him, the tool flew from his grasp, and he stood one instant staring at the speaker. 赛昆德拉吓了一跳，嘴里不禁叫了一声，拿着的工具也从手里滑脱，他站在那里瞪着威廉爵士。
The next, swift as an arrow, he sped for the woods upon the farther side; and the next again, throwing up his hands with a violent gesture of resolution, he had begun already to retrace his steps. 然后像离弦之箭朝对面的密林逃跑，接着不知怎么回事又开始绝望地举起双手原路返回。
“Well, then, you come, you help—” he was saying. “太好了，你们来了，求你们帮帮忙。”他说。
But by now my lord had stepped beside Sir William; the moon shone fair upon his face, and the words were still upon Secundra’s lips, when he beheld and recognised his master’s enemy. 这时爵爷已经走到威廉爵士身边，月光洒在他脸上，赛昆德拉还没有说完就一眼认出了大少爷的敌人——我家爵爷。
“Him!” he screamed, clasping his hands, and shrinking on himself. 他双手一拍，浑身打战，尖叫道：“就是他！”
“Come, come!” said Sir William. 威廉爵士说：“别怕，别怕。
“There is none here to do you harm, if you be innocent; and if you be guilty, your escape is quite cut off. 如果你是无辜的，这儿没人会伤害你，如果你有罪，你也休想逃走。
Speak, what do you here among the graves of the dead and the remains of the unburied?” 说吧，你到坟堆里，到埋死尸的地方来干什么？”
“You no murderer?” inquired Secundra. “你们不是杀人犯？”赛昆德拉说，
“You true man? you see me safe?” “你们是好人？会保证我的安全吗？”
“I will see you safe, if you be innocent,” returned Sir William. 威廉爵士回答说：“如果你是清白的，我会保证你的安全。
“I have said the thing, and I see not wherefore you should doubt it.” 我说出的话，你没必要怀疑。”
“There all murderers,” cried Secundra, “that is why! “都是一群杀人犯，”赛昆德拉说，“这就是为什么！
He kill—murderer,” pointing to Mountain; “there two hire-murderers,” pointing to my lord and myself—“all gallows—murderers! 他就是杀人犯，”手指指向芒廷，接着又指着爵爷和我说，“这两个是罪该万死的谋杀犯。
Ah! 啊！
I see you all swing in a rope. 我明白了。
Now I go save the sahib; he see you swing in a rope. 你们串通好了，现在我要去把我家主人救出来。”
The sahib,” he continued, pointing to the grave, “he not dead. “我家主人没有死，”他指着墓穴说，
He bury, he not dead.” 他埋在地底下，但他没有死。”
My lord uttered a little noise, moved nearer to the grave, and stood and stared in it. 爵爷哼了一声，走进坟墓，站在那里直勾勾地看着。
“Buried and not dead?” exclaimed Sir William. “埋了却没有死？”威廉爵士说，
“What kind of rant is this?” “你胡说八道些什么？”
“See, sahib,” said Secundra. “你看着，先生，”赛昆德拉说，
“The sahib and I alone with murderers; try all way to escape, no way good. “我家主人和我与一群谋杀犯在一起，我们想方设法地逃走，但都没有成行。
Then try this way: good way in warm climate, good way in India; here, in this dam cold place, who can tell? 我们只好试试这个办法，这方法在温暖的天气里行得通，在印度行得通，而在这个冻得要命的地方，谁知道能不能行呢？
I tell you pretty good hurry: you help, you light a fire, help rub.” 我告诉你们得赶紧，帮帮忙，生起火，帮忙给他摩擦。”
“What is the creature talking of?” cried Sir William. 威廉爵士说：“这家伙到底在说些什么？
“My head goes round.” 我被他弄糊涂了。”
“I tell you I bury him alive,” said Secundra. 赛昆德拉说：“我告诉你，我埋他的时候，他还活着。
“I teach him swallow his tongue. 我教他把舌头吞进去。
Now dig him up pretty good hurry, and he not much worse. 现在赶紧把他挖出来，或许他还没有死。
You light a fire.” 你们生火吧。”
Sir William turned to the nearest of his men. 威廉爵士转身面对离他最近的身边人。
“Light a fire,” said he. “生火，”他说，
“My lot seems to be cast with the insane.” “似乎我也疯了一样。”
“You good man,” returned Secundra. “你可真是个好人，”赛昆德拉说，
“Now I go dig the sahib up.” “我现在就去把我家主人挖出来。”
He returned as he spoke to the grave, and resumed his former toil. 说着他又回到墓穴里，继续挖着。
My lord stood rooted, and I at my lord’s side, fearing I knew not what. 爵爷直挺挺地站着，我紧紧挨在他身边，心里有种莫名的恐惧。
The frost was not yet very deep, and presently the Indian threw aside his tool, and began to scoop the dirt by handfuls. 霜并不是很厚，不一会儿那个印度人就把工具扔在一边，开始用手挖土。
Then he disengaged a corner of a buffalo robe; and then I saw hair catch among his fingers: yet, a moment more, and the moon shone on something white. 他掀开一张牛皮大衣的一角，我看到他手指间夹着的头发，又过了一会儿，月光下露出一个白色的东西。
Awhile Secundra crouched upon his knees, scraping with delicate fingers, breathing with puffed lips; and when he moved aside, I beheld the face of the Master wholly disengaged. 赛昆德拉跪在墓穴里，小心翼翼地用手指拨弄着，嘴里轻轻地呼吸。当他把身子侧到一边时，我看清了大少爷那张木然的面孔。
It was deadly white, the eyes closed, the ears and nostrils plugged, the cheeks fallen, the nose sharp as if in death; but for all he had lain so many days under the sod, corruption had not approached him, and (what strangely affected all of us) his lips and chin were mantled with a swarthy beard. 他脸色苍白，眼睛闭着，耳朵和鼻昆塞满了东西，脸颊下垂，鼻子尖尖的像个死人，但他在地下埋了这么多天，身体没有任何腐烂的迹象，令我们奇怪的是他的嘴唇和下巴上都覆盖着新长出来的黑色胡须。
“My God!” cried Mountain, “he was as smooth as a baby when we laid him there!” 芒廷喊道：“天啊！他跟我们埋他的时候一样安详。”
“They say hair grows upon the dead,” observed Sir William; but his voice was thick and weak. 威廉爵士观察了一阵，声音浑厚而微弱地说：“据说死人身上会长毛的。”
Secundra paid no heed to our remarks, digging swift as a terrier in the loose earth. 赛昆德拉没有理会我们的议论，继续在松软的泥土中挖着，快得要命。
Every moment the form of the Master, swathed in his buffalo robe, grew more distinct in the bottom of that shallow trough; the moon shining strong, and the shadows of the standers- by, as they drew forward and back, falling and flitting over his emergent countenance. 洞穴里头，大少爷裹着牛皮大衣的身体越来越清晰。月光越来越亮，围观的人来回走动的身影不停地映射在他的面容上。
The sight held us with a horror not before experienced. 看到这幅景象，我们万分惊恐，这样的恐惧感我们平生从未有过。
I dared not look my lord in the face; but for as long as it lasted, I never observed him to draw breath; and a little in the background one of the men (I know not whom) burst into a kind of sobbing. 我不敢看爵爷的脸，可也一直听不到他的呼吸，我从没看见过他屏住呼吸。这时旁边的人群中不知是谁在啜泣。
“Now,” said Secundra, “you help me lift him out.” 赛昆德拉说：“来，大伙帮我把他抬出来。”
Of the flight of time, I have no idea; it may have been three hours, and it may have been five, that the Indian laboured to reanimate his master’s body. 我脑子里根本没了时间的概念，三个小时过去了，也或者是五个小时，那个印度人不停地给大少爷恢复元气。
One thing only I know, that it was still night, and the moon was not yet set, although it had sunk low, and now barred the plateau with long shadows, when Secundra uttered a small cry of satisfaction; and, leaning swiftly forth, I thought I could myself perceive a change upon that icy countenance of the unburied. 我只知道，此时还是晚上，月亮还挂在天上，只是下落了许多，高原也拉出了长长的影子。赛昆德拉突然得意地叫了一声，我俯身低头看去，之前从坟墓挖出的尸体的面容有了一点儿变化。
The next moment I beheld his eyelids flutter; the next they rose entirely, and the week-old corpse looked me for a moment in the face. 接着我又看到他的眼皮动了一下，然后完全睁开了眼，那具死去了一个星期的尸体居然盯着我的脸看了好一阵。
So much display of life I can myself swear to. 我发誓，我亲眼看到的生命迹象仅此而已。
I have heard from others that he visibly strove to speak, that his teeth showed in his beard, and that his brow was contorted as with an agony of pain and effort. 后来我听别人说大少爷还想说话，胡须下面的牙齿都露了出来，眉头紧蹙，一副痛苦的表情。
And this may have been; I know not, I was otherwise engaged. 或许事情是这样的，我并不太清楚，因为当时我正忙于其他事。
For at that first disclosure of the dead man’s eyes, my Lord Durrisdeer fell to the ground, and when I raised him up, he was a corpse. 一看到死人睁开眼睛，达里斯迪尔爵爷便跌倒在地，等我将他扶起来的时候，他已经变成了一具死尸。
Day came, and still Secundra could not be persuaded to desist from his unavailing efforts. 天亮了，赛昆德拉始终不肯听从劝告，一直在做着他那徒劳无功的差事。
Sir William, leaving a small party under my command, proceeded on his embassy with the first light; and still the Indian rubbed the limbs and breathed in the mouth of the dead body. 威廉爵士，留下一小队人听从我指挥，天一亮就出发了。那个印度人还在玩命地揉搓着死尸的四肢，并不时地做着人工呼吸。
You would think such labours might have vitalised a stone; but, except for that one moment (which was my lord’s death), the black spirit of the Master held aloof from its discarded clay; and by about the hour of noon, even the faithful servant was at length convinced. 你可以想象这样的镜头，即使是块石头也快被他弄活了。除了爵爷猝死的那一刻，大少爷的灵魂始终不肯回到身体上来。接近中午的时候，即便是最忠诚的奴仆也失去了信心。
He took it with unshaken quietude. 他神色平静。
“Too cold,” said he, “good way in India, no good here.” “太冷了，”他说道，“在印度还行得通，在这里不行。”
And, asking for some food, which he ravenously devoured as soon as it was set before him, he drew near to the fire and took his place at my elbow. 他向我们要了点儿吃的东西，狼吞虎咽地填了下去，然后他凑到火边，坐到了我的身边。
In the same spot, as soon as he had eaten, he stretched himself out, and fell into a childlike slumber, from which I must arouse him, some hours afterwards, to take his part as one of the mourners at the double funeral. 他吃完饭，便伸了伸懒腰，像个孩子似的睡着了。几个小时后，我必须叫醒他，在这两兄弟共同的葬礼上凑了个数。
It was the same throughout; he seemed to have outlived at once and with the same effort, his grief for his master and his terror of myself and Mountain. 他对大少爷始终不渝地哀悼着，对我和芒廷的恐惧则已消散。
One of the men left with me was skilled in stone-cutting; and before Sir William returned to pick us up, I had chiselled on a boulder this inscription, with a copy of which I may fitly bring my narrative to a close: 我们随行的人中，有人擅长石刻，在威廉爵士回来与我们重逢前，我让他在一块巨石上镂刻了一个墓志铭，作为本书的结尾：
J. D., 詹姆斯·迪里
Heir to a Scottish Title, 苏格兰贵族之子，
A Master of the Arts and Graces, 一位才华横溢、举止优雅的大少爷，
Admired in Europe, Asia, America, 广受欧亚和美洲的赞誉，
In War and Peace, 不论是战争还是和平，
In the Tents of Savage Hunters and the 不论身处野蛮人狩猎的帐篷内还是
Citadels of Kings, After So Much 国王的城堡中，
Acquired, Accomplished, and 获得荣誉、赢得功勋、
Endured, Lies Here Forgotten. 忍受折磨，终究悄然长眠于此。
H. D., 亨利·迪里，
His Brother, 他的弟弟，
After a Life of Unmerited Distress, 终生忍辱，
Bravely Supported, 节操不移，
Died Almost in the Same Hour, 同时同刻
And Sleeps in the Same Grave 同墓而眠
With His Fraternal Enemy. 与其夙敌胞兄。
The Piety of His Wife and One Old 其妻及老仆
Servant Raised this Stone 为昆仲二人立碑
To Both. 致哀
[1] Unwilling. [1]不愿意
[2] Ring. [2] 响动
